Wrightful — Architecture Deepening Review

Surfacing deepening opportunities — refactors that turn shallow modules into deep ones — for testability and AI-navigability. Findings use the language of modules, interfaces, seams, depth, leverage and locality.

Verified findings
94
Severity
4 high · 38 med · 52 low
Subsystems reviewed
14 + 5 gap areas
ADR-touching
5
Review method
123 agents
fan-out + adversarial verify

Executive summary

Wrightful is architecturally healthy at its core: the ingest pipeline (openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun in src/lib/ingest.ts) is a genuinely deep module that hides ownership-check, heterogeneous db.batch assembly, summary extraction, activity-bump and void/live broadcast behind three small calls, and the trickiest pure algorithms inside it (computeAggregateDelta, mergeRunStatus, buildChangedTests) are extracted and unit-tested. The wire contract is deliberately mirrored (reporter types.ts + dashboard schemas.ts) and held honest by contract.test.ts. The branded AuthorizedProjectId/AuthorizedTeamId on TenantScope is the right idea for type-enforcing logical tenant isolation. The dominant pattern in the findings is not architectural rot but incomplete concentration: several high-leverage invariants are implemented correctly once and then re-derived by hand across many call sites, so depth that should live behind a seam is instead smeared across consumers.

The single highest-leverage theme is that the tenant-isolation brand gates id construction but not query consumption. The brand stops you assigning a raw string to a scoped id, but every run-scoped query still re-types the projectId/teamId predicate by hand at ~18 sites, and at least one reader (the test-detail loader's four child-table reads) omits the projectId filter entirely — a latent cross-tenant read gap against the project's THE security invariant. The deletion test is decisive here: a scoped-data-access seam (scopedSelect(scope, table) / requireRunInScope(scope, runId)) would concentrate complexity that is currently duplicated across runs/* handlers, page loaders, analytics loaders, live.ts and register.ts, and would make the missing predicate impossible to forget rather than merely impossible to mistype. This is the work that most strengthens the durable decision rather than reopening it.

The second cluster is testability of deep modules whose interface doesn't expose their behaviour. The ingest orchestration glue, the realtime changedTests->byId reducer fused into useRunProgress, the artifact register->correlate->PUT pipeline buried in private reporter methods, the API-key hash/timing-safe-compare gate, and the artifact download Range/206/304 math are all correct but only reachable end-to-end (a browser, a live D1, or stubbed fetch). The unifying fix is the project's already-acknowledged missing real-D1 harness plus a handful of pure-reducer/pure-builder extractions — and the ingest pipeline should be its first consumer because it has the highest blast radius. A sharp footnote: the one merge-run-status unit test exercises a JS reference that completeRun never calls (completeRun re-implements the merge as hand-built SQL), so the most-tested invariant is tested in the wrong place.

The remaining findings are mostly low-risk concentration wins — credential-byte crypto duplicated across four files, the user/account raw-SQL reads with no owning module, branch-param decode and querystring href builders copy-pasted across 6-7 loaders, the status taxonomy smeared across ~10 frontend components in four conflicting encodings (with lib/status.ts hex drifting from the styles.css oklch tokens) — plus a small set of true risks that are NOT deepenings: the lone ansi XSS sink is untested with CSP weakened to script-src 'unsafe-inline', the cron watchdog force-interrupts live runs because it has no liveness signal and can self-DoS on a mass-stranding event, rate limiting is declared-but-unprovisioned, and the demo bootstrap screen-scrapes a route/cookie the app already removed. Overall: a deep, well-factored core with several seams half-built; the highest return is finishing the concentration the architecture already implies.

How this was produced

This review was generated by a deterministic multi-agent workflow rather than a single read-through, so coverage is broad and each claim is checked against the code before it lands here:

  1. Survey — one agent inventoried every subsystem, its heaviest modules, and a first-pass health read to ground the rest.
  2. Fan-out finders — 14 agents, one per subsystem, each read the actual files and proposed deepening opportunities against the deletion test.
  3. Adversarial verification — every individual finding was handed to a separate skeptic agent prompted to refute it: open the cited files, confirm the friction is real, re-run the deletion test, and check whether it quietly contradicts a settled migration decision. Findings that misread the code were dropped; framings that were off were revised (titles/solutions you see may be the verifier's sharpened version).
  4. Completeness critic — a critic examined the full finding set for whole categories that were under-covered and spawned 5 targeted gap-finders (cron watchdog, capability credentials, route-shape coupling, output/origin safety, config & secrets) — themselves verified.
  5. Synthesis — the verified set was grouped into themes and a prioritized roadmap.
Reading the verdict badges. revise means the verifier kept the insight but sharpened the framing; keep means it survived refutation as written. Confidence reflects how sure the verifier was after reading the cited code. The durable migration decisions (single D1, logical tenancy, void-managed auth tables, void/live, isomorphic pages, no nuqs, no ETL) were treated as settled — findings that touch them are flagged and, in nearly every case, reinforce rather than reopen them.

Completeness critic’s read

The findings densely cover the read/write data paths (ingest, tenancy-authz, analytics, routes-middleware, frontend, reporter, artifacts) but systematically under-cover the operational and security perimeter — the seams that aren't on the run-detail/analytics happy path. Four whole categories are barely or not touched: (1) the cron watchdog as its own module (only its shared batch-tail is noted, never its staleness predicate, unboundedness, or concurrency); (2) the capability-credential / crypto-primitive seam — base64url, timing-safe-equal, and SHA-256-hex are each re-implemented across artifact-tokens / invite-tokens / api-key in incompatible forms, and the untested ones are precisely the duplicated ones; (3) the route-shape knowledge that is triple-encoded as regexes across 02.api-auth, 03.rate-limit, and the route tree, coupling auth-gating to throttling with no test holding them in sync; (4) the config/secrets + content-security policy seam — the ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET fallback, the CSP in void.json, the SAFE_CONTENT_TYPES allowlist, and the ansi→HTML escaping together form one "don't execute attacker-controlled bytes on our origin" policy that is smeared across five files with nothing tying them. The KNOWN-OUTSTANDING note that rate limiting is 'declared but not provisioned' is now stale — it is wired (03.rate-limit.ts + wrangler ratelimits + a regression test), which reframes it from a TODO into an active, untested coupling surface. The reporter (incl. pr-comment) is genuinely well-covered by existing tests; do not re-send it.

Cross-cutting themes

Ten patterns recur across subsystems. Each lists its member findings; click through to the detail.

The tenant-isolation brand gates id construction but not query consumption · 9 findings

AuthorizedProjectId/AuthorizedTeamId stop you mistyping a scoped id, but the projectId/teamId predicate is re-derived by hand at every run-scoped query site, inconsistently — and one reader omits it entirely, opening a latent cross-tenant gap against THE durable security invariant. A scoped-data-access / requireRunInScope seam concentrates this and makes the filter impossible to forget, not merely impossible to mistype.

  • Branded TenantScope gates id construction but not query consumption — every run-scoped query re-derives the scope predicate by hand, inconsistently; concentrate it behind a scoped-data-access seam
  • Test-detail loader reads four child tables by testResultId with no projectId predicate — the lone reader that omits the scope every other reader already carries (latent cross-tenant gap)
  • A canonical "fetch run R within scope S or 404" seam is missing; ~3 handlers re-derive the scoped run-ownership SELECT, and single-run lookups drift from the documented (teamId, projectId) scope
  • Run-ownership authorization is re-derived per call site, and the live.ts websocket path uses a membership join a scope-predicate refactor would silently miss
  • The 'fetch this run, scoped to project' read probe is hand-rolled in 4 page/API sites — one already drops the branded id
  • Run-ownership verification is a copy-pasted projectId+id SELECT smeared across five call sites instead of one seam
  • scopedRunsWhere discards the AuthorizedProjectId/AuthorizedTeamId brand by taking plain string ids — tighten it to take TenantScope like loadProjectBranches
  • Tenant-scope brand is enforced only at the query-builder seam; child-row reads in the test-detail loader omit the projectId predicate by convention
  • Tenant-isolation scope predicates are emitted in 18 inline query sites but asserted only by one 5-case live browser spec covering 2 endpoints

Deep modules whose behaviour is unreachable through their own interface · 10 findings

The deepest, highest-blast-radius modules (ingest orchestration, the realtime reducer, the artifact upload pipeline, API-key resolution, the download HTTP math) are correct but only testable end-to-end. The fix is the missing real-D1 harness plus pure-reducer/pure-builder extractions — and the ingest pipeline should be the harness's first consumer.

  • The ingest write pipeline is a correct deep module whose orchestration glue (batch assembly, summary-from-last-row, status merge) is unreachable through its own interface — make it the first consumer of the missing real-D1 harness
  • Ingest orchestrators' composition is untestable through their interface — and the one "merge" unit test exercises a JS reference completeRun never calls
  • useRunProgress fuses the live transport, the changedTests→byId accumulator, and SSR seeding into one React hook — the reducer is only testable through a browser
  • Artifact register->correlate->PUT pipeline lives in private reporter methods with no isolated test surface for the positional-alignment invariant
  • The retries->done buffering Map (onTestEnd accumulation + onEnd fallback drain) is reporter instance state, so the buffer-until-final-retry lifecycle is only testable end-to-end via stubbed fetch
  • API-key resolution (hash lookup + revocation + timing-safe compare) has no unit coverage despite being pure-enough to extract
  • Range/206/304/Content-Range math in the artifact download handler is welded to the R2Object shape — extract a pure response builder so the protocol logic is unit-testable
  • The sole realtime tenant-isolation gate (onSubscribe runs⋈memberships check) is inlined in the defineLiveStream literal, so the isolation decision can't be unit-tested without a void/live handshake + real D1
  • Artifact-register handler skips the ingest.ts planning/IO split, leaving safeKeySegment + artifactIdentity (idempotency key + key-sanitizer) with no unit seam
  • SQL-semantics builders (LIKE-escape, bucket divisor, status→bucket recompute) lack parity/escaping unit tests

Same invariant transcribed twice — JS/SQL and cross-package drift · 7 findings

Several load-bearing invariants exist as two transcriptions with no enforcing link: completeRun's status-merge as JS and as hand-built SQL CASE; the v3 wire contract as reporter TS and dashboard Zod; the X-Wrightful-Version literal; the artifact-token secret fallback; the SQL↔JS bucket-key equivalence. The risk is silent divergence the type system can't catch.

  • completeRun re-implements mergeRunStatus as a hand-built SQL CASE that the test suite cannot reach, risking silent JS/SQL drift
  • The v3 wire contract is two hand-maintained copies (reporter types.ts + dashboard schemas.ts) with no shared module — only a cross-package relative-import test holds them together
  • contract.test.ts guards wire-payload shapes but not the X-Wrightful-Version literal, which drifts independently across reporter and dashboard
  • E2e artifact-token forger silently diverges from the dashboard the moment a dedicated ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is set — the fixture injects BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, not the resolved signing secret
  • SQL↔JS bucket-key equivalence is an untested cross-file contract with a silent-empty-chart failure mode
  • The summary-extraction contract ('last batch row is the summary') is an implicit positional convention enforced by every caller, not by the seam
  • Zod wire schemas and reporter TS interfaces are duplicated — but this duplication is correctly guarded and should NOT be collapsed

Missing owner modules for cross-cutting primitives · 9 findings

Three primitive families are re-derived everywhere because no module owns them: credential-byte crypto (sha256/base64url/timing-safe/mint) across 4 files, raw-SQL reads of the void-owned user/account tables across 6 callers, and the caller's invite identity across 4 redemption paths. These are textbook deletion-test wins — concentrate the complexity currently smeared across N callers.

  • Token/credential-bytes crypto (sha256 hex, base64url, timing-safe compare, mint) duplicated across 4 files with no shared seam
  • No owner module for void-managed auth tables — raw SQL + result-envelope casts against "user"/"account" are duplicated across 6 invite/profile/members callers
  • Identity resolution against the void-owned user/account tables (raw SQL + cast + email/githubLogin matchConds) is copy-pasted across four invite/email call sites with a fifth account-table variant
  • Caller's directed-invite identity (raw-SQL user.email + githubLogin) is re-resolved in four redemption paths; the matchConds predicate in three
  • User-invite-identity lookup is copy-pasted three times beside an existing invite-identity.ts
  • Three-way duplicated `→ TenantScope` brand-cast projection; one true pass-through (tenantScopeForUserBySlugs) to inline
  • No change.
  • GitHub-login mirror hook is best-effort glue welded into config, with no test seam and a silently-swallowed failure
  • profile loader embeds void account-table storage knowledge (createdAt number/string coercion + credential/github providerId semantics) — fold into finding #1's getUserAccounts adapter rather than extract standalone

The analytics read tier has no deep query module · 7 findings

The analytics lib captures only trivial fragments; every loader hand-writes the same ranked-CTE skeleton, percentile picker, status buckets and scope-join inside db.run(sql...), invisible to Drizzle. The day-bucket fragment hardcodes runs.createdAt so one straggler is off the seam. A latest-per-test query module would concentrate this without one omnibus builder.

  • No deep "latest-per-test" analytics query module — three loaders re-inline the same ranked-CTE + status-counter SQL
  • Analytics read loaders hand-rebuild shared SQL fragments (scope-join, status buckets, percentile picker) invisible to Drizzle
  • Discrete-percentile picker fragment is re-stated 7× across two analytics loaders
  • bucketExpr hardcodes runs.createdAt, so slowest-tests' day-bucket + the D1 text-affinity caveat are re-implemented inline (one straggler off the seam)
  • Analytics loaders re-derive branchFilter, window math, and segment defaults inline — with the window math diverged into three forms
  • Analytics range/bucketing pure functions are untested — the cheap UTC-month-key vs SQL strftime contract is the real gap (bucketKey is trivial)
  • branches-query.ts documents and relies on an index that does not exist

Handler preamble and request-shape duplication · 8 findings

Tenant read-API handlers, owner-gated and member-gated settings paths, JSON-or-form body parsing, and the ingest-route shape (Bearer-gate + throttle-gate) all re-implement the same preambles inline. settings-scope.ts already proves the deep-seam pattern; the work is extending it to the paths it doesn't yet cover and pulling the route-shape matcher into one predicate.

  • Tenant read-API handlers re-implement the same auth+param+scope+404 preamble four times
  • Run-detail loader re-inlines loadRunResultsPage's testResults query and skips its status normalization
  • Owner-gated API handlers bypass requireOwnedProjectScope and hand-roll a divergent 403 gate
  • Member-gated settings loaders open-code requireAuth->resolve->404 instead of a sibling member seam (owner seam already exists in settings-scope.ts)
  • requireTeamOwner signals not-owner via a bare Error, forcing callers into untyped catches that swallow D1 failures as 404 (invisible to Tail)
  • JSON-or-form body parsing for owner mint endpoints is duplicated inline
  • 00.errors.ts is a deep error gate, but its status->outcome policy is duplicated across the catch arm and the post-next() arm (plus a separately-duplicated API logging predicate)
  • The ingest-route shape is duplicated byte-for-byte across the Bearer-gate (02) and throttle-gate (03) with no shared matcher — drift silently ships an authed-but-unthrottled or throttled-but-500ing route

Frontend: status taxonomy and querystring/list-page primitives smeared across pages · 9 findings

The status domain is encoded in four conflicting forms across ~10 components with hex drifting from the oklch theme tokens; querystring href builders, branch-param decode, sparklines, stacked-status bars and search-filter markup are each copy-pasted across the insights/tests/flaky family — and one search input ships dead (a no-op bug). Make lib/status.ts the single registry and extract the shared list-page primitives.

  • Status taxonomy (color token / label / badge variant / severity / collapse rule) is smeared across ~10 frontend components in four conflicting encodings, with lib/status.ts hex silently drifting from the styles.css oklch tokens
  • Scalar query-string href builders (hrefWith / pageHref / rangeHref) are copy-pasted across ~7 insights/tests/flaky page modules and have already drifted
  • Branch-param decode (`__all__`/empty -> null) is duplicated in 6 loaders instead of living with ALL_BRANCHES
  • The branchFilter normalization (ALL_BRANCHES->null) is copy-pasted across 6 loaders; raw-SQL branch/search fragments add minor inline duplication
  • Search-filter input markup is copy-pasted across flaky/tests/run-progress (one copy is a dead, no-op input — a shipped bug); extract a presentational SearchFilterInput
  • OutcomeBar and the page-local OutcomeMix are the same stacked-status-bar reimplemented
  • Two numeric-line sparklines (MetricSparkline + page-private DurationSparkline) duplicate the same job with incompatible x-spacing
  • RunProgress re-implements grouping/severity-ordering inline instead of using the existing pure groupTestsByFile module — duplicated, drifting, untestable
  • app-layout and workspace-switcher hand-roll local Team/Project/SelectedTeam types, widening the branded TeamRole to a loose string at the owner gate

The live summary seam is dishonest and the realtime path carries vestiges · 6 findings

Ingest builds and broadcasts a transactionally-consistent run summary; useRunProgress accumulates it; then RunProgress discards it (_summary) and the header tiles render from static SSR props — so the one e2e that names 'summary counters' actually exercises a different recompute path. Around it sit two cosmetic wrapper layers and a dead useSyncedState alias with vestigial DO prose.

  • RunProgressEvent.summary is produced transactionally in ingest, accumulated by the hook, then discarded by RunProgress (_summary); the header tiles/OutcomeBar/tab-count render from static SSR props and the e2e that names "summary counters" actually exercises the row-recompute path
  • broadcastRunUpdate is a one-line payload assembler over publishRunUpdate; the two-wrapper stack is cosmetic, not a real seam
  • Dead useSyncedState alias (zero importers) plus vestigial SyncedStateServer/DO prose across live-client.ts, live.ts, ingest.ts, and the realtime e2e spec
  • Dead `useSyncedState` alias in live-client.ts is the only true vestige; the other "shims" are either a legitimate adapter (navigate) or cosmetic
  • `rateLimit()` per-route middleware factory is exported but has zero callers
  • rateLimit() per-route factory is dead code masquerading as a co-equal throttling seam

Param-chunk and db.batch glue lacks an owning seam · 6 findings

The D1 <=99-param chunking and the heterogeneous db.batch + forced as never cast + last-row extraction are core architectural decisions with no owning module — chunk column counts are un-derived magic literals decoupled from the schema, and the cast/extraction is repeated across 7 files. Derive counts from the row shape and add thin typed batch wrappers; fold the shared finalize tail so cron and completeRun share by construction.

  • Param-chunk column counts are un-derived magic literals that can silently drift from the schema/insert shapes they protect
  • Per-table column-count constants are hand-maintained and decoupled from the schema
  • Typed db.batch wrapper concentrates the forced `as never` call-site cast + result extraction across 7 files
  • finalizeStaleRun and completeRun share a batch-recompute-broadcast tail by copy, not by construction (no enforcing seam)
  • R2 key construction (register) and its filename-reversal (download) encode the same trailing-segment convention in opposite directions with nothing tying them
  • Artifact write pipeline (register + upload) is inlined in handlers, breaking the ingest.ts deep-module precedent the runs/* handlers follow

Seeding/scripts and config flags drift from the production seams · 16 findings

The seed/upload scripts hand-roll untested copies of the reporter's StreamClient and the v3 wire payload (already drifted), screen-scrape form 302s and a key-reveal cookie the app removed, and name the base-URL env var two ways. Feature flags (GitHub-enabled, open-signup) and the artifact secret fallback are decoded by multiple incompatible rules. Reuse the real seams instead of re-deriving them.

  • History-seeding loop hand-rolls an untested, no-retry copy of the reporter's StreamClient ingest path
  • Synthetic-run seeder hand-builds the v3 wire payload as an untested third copy of the reporter contract, and has already drifted (omits projectName/workerIndex)
  • Demo bootstrap screen-scrapes form-action 302s for team/project creation; seed-demo.mjs still parses a key-reveal cookie that the app already removed
  • upload-fixtures.mjs re-derives dev-server.mjs's dashboard-readiness probe instead of importing it
  • Base-URL env var is named two different ways across the script pipeline
  • sha40 helper duplicated across upload-fixtures and the seed generator with two divergent algorithms (minor duplication, not a depth win)
  • The github-enabled predicate is re-derived in four loaders and open-signup is decoded by two incompatible rules — no shared flag helper
  • ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP truthiness is decoded by two unrelated rules (regex vs void boolean coercion) that can drift
  • "Is GitHub OAuth enabled" is inlined in four loaders, splitting an unavoidable config-time/request-time env-source choice across copies
  • Retry/backoff loop is duplicated between fetchWithRetry and uploadArtifact instead of one retry policy
  • Theme contract (`'theme'` key, dark default, class toggle) is encoded independently in the FOUC script and the toggle component
  • env.ts comment overstates artifact byte-cap enforcement: upload only matches the registered size, it does not re-check the cap
  • "Presigned R2 URL" is fiction — the documented interface lies about what register/download actually do
  • Download-URL shape is re-derived at four dashboard sites and the e2e suite hand-clones the signing algorithm (with a latent secret divergence)
  • Artifact idempotency invariant is implied by a lookup, not declared near the schema or enforced by a DB unique index
  • Rate-limiter binding-to-path-set pairing exists only as adjacency + prose; no test pins the config-vs-code mapping or the strict/loose budget ordering

Prioritized roadmap

Ordered by leverage-per-effort and risk. Not every finding appears here — the long tail of low-severity cleanups lives in the catalog below.

Now

(high leverage, low risk)

Lead with two things that are both cheap and protect the project's security invariant and only XSS sink. First close the latent cross-tenant gap: add the missing projectId predicate to the test-detail loader's four child reads, and unit-test the scope-predicate emission (no-DB) so the 18 inline sites are pinned — these reinforce durable decision #2 without reopening it. Pair that with a unit test on the lone ansi sink (a one-file test, no signature change). Then bank the trivially-correct concentration wins: extract requireRunInScope/assertRunOwned for the copy-pasted ownership SELECT, the credential-byte crypto module, the auth-tables/invite-identity owner module, the tenant read-handler preamble helper, the scalar href + branch-param + status-registry frontend extractions, and the JS/SQL merge-status collapse (so the most-tested invariant is tested where completeRun actually calls it). Delete the dead useSyncedState alias and the unused rateLimit() factory. Fix the seed-demo.mjs cookie/route bug and standardise WRIGHTFUL_URL. All small-effort, mostly duplication/dead-code, and each removes a documented drift hazard.

  1. Test-detail loader reads four child tables by testResultId with no projectId predicate — the lone reader that omits the scope every other reader already carries (latent cross-tenant gap)
  2. ansiToHtml is the app's only untrusted-text→dangerouslySetInnerHTML seam and is completely untested
  3. Tenant-isolation scope predicates are emitted in 18 inline query sites but asserted only by one 5-case live browser spec covering 2 endpoints
  4. Run-ownership verification is a copy-pasted projectId+id SELECT smeared across five call sites instead of one seam
  5. completeRun re-implements mergeRunStatus as a hand-built SQL CASE that the test suite cannot reach, risking silent JS/SQL drift
  6. Token/credential-bytes crypto (sha256 hex, base64url, timing-safe compare, mint) duplicated across 4 files with no shared seam
  7. No owner module for void-managed auth tables — raw SQL + result-envelope casts against "user"/"account" are duplicated across 6 invite/profile/members callers
  8. Caller's directed-invite identity (raw-SQL user.email + githubLogin) is re-resolved in four redemption paths; the matchConds predicate in three
  9. Tenant read-API handlers re-implement the same auth+param+scope+404 preamble four times
  10. Scalar query-string href builders (hrefWith / pageHref / rangeHref) are copy-pasted across ~7 insights/tests/flaky page modules and have already drifted
  11. Branch-param decode (`__all__`/empty -> null) is duplicated in 6 loaders instead of living with ALL_BRANCHES
  12. Status taxonomy (color token / label / badge variant / severity / collapse rule) is smeared across ~10 frontend components in four conflicting encodings, with lib/status.ts hex silently drifting from the styles.css oklch tokens
  13. Search-filter input markup is copy-pasted across flaky/tests/run-progress (one copy is a dead, no-op input — a shipped bug); extract a presentational SearchFilterInput
  14. Dead useSyncedState alias (zero importers) plus vestigial SyncedStateServer/DO prose across live-client.ts, live.ts, ingest.ts, and the realtime e2e spec
  15. `rateLimit()` per-route middleware factory is exported but has zero callers
  16. Demo bootstrap screen-scrapes form-action 302s for team/project creation; seed-demo.mjs still parses a key-reveal cookie that the app already removed
  17. Base-URL env var is named two different ways across the script pipeline
  18. Param-chunk column counts are un-derived magic literals that can silently drift from the schema/insert shapes they protect
  19. contract.test.ts guards wire-payload shapes but not the X-Wrightful-Version literal, which drifts independently across reporter and dashboard

Next

(medium leverage, some structural work)

Land the project's missing real-D1 harness and make the ingest pipeline its first consumer — this unblocks the whole untestable-deep-module theme and de-risks the highest-blast-radius code. With the harness in place, extract the pure pieces that the harness or simple unit tests can then drive: the useRunProgress reducer, the API-key resolver, the artifact upload pipeline + planArtifactRegistration, the download HTTP-math builder, the onSubscribe authz function, the reporter TestAccumulator. In parallel build the two structural seams the rest of the codebase keeps re-deriving: the scoped-data-access seam (scopedSelect/requireRunInScope, tightening scopedRunsWhere to take TenantScope) and the artifacts.ts write module mirroring ingest.ts. Fix the dishonest live-summary seam (lift the counters into a live island or stop broadcasting the summary) and the watchdog liveness bug (add lastActivityAt) since both are correctness issues that need a schema/design decision while the initial migration is still unfrozen. Medium effort, higher coordination, but each pays off across many of the Now-phase extractions.

  1. The ingest write pipeline is a correct deep module whose orchestration glue (batch assembly, summary-from-last-row, status merge) is unreachable through its own interface — make it the first consumer of the missing real-D1 harness
  2. Branded TenantScope gates id construction but not query consumption — every run-scoped query re-derives the scope predicate by hand, inconsistently; concentrate it behind a scoped-data-access seam
  3. A canonical "fetch run R within scope S or 404" seam is missing; ~3 handlers re-derive the scoped run-ownership SELECT, and single-run lookups drift from the documented (teamId, projectId) scope
  4. useRunProgress fuses the live transport, the changedTests→byId accumulator, and SSR seeding into one React hook — the reducer is only testable through a browser
  5. API-key resolution (hash lookup + revocation + timing-safe compare) has no unit coverage despite being pure-enough to extract
  6. Artifact write pipeline (register + upload) is inlined in handlers, breaking the ingest.ts deep-module precedent the runs/* handlers follow
  7. Artifact register->correlate->PUT pipeline lives in private reporter methods with no isolated test surface for the positional-alignment invariant
  8. Range/206/304/Content-Range math in the artifact download handler is welded to the R2Object shape — extract a pure response builder so the protocol logic is unit-testable
  9. The sole realtime tenant-isolation gate (onSubscribe runs⋈memberships check) is inlined in the defineLiveStream literal, so the isolation decision can't be unit-tested without a void/live handshake + real D1
  10. RunProgressEvent.summary is produced transactionally in ingest, accumulated by the hook, then discarded by RunProgress (_summary); the header tiles/OutcomeBar/tab-count render from static SSR props and the e2e that names "summary counters" actually exercises the row-recompute path
  11. Watchdog measures 'old since open', not 'stuck' — no liveness signal on the runs row
  12. No deep "latest-per-test" analytics query module — three loaders re-inline the same ranked-CTE + status-counter SQL
  13. Run-detail loader re-inlines loadRunResultsPage's testResults query and skips its status normalization
  14. RunProgress re-implements grouping/severity-ordering inline instead of using the existing pure groupTestsByFile module — duplicated, drifting, untestable
  15. requireTeamOwner signals not-owner via a bare Error, forcing callers into untyped catches that swallow D1 failures as 404 (invisible to Tail)
  16. Member-gated settings loaders open-code requireAuth->resolve->404 instead of a sibling member seam (owner seam already exists in settings-scope.ts)
  17. The summary-extraction contract ('last batch row is the summary') is an implicit positional convention enforced by every caller, not by the seam
  18. Typed db.batch wrapper concentrates the forced `as never` call-site cast + result extraction across 7 files
  19. finalizeStaleRun and completeRun share a batch-recompute-broadcast tail by copy, not by construction (no enforcing seam)
  20. GitHub-login mirror hook is best-effort glue welded into config, with no test seam and a silently-swallowed failure

Later

(larger or lower-leverage)

Defer the larger structural moves and the lower-severity polish. The shared protocol package and the analytics query module are real wins but large-effort and one touches a durable decision (mark adrConflict) — do them once the harness proves out the contract tests that would protect the refactor. The CSP nonce restoration is large and only a backstop once the ansi sink is tested in Now. The watchdog self-DoS hardening, the analytics fragment/window-math consolidations, the seeder StreamClient reuse, the feature-flag/secret-fallback helpers, sparkline/OutcomeBar consolidation, and the various interface-truth/documentation fixes (presigned-URL fiction, byte-cap comment, branches index comment) are all genuine but lower leverage-per-effort; batch them as cleanup once the high-value seams exist. Keep the deliberately-duplicated wire schemas as-is unless the shared package lands.

  1. The v3 wire contract is two hand-maintained copies (reporter types.ts + dashboard schemas.ts) with no shared module — only a cross-package relative-import test holds them together
  2. Analytics read loaders hand-rebuild shared SQL fragments (scope-join, status buckets, percentile picker) invisible to Drizzle
  3. script-src 'unsafe-inline' (a nonce-CSP regression from the Void migration) removes CSP as a backstop for the lone ansi XSS sink
  4. Watchdog cron can self-DoS on a mass-stranding event: unbounded sweep SELECT + strict-serial finalize, no per-pass budget
  5. Run-ownership authorization is re-derived per call site, and the live.ts websocket path uses a membership join a scope-predicate refactor would silently miss
  6. Analytics loaders re-derive branchFilter, window math, and segment defaults inline — with the window math diverged into three forms
  7. Discrete-percentile picker fragment is re-stated 7× across two analytics loaders
  8. bucketExpr hardcodes runs.createdAt, so slowest-tests' day-bucket + the D1 text-affinity caveat are re-implemented inline (one straggler off the seam)
  9. SQL↔JS bucket-key equivalence is an untested cross-file contract with a silent-empty-chart failure mode
  10. History-seeding loop hand-rolls an untested, no-retry copy of the reporter's StreamClient ingest path
  11. Synthetic-run seeder hand-builds the v3 wire payload as an untested third copy of the reporter contract, and has already drifted (omits projectName/workerIndex)
  12. R2 key construction (register) and its filename-reversal (download) encode the same trailing-segment convention in opposite directions with nothing tying them
  13. Download-URL shape is re-derived at four dashboard sites and the e2e suite hand-clones the signing algorithm (with a latent secret divergence)
  14. The ingest-route shape is duplicated byte-for-byte across the Bearer-gate (02) and throttle-gate (03) with no shared matcher — drift silently ships an authed-but-unthrottled or throttled-but-500ing route
  15. The github-enabled predicate is re-derived in four loaders and open-signup is decoded by two incompatible rules — no shared flag helper
  16. Two numeric-line sparklines (MetricSparkline + page-private DurationSparkline) duplicate the same job with incompatible x-spacing
  17. OutcomeBar and the page-local OutcomeMix are the same stacked-status-bar reimplemented
  18. Theme contract (`'theme'` key, dark default, class toggle) is encoded independently in the FOUC script and the toggle component
  19. "Presigned R2 URL" is fiction — the documented interface lies about what register/download actually do
  20. Artifact idempotency invariant is implied by a lookup, not declared near the schema or enforced by a DB unique index
  21. env.ts comment overstates artifact byte-cap enforcement: upload only matches the registered size, it does not re-check the cap
  22. branches-query.ts documents and relies on an index that does not exist
  23. app-layout and workspace-switcher hand-roll local Team/Project/SelectedTeam types, widening the branded TeamRole to a loose string at the owner gate
  24. 00.errors.ts is a deep error gate, but its status->outcome policy is duplicated across the catch arm and the post-next() arm (plus a separately-duplicated API logging predicate)
  25. Retry/backoff loop is duplicated between fetchWithRetry and uploadArtifact instead of one retry policy

Top risks

These are not simple deepenings — they are correctness, security or operational risks that the review surfaced and that deserve attention regardless of the refactoring roadmap.

  1. Cross-tenant read gap: the test-detail loader reads testResultAttempts/testTags/testAnnotations/artifacts by testResultId with NO projectId predicate, against the project's own stated THE security invariant. Logical isolation is type-enforced only at id construction; the brand cannot catch a forgotten predicate at the query site. This is a latent data-leak path, not merely a deepening — close it in Now.

  2. Untested XSS sink with a weakened backstop: ansiToHtml is the only attacker-controlled-text -> dangerouslySetInnerHTML path (anyone with a project API key can write errorMessage/errorStack via ingest), it has zero tests, AND CSP was regressed to script-src 'unsafe-inline' in the Void migration, removing the script backstop. Two independent failures guarding the same origin-execution boundary.

  3. Cron watchdog force-interrupts LIVE runs: the stuck-run predicate keys off run-open time (createdAt < cutoff) with no liveness signal on the runs row, so any legitimately long-running run is marked interrupted — a correctness bug that contradicts the watchdog's own docstring. Compounded by an unbounded sweep SELECT + strict-serial finalize that can self-DoS the single-region writer on a mass-stranding event.

  4. Rate limiting is declared-but-unprovisioned: middleware/03.rate-limit.ts and the wrangler ratelimits entries exist, checkRateLimit fails OPEN when the binding is missing, and no test pins the binding-to-path mapping or strict/loose budgets. Until provisioned and verified, the ingest/auth/artifact routes are effectively unthrottled in any environment where the binding isn't wired.

  5. Tenant isolation has almost no automated proof: 18 inline scope predicates are asserted only by a single 5-case live-browser spec covering 2 endpoints. There is no no-DB unit test that the scoped predicate is actually emitted, and the live.ts websocket subscription authz uses a structurally different membership join that a scope-predicate refactor would silently miss.

  6. Build/deploy/E2E against the Void dashboard is not yet exercised, and the missing real-D1 harness means the deepest modules (ingest orchestration, artifact register planning, status-merge SQL) have never run against a real database in test. The most-tested invariant (mergeRunStatus) is unit-tested via a JS reference that completeRun never calls — it ships hand-built SQL instead.

  7. Seeding/bootstrap scripts are silently broken or drifting against production: seed-demo.mjs targets a key-reveal cookie + route the app already removed, the synthetic seeder hand-builds a v3 payload that has already drifted (omits projectName/workerIndex), and the base-URL env var is named two ways across the pipeline — so local/demo setup can fail or produce wrong-shaped data without warning.

  8. E2E artifact-token forger injects BETTER_AUTH_SECRET rather than the resolved signing secret, so the moment a dedicated ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is set in production the test fixture signs tokens the dashboard will reject — a config-fallback divergence that makes the e2e a false positive exactly when the secret split matters.

Subsystem survey

Wrightful is a two-package monorepo (~35.6k lines of TS/TSX) split cleanly along its one real network seam: packages/reporter (a Playwright reporter, ~1.6k impl + ~2.6k test) emits a versioned wire payload; apps/dashboard (a Void/Cloudflare app) ingests it. The wire contract is the spine of the system and is genuinely well-seamed: it exists as TS interfaces (reporter/src/types.ts) and Zod schemas (dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts), with a cross-package contract test (reporter/src/__tests__/contract.test.ts) acting as the canary. The protocol version header (X-Wrightful-Version, only v3 accepted) is a hard gate in api-auth.ts. This is the healthiest part of the codebase.

The architectural center of gravity is the ingest pipeline. src/lib/ingest.ts (849 lines, the single heaviest module) is the project's one deliberately deep module: route handlers under routes/api/runs/* are 26-40 lines of auth+translation each, and the whole "verify ownership → compose D1 batch → extract transactionally-consistent summary → bump activity → broadcast" pipeline lives behind openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun. It absorbs real complexity that would otherwise smear across callers: param-chunking to D1's 99-param ceiling, sharded-suite idempotency (onConflictDoNothing prefill, severity-ranked atomic status merge in SQL), and aggregate-delta counters to avoid full re-scans. The deletion test passes decisively — delete it and the complexity reappears in every route. Tenant isolation is the other strong seam: src/lib/scope.ts brands AuthorizedProjectId/AuthorizedTeamId so the type system forces every run-scoped query through an auth-checked id, and projectId/teamId are denormalized onto child tables so scope is enforced without joins.

Health is mixed at the edges. The analytics/insights loaders (flaky.server.ts 329, slowest-tests.server.ts 263, tests.server.ts 265, suite-size.server.ts) are the largest concentration of hand-written raw SQL — each is a self-contained, multi-pass CTE query with its own range-parsing, branch-filter, and pagination logic that is structurally similar across files but not consolidated, the most visible candidate for deepening. middleware/00.errors.ts (167) is dense with framework-specific workarounds (Hono swallows thrown Errors into c.res before next() unwinds, requiring a dual catch + post-next inspection) — necessary but shallow-feeling. The UI layer is broad and conventional: 54 ui/ wrappers (~7.3k lines) over Base UI plus 32 feature components (~4.8k), with sidebar.tsx (740) and drawer.tsx (626) being vendored/scaffolded bulk rather than authored depth. Known-outstanding items (no real-DB test harness for the ingest lib, rate limiting declared-not-provisioned, run-progress.tsx is actually a full 416-line island not a stub) bound the verified test coverage.

Subsystems

Ingest pipeline

Open/append/complete streaming runs: verify ownership, compose atomic D1 batches (chunked <=99 params), compute aggregate-delta counters, merge sharded-suite terminal status atomically in SQL, broadcast progress. Handlers are auth+translation only.

Deep — the canonical deep module; small handler interface over a large pipeline, passes the deletion test (complexity would reappear across every route). Only gap is the unported real-DB integration tests.

Deep — the brand is leverage: it makes the query-scoping invariant a compile-time error to violate, concentrating an otherwise-smeared discipline into the type system.

Vocabulary

Every finding is written in one consistent architectural vocabulary. The terms are deliberately precise:

Module — anything with an interface and an implementation (a function, a class, a package, a tier-spanning slice). Interface — everything a caller must know to use it correctly: types, invariants, ordering, error modes, required config — not just the type signature. Depth — leverage at the interface: a lot of behaviour behind a small interface. A module is deep when a large amount of behaviour sits behind a small interface, and shallow when the interface is nearly as complex as the implementation. Seam — where an interface lives; a place behaviour can be altered without editing in place. Leverage — what callers get from depth (capability per unit of interface learned). Locality — what maintainers get from depth (change, bugs and knowledge concentrate in one place).

The deletion test is the recurring tool: imagine deleting the module. If complexity vanishes, it was a pass-through. If complexity reappears across N callers, it was earning its keep — which is exactly what a good deepening creates.

Findings catalog

All 94 verified findings, grouped by subsystem. Use the toolbar to filter by severity or search titles and problems.

High Medium Low

Ingest pipeline · 6 findings

#1 · Ingest pipeline
completeRun re-implements mergeRunStatus as a hand-built SQL CASE that the test suite cannot reach, risking silent JS/SQL drift
medium severity effort: small confidence: high deep but fragile
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:730-735
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:745-751
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:782-783
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/merge-run-status.test.ts
Problem — the friction

The monotonic status-merge invariant exists in two forms: the JS mergeRunStatus (ingest.ts:730), which merge-run-status.test.ts exercises thoroughly, and a hand-rolled SQL expression statusExpr (ingest.ts:782-783) built from currentStatusSeveritySql() that completeRun actually executes. The comment at ingest.ts:737-744 asserts the SQL 'can't drift from mergeRunStatus' because both read RUN_STATUS_SEVERITY — but they are independent expressions of the algorithm. mergeRunStatus uses inc > cur (strict, keeps current on ties); statusExpr uses currentSeverity < incomingSeverity (strict, keeps current on ties) — they happen to agree today, but the tie-breaking, the running special-case, and the ?? 0 fallback are encoded twice. The tested function is NOT the one that runs in production. A maintainer who 'fixes' a tie-break in the JS reference, sees green tests, and ships, has changed nothing about the actual UPDATE. The genuinely deep, race-closing atomic-merge-in-SQL is correct but fragile: its correctness rests on a hand-transcribed CASE that no test executes.

Solution — the deepened module

Two complementary fixes, pick per appetite. (a) Harness-independent, do now: collapse the two transcriptions to one. The SQL builder and mergeRunStatus both encode {running-special-case, severity-compare, tie-break}; factor the decision into a single source so statusExpr is derived from the same comparison the JS reference exercises (today only the RUN_STATUS_SEVERITY *table* is shared, not the comparison logic). This removes the drift surface that the "can't drift" comment wrongly claims is already closed. (b) Bind with an executable assertion via the real-D1 harness (KNOWN-OUTSTANDING #1): open a run, complete it from two shards in both arrival orders, assert persisted runs.status === mergeRunStatus(a,b). (b) is the stronger guarantee because it executes the live UPDATE; (a) is the cheaper interim and does not depend on the harness. Either way, weaken the ingest.ts:737-744 comment to stop asserting drift-immunity it does not have.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: callers keep one completeRun that is sharding-safe with no race window. LOCALITY: the merge rule stops being maintained in two unbound places — a change to severity ordering is caught by a test that runs the actual SQL, not just the JS twin.

Deletion test

The atomic SQL merge earns its keep (deleting it reopens the two-shard read-modify-write race in completeRun, the sole caller). The fragility — an untested SQL transcription of a tested JS function — is the defect to close, not a module to delete.

Testability impact

The production status-merge path becomes executable-testable for the first time; currently merge-run-status.test.ts gives false confidence because it tests a reference twin, not the running SQL.

Interface sketch
// test (real D1): complete(runId, A) then complete(runId, B) in both orders // expect(persistedStatus).toBe(mergeRunStatus(A, B)) // binds JS reference to executed SQL
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited code; the finding holds.

EVIDENCE:
- Two independent encodings of the monotonic-status-merge invariant exist:
1. JS mergeRunStatus(current, incoming) (ingest.ts:730-735): if running -> incoming; cur=SEVERITY[current]??0; inc=SEVERITY[incoming]??0; return inc>cur ? incoming : current.
2. SQL statusExpr (ingest.ts:782-783): case when status='running' then payload.status when (currentStatusSeveritySql() < incomingSeverity) then payload.status else status end, with incomingSeverity = SEVERITY[payload.status] ?? 0 and currentStatusSeveritySql() (745-751) building a CASE with else 0.
- grep confirms the load-bearing claim: mergeRunStatus is exported but NEVER called in production — it appears only at its definition (line 730) and in two prose comments (739, 779). The sole executable caller is merge-run-status.test.ts. The production path (completeRun, the only caller, reached via routes/api/runs/[id]/complete.ts:27) runs statusExpr, which no test executes. So the tested function is provably not the one that runs.
- The "can't drift from mergeRunStatus" comment (738-744) is overstated. Sharing RUN_STATUS_SEVERITY prevents severity-RANK drift, but the comparison operator, the strict-vs-nonstrict tie-break, the running special-case, and the ?? 0 / else 0 fallback are hand-transcribed twice. I traced all branches (running / tie / escalation / unknown-current / unknown-incoming) and the two encodings agree today — confirming the finder's "happen to agree" framing, not a present-day bug.

DELETION TEST: passes. Deleting the SQL atomic merge and reverting to SELECT-then-UPDATE reopens a genuine TOCTOU window when two shards' /complete calls overlap on a shared idempotencyKey (the documented sharding race at 759-762). The atomic-merge-in-SQL is the deep, race-closing module and earns its keep — the defect is the untested transcription, not redundant indirection. This is correctly a 'deep-but-fragile' finding, not a consolidation: nothing is smeared across N callers (completeRun is the lone caller); the fragility is the test-coverage gap on a single deep statement.

SEVERITY: medium is right. It is latent, not active — no current divergence. But the failure mode (edit JS reference, see green tests, ship, production UPDATE unchanged) is exactly the silent-drift trap, and this is the run's terminal correctness across shards.

ADR CONFLICT: none. The atomic SQL UPDATE is fully consistent with durable decision #1 (single-region D1 writer) and #10 (db.batch atomicity). The proposed fix does not touch any durable decision.

ONE CAVEAT on framing: the solution ties this to the not-yet-built real-D1 harness (KNOWN-OUTSTANDING finding #1). That dependency is honest and correct — you cannot bind the SQL encoding with an executable assertion without executing real SQL — but it means this finding cannot be closed standalone. A cheaper, harness-independent interim option also exists: extract the comparison into one shared predicate that BOTH the JS reference and the SQL builder consume (e.g. derive statusExpr's branch ordering from the same severity-compare helper), collapsing two transcriptions to one. That is worth noting because it removes the drift surface without waiting on the harness, though it does not exercise the live UPDATE the way an integration test would.

#2 · Ingest pipeline
Param-chunk column counts are un-derived magic literals that can silently drift from the schema/insert shapes they protect
medium severity effort: small confidence: high deep but fragile revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:52-56
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:113-149
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:328-342
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:11
Problem — the friction

chunkByParams is a genuinely deep helper (it hides D1's 100-param ceiling behind one call). But its correctness depends on the caller passing the RIGHT column count: TEST_RESULTS_COLUMNS=14, TEST_TAGS_COLUMNS=4, TEST_ANNOTATIONS_COLUMNS=5, TEST_RESULT_ATTEMPTS_COLUMNS=9 (ingest.ts:53-56) and ARTIFACT_COLUMNS=12 (register.ts:11) are hand-counted against the insert object shapes. Add a column to testResults in db/schema.ts and the insert row at ingest.ts:266-281 grows to 15 fields, but TEST_RESULTS_COLUMNS stays 14 — the chunker now packs rows that exceed 99 params and D1 rejects the statement at runtime, in production, with no compile error and no test (the chunking logic is untested per finding #1). The number that makes the whole batch safe is a literal a maintainer must remember to bump in lockstep with the schema and the insert object.

Solution — the deepened module

Eliminate the standalone count constants so there is nothing to drift. Derive columnsPerRow from the row shape at the call site rather than asserting a hand-typed literal: have the row-builder produce its rows from a single object factory and feed chunkByParams the actual key count (e.g. Object.keys(sampleRow).length) — or better, type the row arrays as typeof testResults.$inferInsert (instead of the current inline structural types) and key the chunk size off the schema's column count via a helper like columnCountOf(testResults). Either way the param width is computed from the same source of truth as the insert, so adding a column (nullable or not) cannot leave the count stale. If a literal must remain for clarity, co-locate it next to the row-builder with a compile-time/startup assertion that it equals the row's key count. Independently, cover chunkByParams with a unit test that builds a max-width row from the real insert shape for each of the 5 tables and asserts no produced chunk exceeds 99 params — this is cheap (pure function, no DB) and closes the gap until the real-DB harness lands. Depth (one chunk call) is preserved; only the silent-drift footgun is removed.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: callers still get one chunkByParams call. LOCALITY: the param-budget invariant is tied to the row shape, not a remembered literal; a schema change can no longer silently produce over-limit batches.

Deletion test

chunkByParams earns its keep (delete it and the rowsPerStatement math reappears in 5 insert sites across ingest + artifacts). The defect is the un-derived, untested column constants, not the chunker.

Testability impact

Param-budget safety becomes a unit assertion against the real insert shape instead of a runtime D1 error discovered only in production after a schema change.

Interface sketch
// derive at call: chunkByParams(rows, Object.keys(rowShape).length) — or assert(TEST_RESULTS_COLUMNS === keys(row).length) // test: assert every chunk of a max-width testResults batch has <=99 params
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. chunkByParams (ingest.ts:58-68) hides D1's 100-param ceiling behind Math.floor(99/columnsPerRow); it is genuinely deep. Deletion test PASSES: it feeds 6 chunked insert sites — testResults in prefill (147) and results (329), testTags (332), testAnnotations (335), testResultAttempts (341), and artifacts in register.ts (182). Deleting it re-smears the rowsPerStatement arithmetic across all of them. The single-row runs insert (ingest.ts:587) correctly does NOT use it.

I independently re-counted every column constant against db/schema.ts and all five are CORRECT TODAY: testResults=14 (id,projectId,runId,testId,title,file,projectName,status,durationMs,retryCount,errorMessage,errorStack,workerIndex,createdAt), testTags=4, testAnnotations=5, testResultAttempts=9, artifacts=12. The finding doesn't claim they are wrong now — it claims they are fragile, which is accurate.

The fragility is real and arguably worse than stated. Each table's shape is hand-maintained in THREE+ parallel places that must stay in lockstep: (1) db/schema.ts, (2) an inline STRUCTURAL row type (ingest.ts:168-207 — note these are NOT typeof table.$inferInsert), (3) the pushed object literal (e.g. 266-281), and (4) the bare numeric count constant (53-56, register.ts:11). Only schema↔object has any compile pressure, and only for NOT-NULL columns: $inferInsert makes nullable columns optional, so adding a nullable column (the common case here — projectName/workerIndex/errorMessage/role/snapshotName were all added incrementally per docs/worklog/2026-04-19-artifact-attempts.md) produces ZERO compile error anywhere, the count stays low, the chunk overflows 99 params, and D1 rejects at runtime in prod. The count constant itself has no type relationship to anything in any scenario.

Untested: confirmed grep shows chunkByParams is referenced only in ingest.ts; no test file mentions 'chunk' and there is no ingest test at all (consistent with KNOWN-OUTSTANDING #1). No ADR conflict — solution keeps db.batch atomicity (decision 10), the ≤99-param chunking, and single D1.

One correction to framing: the finding's 'no compile error' is true for nullable-column drift but understates that a not-null addition WOULD trip Drizzle's .values() on the row object (not the constant). The core insight — the count is an un-derived, untested magic literal that can silently drift from the schema it protects — is sound and the deepening is the right move.

#3 · Ingest pipeline
Run-ownership verification is a copy-pasted projectId+id SELECT smeared across five call sites instead of one seam
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier touches a durable decision
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:660-665
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:770-775
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:68-73
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:40-54
Problem — the friction

The invariant 'this runId is owned by scope.projectId, else 404' is re-implemented as a bespoke db.select({id: runs.id}).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId,...), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) in appendRunResults (ingest.ts:660), completeRun (ingest.ts:770), and the artifacts register route (register.ts:68) — three near-identical hand-rolled ownership probes. (live.ts:40 is a related-but-distinct membership check.) A maintainer adding any new run-scoped endpoint must remember to write this probe AND remember the projectId filter (the whole point of logical tenancy). Each copy is a place the projectId filter could be dropped — exactly the bypass AuthorizedProjectId exists to prevent, but the brand only forces the column to be present, not that the ownership row was actually checked. The artifacts route's copy even shares this with a second copy-pasted concern (the chunked testResultId validation), compounding the smear.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract one guard in src/lib/ingest.ts: assertRunOwned(scope: TenantScope, runId: string): Promise<{ id: string } | null> running the single canonical select({id: runs.id}).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) and returning rows[0] ?? null. Callers map null to their own error form (appendRunResults/completeRun -> {kind:"notFound"}; register.ts -> c.json 404; loadRunResultsPage -> null) — keep that mapping at the seam, do NOT switch ingest.ts to a thrown exception, since ingest.ts deliberately uses explicit discriminated-union outcomes everywhere (AppendRunResultsOutcome/CompleteRunOutcome) and a throw would fight that style. summary.ts is the one caller that needs the full run row, not just {id}; either let it keep its own select (it already does the ownership filter inline) or give the guard an optional column-set param so summary.ts gets its row from the same checked query. The win is that the projectId-filter invariant lives in exactly one query that every run-scoped endpoint routes through.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: every run-scoped handler gets ownership-or-404 in one call, no hand-written WHERE clause. LOCALITY: the tenant-isolation query for runs lives in one function — change the table, add soft-delete, or add a teamId assertion once; the three (soon N) callers can't drift or forget the filter.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete the helper and the identical ownership SELECT reappears verbatim in 3 current callers (appendRunResults, completeRun, artifacts/register) and in every future ingest endpoint. The complexity it hides (correct projectId+id filtering = tenant isolation) reappears N-fold, which is the good direction.

Testability impact

Ownership/404 behavior becomes a single tested function rather than three untested inline copies; the artifacts route and ingest pipeline can share one ownership-test fixture.

Interface sketch
export async function assertRunOwned(scope: TenantScope, runId: string): Promise<{ id: string } | null> // returns null -> caller maps to 404; never returns a row for another project
Durable-decision note

Touches durable decision #2 (logical tenant isolation, type-enforced). Reinforces it rather than reopening it — a central assertRunOwned makes the projectId filter harder to forget than the brand alone does; worth doing precisely to strengthen the ADR.

Verifier notes

Confirmed against the files. The exact probe db.select({id: runs.id}).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1); if (!owner[0]) ... is real and copy-pasted at ingest.ts:660-665 (appendRunResults, returns {kind:"notFound"}), ingest.ts:770-775 (completeRun, returns {kind:"notFound"}), and routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:68-73 (returns c.json 404). The finder UNDERCOUNTED: a grep turned up two more identical-shape ownership filters — routes/api/t/.../runs/[runId]/results.ts:86-91 (loadRunResultsPage, select({id})...same where...limit(1); if(!owner[0]) return null) and routes/api/t/.../runs/[runId]/summary.ts:60-62 (selects the full run row but with the byte-identical where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) ownership clause). So the smear is at least 5 call sites, not 3.

The finder's exclusions are honest and correct: live.ts:40-54 is a genuinely different shape (innerJoins memberships, returns teamId, filters by user membership not projectId — a subscribe-time auth check, not the ingest ownership invariant), and they flagged it as "related-but-distinct." openRun's lookup at ingest.ts:552 is by idempotencyKey, not runId — correctly not part of the smear. The aggregateDelta/aggregateRecompute statements (ingest.ts:416/434) reuse the same where-clause but are UPDATE statements composed into the atomic batch, a different role from the standalone read-probe.

DELETION TEST: passes. The probe encodes the tenant-isolation invariant (projectId+id filter = the thing branded AuthorizedProjectId exists to enforce at the type level but cannot enforce at the row level). Deleting a shared guard makes the identical 4-line SELECT reappear verbatim across all ≥5 callers, and each copy is exactly where a maintainer could silently drop the eq(runs.projectId, ...) filter — the bypass. This concentrates currently-smeared complexity into one query; it does not merely move it.

ADR check: touches durable decision #2 (logical, type-enforced tenant isolation). It reinforces, does not reopen — the finder flagged this correctly. No conflict.

Severity stays medium: real duplication with a security-relevant invariant, but every current copy is correct, so this is hardening/locality not an active bug.

#4 · Ingest pipeline
The ingest write pipeline is a correct deep module whose orchestration glue (batch assembly, summary-from-last-row, status merge) is unreachable through its own interface — make it the first consumer of the missing real-D1 harness
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:547-640
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:654-702
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:764-808
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:824-849

Problem — the friction

openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun ARE the deep module — they hide ownership-check -> resolve ids -> compose a heterogeneous db.batch -> extract the summary from the LAST batch row -> bump activity -> broadcast. But none of that is reachable in a unit test. The void-db-stub (helpers/void-db-stub.ts:55-66) throws on any db.* access, and no test mocks void/db. So the only covered logic is the three leaf pure helpers (computeAggregateDelta, mergeRunStatus, buildChangedTests). The high-leverage glue — that the summary is read from batchResults[length-1], that the no-delta path swaps in a SELECT, that ownership returns notFound, that chunked inserts/updates/deletes are assembled in the right order, that appendRunResults wires prevStatus -> delta -> returning correctly — is guarded only by prose. A maintainer changing batch ordering, or the position of the summary statement, gets zero test signal; they must boot a real run end-to-end. The deepest, highest-blast-radius code in the subsystem has the thinnest test net.

Solution — the deepened module

Land the project's still-missing real-D1 test harness (better-sqlite3 or miniflare D1 via vi.mock("void/db", ...) per the stub's own instructions) FIRST on the ingest pipeline, since it is the deepest, highest-blast-radius module. Drive the three entry points through their existing TenantScope-in / typed-outcome-out interface with publishRunUpdate spied: (a) openRun twice with the same idempotencyKey, assert the second returns duplicate:true and still prefills this shard's queued rows via onConflictDoNothing; (b) appendRunResults with two overlapping batches, assert prevStatus transitions feed computeAggregateDelta correctly and the broadcast summary equals the persisted runs row (proving the batchResults[last] contract and the deltaStmt vs SELECT swap); (c) completeRun across shards in worst-last and worst-first order, asserting the SQL CASE never downgrades severity. No production change; reuse the now-tested pure helpers rather than re-asserting their math. Frame this in the worklog as the first concrete consumer of the tracked-but-unbuilt harness, not as net-new infrastructure.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: callers (the three handlers + the cron) already get a clean typed surface; this adds confidence that the surface's contract holds. LOCALITY: the batch-ordering / summary-extraction / idempotency invariants become regression-protected in one place instead of re-verified by hand on every change; an AI editing the batch can run a test instead of reasoning about D1 transaction semantics.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. The pipeline is not a pass-through: delete openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun and the verify -> chunk -> batch -> summarize -> broadcast complexity reappears in all 4 callers (routes/api/runs/index.ts, [id]/results.ts, [id]/complete.ts, crons/sweep-stuck-runs.ts). It is already a correct deep module; this finding is about the missing test surface, not collapsing the module.

Testability impact

Turns the entire orchestration from integration-only/manual into interface-testable: idempotent re-open, shard prefill via onConflictDoNothing, the no-delta summary-SELECT branch, ownership 404, and the atomic recompute all become unit-assertable against a real D1 without booting the Worker or the reporter.

Interface sketch
// no interface change — wire a real D1 binding into vi.mock('void/db') // test: openRun(scope, payload, t0) -> append(scope, runId, batchA) -> append(batchB) -> complete(scope, runId, {status}) // assert: testResults rows, runs aggregate columns, publishRunUpdate spy summary
Verifier notes
