#5 · Ingest pipeline
The summary-extraction contract ('last batch row is the summary') is an implicit positional convention enforced by every caller, not by the seam
medium severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:683-696
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:786-802
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:828-845
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:453-461
Problem — the friction

Three pipeline operations independently rely on the same unwritten rule: 'push the summary-producing statement (a .returning() UPDATE or aggregateSummarySelectStatement) LAST into the batch, then read batchResults[batchResults.length-1][0] back as RunAggregateSummary.' appendRunResults (ingest.ts:685, :692-695), completeRun (ingest.ts:795, :799-802), and finalizeStaleRun (ingest.ts:839, :842-845) each re-encode this positional coupling plus the as readonly unknown[] / as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] casts. The batch is a heterogeneous PromiseLike<unknown>[] (ingest.ts:213) so the type system gives zero help: insert the summary statement second-to-last by accident, or add a trailing statement later, and the broadcast silently publishes the wrong row (or undefined -> a spurious notFound at ingest.ts:696). The 'transactionally-consistent summary' guarantee — a real piece of depth — is held together by hand-counted array positions in three places.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce a tiny runBatchWithSummary(statements, summaryStatement): Promise<RunAggregateSummary | null> helper that owns the convention: it appends the summary statement last, runs db.batch, and types/extracts the final row. The three operations stop hand-indexing batchResults; the positional contract and the cast live in one place behind a named seam.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: the three operations express intent ('run these writes, give me the consistent summary') instead of array bookkeeping. LOCALITY: the 'summary is last' rule and the unavoidable D1 cast are concentrated once; adding a future trailing statement can't silently break the broadcast in three handlers.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete it and the append-last + read-last-row + cast logic reappears identically in appendRunResults, completeRun, and finalizeStaleRun (N=3). It concentrates a convention currently smeared across all three.

Testability impact

The 'summary comes back transactionally consistent' behavior becomes one testable function (feed a fake batch result, assert extraction) rather than re-verified inside each operation's integration path.

Interface sketch
async function runBatchWithSummary(writes: PromiseLike<unknown>[], summary: SummaryStmt): Promise<RunAggregateSummary | null> // invariant: summary stmt is always executed LAST; returns row[0] or null
Verifier notes

Verified all three callers in apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts. (1) appendRunResults: statements.push(summaryStmt as never) at :685 (summaryStmt = aggregateDeltaStatement's .returning() UPDATE OR aggregateSummarySelectStatement's SELECT), then reads batchResults[batchResults.length-1] as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] | undefined at :692-695. (2) completeRun: aggregateRecomputeStatement is the trailing array element at :795, read back identically at :799-802. (3) finalizeStaleRun: same recompute-last + read-last + identical cast at :839/:842-845. The batch array is typed PromiseLike<unknown>[] (:213) and every batch call uses as never, so the positional contract has zero type-system enforcement — exactly as claimed. The "transactionally-consistent summary" depth is real and documented at :447-451 and :646-652. Failure mode confirmed: an appended trailing non-returning statement makes summaryRows?.[0] undefined → in appendRunResults this returns a spurious {kind:"notFound"} (:696); in completeRun/finalizeStaleRun it silently skips the broadcast. Deletion test passes: N=3 callers each re-encode append-last + read-last-element + the as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] | undefined cast + ?.[0]; the proposed helper concentrates that one convention rather than relocating it. NOT a one-adapter hypothetical seam.

Two corrections/refinements: (a) openRun (ingest.ts:579,:623) is NOT a fourth instance — it constructs its summary by hand (const summary: RunAggregateSummary = {...} at :627) and its db.batch calls return no summary row, so the finder correctly scoped N=3. (b) The finder slightly understated a point that strengthens the case: in appendRunResults the summary statement's return shape genuinely varies (a .returning() UPDATE vs a .select()), yet both yield RunAggregateSummary[] via the shared AGGREGATE_SUMMARY_COLUMNS projection — so the helper must accept "any summary-producing statement," which is precisely the convention worth naming. No ADR conflict: the helper stays inside decision #10 (db.batch + ≤99-param chunking) and touches none of DOs/tenancy/auth/realtime. Severity medium is right: latent (no live bug today), but silent failure mode + the as never/hand-counted-index pattern is a footgun for future edits.

#6 · Ingest pipeline
Zod wire schemas and reporter TS interfaces are duplicated — but this duplication is correctly guarded and should NOT be collapsed
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts:1-148
  • packages/reporter/src/types.ts:1-69
  • packages/reporter/src/__tests__/contract.test.ts:18-233
Problem — the friction

The wire contract is expressed twice: as Zod schemas in the dashboard (schemas.ts) and as TS interfaces in the reporter (types.ts). On its face this is a duplication smell — OpenRunPayload/AppendResultsPayload/CompleteRunPayload/TestAttempt fields are restated in both packages, and a maintainer changing the contract must edit two files. I am flagging it explicitly so it is NOT mistaken for a deepening opportunity: the contract.test.ts canary imports the dashboard's Zod schemas across the package boundary and parses reporter-built payloads through them, so any drift fails the build. Collapsing the two into a single shared schema package would couple the reporter (a standalone npm artifact shipped into users' Playwright configs, bundled by vp pack) to the dashboard's Zod dependency and runtime, which is a worse trade than the guarded duplication.

Solution — the deepened module

No change recommended. Keep the two encodings; keep contract.test.ts as the binding seam. The only improvement worth considering is ensuring contract.test.ts also covers the RESPONSE shapes (the clientKey -> testResultId mapping and runUrl), since today it only validates request payloads — the response contract between appendRunResults's mapping and the reporter's appendResults parser (client.ts:128-139) is unguarded.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: reporter stays dependency-light and independently shippable. LOCALITY: drift is caught by one canary test rather than a shared-package version bump rippling into users' installs.

Deletion test

NOT a deepening. Merging the duplication would create coupling (reporter -> dashboard Zod) without concentrating complexity that's currently smeared — the two encodings serve two runtimes. Listed to forestall a wrong refactor and to surface the one real gap (untested response contract).

Testability impact

Adding response-shape cases to contract.test.ts would make the appendResults/openRun response parsing drift-detectable; currently only request parsing is.

Verifier notes

Every cited claim checks out against the code.

DUPLICATION IS REAL AND CORRECTLY GUARDED:
- schemas.ts:64-148 expresses OpenRunPayload/AppendResultsPayload/CompleteRunPayload/TestAttempt/TestResult as Zod; types.ts:7-69 restates the same fields as TS interfaces. The file headers on both sides explicitly say "keep in sync" (schemas.ts:9-10, types.ts:1-3).
- contract.test.ts:1-233 is the binding seam exactly as described: it imports the dashboard's compiled Zod schemas across the package boundary (line 7, relative "../../../../apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.js") and parses reporter-built payloads (buildPayload/buildTestDescriptor) through them. It also tests negative cases (empty batch line 212-215, bad enum line 217-232). So request-side drift fails the build.

COUPLING ARGUMENT IS STRONGER THAN STATED — I verified it: zod is a *devDependency* in packages/reporter/package.json (line 57), NOT a runtime/peer dependency. The shipped artifact declares only @playwright/test as peerDependency (line 59-61) and ships ./dist. So Zod is present solely to run contract.test.ts. Collapsing into a shared Zod schema package would pull Zod into the reporter's runtime bundle (vp pack) and into users' Playwright configs — concrete confirmation of the "worse trade" claim, not a hypothetical.

DELETION TEST: This is honestly framed as NOT a deepening. Deleting one encoding does not concentrate complexity smeared across N callers — there is exactly one consumer per encoding (the reporter runtime uses the TS interfaces; the dashboard ingest handlers use the Zod schemas), serving two distinct runtimes. Merging would MOVE complexity and create a new reporter→dashboard-Zod coupling. deletionTestPasses=false is correct, and the finder agrees.

THE REAL GAP IS CONFIRMED — response contract is unguarded:
- routes/api/runs/index.ts:7,32-35 builds runUrl() inline and returns c.json({ runId, runUrl }) with no Zod schema.
- routes/api/runs/[id]/results.ts:25 returns c.json({ results: result.mapping }) — the clientKey→testResultId mapping (ingest.ts:70-73 ResultMapping, populated at ingest.ts:216-219) — also unschematized.
- client.ts:101-105 and 128-131 parse both responses with inline as casts ({ runId?, runUrl? } and { results?: Array<{ clientKey; testResultId }> }).
- contract.test.ts contains zero references to runUrl/mapping/response — request payloads only. Grep confirmed no *ResponseSchema in schemas.ts.
So the response side (mapping + runUrl) has no canary; a field rename on either side would silently break the artifact-registration step that depends on the clientKey→testResultId map.

ADR check: no durable decision is reversed. The finding explicitly preserves the two-runtime separation (reporter as standalone npm artifact) which aligns with the migration's packaging stance. No adrConflict.

Severity: low is right for the duplication-as-non-finding. The genuine sub-finding (untested response contract) is also low-to-medium but is correctly scoped as the one actionable improvement, not a deepening. Keeping as-is because the value of this finding is precisely to forestall a wrong "DRY the schemas" refactor while surfacing the response-contract gap.

Tenant isolation & authorization · 6 findings

#7 · Tenant isolation & authorization
Branded TenantScope gates id construction but not query consumption — every run-scoped query re-derives the scope predicate by hand, inconsistently; concentrate it behind a scoped-data-access seam
high severity effort: medium confidence: high shallow module revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:12-22
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:66-75
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/branches-query.ts:18-26
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/index.server.ts:42-68
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-90
Problem — the friction

The CLAUDE.md narrative claims the branded AuthorizedProjectId makes it 'impossible to forget' the projectId filter and enforces scope 'through the type system'. In reality the brand only constrains the *construction* side: you cannot assign a raw string into a TenantScope without going through tenantScope*/requireTenantContext. But the *consumption* side — the actual query — has no type-level link to the brand. Drizzle's eq(runs.projectId, x) accepts any string, so a maintainer/AI writing a new loader composes the predicate and(eq(runs.teamId, scope.teamId), eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), ...) entirely by hand and by copy-paste. Nothing fails to compile if they query runs and forget the predicate, or filter only by runId. The interface (one type) is almost as complex as what it buys (one assertion at the edge); the leverage a deep seam should provide — every run-scoped query is automatically scoped — does not exist. The brand even gets silently widened back to string (scopedRunsWhere(teamId: string, projectId: string), getTeamRole(userId, teamId: string)), so the type information is discarded the moment it crosses into the helpers that build the WHERE clauses.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce a deep "scoped data access" seam in src/lib that owns the ONLY blessed way to touch a run-scoped table, and make it cover the real call shapes observed:

1. scopedSelect(scope, table) / scopedSelectDistinct(scope, table, cols) — returns a Drizzle builder pre-filtered to and(eq(table.teamId?, scope.teamId), eq(table.projectId, scope.projectId)), chainable with .where(extraFilters). (teamId only where the table carries it — runs has it; testResults/artifacts/etc. carry projectId.)
2. scopedRunById(scope, runId) — the 6+ run-detail/ingest/route lookups that hand-roll and(eq(runs.projectId, ...), eq(runs.id, runId)) collapse to one call. This is the single most-duplicated shape.
3. A join helper for the innerJoin-on-runs cases (flaky.server:89, test-detail:137, live.ts:50) so they don't stay on the raw path.

Make the brand load-bearing, not decorative: the builder params REQUIRE a TenantScope (not string), and fix the two helpers that currently launder the brand back to string — scopedRunsWhere must take scope: TenantScope (or AuthorizedTeamId/AuthorizedProjectId) and getTeamRole should take AuthorizedTeamId. Then add a lint/review rule that flags db.select().from(<run-scoped table>) outside this module, so the raw path is the thing reviewers catch. The predicate (and its teamId-vs-projectId consistency) lives in exactly one place behind the seam.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: every caller gets correct (projectId, teamId) scoping for free and can no longer express an unscoped run-table query through the blessed path; new loaders shrink to the part that actually differs (the extra filters). Locality: the exact set of columns that constitute 'scope' and the teamId-vs-projectId policy live in ONE module instead of being smeared across ~12 call sites; changing the isolation predicate (e.g. adding an orgId tier later) is a one-file edit.

Deletion test

Deleting this module makes complexity REAPPEAR across every run-scoped reader/writer: the index.server runs-list (3 distinct-option queries + count + page), run-detail history + tests, test-detail (5 child queries), flaky.server, insights/index, insights/suite-size, results.ts, summary.ts, test-preview.ts, tests/summary.ts, and the ingest pipeline's run lookups — each re-derives and(eq(...teamId), eq(...projectId)) by hand. It earns its keep by concentrating the scope predicate those ~12+ callers currently duplicate.

Testability impact

Today, asserting 'no run-scoped query can leak across tenants' requires an integration test per loader against a real D1 with two seeded tenants (the harness that CLAUDE.md notes is not built). With the seam, the predicate-injection becomes unit-testable in isolation: assert that scopedSelect(scope, runs).toSQL() always contains the projectId bind, independent of any DB. The N call sites stop needing individual leak tests because they can no longer omit the filter.

Interface sketch
scopedSelect(scope: TenantScope, table: RunScopedTable): PreScopedQuery // always ANDs eq(table.projectId, scope.projectId) [+ teamId on runs]; raw db.select().from(runScopedTable) becomes the lint-flagged escape hatch
Verifier notes

Every checkable claim verified against the code.

(1) Brand gates construction only: scope.ts:12-22 defines AuthorizedTeamId/AuthorizedProjectId as branded strings, and TenantScope is only constructible via tenantScopeForUserBySlugs / tenantScopeForApiKey / requireTenantContext. But Drizzle's eq(runs.projectId, x) accepts any string, so the consumption side has no type-level link to the brand. Nothing fails to compile if a loader queries runs and forgets the projectId predicate.

(2) Brand silently widened back to string — verified verbatim: runs-filters-where.ts:66-68 scopedRunsWhere(teamId: string, projectId: string, filters) and authz.ts:14-17 getTeamRole(userId: string, teamId: string). The branded type is discarded at the helper edge.

(3) Manual/copy-paste/inconsistent scope predicates: 16 files, ~43 eq(.projectId, ...) occurrences. The predicate is genuinely smeared, AND inconsistent — a locality smell: run-detail/index.server.ts hand-rolls THREE different scope predicates (run lookup at :29 uses only projectId; history at :44-47 uses teamId+projectId; tests at :83-85 use projectId+runId). test-artifact-actions.ts:116 and the entire ingest pipeline filter by projectId ONLY (no teamId). branches-query.ts and runs-list use teamId+projectId. So callers disagree on what "scoped" means — exactly the divergence a single seam removes.

(4) No existing scoped query builder/repository — grep for scopedSelect/scopedQuery/withScope/scopedFrom returns nothing, so the proposed module is not redundant.

(5) Bonus real instance: src/live.ts:40-51 looks up a run by eq(runs.id, runId) with scope enforced ONLY via a membership innerJoin and NO projectId predicate — concrete proof the brand gives zero protection at the query site.

DELETION TEST (passes): deleting a scopedSelect(scope, table) seam makes the and(eq(...projectId), eq(...teamId)) predicate reappear across ingest.ts (~13 sites: lines 96,240,250,260,291,425,443,460,557,663,773,794,834), runs-list (3), run-detail (3), test-detail (index.server.ts:70,137 + 3), insights/index, insights/suite-size (4), flaky.server, results.ts, summary.ts, test-preview.ts, tests/summary.ts, and live.ts. It concentrates currently-duplicated complexity rather than moving it. The finder's caller list is accurate.

ADR check: durable decision 2 says tenant isolation is logical and *type-enforced* via the brand. This finding STRENGTHENS that decision (makes the brand load-bearing instead of decorative); it does not reverse it. No adrConflict.

Why revise rather than keep: (a) the solution must explicitly require that the brand-widening helpers (scopedRunsWhere, getTeamRole) take TenantScope / AuthorizedTeamId so the brand stops leaking to string; (b) the seam must cover more than plain select().from(table) — several real callers need runId+scope lookups (ingest, run-detail :29, summary/results routes), inner joins on runs (flaky.server:89, test-detail:137, live.ts), and selectDistinct (branches/runs-list options). A naive scopedSelect(scope, runs) that only handles the simple case would strand those callers on the raw path and leave the seam half-deep. The revised solution names these so the seam is genuinely the single blessed path.

#8 · Tenant isolation & authorization
Test-detail loader reads four child tables by testResultId with no projectId predicate — the lone reader that omits the scope every other reader already carries (latent cross-tenant gap)
medium severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:89-125
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:275
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:293
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:309
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:335
Problem — the friction

CLAUDE.md is explicit: 'Every query against runs / testResults / testResultAttempts / testTags / testAnnotations / artifacts MUST filter by projectId'. The schema dutifully denormalizes projectId onto all four child tables (schema.ts:275/293/309/335). But the test-detail loader queries all four by eq(testTags.testResultId, testResultId) / eq(artifacts.testResultId, testResultId) alone — no projectId, no teamId. The only thing standing between an attacker and another tenant's tags/annotations/attempts/artifacts is the prior testResults lookup at lines 55-66, which IS scoped; if that returns a row, the code assumes the testResultId is safe and fans out unscoped reads. This is precisely the 'run-scoped query that bypasses the brand' the design is supposed to prevent — and the brand provides zero protection because the scope object is never referenced in these five statements. It is currently not exploitable (testResultId is server-derived from a scoped row), but it is a latent leak: any future caller that passes a client-supplied testResultId straight into these helpers inherits a cross-tenant read, and a reviewer scanning for the projectId predicate would (correctly) flag this file as violating the rule.

Solution — the deepened module

Add the missing eq(<table>.projectId, project.id) predicate (AND-ed with the existing testResultId equality) to the four child-table reads in index.server.ts:89-125, bringing this loader in line with the convention already followed by suite-size.server.ts, artifacts/[id]/upload.ts, and test-artifact-actions.ts. This makes the reads defense-in-depth correct independent of how testResultId was obtained and removes the implicit "prior scoped lookup sanitizes the id" coupling. If a scopedSelect(scope, table) seam is introduced by a separate deepening, route these through it then — but that is an enhancement, not a prerequisite; this fix stands alone as a one-file invariant-compliance change.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: child reads become self-defending — they no longer depend on an out-of-band, several-lines-earlier ownership check to be safe. Locality: the tenancy guarantee for tags/annotations/attempts/artifacts lives in the query itself, not in the reader's mental model of statement ordering.

Deletion test

This is fixing an existing leaky seam, not adding a pass-through. If you 'delete' the implicit guard (the assumption that the prior scoped testResults lookup sanitizes testResultId), the missing complexity — the projectId filter — must reappear on all four child queries. It belongs ON each query, which is exactly what the scoped seam concentrates.

Testability impact

Becomes unit-testable via the seam: a test seeding the same testResultId-shaped ids under two projects can assert the child queries return rows only for the in-scope project. Today this can only be caught by an end-to-end test of the whole loader, which doesn't exist.

Interface sketch
scopedSelect(scope, testTags).where(eq(testTags.testResultId, id)) // projectId predicate injected; same for testAnnotations / testResultAttempts / artifacts
Verifier notes

VERIFIED REAL. index.server.ts:89-125 queries all four child tables exactly as described: .from(testTags).where(eq(testTags.testResultId, testResultId)), .from(testAnnotations).where(eq(testAnnotations.testResultId, testResultId)), .from(artifacts).where(eq(artifacts.testResultId, testResultId)), .from(testResultAttempts).where(eq(testResultAttempts.testResultId, testResultId)) — none carry a projectId/teamId predicate. The schema does denormalize projectId onto all four (schema.ts:275/293/309/335, .notNull() with FK to projects). The testResults lookup above (lines 55-66) IS scoped (projectId + id + runId), and testResultId is server-derived from c.req.param, so this is NOT currently exploitable — the finding correctly states this. It is a latent gap + an inconsistency with the stated invariant.

DELETION TEST FAILS as a *deepening*. I checked every other reader of these tables and they ALL already carry the scope: suite-size.server.ts:130-145 reads testTags via innerJoin(testResults)+eq(testResults.projectId, scope.projectId); routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts:23-36 reads artifacts with eq(artifacts.projectId, scope.projectId); src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts:103-123 reads artifacts with eq(artifacts.projectId, scope.projectId). So index.server.ts is the SINGLE outlier, not the representative of complexity smeared across N callers. Adding a projectId predicate to four queries in one file concentrates nothing — it brings one file into line with an already-universal convention. That is a correctness/consistency fix, not a deepening that concentrates smeared complexity.

The proposed solution references scopedSelect(scope, ...) "from finding 1" — I grepped: no scopedSelect/scopedQuery/scopedFrom helper exists in the codebase. So this finding is parasitic on a separate (unproven here) deepening proposal. On its own merits it should be reframed as: add the missing projectId predicate to the four child reads in this loader, matching the convention the other three readers already follow.

adrConflict: none — fully consistent with durable decision 2 (logical tenant isolation, every run-scoped query filters by projectId). It actually reinforces it.

Severity downgraded high->medium: not exploitable today (server-derived id), and the surrounding reads are already correct; this is a defense-in-depth / invariant-compliance gap on one loader, not an active cross-tenant leak.

#9 · Tenant isolation & authorization
A canonical "fetch run R within scope S or 404" seam is missing; ~3 handlers re-derive the scoped run-ownership SELECT, and single-run lookups drift from the documented (teamId, projectId) scope
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-32
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:55-72
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/results.ts:85-98
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/summary.ts:60-65
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/test-preview.ts:62-69
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:425
Problem — the friction

Six+ handlers independently implement the same two-step dance: (1) SELECT a run filtered by and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId)), 404/null if absent; (2) then read the run's children filtered by eq(testResults.projectId, ...), eq(testResults.runId, runId). The step-1 predicate is copy-pasted verbatim; worse, it is inconsistent — run-list history (index.server.ts:44-47) and suite-size include eq(runs.teamId, ...) in the run predicate, while the single-run lookups (run-detail:29, test-detail:70, summary:61, results:89) filter only by projectId and drop teamId. The schema header at schema.ts:181 says the canonical scope is (teamId, projectId), so the projectId-only variants are technically narrower than the documented contract. A maintainer adding a new run-scoped endpoint has to know this pattern by osmosis, pick the right id set, and remember to 404 before touching children. There is no module that says 'give me run R within scope S, or 404'.

Solution — the deepened module

Add requireRunInScope(scope, runId): Promise<Run | null> (or throwing variant -> 404) to src/lib/ingest.ts (or a thin src/lib/runs.ts), owning ONE canonical run-ownership predicate. The primary value is making the documented "(teamId, projectId)" scope from schema.ts:179-186 the single source of truth — decide once whether the run predicate includes teamId (recommend YES, to match the schema's defense-in-depth contract) and stop the projectId-only vs teamId+projectId drift between single-run lookups and history/analytics. Collapse run-detail (index.server.ts:26-32), loadRunResultsPage (results.ts:85-91), and the test-detail run lookup (tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:67-72) to const run = await requireRunInScope(scope, runId). appendRunResults/completeRun (ingest.ts:660-665, 770-775) can adopt it too for consistency. Note explicitly that summary.ts is a single run read (not a verify-then-children case) and test-preview.ts deliberately skips run-verify by trusting the child's denormalized projectId — leave test-preview as-is or document why it's safe; do not force the helper onto it.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get the ownership-check + 404 + correct id set for free, in one call. Locality: the answer to 'what predicate proves a run belongs to a scope, and do we include teamId?' lives in one function instead of six divergent copies; the current inconsistency is resolved by construction.

Deletion test

Deleting requireRunInScope makes the verify-then-404 logic reappear in all 6+ named handlers (run-detail, test-detail, results, summary, test-preview, ingest.openRun-adjacent lookups). It concentrates real, currently-smeared complexity — passes the deletion test as a deepening.

Testability impact

The ownership/404 semantics become testable once (does a foreign-project runId return null? does a missing runId? is teamId enforced?) instead of re-tested or untested per handler. Removes the need for six near-identical integration cases.

Interface sketch
requireRunInScope(scope: TenantScope, runId: string): Promise<Run> // 404 if run not in (projectId[,teamId]); single canonical ownership predicate
Verifier notes

Read all 6 cited sites plus all eq(runs.id matches and scope.ts/schema.ts.

THE PATTERN IS REAL but at FEWER sites than claimed, and 2 of the 6 cited files do NOT exhibit it:

Genuine "SELECT run scoped by (projectId,id) -> 404/null -> then touch children by runId" instances:
- index.server.ts:26-32 (run-detail): SELECT run, 404, then testResults by (projectId,runId). YES.
- tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:67-72 (test-detail): SELECT run by (projectId,id) — but here the run lookup is primarily metadata + 404; the testResults row itself (55-65) carries the (projectId,id,runId) filter. Partial.
- results.ts:85-91 (loadRunResultsPage): explicit "Confirm the run belongs to this project" SELECT, null->404, then paginated children. YES.
- ingest.ts:660-665 (appendRunResults) and 770-775 (completeRun): owner SELECT -> notFound -> child writes. YES — but these two already live inside the deep src/lib/ingest.ts module, so they aren't "smeared across handlers."

COUNTEREXAMPLES the finder got WRONG:
- summary.ts:60-65 is NOT a verify-then-children pattern. It is a single scoped read of the run row, which IS the response payload. No children read; nothing to "verify before touching."
- test-preview.ts:62-69 does NOT verify run ownership at all. It queries testResults directly by (projectId,runId,status) with no run SELECT and no 404-before-children. It is the *counter-pattern* — it relies on the denormalized projectId on the child to skip the run-verify step. Citing it as a member of the dance is incorrect; it contradicts the finder's own claim that "all six independently implement the dance."

So the real smeared-across-handlers count is ~3 page/route handlers (run-detail, results, test-detail), not 6+. The ingest two are already encapsulated.

teamId-inconsistency sub-claim: PARTLY TRUE, mischaracterized. The schema header (schema.ts:179-186) does say the canonical scope is "(teamId, projectId)" and explicitly frames teamId as defense-in-depth so "a leaked project id can't cross teams even if the brand check is bypassed." History (index.server.ts:44-47) and analytics filter by teamId+projectId; single-run lookups filter by projectId only. So the single-run variants ARE narrower than the documented intent. BUT: projectId is a real FK to projects.id, a project belongs to exactly one team, and AuthorizedProjectId is already auth-checked, so a projectId-only filter cannot actually cross teams. The teamId filter is strictly belt-and-suspenders — this is a documented-contract drift / defense-in-depth gap, NOT a tenant-isolation bug. (ADR durable decision 2 — logical isolation via denormalized projectId — is satisfied either way.)

DELETION TEST: passes in the narrow sense — deleting requireRunInScope makes the SELECT-run+null-check reappear in run-detail, results, and test-detail. BUT the per-site "complexity" is a shallow 5-line scoped existence check; the helper's interface (scope, runId -> Run|404) is barely smaller than its implementation. The genuine depth comes ONLY from canonicalizing the teamId-vs-projectId scope decision and the 404 contract in one place — i.e. it earns its keep as a CONSISTENCY/contract seam, not as a complexity sink. This is a modest DRY+contract win, not a high-leverage deep module.

No existing helper found (grepped requireRun/runInScope/getRun/loadRun/verifyRun/runOwner — none). No ADR conflict.

Net: keep the insight, fix the framing (overstated call count, 2 wrong citations, overstated complexity-concentration), drop severity to low.

#10 · Tenant isolation & authorization
Run-ownership authorization is re-derived per call site, and the live.ts websocket path uses a membership join a scope-predicate refactor would silently miss
low severity effort: large confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:40-54
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:425
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/results.ts:86-91
  • apps/dashboard/middleware/01.context.ts:112-127
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:61-84
Problem — the friction

The question 'is principal P allowed to touch run R' is answered four structurally different ways: (a) live.ts joins runs⋈memberships on runs.teamId to authorize a websocket subscription; (b) the ingest pipeline authorizes via api-key→tenantScopeForApiKey then filters runs by projectId; (c) the session /api/t routes authorize via tenantScopeForUserBySlugs then filter runs by projectId; (d) page loaders authorize via middleware-populated activeProject then filter runs by projectId. live.ts even queries eq(runs.id, runId) with NO projectId — safe only because the membership join carries the tenancy, a subtlety a maintainer must verify by reading the join. There is no single notion of 'the authorization decision for a run'; the membership-vs-key-vs-activeProject branches are each correct today but drift independently, and the live.ts variant is the only one that scopes via join rather than via a stored predicate — meaning a refactor of the scope predicate would miss it.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a single run-ownership guard, requireRunInScope(scope, runId) in src/lib/scope.ts (or a sibling run-authz module), wrapping the canonical db.select({id: runs.id}).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) ownership check. Funnel the read-path ownership CHECKS through it: results.ts:86-91, summary.ts:61, the run-detail and test-detail loaders, and the two ingest verify SELECTs (appendRunResults :660-664, completeRun :770-774). Leave the inline scope predicates on the aggregate UPDATE/SELECT statements (ingest.ts 425/443/460/794) as-is — they must stay inline on the mutation for atomic scoping; do not pretend the guard replaces them. Treat live.ts separately and honestly: it authorizes a user (not a resolved scope) against a run because no TenantScope exists at subscribe time, so it cannot share the predicate query. Either (a) leave it as an explicitly-documented sibling that the run-authz module owns alongside the predicate guard, or (b) co-locate its membership-join query in the same module as authorizeRunForUser(userId, runId) so a future change to "what makes a run reachable" updates both the predicate guard and the join variant in one file. The concrete win is locality: one module owns every notion of "is this principal allowed to touch this run," so a scope-predicate refactor can't silently skip the live.ts join.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: each subsystem asks the auth module 'can this principal see this run?' rather than re-implementing the join/predicate. Locality: the four currently-divergent run-authorization mechanisms converge so a change to tenancy rules (or a bug) is fixed once; the live.ts 'scope-via-join' subtlety is captured in the module's contract instead of an inline comment.

Deletion test

Deleting the module makes the run-authorization logic reappear in all four subsystems (live onSubscribe, ingest verify-ownership, /api/t routes, page loaders). It concentrates a genuinely-smeared, security-critical decision — earns its keep.

Testability impact

Run authorization becomes testable as a single contract across both principal types, including the negative cases (non-member, foreign project, revoked key) that currently can only be exercised through three different integration entry points (websocket handshake, ingest POST, session GET).

Interface sketch
authorizeRunForUser(userId, runId): Promise<TenantScope | null> // membership-join variant; requireRunInScope(scope, runId) for predicate paths — one canonical run-ownership notion behind both
Verifier notes

All four cited paths verified.

(a) live.ts:40-54 onSubscribe — confirmed. For topic run:<runId> it does db.select({teamId: runs.teamId}).from(runs).innerJoin(memberships, and(eq(memberships.teamId, runs.teamId), eq(memberships.userId, user.id))).where(eq(runs.id, runId)).limit(1). Line 50 is eq(runs.id, runId) with NO projectId filter — tenancy is carried entirely by the membership join. This is genuinely the lone structural outlier, and the finder's most valuable claim is correct: a refactor of the (projectId, runId) scope predicate would silently miss this site because it doesn't use that predicate at all.

(b) ingest pipeline — confirmed but the finder cited the wrong line. Line 425 is the aggregate-delta UPDATE's WHERE, not the verify-ownership SELECT. The actual ownership SELECTs are appendRunResults (ingest.ts:660-664) and completeRun (ingest.ts:770-774): db.select({id: runs.id}).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))). openRun uses a different idempotency-key SELECT. Scope comes from tenantScopeForApiKey.

(c) results.ts:86-91 — confirmed. loadRunResultsPage runs the same (projectId, runId) ownership SELECT; scope from tenantScopeForUserBySlugs (route line 177).

(d) page loaders — confirmed. runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-30 and tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:70 use the same predicate; scope from requireTenantContext(c) (middleware-populated activeProject).

The decisive grep: the (runs.projectId, runs.id) predicate appears at 10 sites — ingest.ts 425/443/460/663/773/794, run-detail loader :29, test-detail loader :70, summary.ts:61, results.ts:89 — plus the lone live.ts join variant. No existing run-ownership helper exists (grep for authorizeRun/requireRunInScope/etc. returns nothing).

DELETION TEST: A run-ownership guard concentrates the ~5-6 ownership-CHECK sites (results.ts, summary.ts, both loaders, the two ingest verify SELECTs) — the predicate genuinely reappears in each, so it earns its keep. BUT it does NOT subsume the inline-WHERE-on-mutation sites (ingest.ts 425/443/460/794): those WHERE clauses are part of the atomic aggregate UPDATE/SELECT statements and must keep the scope predicate inline for the write itself to be scoped — they aren't separable guards. So the concentration is real but narrower than "all four funnel through."

FRAMING CORRECTIONS: (1) "four structurally different ways / three mechanisms" overstates it. Paths (b)(c)(d) already share ONE predicate shape; they differ only in how scope is resolved, and the scope-resolution layer is ALREADY deep — TenantScope + branded AuthorizedProjectId + tenantScopeForApiKey/tenantScopeForUserBySlugs/requireTenantContext (scope.ts, tenant-context.ts). That consolidation is findings 1+3 and is largely done. The genuinely un-consolidated thing is (1) the run-ownership GUARD across read paths, and (2) live.ts as a non-predicate join variant. (2) The proposed solution itself names TWO functions (authorizeRunForUser(userId,runId) for realtime/session, requireRunInScope(scope,runId) for predicate paths), so "single notion of the authorization decision" is aspirational. There's a real reason for two: at websocket-subscribe time there is no URL slug, so no TenantScope can be resolved — live.ts authorizes a user against a run (join), whereas the predicate paths authorize an already-resolved scope against a run. These are two legitimately different questions, not pure incidental drift.

SEVERITY: lowering to low. All paths are correct today; the scope-resolution half is already deep; the residual is a maintainability/locality risk (a scope-predicate refactor missing the live.ts join), not a present bug. ADR check: no conflict — this reinforces logical tenant isolation (decision 2), does not reopen per-team DOs or any settled decision.

#11 · Tenant isolation & authorization
scopedRunsWhere discards the AuthorizedProjectId/AuthorizedTeamId brand by taking plain string ids — tighten it to take TenantScope like loadProjectBranches
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:66-75
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:14-24
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/branches-query.ts:13-26
Problem — the friction

The subsystem is inconsistent about whether the brand is honored. branches-query.loadProjectBranches takes a full TenantScope (good — the brand is preserved). But scopedRunsWhere(teamId: string, projectId: string, filters) takes plain strings, immediately discarding AuthorizedTeamId/AuthorizedProjectId — so a caller could pass any string and the type system would not object; the only reason it's safe is that index.server.ts:35 happens to pass scope.teamId/scope.projectId. getTeamRole(userId, teamId: string) likewise takes a raw string. This inconsistency means the brand's guarantee is only as strong as its weakest helper, and a maintainer can't rely on 'if it compiles, the id is auth-checked' — some helpers enforce it, others don't.

Solution — the deepened module

Change scopedRunsWhere to consume the branded scope rather than raw strings: scopedRunsWhere(scope: TenantScope, filters: RunsFilters), building and(eq(runs.teamId, scope.teamId), eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), ...) internally. Update both call sites in index.server.ts (lines 35, 94) to pass scope directly. While there, fold the three raw inlined scope predicates in that same file (lines 42-68) into the helper or a shared scopePredicate(scope) so the file doesn't half-delegate, half-inline the same filter. This makes the brand survive to the query in the only place run-scoping is built today, matching loadProjectBranches. Leave getTeamRole out of scope — it has no callers; either delete it or, if kept as a future primitive, note it operates during scope construction and legitimately predates a TenantScope. Do not present this as a new module/seam; it is interface tightening so the brand invariant is uniform.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers can pass the scope object directly (less unpacking), and cannot accidentally pass an unverified id. Locality: 'which functions are allowed to take a raw id' collapses to the small, documented scope-construction set; everything downstream uniformly demands a brand.

Deletion test

This is a tightening of existing shallow interfaces rather than a new module; the relevant deletion test is finding 1's. Standalone it's an inconsistency fix — its value is making the brand's invariant uniform so finding 1's seam can actually rely on it.

Testability impact

Minor on its own, but it's a precondition for finding 1: once helpers take TenantScope, a type-level test (the helpers won't accept a bare string) substitutes for runtime leak tests at those call sites.

Interface sketch
scopedRunsWhere(scope: TenantScope, filters: RunsFilters): SqlFragment // brand preserved end-to-end; raw-string entry only in documented scope-construction helpers
Verifier notes

The friction is real and the code is read correctly. scopedRunsWhere (runs-filters-where.ts:66-75) takes plain teamId: string, projectId: string and immediately builds eq(runs.teamId, teamId) etc., so the AuthorizedTeamId/AuthorizedProjectId brand is silently widened to string at the seam. loadProjectBranches (branches-query.ts:13) by contrast takes the full branded TenantScope and reads scope.teamId/scope.projectId. So the brand's "if it compiles, the id is auth-checked" guarantee is genuinely non-uniform across the two run-scoping helpers. Confirmed.

Caller reality check (this is where the finding overstates): scopedRunsWhere has exactly ONE caller file — index.server.ts, at lines 35 and 94 — and that caller does hold a real TenantScope from requireTenantContext(c), so it passes scope.teamId/scope.projectId. Safety is incidental (type system doesn't enforce it) but there is no second caller smearing the risk. Notably, the SAME file inlines the identical scope predicate three more times raw (lines 42-48, 52-58, 62-68: and(eq(runs.teamId, scope.teamId), eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), isNotNull(...))) — so scopedRunsWhere is barely earning its keep even before tightening.

getTeamRole correction: the finder cites getTeamRole(userId, teamId: string) (authz.ts:14-24) as a second instance of the inconsistency, but grep shows it has ZERO production callers — only two worklog-doc references. It is effectively dead code, not a live inconsistency. The finder's own "legitimate exception, document it" carve-out is moot for a function nothing calls.

Deletion test: this is not a deepening. Changing scopedRunsWhere(teamId, projectId, filters) -> scopedRunsWhere(scope, filters) tightens one existing signature at one seam; it does not concentrate complexity currently duplicated across N callers (there is one caller). The finder is honest that the deletion test rides on "finding 1"; standalone, deletionTestPasses=false. It's a valid inconsistent-interface / type-hygiene tightening, just not a concentrate-the-smear deepening.

No ADR conflict — this strengthens decision #2 (type-enforced logical tenancy via branded AuthorizedProjectId). adjustedSeverity stays low: single caller, already safe in practice, pure compile-time hardening.

Verdict revise: keep the real core (brand discarded at the scopedRunsWhere seam vs preserved at loadProjectBranches), drop the getTeamRole framing (dead code, not live inconsistency), and frame it honestly as an interface-tightening that lets a future scoping seam rely on the brand, not as a standalone deepening.

#12 · Tenant isolation & authorization
Three-way duplicated `→ TenantScope` brand-cast projection; one true pass-through (tenantScopeForUserBySlugs) to inline
low severity effort: medium confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:31-57
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:193-267
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:269-301
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:39-53
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:61-84
Problem — the friction

Resolving 'is this user authorized for this team/project, and what is the scope' is spread across five functions with overlapping SQL: resolveTeamBySlug (teams⋈memberships), resolveTenantBundleForUser (memberships⋈teams⟕projects, the full bundle), resolveProjectBySlugs (projects⋈teams⋈memberships), tenantScopeForUserBySlugs (a thin wrapper that imports resolveProjectBySlugs then re-shapes into TenantScope), and tenantScopeForApiKey (projects⋈teams, no membership — the key IS the auth). Three of them re-express the same membership join with slightly different SELECT lists and slightly different null semantics (bundle never 404s; the others do). tenantScopeForUserBySlugs is a near pass-through over resolveProjectBySlugs with field-renaming. A maintainer has to know which of the five to call for a given route shape (page loader vs /api/t session route vs ingest), and the membership-join correctness is replicated rather than centralized. getTeamRole and requireTeamOwner add two more membership lookups in the same file.

Solution — the deepened module

Two narrow, independent moves — not a unifying resolveMembership core:

(a) Inline tenantScopeForUserBySlugs into a single shared TenantScope factory. Today the {teamId, projectId, teamSlug, projectSlug} → TenantScope projection (with the two as Authorized*Id brand casts) is duplicated across scope.ts:47-52, scope.ts:78-83, and tenant-context.ts:28-35. Export one makeTenantScope({teamId, projectId, teamSlug, projectSlug}) from scope.ts and have all three call it. This concentrates the brand casts (the security-critical part) in one place and is a clean deletion-test win. tenantScopeForUserBySlugs then becomes resolveProjectBySlugs(...) → makeTenantScope(...).

(b) Leave resolveTeamBySlug / resolveProjectBySlugs / resolveTenantBundleForUser as separate queries. They are intentionally different shapes (slug-targeted single-row inner joins vs the all-teams left-join picker query) and the only common substance is a two-predicate and(...) — not worth a wrapper. Do NOT make resolveProjectBySlugs return a TenantScope; its consumers need role, which TenantScope lacks.

Net: one TenantScope factory (kills the triple-duplicated brand-cast projection) + inline the one true pass-through. The five-way membership-join consolidation is not justified.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers pick by *auth axis* (session-slug vs api-key) rather than by accidental SELECT-list differences; the TenantScope shape is produced in exactly two places. Locality: the membership join — the security-critical SQL — is written once; a bug fix or an added isolation tier touches one query, not three.

Deletion test

Collapsing tenantScopeForUserBySlugs passes cleanly (it is a pass-through over resolveProjectBySlugs — deleting it makes near-zero complexity vanish, so it should be inlined). Factoring resolveMembership passes the deepening test: the join reappears in resolveTeamBySlug, resolveProjectBySlugs, and resolveTenantBundleForUser if removed — it earns its keep by concentrating the membership predicate those three duplicate.

Testability impact

One membership-resolution core means one place to test the 'non-member → null' and 'wrong-team → null' contracts, instead of re-verifying them in three resolvers with subtly different null behavior (bundle returns nulls-in-object, the others return null). Reduces the integration-test surface the unbuilt real-DB harness would otherwise have to cover.

Interface sketch
resolveMembership(userId, teamSlug, projectSlug?) -> scoped row | null (single join core); resolveProjectBySlugs / resolveTeamBySlug = projections; tenantScopeForUserBySlugs collapsed into resolveProjectBySlugs
Verifier notes

Read both cited files in full plus all callers. The friction partially exists but the headline overstates it, and the proposed solution is partly wrong.

CONFIRMED:
- The functions exist as described. getTeamRole (authz.ts:14-24), resolveTeamBySlug (31-57), resolveTenantBundleForUser (193-267), resolveProjectBySlugs (269-301), requireTeamOwner (147-156); tenantScopeForUserBySlugs (scope.ts:39-53), tenantScopeForApiKey (scope.ts:61-84). The finder MISSED a sixth scope-producer: toScope() in tenant-context.ts:28-35.
- tenantScopeForUserBySlugs IS a near pass-through over resolveProjectBySlugs: dynamic import + a 4-field reshape (scope.ts:44-52). Deleting/inlining it makes near-zero complexity vanish. This sub-claim is correct.

REFUTED / OVERSTATED:
1. The solution "have resolveProjectBySlugs return a TenantScope directly / collapse the two" is WRONG. resolveProjectBySlugs's only two real consumers — keys.ts:46 and settings-scope.ts:76 — both do project.role !== "owner". TenantScope (scope.ts:17-22) carries NO role field; its consumers (results.ts, summary.ts, test-preview.ts, tests/.../summary.ts) only read scope.projectId. The two return shapes diverge for a genuine reason (one needs role for owner checks, the other is a pure query-scope token). You cannot merge them without either bloating TenantScope with role or breaking the owner check.

2. The headline "five overlapping membership joins with no shared core" and the proposed resolveMembership(userId, teamSlug, projectSlug?) core do NOT survive the deletion test. The three "duplicated" queries are materially different: resolveTeamBySlug is teams ⋈ memberships WHERE teams.slug=? (single row); resolveProjectBySlugs is projects ⋈ teams ⋈ memberships WHERE teams.slug=? AND projects.slug=? (single row); resolveTenantBundleForUser is memberships ⋈ teams ⟕ projects WHERE memberships.userId=? — NO slug filter, returns the user's ENTIRE team/project set and derives userTeams/teamProjects/activeProject buckets in JS (middleware/01.context.ts:112-124 needs all three). A resolveMembership keyed on a specific teamSlug cannot produce the bundle's "all teams" picker output. The genuinely shared substance is only and(eq(memberships.userId, userId), eq(memberships.teamId, teams.id)) — two trivial predicates, a one-liner each place. Extracting that MOVES a triviality; it does not CONCENTRATE complexity smeared across callers. Deleting the hypothetical core makes the predicate "reappear" as a single and(eq,eq) clause, which is the cheapest possible thing — the opposite of earning its keep.

3. The real, smaller, deletion-test-passing duplication is the {teamId, projectId, teamSlug, projectSlug} → TenantScope field-rename projection, replicated THREE times (scope.ts:47-52, scope.ts:78-83, tenant-context.ts toScope 28-35), each re-applying the same two as AuthorizedTeamId/AuthorizedProjectId brand casts. That projection is the thing worth centralizing because the brand casts are the security-load-bearing bit and live in 3 places.

No ADR conflict (logical tenancy / branded ids are preserved by any of these refactors).
