#13 · Data layer & schema
Analytics read loaders hand-rebuild shared SQL fragments (scope-join, status buckets, percentile picker) invisible to Drizzle
medium severity effort: large confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/flaky.server.ts:204
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:152
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/tests.server.ts:222
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:72
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.server.ts:95
Problem — the friction

Five analytics loaders each open db.run(sql\...\) and hand-write the same CTE skeleton: with ranked as (select ... row_number() over (partition by tr."testId" order by tr."createdAt" desc) as rn from "testResults" tr inner join runs on runs.id = tr."runId" where tr."projectId" = ${projectId} ...). flaky.server.ts (loadSparklinesAndMeta, loadRecentFailures), tests.server.ts (runAggregateQuery), and slowest-tests.server.ts (bottlenecks) all repeat the same per-testId ranking + latest-row extraction (max(case when rnTime = 1 then title end)) + status-bucket counters (sum(case when status in ('failed','timedout') then 1 ...)). A maintainer fixing a scoping bug, a status-bucket definition, or a percentile formula must find and edit N near-identical SQL strings; the typed Zod result interfaces (RankedTest, BottleneckRow, AggregateRow, TestsPageRow) are also re-declared per file with overlapping fields. The raw SQL is invisible to Drizzle's type checker — a typo in a column name surfaces only at runtime against a real D1.

Solution — the deepened module

Extend the existing src/lib/analytics/ module with targeted, typed SQL-fragment shapers — NOT one omnibus 5-loader ranked CTE builder. Concretely: (1) a testResultScopeJoin(scope, { branch, q, testIds? }) helper returning the shared inner join runs ... where tr."projectId" = ${scope.projectId} + branch + LIKE-search + testId-IN predicate fragment (callers: tests, slowest-tests, flaky x2); (2) statusCounters() emitting the canonical passed/flaky/failCount(failed+timedout)/skipped CASE block (callers: tests, slowest-tests); (3) latestPerTest(cols) emitting max(case when rnTime=1 then col end) for a column list (callers: tests, slowest-tests); (4) discretePercentile(rnCol, cntCol, q) owning the min(case when rn = max(1, round(cnt*q)) ...) invariant (callers: slowest-tests, run-duration). Co-locate the overlapping result-row interfaces. Leave run-duration's runs-table percentile use and suite-size's tests-added subquery as separate callers of (4) only — do not force them through a testId-ranking builder. Add unit tests over the shaper output strings so the type-invisible SQL gets a regression net.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: loaders shrink to param-parsing + presentation; callers express 'rank tests by p95 in this window' instead of 40 lines of SQL. Locality: scope predicate, branch/search fragment composition, status-bucket semantics, and percentile math each change in one file; a new analytics page reuses the primitives instead of copy-pasting a CTE.

Deletion test

Delete the module and the CTE skeleton + scope-join + status-counter CASE blocks reappear verbatim across the 5 loaders named above — it earns its keep by concentrating complexity currently smeared across them.

Testability impact

Today these queries are only exercisable against a live D1 (no real-DB harness exists), so they are effectively untested. A query module lets the SQL-fragment builders (predicate composition, percentile rank expression, status-bucket CASE) be unit-tested as pure functions that emit a Drizzle SQL object, and lets the integration surface be a handful of named functions rather than inline strings in page loaders.

Interface sketch
rankedTestResults(scope: TenantScope, opts: { windowStartSec; branch?: string|null; q?: string|null; testIds?: string[] }): SQL // emits shared `ranked` CTE flakyAggregates / bottlenecks / testCatalog wrap it. Invariant: every builder injects eq(projectId) — raw projectId never reaches a loader.
Verifier notes

Read all 5 cited files plus the existing src/lib/analytics/{range,bucketing,bucketing-sql}.ts and src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts. The duplication is REAL but the finding's "same ranked CTE skeleton across all 5" framing is inflated; the overlap is fractured into several distinct primitives that cluster across DIFFERENT 2-3 file subsets, not one 5-file skeleton.

Verified verbatim repeats (grep + read):
- branch fragment branchFilter ? sql\and runs.branch = ${...}\ : sql\\` hand-rebuilt in slowest-tests (3x usage), tests (passed as arg), run-duration, AND twice inside flaky's two raw helpers (lines 210, 261). Most-smeared primitive.
- scope-join inner join runs on runs.id = tr."runId" where tr."projectId" = ... in raw SQL: 8 occurrences across tests.server, flaky.server, slowest-tests.server.
- status-bucket CASE sum(case when status in ('failed','timedout') then 1 ...): ONLY tests.server + slowest-tests.server (2 files).
- discrete percentile picker min(case when rn = max(1, cast(round(cnt * 0.XX) as integer)) ...): ONLY slowest-tests.server + run-duration.server (2 files) — carries a subtle invariant (rank clamped to [1..cnt]) that is a real correctness hotspot.
- latest-row extraction max(case when "rnTime" = 1 then ... end): ONLY tests.server + slowest-tests.server (2 files).
- per-testId ranking row_number() over (partition by tr."testId" order by tr."createdAt" desc): tests.server (1x) + flaky.server (2x). NOT in slowest-tests (it partitions by testId order by durationMs in a filtered->ranked two-level CTE) and NOT in run-duration.

Where the finding is WRONG:
- run-duration.server.ts scans the runs table (from runs; runs."projectId"; lines 79/103), NOT testResults. It has no testId partition, no status buckets, no scope-join-on-testResults. Its ONLY shared primitives are the percentile picker and the branch fragment. The proposed rankedTestResults({scope,...,testIds}) builder would not serve it.
- suite-size.server.ts is almost entirely Drizzle (db.select + bucketExpr + and(eq...)); its only raw SQL is the unique tests-added NOT EXISTS subquery. It shares essentially none of the named primitives (no testId-ranking, no status CASE, no percentile picker). Including it inflates the count.
- flaky.server's AGGREGATES use Drizzle (db.select.innerJoin, lines 81-94), not raw CTE; only its two helper fns are raw.
- "no deep query module" is too strong: src/lib/analytics/ ALREADY concentrates range parsing, segment bucketing, and the D1-affinity bucketExpr; runs-filters-where.ts already gives scopedRunsWhere. The solution is an EXTENSION of an existing module, not net-new.

Deletion test: PASSES, but narrower than claimed. The percentile picker (2 callers, subtle off-by-one invariant), status-bucket CASE (2 callers; "timedout" classification is a domain definition that would otherwise need N edits), and the scope-join+branch+search predicate (3-4 callers) genuinely concentrate complexity that is currently smeared and is invisible to Drizzle's typechecker (all via db.run(sql\\) with as` casts — ties into the known ~67 no-unsafe-type-assertion warnings). Real locality win. No ADR conflict (logical tenancy preserved — a shared scope-join helper still bakes projectId/teamId in, reinforcing decision #2).

Severity lowered high->medium: write-side ingest is the deep module; these are read-side analytics loaders, lower blast radius, and the riskiest shared piece (percentile/status definitions) spans only 2 files each.

#14 · Data layer & schema
Tenant-scope brand is enforced only at the query-builder seam; child-row reads in the test-detail loader omit the projectId predicate by convention
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier touches a durable decision
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:92
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:99
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:124
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:13
Problem — the friction

The durable decision is 'every run-scoped query MUST filter by projectId', and AuthorizedProjectId is branded specifically to make that impossible to forget. But the type only protects Drizzle query-builder call sites — the analytics loaders go through db.run(sql\...\) and pass scope.projectId as a plain interpolated string, so the brand provides zero guarantee there; correctness is purely by convention. Worse, the test-detail loader reads child tables (testTags, testAnnotations, testResultAttempts) filtered by testResultId ONLY — no projectId predicate (lines 92/99/124) — even though it has project.id in scope. The parent testResults row IS scoped (line 61), so it is not currently exploitable, but it directly contradicts the stated invariant and is the kind of asymmetry that becomes a cross-tenant leak the moment a future query loads children before/without the scoped parent.

Solution — the deepened module

Two distinct moves with different payoff. (1) Strong: centralize the four child-table reads in the test-detail loader behind scope-carrying helpers — tagsForResult(scope, testResultId), annotationsForResult(scope, testResultId), attemptsForResult(scope, testResultId), artifactsForResult(scope, testResultId) — that always inject eq(table.projectId, scope.projectId) alongside the testResultId predicate. This restores the brand at the only doors that reach these tables and matches the already-correct pattern in routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts. (2) Weaker but worthwhile for the brand's integrity: keep AuthorizedProjectId through the analytics helper signatures instead of widening to projectId: string (the predicate text is already present in those CTEs; the win is type-enforcement, not de-duplication). Do not frame this as fixing an injection risk — Drizzle sql interpolation is already parameterized. Frame it as: the brand currently guards only the Drizzle query-builder seam; these helpers extend that guarantee to child-row and raw-SQL reads.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers cannot construct an unscoped child read; they pass scope and get a correctly-filtered query. Locality: the projectId-predicate rule lives in the helper, not replicated (and occasionally omitted) across loaders; one place to audit for tenant isolation.

Deletion test

Delete the helpers and the projectId predicate must be re-added to every child read in test-detail + every raw analytics CTE — complexity reappears across ~7 sites. It earns its keep as the enforcement point the brand currently only pretends to be at the raw-SQL layer.

Testability impact

Makes 'does this read filter by projectId' a unit-testable property of each helper (assert the emitted WHERE contains the projectId eq), instead of an unverifiable convention spread across inline queries that only a live cross-tenant integration test could catch.

Interface sketch
scopedFrom(scope): SQL // `"testResults" tr ... where tr."projectId" = ${scope.projectId}` tagsForResult(scope, testResultId): Promise<{tag}[]> // injects eq(projectId) Invariant: no exported reader accepts a bare projectId string.
Durable-decision note

Touches durable decision #2 (logical tenant isolation, type-enforced) but reinforces rather than reopens it — the brand's promise is currently unmet at the raw-SQL seam; this closes the gap.

Verifier notes

Verified all cited code. The test-detail loader friction is REAL: index.server.ts reads testTags (line 92), testAnnotations (line 99), testResultAttempts (line 124), AND artifacts (line 113) filtered by testResultId ONLY — no projectId predicate — while testResults (line 61) and the history query (line 140) ARE scoped by project.id. All four child tables DO carry a projectId column (schema.ts: testTags 275, testAnnotations 293, testResultAttempts 309, artifacts 335), so the predicate is possible and simply omitted. Not currently exploitable: the scoped parent fetch (lines 55-72) verifies testResultId belongs to this project+run and short-circuits to not_found (76-85) before any child read runs; the children reuse that same testResultId. The finder correctly concedes this.

Inconsistency claim is the strongest part and is demonstrable: routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts:32 DOES scope artifacts by eq(artifacts.projectId, scope.projectId) AND id — the exact same artifacts table the test-detail loader reads unscoped. So enforcement is by-convention and applied unevenly across call sites.

CORRECTION to the raw-SQL framing: the finding says projectId is "passed as a plain interpolated string" implying an injection/concatenation risk. That is FALSE. Every raw-SQL site uses Drizzle's sql\...${projectId}\` template tag which emits a BOUND PARAMETER, not concatenated text (verified in tests.server.ts:201/239, flaky.server.ts:226/281/321, insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:101/133/165/212, insights/suite-size.server.ts:100/106, insights/run-duration.server.ts:80/103, and ingest.ts:437-441). Moreover every one of those raw-SQL CTEs ALREADY includes where tr."projectId" = ${projectId}. The real, narrower defect: the analytics helper signatures take projectId: string (e.g. tests.server.ts:187/217, flaky.server.ts:205/256/314), erasing the AuthorizedProjectId brand at the seam, so the type cannot force the predicate. The gap is "the brand's promise is unmet at the raw-SQL layer," not "the predicate is missing" or "it's injectable."

Deletion test: passes modestly. Genuine smear = 4 unscoped child reads in the test-detail loader. Centralizing them behind scope-carrying helpers (tagsForResult/attemptsForResult/annotationsForResult/artifactsForResult) concentrates the predicate and re-attaches the brand. The raw-SQL scopedFrom(scope) fragment half is weaker — the predicates already exist, so a fragment helper mostly relocates where tr."projectId" = ${...}` rather than removing real duplication; that leans toward moving complexity.

ADR: reinforces durable decision #2 (logical, type-enforced tenant isolation) rather than reopening it. No conflict — the finder's adrConflict note is accurate.

Severity lowered high -> medium: not currently exploitable, no injection vector, raw-SQL predicates present today; this is a latent-invariant / defense-in-depth gap, not an active leak.

#15 · Data layer & schema
branches-query.ts documents and relies on an index that does not exist
low severity effort: small confidence: high deep but fragile
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/branches-query.ts:11
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:222
Problem — the friction

loadProjectBranches's doc-comment asserts 'The composite index runs_project_branch_idx lets SQLite skip-scan distinct values' (branches-query.ts:11). No such index exists in schema.ts — the closest is runs_project_branch_created_at_idx on (projectId, branch, createdAt) (schema.ts:222). The SELECT DISTINCT runs.branch query (the 7-loader hot path that feeds every filter bar) can use the leading (projectId, branch) prefix of that index for the distinct scan, so it is not unindexed — but the function's stated contract names a phantom index. Any maintainer auditing index coverage, or trusting the comment when tuning, will be misled; if someone 'cleans up' the unused-looking created_at index believing the branch index is the real one, the distinct scan degrades. The fragility is that the deep, hot function's documented performance characteristic (part of its interface) is wrong.

Solution — the deepened module

Correct the comment to name the real index (runs_project_branch_created_at_idx) and note that the distinct scan uses its (projectId, branch) prefix. If the distinct-branch query proves hot enough to warrant a dedicated narrower index, add runs_project_branch_idx on (projectId, branch) in a new numbered migration — but the decision should be measured, not implied by a comment.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers/maintainers can trust the documented perf characteristic, which is part of the function's interface. Locality: index reality and the doc-comment agree, so index audits and migrations don't act on a fiction.

Deletion test

N/A as an extraction — this is a fragility/accuracy fix on an already-deep helper; deleting the false comment removes a landmine without removing behavior.

Testability impact

Indirect: an EXPLAIN QUERY PLAN assertion in a future real-DB harness could pin the distinct scan to the real index; today the comment is the only (and wrong) documentation of the access path.

Verifier notes

Verified all cited code. branches-query.ts:11 doc-comment asserts the composite index runs_project_branch_idx enables the distinct skip-scan. A repo-wide grep confirms runs_project_branch_idx appears NOWHERE except inside that comment — it is a genuine phantom. The real index (schema.ts:222 and migration 20260523124136_dizzy_wong.sql:86) is runs_project_branch_created_at_idx on (projectId, branch, createdAt). The "7-loader hot path" claim is exactly right: loadProjectBranches is imported by 7 distinct page loaders (tests, insights/index, flaky, insights/slowest-tests, runs/[runId]/index, insights/suite-size, insights/run-duration). The prefix-scan reasoning is also technically sound — the (projectId, branch) leading prefix of the existing 3-col index covers the equality filter on projectId plus the DISTINCT+ORDER BY branch ASC scan, so the query is genuinely indexed; only the comment's index NAME is wrong, not the existence of coverage. This is therefore an accuracy/fragility fix, not a deepening: there is no smeared complexity to concentrate across the 7 callers (they all just call loadProjectBranches and pass scope). The finder correctly marked deletionTest N/A; I set deletionTestPasses=false to reflect that a comment correction is not a depth-increasing extraction. The "landmine" framing (an auditor dropping the created_at index believing the branch index is the real one) is plausible but somewhat speculative — the *_created_at_idx naming and the recency-sorted run-history filters make that index's purpose discoverable. No ADR conflict: fix is a one-line comment edit; the optional dedicated index is correctly gated on measurement per durable decision #8 (new numbered migration). Severity low is accurate.

#16 · Data layer & schema
Per-table column-count constants are hand-maintained and decoupled from the schema
low severity effort: small confidence: high coupling revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:53
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:11
  • apps/dashboard/db/schema.ts:236
Problem — the friction

The param-chunking that keeps D1 batches under 99 params depends on literal column counts: ingest.ts declares TEST_RESULTS_COLUMNS = 14, TEST_TAGS_COLUMNS = 4, TEST_ANNOTATIONS_COLUMNS = 5, TEST_RESULT_ATTEMPTS_COLUMNS = 9, and register.ts independently declares ARTIFACT_COLUMNS = 12. These integers must equal the number of columns inserted per row, which is defined in db/schema.ts — but nothing links them. Add a nullable column to testResults and forget to bump the 14, and chunkByParams under-counts params; a batch can then exceed D1's 100-param ceiling and fail at runtime only under large flushes. The coupling is invisible: the constant lives in ingest.ts/register.ts, the source of truth lives in schema.ts, and only a human remembering the rule keeps them aligned.

Solution — the deepened module

Co-locate the column count with each insert-row builder rather than computing from rows[0] (the finder's Object.keys(row).length breaks on the empty arrays — tagRows/annotationRows are frequently empty, where chunking is a no-op anyway). Concretely: define each per-table count as Object.keys(templateRow).length of a single representative row literal kept next to the builder (or expose columnCount from the same row-factory proposed in the denormalization finding), and have the artifact route import that shared source instead of its own literal 12. Optionally add a cheap unit test that asserts each constant equals the count of NOT-NULL-plus-defaulted columns drilled from the Drizzle table's column metadata, so any future schema column addition fails CI rather than at runtime. Either path makes the count track the actual insert automatically.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: chunkByParams callers no longer pass a magic integer that can drift. Locality: the column count is defined where the insert row is shaped, so a schema/insert change updates it automatically; no second place to remember.

Deletion test

This is a collapse, not an extraction: deleting the standalone constants in favor of derived counts removes a class of silent drift; the literals are a shallow restatement of information schema.ts already holds.

Testability impact

A unit test can assert columnCount === Object.keys(insertRow).length for each table; today the only signal that 14 is wrong is a 100-param D1 failure under a large real batch, which no current test can produce.

Interface sketch
const TEST_RESULT_INSERT_COLUMNS = Object.keys(makeTestResultRow(...)).length // or factory.columnCount Invariant: count is derived from the same object that is inserted.
Verifier notes

Confirmed against the files. ingest.ts:53-56 declares TEST_RESULTS_COLUMNS=14, TEST_TAGS_COLUMNS=4, TEST_ANNOTATIONS_COLUMNS=5, TEST_RESULT_ATTEMPTS_COLUMNS=9; register.ts:11 independently declares ARTIFACT_COLUMNS=12. All five feed chunkByParams (ingest.ts:58) which keeps db.batch statements under MAX_PARAMS_PER_STATEMENT=99 (decision 10). I counted columns in both the schema.ts tables and the insert-row object literals inside buildResultInsertStatements (ingest.ts:168-207, 266-281) / buildQueuePrefillStatements (125-140) / the artifact route (register.ts:159-172): every literal is correct today (14/4/5/9/12 all match). So the finder did not misread — the friction is exactly the decoupling described: the param count is restated by hand in ingest.ts/register.ts while the source of truth is the insert shape (and schema.ts). No test pins these constants — grep over apps/dashboard/src/__tests__ found chunkByParams/COLUMNS are never exercised — so drift surfaces only at runtime, and only above the per-table row threshold (e.g. >7 testResults rows since floor(99/14)=7) under a large flush. Combined with the known-outstanding no-real-DB-test-harness gap, nothing would catch a stale literal in CI. Deletion test passes: the integer 14 is literally Object.keys(insertRow).length by construction, so deriving it collapses a duplicated fact rather than introducing a hypothetical seam — complexity currently smeared across 5 call sites in 2 files concentrates at the insert builder. NO ADR conflict: this protects decision 10 (db.batch chunked to <=99 params), it does not reverse anything. Severity correctly low: literals are correct now, failure is latent (schema-change + large-flush), not a live bug.

#17 · Data layer & schema
The branchFilter normalization (ALL_BRANCHES->null) is copy-pasted across 6 loaders; raw-SQL branch/search fragments add minor inline duplication
low severity effort: medium confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/branches-query.ts:13
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:66
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:86
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/tests.server.ts:90
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:68
Problem — the friction

Branch filtering appears in 7 loaders (per the loadProjectBranches usage grep). Two pieces are centralized: loadProjectBranches (branches-query.ts) for the dropdown options, and scopedRunsWhere/buildRunsWhere (runs-filters-where.ts) for the Drizzle-builder runs-list path. But the raw-SQL analytics loaders each re-derive the same two fragments inline: const branchSql = branchFilter ? sql\and runs.branch = ${branchFilter}\ : sql\\` and const qSql = pattern ? sql\and (tr.title like ${pattern} or tr.file like ${pattern})\ : sql\\` — repeated near-verbatim in slowest-tests.server.ts:86-91, tests.server.ts:90-95, run-duration.server.ts:68, suite-size, and flaky (branchSql/joinSql variants). The ALL_BRANCHES/branchFilter normalization is also re-parsed per loader. So branch handling has two homes for two access styles and N inline copies for the third (raw SQL).

Solution — the deepened module

Add three small helpers to a shared module (e.g. src/lib/analytics/filters.ts): (1) parseBranchFilter(param: string | null): string | null — the single home for the ALL_BRANCHES normalization, replacing the 6 inline copies; (2) branchFragment(branch: string | null) emitting sql\and runs.branch = ${branch}\` or empty sql\\, with a joinSql sibling for flaky's conditional-join case; (3) searchFragment(q: string | null) emitting sql\and (tr.title like ${pattern} or tr.file like ${pattern})\. Keep all fragments parameterized (sql${}`) to preserve injection safety. The qSql piece only deduplicates 2 call sites (tests + slowest-tests) so it is optional; the normalization helper is the load-bearing win across 6 loaders. Do NOT couple this to a hypothetical separate "analytics query module" — these are standalone pure helpers.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: a loader expresses 'filter by this branch and search' once; the LIKE-escaping and ALL_BRANCHES semantics come for free. Locality: changing the searchable columns or the branch-all sentinel is one edit, not five; the Drizzle path (runs-filters-where) and raw path share the same branch/search semantics instead of drifting.

Deletion test

Delete the fragment helpers and the branchSql/qSql ternaries + branchFilter normalization reappear across the 5 raw-SQL loaders — earns its keep by concentrating the filter-fragment construction smeared across them.

Testability impact

branchFragment/searchFragment and the branch normalizer become pure, unit-testable (assert emitted SQL + LIKE escaping + ALL_BRANCHES collapse), whereas the inline ternaries are only exercised through full loader integration against a real DB.

Interface sketch
branchFragment(branch: string|null): SQL searchFragment(q: string|null, cols: SQLColumn[]): SQL normalizeBranch(param: string|null): string|null // collapses ALL_BRANCHES + empty to null
Verifier notes

Read all cited files plus suite-size.server.ts, flaky.server.ts, and grepped the repo. The core duplication is real, but the finding inflates two of its three counts.

VERIFIED (real):
- loadProjectBranches is genuinely used in 7 loaders (tests, flaky, insights/index, suite-size, slowest-tests, run-duration, runs/[runId]/index) — grep confirms. Already centralized; not the friction.
- scopedRunsWhere/buildRunsWhere (runs-filters-where.ts) is the Drizzle-builder path for the runs LIST — confirmed, also already centralized.
- The branchFilter NORMALIZATION !branchParam || branchParam === ALL_BRANCHES ? null : branchParam is copied near-verbatim in SIX loaders: tests.server.ts:79-80, slowest-tests:73-74, run-duration:58-59, suite-size:50-51, insights/index:29, and flaky:66-67 (a trivial two-line variant). This is the strongest, cleanest piece of the finding — six identical copies of a pure-function normalization.
- The raw-SQL branchSql fragment branch ? sql\and runs.branch = ${...}\ : sql\\` is duplicated ~6 times across 4 files: tests:90-92, slowest-tests:86-88 AND :202-204 (branchSparkSql), run-duration:68-70, flaky:210 AND :261 (with a sibling joinSql variant). Real.

INACCURATE (corrections):
- The qSql search fragment and (tr.title like ${pattern} or tr.file like ${pattern}) appears in only TWO files (tests:94, slowest-tests:90), NOT "repeated near-verbatim across 5 raw-SQL loaders". run-duration, flaky, and suite-size have no search fragment at all.
- suite-size is mislabeled as a raw-SQL loader with branchSql. It actually filters branch via the Drizzle builder path: if (branchFilter) trendConditions.push(eq(runs.branch, branchFilter)) (suite-size:65) and flaky's agg also uses eq(runs.branch, branchFilter) (flaky:79). So the "5 raw-SQL loaders re-derive branchSql" claim overstates: it's 4 files, and two of the analytics loaders use Drizzle eq() for branch, not the raw fragment.

DELETION TEST (passes): Extract parseBranchFilter(param), branchFragment(branch), searchFragment(q, cols) and delete them → the === ALL_BRANCHES ternary reappears in 6 loaders, the branchSql ternary in 4 files, the qSql ternary in 2. Complexity is genuinely smeared, so this concentrates rather than relocates it. The normalizer extraction in particular is the cheapest, highest-leverage win.

SEVERITY: downgraded medium->low. The fragments are 1-3 line ternaries; the real value is killing the 6x normalization copy-paste (a correctness hazard if ALL_BRANCHES semantics ever change), not the SQL fragments which are trivial. Not high-leverage depth — modest locality improvement.

ADR: no conflict. Pure helper extraction; doesn't touch single-D1, logical tenancy, branded AuthorizedProjectId, Better Auth tables, nuqs, or ETL. The branchFragment helper must keep emitting parameterized sql${}` (not string interpolation) to preserve injection safety — current code already does this.

#18 · Data layer & schema
Typed db.batch wrapper concentrates the forced `as never` call-site cast + result extraction across 7 files
low severity effort: small confidence: high shallow module revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:213
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:687
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/general.server.ts:136
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/new.server.ts:107
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/accept.ts:91
  • apps/dashboard/pages/invite/[token]/index.server.ts:166
Problem — the friction

Atomic multi-statement writes are a core architectural decision (durable #10: D1 db.batch for atomicity, chunked to <=99 params), but the project has no module owning it. Instead each call site assembles a heterogeneous PromiseLike<unknown>[] / unknown[] of Drizzle builders and casts as never to get past db.batch's tuple type (ingest.ts:213 comments on why; the cast recurs in general.server.ts:136 ops as never, new.server.ts:107, accept.ts:91, invite/index.server.ts:166). The result-array indexing is also hand-rolled and re-cast (batchResults[batchResults.length - 1] as readonly RunAggregateSummary[]) at ingest.ts:692/799/842. The atomicity guarantee, the param-cap discipline, and the result-extraction pattern have no shared home; each caller re-derives them and each as never is an un-narrowed type hole (part of the ~67 no-unsafe-type-assertion warnings noted as outstanding).

Solution — the deepened module

Add src/lib/db-batch.ts with two thin typed wrappers, scoped to the CALL site only (do not fold in chunkByParams — ingest.ts already owns the <=99-param invariant):
- runBatch(statements: PromiseLike<unknown>[]): Promise<readonly unknown[]> — performs the as never cast once internally, calls db.batch, returns results. Replaces the cast at the 7 call sites (ingest 579/623/688/796/840, general:136, keys:153, new:107, accept:91, invite:166).
- runBatchReturningLast<T>(statements): Promise<readonly T[] | undefined> — types the final .returning() row, killing the 3 hand-written batchResults[batchResults.length - 1] as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] | undefined casts at ingest.ts 692/799/842.

Explicitly out of scope: the per-element as never casts at ingest.ts 243/253/263/294/685 inside buildResultInsertStatements — those come from the heterogeneous array element type and are not removed by this helper. State that honestly so the helper is not oversold.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers express 'run these statements atomically, give me the last returning row typed' without touching as never or index math. Locality: the single unavoidable cast, the param-cap rule, and the result-extraction pattern live in one file; the no-unsafe-type-assertion suppressions collapse from 6 scattered sites to one.

Deletion test

Delete the helper and the as never cast + manual last-element extraction reappear across all 6 batch call sites — it earns its keep by concentrating the one type hole D1's batch API forces.

Testability impact

runBatchReturningLast becomes the typed seam ingest depends on, so appendRunResults/completeRun can be tested against a faked batch runner that returns canned summary rows — today the result extraction is interleaved with db.batch and only reachable via a real D1.

Interface sketch
runBatch(stmts: PromiseLike<unknown>[]): Promise<unknown[]> runBatchReturningLast<T>(stmts): Promise<T | undefined> Invariant: single internal `as never`; callers never cast.
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited code. The friction is real: every db.batch call carries an as never cast, and the finding's premise (no module owns the cast/result-extraction pattern) holds.

CALL SITES CONFIRMED (all 6 cited + 1 missed):
- ingest.ts:688 db.batch(statements as never), plus :579 prefill as never, :623 stmts as never, :796 and :840 (the inline [...] as never).
- general.server.ts:136 db.batch(ops as never) (ops is unknown[] built at :122).
- new.server.ts:107, accept.ts:91, invite/index.server.ts:166 — literal-tuple [...] as never.
- MISSED by the finder: keys.server.ts:153 db.batch([...] as never) — same pattern, 7th file. So 10 batch call sites across 6 files, not "6 files" as titled.

RESULT-EXTRACTION repetition CONFIRMED: batchResults[batchResults.length - 1] as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] | undefined is verbatim 3x in ingest.ts (692, 799, 842). A runBatchReturningLast<T> would genuinely concentrate this.

DELETION TEST: passes for the call-site cast and the last-element extraction — delete the helper and as never + manual indexing reappear across 7 files. This concentrates a type hole D1/Drizzle's batch tuple type forces, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam. Real.

CORRECTIONS TO THE SOLUTION (why revise, not keep):
1. The solution's "fold in chunkByParams / own the <=99-param cap here too" is REDUNDANT. chunkByParams (ingest.ts:58) + the MAX_PARAMS_PER_STATEMENT=99 constant ALREADY own that invariant and are used at ingest.ts:146/328/331/334/337. The param cap is not smeared; it lives in one place. A db-batch helper should NOT claim it.
2. The solution overstates reach. Inside buildResultInsertStatements there are PER-ELEMENT as never casts (243, 253, 263, 294, 685) caused by pushing heterogeneous SQLiteUpdate/SQLiteDelete builders into PromiseLike<unknown>[] — these come from the ARRAY ELEMENT TYPE, not the db.batch CALL signature, so runBatch(statements) does NOT remove them. The helper absorbs the call-site cast and the result cast only.
3. The atomicity guarantee already HAS a home: ingest.ts is the documented deep module (comment lines 40-48 explain db.batch is the atomicity boundary). The new helper would own the TYPE ergonomics of batch, not the atomicity decision.

Severity adjusted high->low...actually medium->low: this is a small typing-ergonomics convenience (one cast + one extraction concentrated), overlapping the already-tracked ~67 no-unsafe-type-assertion warnings. It is not a structural deepening. Worth doing, low risk, low payoff.

No ADR conflict — does not touch durable decision #10 (db.batch atomicity / chunking stays); it just types the seam.

Realtime (void/live) · 5 findings

#19 · Realtime (void/live)
RunProgressEvent.summary is produced transactionally in ingest, accumulated by the hook, then discarded by RunProgress (_summary); the header tiles/OutcomeBar/tab-count render from static SSR props and the e2e that names "summary counters" actually exercises the row-recompute path
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/run-progress.tsx:67
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.tsx:172
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.tsx:186
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.tsx:234
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:86
  • packages/e2e/tests-dashboard/realtime.spec.ts:152
Problem — the friction

Every ingest write builds and broadcasts a transactionally-consistent summary (the whole point of pushing the .returning()/SELECT through broadcastRunUpdate in ingest.ts), useRunProgress accumulates it via setSummary, and then RunProgress destructures it as _summary and throws it away (run-progress.tsx:67). Meanwhile the run-detail page renders the passed/failed/flaky/skipped tiles (index.tsx:172-181), the OutcomeBar (index.tsx:186-193), and the Tests-tab count (index.tsx:234 run.totalTests) from the static SSR run.* object, which lives in the page component OUTSIDE the RunProgress island and never re-renders on a live event. The seam claims summary flows live to the UI but it does not: the only thing that updates live is the per-test row list, whose counts RunProgress recomputes itself from byId (run-progress.tsx:81). This is a contract that lies. Worse, the e2e test 'summary counters update live' (realtime.spec.ts:152) asserts the Failed tile gains a digit — but that tile renders run.failed from SSR, so either the test is asserting against the wrong element or it only passes incidentally; a maintainer trusting it would believe live summary works when it doesn't.

Solution — the deepened module

Pick one owner for the live summary and make the seam honest.

(a) If these header counters SHOULD be live: lift the live summary into a small client island that wraps the SummaryStat tiles + OutcomeBar + Tests-tab count, reading useRunProgress(runId).summary (seeded by initialSummary). This concentrates the published snapshot into N=3 consumers that today read static SSR props, and finally makes the broadcast load-bearing — including on completeRun, where summary is the only payload. Keep "use client" at this leaf island, not the page root (per the islands ADR).

(b) If SSR-only header counters are the intended product behaviour: delete summary from RunProgressEvent (live.ts), stop SELECTing/returning it and passing it to broadcastRunUpdate in ingest.ts, and drop setSummary/initialSummary from the hook + RunProgress. RunProgress already computes its own live counts from byId, so nothing on the client regresses.

Either way, fix the misleading e2e: rename/rescope realtime.spec.ts:121 so its name matches what it asserts. It currently verifies the SegmentedControl filter button's count (live via the changedTests->byId recompute), NOT the published summary snapshot. If you keep option (a), add an assertion against the SSR tiles/OutcomeBar to actually cover the summary path; if option (b), drop the "summary" framing entirely.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get a single source of truth for run counts — either the live summary is authoritative everywhere or the SSR snapshot is, not a silent split where the tile and the in-list recomputed counts can disagree mid-run. Locality: the decision 'what is authoritative for run counts' lives in one place; a maintainer changing counter behaviour edits one path instead of reconciling SSR props against an unused hook return.

Deletion test

If option (b) — deleting summary from the event/accumulator — removes complexity cleanly (the publisher stops building it, the hook stops storing it, nothing on the client regresses because nothing reads it). That is the tell that the summary half is currently a pass-through that earns nothing on the client. If option (a), the complexity is justified but must actually be wired to N=3 consumers (tiles, OutcomeBar, tab count). Either way the current state — produced but discarded — fails the test.

Testability impact

Removes a false-positive e2e assertion. If summary is wired live (a), the reducer extraction above makes 'summary replaces correctly' a unit test and the e2e can target a real live-updating element. If summary is dropped (b), the ingest summary-consistency machinery no longer needs an end-to-end client test at all because nothing downstream depends on it.

Interface sketch
Option A: <RunSummaryLive runId initialSummary> reads useRunProgress(runId).summary and renders tiles+OutcomeBar; page passes run.* only as initialSummary. Option B: RunProgressEvent = { type:'progress'; changedTests: RunProgressTest[] } — summary removed from wire + ingest broadcast.
Verifier notes

VERIFIED against the cited code; the core insight holds.

CLIENT DISCARD CONFIRMED: run-progress.tsx:67 destructures summary: _summary and the value is used nowhere. A repo-wide grep for consumers of useRunProgress's summary returns only this single call site (the run-history-bar-hover.tsx "summary" hits are an unrelated hover-card prop, not RunProgressEvent.summary). RunProgress derives every count it shows from the live row accumulator instead: statusCounts is recomputed from tests=Object.values(byId) (run-progress.tsx:81-93), and the SegmentedControl option counts read statusCounts.* (run-progress.tsx:172-196). So summary is the sole client consumer and it throws it away.

SSR TILES CONFIRMED OUTSIDE THE ISLAND: SummaryStat tiles (index.tsx:172-181), OutcomeBar (index.tsx:186-193) and the Tests-tab count run.totalTests (index.tsx:234) all render from the static SSR run.* Props object in the page component, which is RSC/non-island and never re-renders on a live event. RunProgress is the only island on the page (index.tsx:242). Confirmed.

PRODUCER COST CONFIRMED: ingest.ts genuinely builds a transactionally-consistent summary on every write — appendRunResults SELECTs the aggregate as the last batch statement and passes it to broadcastRunUpdate (ingest.ts:683-699); completeRun and the no-delta path do the same (ingest.ts:799-807, 627-637, 842-847). So the "produced then discarded" cost claim is real.

DELETION TEST (option b): deleting summary from RunProgressEvent (live.ts:82-97), from ingest's broadcasts, and from the hook's setSummary (live-client.ts:80) removes complexity with zero client regression — there is exactly N=1 client consumer and it discards the value. That is the signature of a pass-through earning nothing on the client. deletionTestPasses=true for option (b). (Option a would CONCENTRATE the live summary into one island wrapping the 3 SSR consumers — also legitimate, but it adds a consumer that doesn't exist today.)

WHY REVISE NOT KEEP-AS-IS: the e2e critique is slightly mis-stated and should be corrected, because a reader will check it. The test 'summary counters update live' (realtime.spec.ts:121-159) asserts on getByRole("button", { name: /^Failed/ }). The ONLY button whose accessible name starts with "Failed" is the SegmentedControl filter pill inside RunProgress (segmented-control.tsx:53-83 renders each option as <button type=button> with label+count); the SSR SummaryStat is a <span> (index.tsx:357-376), so it is NOT the matched element. The test therefore PASSES, and not incidentally — it exercises a real live path (changedTests -> byId -> statusCounts recompute). The accurate framing is: the test does NOT validate the summary snapshot at all; it validates the row-recompute path while its docstring (realtime.spec.ts:8 "summary counters tick up") implies it covers the published summary. So the false confidence is real, but the mechanism is "tests a different live path than its name claims," not "asserts against the wrong element / passes incidentally."

ONE NUANCE THE FINDER UNDERSTATES: completeRun broadcasts changedTests:[] + summary only (ingest.ts:803-807) — on run completion the summary is the entire live payload. Since nothing reads it, run completion is effectively not reflected live at all (the header StatusGlyph reads SSR run.status too). Consistent with the thesis, reinforces it.

SEVERITY: lowering high->medium. This is a genuine leaky-seam / contract-integrity issue with a measurable producer cost and a misleading test, but it causes no incorrect behavior or data exposure today — the live filter counts stay correct via the recompute path; only the header tiles/OutcomeBar/tab-count are static, which may be intended product behaviour. No ADR conflict (realtime via void/live, topic run:<runId> is preserved either way).

#20 · Realtime (void/live)
useRunProgress fuses the live transport, the changedTests→byId accumulator, and SSR seeding into one React hook — the reducer is only testable through a browser
medium severity effort: small confidence: high untestable
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/live-client.ts:42
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/live-client.ts:64
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/live-client.ts:82
  • packages/e2e/tests-dashboard/realtime.spec.ts:88
Problem — the friction

The merge semantics that turn a stream of RunProgressEvents into the rendered test list — seed byId from initialTests, ignore events with cancelled/non-progress type, merge changedTests by id into the accumulator, skip the setById call when changedTests is empty, replace (not merge) the summary — are all written inline inside useRunProgress, interleaved with connectLiveStream, useEffect lifecycle, useState, and the deliberate [runId]-only dependency that freezes the seed at mount. None of that accumulation logic can be exercised without React plus a live WebSocket. The only coverage today is the e2e realtime.spec.ts, which boots a browser, opens a run over HTTP, navigates, and races a 500ms settle against the async topic subscribe. So the highest-churn behaviour in the subsystem (how a partial event mutates rendered state) is validated only by the slowest, flakiest test in the repo, and a maintainer changing merge rules (e.g. handling a deleted/skipped test, or last-writer-wins on retries) has no fast feedback.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract a pure reducer pair, mirroring the already-extracted producer-side buildChangedTests (ingest.ts:478): seedRunProgressState(initialTests, initialSummary) -> { byId, summary } and applyRunProgressEvent(state, event) -> state, where the reducer encodes the four real rules currently inline (ignore non-"progress" events, replace summary, no-op on empty changedTests, merge-by-id). useRunProgress becomes thin glue: seed once at mount, subscribe, and on each event setState(prev => applyRunProgressEvent(prev, event)). Test the reducer as a plain function (no React, no happy-dom hook rendering — sidestepping the documented "Invalid hook call" fragility in vite.config.ts:50-56), exactly as build-changed-tests.test.ts tests its producer counterpart. Lead with testability/symmetry as the justification; the second-subscriber reuse (live.ts:62) is a secondary, future benefit rather than the primary case.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers (the hook, and any future list-view or status-page subscriber) get one canonical merge function instead of re-deriving 'merge changedTests by id, replace summary' at every subscription site. Locality: every rule about how an event mutates rendered state lives in one file; a bug in merge ordering or empty-batch handling changes one function, not a hook embedded in a component tree.

Deletion test

Deleting the reducer makes the accumulation complexity reappear: it would have to be re-inlined into useRunProgress today, and into any second subscriber (a planned team-wide live overview / status page is already noted in live.ts:62 as a future topic). The merge rule is genuinely load-bearing logic, not a pass-through — it earns its keep across at least the hook plus the next subscriber.

Testability impact

The full accumulator becomes unit-testable through its interface in milliseconds: seed-then-event ordering, empty-changedTests no-op, summary replacement, out-of-order events, duplicate-id overwrite, and the never-overwrite-live-with-stale-SSR rule all become table tests. The e2e spec can shrink to a single smoke test that the WebSocket actually delivers an event, rather than being the sole guardian of merge correctness.

Interface sketch
type RunProgressState = { byId: Record<string, RunProgressTest>; summary: RunProgressSummary | null }; function seedRunProgressState(initialTests?, initialSummary?): RunProgressState; function applyRunProgressEvent(prev: RunProgressState, event: RunProgressEvent): RunProgressState; // pure; merges changedTests by id, replaces summary
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited code; the finding is accurate.

live-client.ts:42-102 — useRunProgress inlines the entire accumulator contract: seed byId from initialTests frozen at mount via the deliberate [runId]-only useMemo dep (48-57, with an eslint-disable on exhaustive-deps), ignore non-"progress" events (78), replace (not merge) summary (80), skip setById when changedTests is empty (81), and merge changedTests by id into a cloned accumulator (82-88) — all interleaved with connectLiveStream, an async subscribe, the cancelled/unsubscribe teardown, and useState. None of the merge logic is reachable without React + a live WebSocket.

realtime.spec.ts:88-159 is the only coverage. It boots a browser, opens a run over HTTP, navigates, waits on the /live response, then races a hard waitForTimeout(500) against the async topic subscribe. The in-file comment (96-100) admits a progress event published before the subscribe lands is silently dropped (no replay) — so this is genuinely the slowest and most timing-fragile test exercising the highest-churn behaviour in the subsystem.

Two pieces of evidence STRENGTHEN the finding beyond what the finder claimed:
1. The producer-side counterpart is ALREADY extracted as a pure function: buildChangedTests in src/lib/ingest.ts:478, with its own pure unit test src/__tests__/build-changed-tests.test.ts. So the proposed applyRunProgressEvent/seedRunProgressState mirrors an existing, blessed convention in this exact subsystem — the consumer-side merge is the missing half of a pattern the team already uses.
2. apps/dashboard/vite.config.ts:50-56 documents that the React + void worker test environment has produced "Invalid hook call" failures (worklog 2026-05-23), and isTest mode strips voidReact() (57-59). happy-dom + @testing-library/react are installed, but hook-level testing here is exactly the fragile path the config warns about. That makes a pure reducer (zero React/network deps) the correct target — more robust than trying to test the hook directly.

Deletion test passes: deleting the reducer re-inlines the merge rules into useRunProgress, and live.ts:59-64 explicitly anticipates a second subscriber (status pages / team-wide live overviews) that would re-implement the same accumulator. Callers found: one real present caller (src/components/run-progress.tsx:67, which only consumes byId — confirming the merge semantics, not the rendering, is the load-bearing logic) plus the documented future subscriber.

Scope-honesty caveat: there is exactly ONE consumer today, so the "earns its keep across N callers" framing leans on the planned second subscriber. The stronger present-tense justification is testability + symmetry with the already-extracted producer pure function, not multi-caller reuse. The finding's primary category (untestable) is correct; I'd lean on that rather than the reuse argument.

No ADR conflict. The realtime-via-void/live decision (#5) and isomorphic-pages decision (#6) are untouched — extracting a pure reducer leaves the transport, topic, and "use client" boundary exactly as is. Severity medium is right: real fast-feedback gap on churny logic, but a single small low-risk extraction, currently behind one consumer.

#21 · Realtime (void/live)
broadcastRunUpdate is a one-line payload assembler over publishRunUpdate; the two-wrapper stack is cosmetic, not a real seam
low severity effort: small confidence: high pass-through revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:103
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:503
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:508
Problem — the friction

There are two wrappers in the publish path that each add almost nothing. publishRunUpdate (live.ts:103) does await live.publish('run:'+runId, event, { type: 'progress' }) — its only behaviour is the topic-string format and the redundant { type: 'progress' } metadata (the event object already carries type: 'progress'). broadcastRunUpdate (ingest.ts:503) does await publishRunUpdate(runId, { type: 'progress', changedTests, summary }) — its only behaviour is assembling the event literal. So the actual contract — 'topic is run:<runId>, event is a RunProgressEvent with type progress' — is split across two files and stated three times (the literal in broadcastRunUpdate, the type field, and the publish metadata). A maintainer adding a topic field or a second event variant has to touch both wrappers and keep the duplicated type: 'progress' in sync.

Solution — the deepened module

Leave as-is or, at most, inline broadcastRunUpdate's assembly into publishRunUpdate so the realtime publish path is a single function (publishRunProgress(runId, changedTests, summary)) that lives in live.ts NEXT TO the topic taxonomy comment and RunProgressEvent type. Do NOT collapse the other direction (folding publishRunUpdate into ingest.ts) — that moves the void-specific topic-format + SSE-event-type convention away from its documented home in live.ts and worsens locality of the realtime concern. Critically, do not "dedupe" the two type: 'progress' occurrences as the original finding implies: they are different wire fields (the publish-options arg sets the SSE event-type the client filters on at live-client.ts:78; the payload arg is the typed RunProgressEvent discriminant). Both must stay.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: ingest callers (openRun, appendRunResults, completeRun) get one entry point that can't be called with a mismatched type/topic. Locality: the topic format and event envelope — currently smeared across live.ts and ingest.ts with a duplicated literal — live in one function adjacent to the wire type they implement.

Deletion test

Deleting broadcastRunUpdate: complexity vanishes (it is pure assembly over publishRunUpdate) — classic pass-through, should be collapsed. Deleting publishRunUpdate and folding into ingest: the topic-format knowledge would then live in ingest, fine. Either single wrapper earns its keep across the 3 ingest callers (openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun); keeping both does not.

Testability impact

Minor but real: one wrapper means one place to assert the topic string and envelope shape (e.g. that completeRun broadcasts type:'progress' to run:<id>), instead of two layers where the canary contract test has to thread through both.

Interface sketch
async function publishRunProgress(runId: string, snapshot: { changedTests: RunProgressTest[]; summary: RunAggregateSummary }): Promise<void>; // owns topic 'run:'+runId and { type:'progress', ... } envelope, single source
Verifier notes

The two wrappers exist as described, but the finding's central justification is factually wrong, which collapses its severity.

VERIFIED STRUCTURE:
- live.ts:103 publishRunUpdate(runId, event) → await live.publish('run:'+runId, event, { type: 'progress' }).
- ingest.ts:503 broadcastRunUpdate(runId, changedTests, summary) → await publishRunUpdate(runId, { type: 'progress', changedTests, summary }).
- Callers: broadcastRunUpdate has 4 call sites, ALL in ingest.ts (637 openRun, 699 appendRunResults, 804 completeRun, 847 finalizeStaleRun — the finder missed finalizeStaleRun, so it's 4 not 3). publishRunUpdate has exactly ONE caller: broadcastRunUpdate. No other callers anywhere (grep confirmed).

THE FINDING'S KEY CLAIM IS FALSE. The finder says the third arg { type: 'progress' } to live.publish is "redundant... the event object already carries type: 'progress'". It is NOT redundant. I checked void's LivePublishOptions (type?: string; eventId?) and the live client. live.publish(topic, data, { type }) sets the SSE event: field, which is DISTINCT from the data payload's type field. The dashboard client (src/lib/live-client.ts:76-79) reads them separately: event.type is the SSE event name and is LOAD-BEARING — line 78 does if (event.type !== "progress") return; to filter the channel — while event.data is the RunProgressEvent payload, and the client never reads data.type at all (it only consumes data.summary and data.changedTests, lines 80-88). So the two type: 'progress' occurrences are NOT a duplicated value smeared across files that must be hand-synced; they are two different wire-protocol fields (SSE event-type selector vs. typed payload discriminant). The finder conflated them.

DELETION TEST:
- publishRunUpdate (the genuinely thin one): exactly one caller. Folding it into ingest would NOT concentrate anything smeared across N callers (N=1). It would MOVE the void-specific publish convention (topic-string format run:<runId> + SSE event-type option) OUT of live.ts — where the topic taxonomy is deliberately documented (live.ts:10-12 "Topic taxonomy: run:<runId>") right next to defineLiveStream and the RunProgressEvent type — and INTO ingest.ts. That worsens locality for the realtime concern. Fails the deletion test (moves, not concentrates).
- broadcastRunUpdate: 4 same-file callers. Deleting it makes the { type: 'progress', changedTests, summary } literal reappear 4× in one file. Weak/real concentration of the payload-assembly literal, but trivially small and all co-located.

CONCLUSION: This is a low-value cosmetic observation, not a deepening opportunity. The publish path is already reasonably factored: live.ts owns the topic taxonomy + SSE-event convention (correct home), ingest.ts owns payload assembly. The proposed collapse would degrade the locality the ADR-documented topic taxonomy currently has. No ADR conflict, but it brushes against decision #5 (realtime topic taxonomy lives with the void/live stream definition).

I'd revise to a much narrower observation if kept at all, and even then it's borderline drop.

#23 · Realtime (void/live)
The sole realtime tenant-isolation gate (onSubscribe runs⋈memberships check) is inlined in the defineLiveStream literal, so the isolation decision can't be unit-tested without a void/live handshake + real D1
low severity effort: small confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:31
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:37
  • apps/dashboard/src/live.ts:40
Problem — the friction

Subscribing to run:<runId> is gated by a per-topic membership check: parse the topic, resolve the user from ctx.user, and run a runs⋈memberships join filtered by the run's teamId and the caller's userId, returning 403 on no match. This is the realtime equivalent of the AuthorizedProjectId scope rule — it is the single thing standing between a logged-in user of team A and the live test stream of team B's run. It is written as an inline async closure inside the defineLiveStream literal, so it can only execute inside a real void/live handshake against a real D1. There is no unit coverage of: the topic regex (does run:abc:def or run: get rejected?), the no-user 403, the empty-rows 403, or the cross-team denial. Given tenant isolation here is logical and type-enforced everywhere else, having the realtime gate be the one isolation check with zero isolatable test is a blast-radius risk.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract the authorization decision into a pure-ish, injectable function colocated with the other authz helpers (src/lib/authz.ts), e.g. authorizeTopicSubscription(userId: string | null, topic: string, runner = db): Promise<{ ok: true } | { ok: false; status: 403 }>. It owns: the topic regex parse, the null-user reject, the runs⋈memberships scope query, and the empty-rows reject. Accepting the query runner as a parameter (defaulting to db from void/db) is the load-bearing part — it lets a unit test pass a fake/seeded runner and assert the regex cases and the cross-team 403 with no void/live handshake and no real D1. onSubscribe then becomes a thin adapter: read ctx.user, call authorizeTopicSubscription, translate { ok:false } to new Response("Forbidden", { status }) and { ok:true } to undefined. This earns its keep today purely on testability of the single realtime isolation gate; the per-topic dedup is a bonus only if/when a second topic type actually ships.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the realtime gate reuses the same membership-resolution shape as the rest of authz instead of hand-rolling the join inline, so a change to the membership model updates one place. Locality: the topic taxonomy (today only run:<id>; live.ts:62 anticipates team-wide topics) and its auth rules concentrate in one function — adding a team:<id> topic means extending one switch, not editing the stream literal.

Deletion test

Deleting this function would force the join + topic parse back inline into onSubscribe (one caller today) — but the moment a second topic type is added (anticipated), the parse/authorize logic would be duplicated per topic. It concentrates the realtime isolation rule that would otherwise smear across topic handlers; it earns its keep as the topic taxonomy grows.

Testability impact

The cross-team denial, no-membership 403, no-user 403, and topic-regex edge cases become unit-testable with a stub/seeded query runner — the same real-DB harness gap noted as known-outstanding, but the parse/branch logic is testable even with a fake runner. Right now this isolation gate is only reachable via a full live handshake.

Interface sketch
async function authorizeTopicSubscription(userId: string, topic: string, db): Promise<{ ok: true } | { ok: false; status: 403 }>; // onSubscribe: const u = ctx.user; if (!u) return 403; const r = await authorizeTopicSubscription(u.id, ctx.topic, db); return r.ok ? undefined : new Response('Forbidden', { status: r.status });
Verifier notes

Cited code verified exactly. live.ts:31-58 — onSubscribe is an inline async closure inside the defineLiveStream({...}) literal. :35-36 reads ctx.user, returns 403 when null. :37 parses topic via /^run:([^:]+)$/. :40-51 runs the runs⋈memberships innerJoin (eq(memberships.teamId, runs.teamId) AND eq(memberships.userId, user.id), where eq(runs.id, runId), limit 1). :52-54 returns 403 on empty rows; :57 returns 403 for any non-run topic.

CLAIM 1 (only tenant-isolation gate) — TRUE. routes/live.ts is pure pass-through: GET=live.connect(c), POST=live.control(c), no auth of its own. identifyConnection (:27-30) only tags user:<id> from the session — that's authentication, not tenant authorization. The runs⋈memberships join in onSubscribe is the sole check that a logged-in user of team A can't subscribe to team B's run:<runId>. It is the realtime analogue of the AuthorizedProjectId scope rule (durable decision #2) and is the one isolation check NOT routed through scope.ts/authz.ts.

CLAIM 2 (zero isolatable test) — TRUE. The only grep hit in __tests__ (group-tests-by-file.test.ts) is a false positive: it imports the RunProgressTest *type* from live-client.ts; it does not touch the stream. No test exercises onSubscribe, the regex, the no-user/empty-rows 403s, or cross-team denial. The closure can only run inside a real void/live handshake against a real D1 — and the real-DB harness is a known-outstanding gap, so this code is effectively untestable today.

DELETION TEST — finder's framing is the weak half and I set deletionTestPasses=false. There is exactly ONE topic type today (run:<runId>); the taxonomy doc comment lists only run:, and live.publish is called from exactly one site (live.ts:107). The "second topic type anticipated" is speculation seeded by the maxSubscriptionsPerTopic comment ("status pages, team-wide live overviews"), not committed work. At N=1 caller, extraction MOVES the authorize+parse out of the literal rather than CONCENTRATING logic smeared across N callers — so it fails the strict deletion test as the finder stated it.

WHY KEEP ANYWAY — the category is 'untestable', and that holds independent of the deletion test. The value of the seam is making the isolation DECISION unit-testable (regex rejection of run:abc:def / run:, no-user 403, empty-rows 403, cross-team denial) without a void/live handshake. That is a real, current friction on the single logical-tenant-isolation gate that has no DO boundary behind it — a genuine blast-radius concern. So isReal=true, but I downgrade severity to low (single inline check, one caller, modest code) and revise the title/solution to stop leaning on the hypothetical second topic and to make the seam actually unit-testable via an injected query runner.

No ADR conflict: extraction keeps the runs⋈memberships logical-isolation query intact and merely co-locates it with the other authz helpers; it does not touch single-D1, DO boundaries, or scope branding.

Artifacts · 6 findings

#24 · Artifacts
Artifact write pipeline (register + upload) is inlined in handlers, breaking the ingest.ts deep-module precedent the runs/* handlers follow
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high shallow module revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:51
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts:16
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts:22
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts
Problem — the friction

CLAUDE.md states 'Ingest is a deep module' — route handlers under runs/* are auth+translation only, with the real pipeline behind openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun in ingest.ts. The artifact half of that same ingest contract does NOT follow this pattern. register.ts inlines the entire reserve-row + idempotency-lookup + presign-URL logic (140 lines of DB orchestration in the handler), upload.ts inlines the scope re-verify + size-check + R2 put, and download.ts inlines token-verify + R2 get + range/304 handling. There is no registerArtifacts(scope, payload) / storeArtifactUpload(scope, id, body, len) equivalent to the run pipeline. A maintainer reasoning about 'the artifact lifecycle' has to read three route files and reconstruct the state machine (row exists => promise to upload; failed PUT => orphan 404) from scattered comments. The asymmetry with the run ingest pipeline is itself friction — the codebase teaches one pattern then breaks it for artifacts.

Solution — the deepened module

Mirror ingest.ts with an artifacts.ts lib module owning the WRITE pipeline: registerArtifacts(scope, payload): Promise<{ uploads }> (absorbing safeKeySegment, artifactIdentity, the owner-run + valid-testResultId verification, the idempotency-by-identity lookup, and the chunked batch insert) and storeArtifactUpload(scope, artifactId, body, contentLength): Promise<Result> (the project-scoped row lookup + size-match check + R2 put). register.ts and upload.ts then shrink to auth+translate like runs/*. Document the orphan-row invariant ("registration == promise to upload; failed PUT => 404") once at the module seam. Do NOT fold download.ts into this module — its concern (token verify + R2 range/304/CORS streaming) already has its deep seam in artifact-tokens.ts; at most extract a small resolveArtifactDownload(token) helper there if the streaming/header logic is duplicated elsewhere (it is not currently, so this is optional). The load-bearing extraction is the register/upload write pair (N=2).

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: handlers become 10-line auth+JSON shims; the artifact lifecycle is one importable surface. Locality: the 'row == promise to upload, failed PUT == orphan' state machine and the idempotency reuse rule live in one module instead of being inferred from three handlers. Consistency with the already-deep run ingest module.

Deletion test

Collapsing the proposed module back into handlers is exactly today's state — so the test is whether the run-ingest precedent justifies the extraction. It does: the same verify-ownership => batch => return-keys shape is duplicated between register.ts and the run handlers, and the scope re-verify appears in both upload.ts and download-adjacent paths. N=3 artifact handlers would each shrink. Earning its keep as a consistency-restoring deepening.

Testability impact

registerArtifacts (idempotent re-registration, unknown-testResultId rejection, oversize 413, chunking >99 params) becomes unit-testable against a fake DB exactly like the run pipeline aspires to — today it is only reachable through the full HTTP handler + auth middleware + live D1.

Interface sketch
registerArtifacts(scope, payload): Promise<{ uploads: Upload[] }> storeArtifactUpload(scope, artifactId, body, contentLength): Promise<UploadResult> resolveArtifactDownload(token): Promise<{ r2Key; contentType } | null>
Verifier notes

The core asymmetry is real and verifiable. Run handlers are genuinely thin auth+translate shells delegating to ingest.ts: routes/api/runs/[id]/results.ts is 26 lines, complete.ts 33, index.ts 40 — each calls appendRunResults/completeRun/openRun. CLAUDE.md explicitly states "Ingest is a deep module" and that runs/* handlers are "auth + translation only." The artifact half breaks this: register.ts is 193 lines with the full pipeline inlined — safeKeySegment + artifactIdentity helpers, the size-limit precheck, owner-run lookup, chunked validId verification, the existingByIdentity idempotency map, and the chunked db.batch insert all live in the handler. There is no registerArtifacts()/storeArtifactUpload() equivalent. The orphan-row state machine ("Rows go in eagerly — existence == promise to upload. A failed PUT leaves an orphan row whose download endpoint will 404") is documented only in a scattered handler comment. So the friction (consistency-breaking, maintainer must reconstruct the lifecycle from route files) is genuine.

Two factual corrections that the finder got wrong:
1. The claim "scope re-verify appears in both upload.ts AND download-adjacent paths" is incorrect. download.ts (verified: routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts) does NOT re-verify scope against the DB at all — it is token-only via verifyArtifactToken and explicitly "skips the DB on the hot path." The project-scoped artifacts lookup (eq(artifacts.projectId, scope.projectId)) appears in exactly TWO handlers: register.ts and upload.ts — confirmed by grep. So N=2, not the claimed N=3.
2. download.ts is a different concern (HMAC token verify + R2 range/304/CORS streaming) and shares almost nothing with register/upload. Its real sibling is the ALREADY-deep artifact-tokens.ts module (signArtifactToken/verifyArtifactToken), with token minting living in src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts and the test-detail page loader (pages/.../tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:153). Folding download under the same registerArtifacts module is weaker than the finding implies; the token half is already well-factored.

Deletion test passes for the WRITE half: extracting registerArtifacts(scope, payload) + storeArtifactUpload(scope, id, body, len) concentrates the verify-ownership -> project-scope-filter -> idempotency-by-identity -> batch logic that is genuinely shared/duplicated across register.ts and upload.ts (the artifact lookup, the orphan-row invariant). It's not a hypothetical one-adapter seam — it mirrors the existing, proven ingest.ts precedent. No ADR conflict; this is a pure consistency-restoring factoring move.

Revising rather than keeping because the title/solution overstate N (3 vs real 2) and miscast download.ts. Severity medium is fair: it's a real navigability/consistency cost, not a correctness bug.

#25 · Artifacts
Download-URL shape is re-derived at four dashboard sites and the e2e suite hand-clones the signing algorithm (with a latent secret divergence)
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts:43
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts:68
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:153
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:34
Problem — the friction

verifyArtifactToken is a clean deep seam, but the MINT side is invoked ad-hoc and the resulting URL is string-built in multiple places. The /api/artifacts/:id/download?t=<token> URL literal appears in test-artifact-actions.ts:43 (trace viewer wrapper), :68 (downloadHref), and is assumed by the e2e suite. Two loaders (test-detail index.server.ts:153 and run-detail via loadFailingArtifactActions) each loop rows, call signArtifactToken with the same { r2Key, contentType } projection, and pair it with the same URL shape. Worst: packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:34 reimplements the entire base64url + HMAC-SHA256 signing algorithm by hand (explicitly 'Mirrors apps/dashboard/src/lib/artifact-tokens.ts'), so a change to the token body shape (add an aud, switch field order) silently breaks e2e with no compile-time link. The signing function knows the token body; nobody owns the download URL that wraps it.

Solution — the deepened module

Two seams, ranked by value.

(1) Dashboard URL concentration (do this): add signedDownloadHref(artifactId, token): string and signedDownloadUrl(origin, artifactId, token): string (or a mint+wrap pair signedDownloadHref(artifactId, { r2Key, contentType }, ttl?): Promise<string>) alongside artifact-tokens.ts, owning the /api/artifacts/:id/download?t=${encodeURIComponent(token)} literal and the trace.playwright.dev wrap. Route all FOUR current literal sites through it: test-artifact-actions.ts:43/68 AND the test-detail page's own copies at index.tsx:99/185 (the page should consume the lib helper instead of re-declaring traceViewerUrl/downloadHref). Loaders keep mapping rows through toArtifactAction.

(2) e2e divergence (do this differently than the finder framed it): don't promise a shared crypto core. Instead share the token-body contract + secret-selection: expose the body shape ({ r2Key, contentType, exp }) and the ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? BETTER_AUTH_SECRET rule as a single tiny module both sides reference, and make dashboard-fixture inject whichever secret the dashboard will actually use. Minimum viable fix: a contract.test-style canary (like the existing reporter↔dashboard Zod canary) that round-trips the e2e-minted token through the real verifyArtifactToken so any body-shape or secret change fails CI at the seam instead of silently in e2e.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get a ready download URL from one function; they never know the route shape or the token body. Locality: a token-body or route change is one edit; the e2e mirror stops being a hand-maintained copy that drifts. The 'token carries the key, URL carries the token' contract lives in one place.

Deletion test

Deleting the helper makes the URL literal and the sign+pair loop reappear in test-artifact-actions and both loaders (N=3 mint sites), and the e2e copy stays orphaned. Earning its keep — concentrates the URL/token pairing currently smeared across loaders and a cross-package clone.

Testability impact

The full mint->URL->verify round-trip (sign, embed in URL, extract t, verify) becomes one pure test with no DB. Today only the raw sign/verify is tested (artifact-tokens.test.ts); the URL assembly and the loaders' pairing are untested, and the e2e clone is verified only by a live HTTP 200.

Interface sketch
signedDownloadHref(artifactId, payload, ttl?): Promise<string> // path + ?t=token signedTraceViewerUrl(origin, artifactId, payload, ttl?): Promise<string>
Verifier notes

Confirmed against the files. The friction is real and the finding actually UNDERSTATES it.

URL-literal sites (the /api/artifacts/:id/download?t= shape):
- test-artifact-actions.ts:43 (server traceViewerUrl) and :68 (server toArtifactAction/downloadHref) — as cited.
- PLUS index.tsx:99 and index.tsx:185 — the test-detail PAGE re-implements both traceViewerUrl (byte-identical to the lib copy) and downloadHref client-side, consuming artifactTokens from the loader. The finder missed these two; that makes 4 dashboard URL-literal sites, not 3.
- e2e.test.ts:273 assumes the same shape.

Mint/sign sites: index.server.ts:153 and test-artifact-actions.ts:156 both call signArtifactToken({ r2Key, contentType }) over a row loop — confirmed, identical projection.

Strongest evidence the finder did not cite: a real LATENT divergence between the canonical signer and the e2e clone. artifact-tokens.ts:50 keys the HMAC on env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET (env.ts:25 declares ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET as optional, rotatable independently). e2e.test.ts:44 signs with BETTER_AUTH_SECRET only, and dashboard-fixture.ts:206 only injects BETTER_AUTH_SECRET. So today the tokens match by accident; the day ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is provisioned, the hand-cloned e2e token silently fails verifyArtifactToken with zero compile-time link. That is exactly the silent-divergence the finding warns about.

DELETION TEST (dashboard helper): deleting a signedDownloadHref/signedDownloadUrl helper makes the URL literal reappear at 4 sites (test-artifact-actions.ts:43/68, index.tsx:99/185) and the sign+pair loop at 2 loaders. Complexity is genuinely smeared across callers (the URL-shape contract is shared knowledge), so the helper concentrates it — passes. verifyArtifactToken is already a clean deep seam; only the MINT+URL-wrap side is unowned.

CAVEAT on the proposed e2e solution: "export the signing core so e2e imports it" is not drop-in. The canonical signer is WebCrypto (crypto.subtle.sign, async, btoa) running in workerd; the e2e clone is Node (createHmac, sync, Buffer) running in the Vitest globalSetup harness. A shared async/WebCrypto core may not import cleanly into the Node e2e context, and the e2e suite forges tokens by design (it deliberately doesn't scrape rendered HTML). The realistic e2e fix is to share the token-BODY shape + secret-selection rule (a single small module both sides agree on), not necessarily the crypto primitive. The dashboard-side concentration is the high-value part.

No ADR conflict. verifyArtifactToken/signArtifactToken depth and the token-carries-r2Key design are untouched by this proposal.

#26 · Artifacts
"Presigned R2 URL" is fiction — the documented interface lies about what register/download actually do
low severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:46
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:152
  • apps/dashboard/middleware/02.api-auth.ts:14
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts:37
Problem — the friction

CLAUDE.md and inline comments describe the flow as 'returns presigned upload URLs' and 'a presigned R2 GET URL', and middleware/02.api-auth.ts:14 labels register as 'reserve + presign'. There is no presign anywhere: register.ts:152 returns a RELATIVE /api/artifacts/:id/upload path, the upload streams the body THROUGH the worker via storage.put (upload.ts:62), and downloads stream THROUGH the worker gated by an HMAC token (not an S3-style R2 presigned URL). The interface description (everything a caller must know) is wrong about the most load-bearing fact: bytes traverse the worker, so the worker is on the data path for every artifact GET/PUT — which has real cost/latency implications (egress, CPU time, request size limits) that 'presigned URL' would imply are offloaded to R2. A maintainer or AI reading the docs will plan capacity and reason about failure modes against a presign model that does not exist.

Solution — the deepened module

Vocabulary/interface-truth fix, not a code-shape change.
