Rename the seam in docs and comments to what it actually is: "worker-proxied upload route" (register/upload) and "HMAC-signed download token" (download), aligning to the already-accurate doc-comment in src/lib/artifact-tokens.ts. Touch all the live surfaces, not just the four cited: register.ts:46-47, upload.ts header, middleware/02.api-auth.ts:14 ("reserve + presign" -> "reserve + return worker upload URL"), test-artifact-actions.ts:37, CLAUDE.md:61, plus packages/reporter/README.md, packages/reporter/src/client.ts:197/203 and its test, docs/PRD.md, docs/ARCHITECTURE.md. Leave docs/worklog/* untouched (historical record). If taking the worker off the byte path via a real R2 presign is ever desired, that is a separate deliberate architectural change — but today the seam must be described honestly so capacity/failure-mode reasoning is correct.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers correctly understand the worker is on the data path (matters for the 50 MiB limit, CPU time, and the Content-Length==sizeBytes check that only works because the worker sees the bytes). Locality: future capacity/cost reasoning starts from the true model. Removes a trap where an AI 'optimizes' by assuming presign offload that isn't there.

Deletion test

N/A as an extraction — this is correcting a leaky/false interface description rather than adding a module. The friction is real: the false 'presign' term touches register, middleware, test-artifact-actions, and the project CLAUDE.md, so every reader is misled in N places.

Testability impact

Indirect — accurate naming prevents tests being written against the wrong model (e.g. assuming the worker is not in the byte path). The Content-Length==sizeBytes invariant in upload.ts:45 only makes sense once you know bytes proxy through the worker.

Verifier notes

Verified against the code — every claim holds.

- register.ts:46-47 doc comment: "Reserves a row per artifact + returns presigned upload URLs." register.ts:152 and :175 both emit uploadUrl: \/api/artifacts/${id}/upload\` — a RELATIVE worker path, not an S3/R2-presigned URL on an r2.cloudflarestorage.com host.
- upload.ts:56-64: const body = c.req.raw.body; ... await storage.put(row.r2Key, body, ...) — the PUT body streams THROUGH the worker into R2. Worker is on the byte path for every upload.
- download.ts:42-75: const object = await storage.get(r2Key, ...) then return new Response(object.body, ...) — GET bytes also stream THROUGH the worker, authorized by verifyArtifactToken (HMAC), not a presigned R2 GET URL. Confirmed HMAC in artifact-tokens.ts (crypto.subtle HMAC-SHA-256, sign/verify, base64url, exp check).
- middleware/02.api-auth.ts:14 labels register "(reserve + presign)".
- test-artifact-actions.ts:37 comment "wrapping a presigned R2 GET URL"; the URL it builds (line 43/68) is /api/artifacts/:id/download?t=<token> — a worker route with an HMAC token, not a presign.
- CLAUDE.md:61 (root) says "register + PUT artifacts ... + presigned R2 URLs."

The interface (everything a caller must know) is wrong about a load-bearing fact: bytes traverse the worker, so the worker sits on the data path for every artifact GET/PUT — a materially different cost/latency/capacity model (egress, CPU, request/response-size limits) than "presigned URL" implies. Capacity planning and failure-mode reasoning against a presign model would be wrong. So isReal=true.

Two corroborating signals the finder did not cite but which strengthen it: (1) artifact-tokens.ts:6-9 doc-comment is ALREADY accurate ("skip the DB on the hot path"), the correct alignment target as the finder says; (2) the reporter client.ts:201-204 effectively admits the truth — it attaches the Bearer token "only when the upload URL is on the same origin as the dashboard (i.e. the dashboard is proxying the upload)", which is the actual, only path today, while describing the presign case as hypothetical ("Presigned R2/S3 URLs ... live on a different host"). So the codebase author already half-knew this is worker-proxied; the docs just never caught up.

deletionTestPasses=false, but this is NOT a strike against the finding: this is a leaky-seam / interface-truth correction, not a module extraction. The finder explicitly marked the deletion test N/A. There is no module to delete and no smeared complexity to concentrate, so the concentration test simply doesn't apply — I set false to be honest, not as a refutation. The synthesizer should treat this as a documentation/vocabulary fix, not a deepening that earns leverage.

No ADR conflict. The finding does NOT propose taking the worker off the byte path (that would be a real architectural change); it only asks to describe the current seam honestly. Severity low is correct — no runtime defect, bounded impact.

Scope note for the fix: the false "presign" term appears in more live surfaces than the four cited files. grep -rni presign` shows it also in packages/reporter/README.md, packages/reporter/src/client.ts (lines 197/203) + its test, docs/PRD.md, and docs/ARCHITECTURE.md. The docs/worklog/* hits (incl. 2026-04-16-e2e-presign-integration.md) are historical and should be left as-is per the worklog convention, but PRD.md, ARCHITECTURE.md, the reporter README, and the reporter client comments are live and carry the same misnomer.

#27 · Artifacts
Artifact idempotency invariant is implied by a lookup, not declared near the schema or enforced by a DB unique index
low severity effort: small confidence: high shallow module revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:34
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:142
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts:150
Problem — the friction

The artifact 'natural identity' for idempotent re-registration is [testResultId, type, name, attempt, role].join(' ') defined privately in register.ts:34 and used to dedupe both across-request (retried flush) and within-request. This tuple IS the uniqueness contract for artifacts, but it is expressed only as an ad-hoc space-joined string inside one handler — there is no DB unique index backing it and no shared declaration tying it to the ArtifactRequestSchema fields (schemas.ts:150) it is computed from. A space in a name could in principle collide identities; more importantly, the dedup rule is invisible to anyone reading the schema or the table, so a maintainer changing what makes an artifact unique (e.g. adding snapshotName to the key for visual diffs) has no signpost that register.ts encodes the rule. The within-request seeding of the map (register.ts:178) and the across-request lookup are two behaviours behind one undocumented tuple.

Solution — the deepened module

Drop the depth framing. The actionable improvement is to make the artifact uniqueness invariant explicit and enforced rather than implied by a lookup: (1) add a partial/unique index on (projectId, testResultId, type, name, attempt, role) to the artifacts table (new numbered migration) so the DB enforces idempotency and closes the lookup-before-insert race window, and (2) co-locate the identity-tuple definition with the artifacts table or ArtifactRequestSchema so a maintainer changing what makes an artifact unique (e.g. adding snapshotName for visual diffs) sees the contract where the fields are declared. Lifting artifactIdentity into a shared module is only worthwhile IF a second real consumer materializes (e.g. an artifact replace/dedup path); on its own it just relocates a one-line helper.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: any future consumer (a dedup sweep, an artifact-replace endpoint) shares the exact identity rule instead of reinventing the join. Locality: 'what makes two artifacts the same' is one named, documented function next to the schema that defines its fields.

Deletion test

Deleting the helper as-is would just re-inline the join (it is already local), so on its own this is borderline. It earns its place when paired with finding 2: the identity is needed both for the across-request reuse and the within-request seed (N=2 uses today) and would be needed by any replace/dedup path. The real value is making the implicit uniqueness contract explicit.

Testability impact

The dedup decision (same tuple => reuse id+r2Key; differing attempt/role => new row) becomes unit-testable as a pure function. Today it is only exercised through a full register handler round-trip against D1, and the space-delimiter collision edge case is untested.

Interface sketch
artifactIdentity(a: { testResultId; type; name; attempt; role }): string // the idempotency key; document delimiter safety
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited code. register.ts:34-42 defines artifactIdentity as [testResultId, type, name, attempt, role ?? ""].join(" "). It is used in exactly two places, BOTH inside register.ts: seeding the across-request lookup map (line 130) and the within-request use + re-seed (lines 143, 178). grep -rn artifactIdentity across apps/dashboard + packages returns nothing outside register.ts; existingByIdentity is likewise file-local. So N=2 and both callers live in the same function — there is no smeared-across-callers complexity to concentrate.

DELETION TEST FAILS: deleting the helper would re-inline the same join in two adjacent lines of one function. Complexity does NOT reappear across independent callers; it stays in one place either way. This is a private 1-line convenience helper, not a shallow pass-through module, and not a deep module earning leverage. The finder honestly concedes this ("borderline... already local") and only rescues it by pairing with a hypothetical "finding 2" artifact module or a future replace/dedup path — i.e. a hypothetical second consumer. That is a one-adapter/zero-real-second-consumer seam today, which is exactly the "moves complexity / adds hypothetical seam" failure mode.

The finding is MISCATEGORIZED as shallow-module. The real, verifiable kernel is a latent-invariant / robustness issue, not a depth issue:
- No DB unique index backs the tuple. The artifacts table (schema.ts:331-361) has only artifacts_testResultId_idx. Idempotency relies entirely on a lookup-before-insert with a race window (correctly noted by finder).
- The space delimiter CAN collide: type/role are enums and attempt is an int, but name is free text (z.string().min(1).max(MAX.NAME), schemas.ts:154). A name containing a space cannot itself flip the split because positional join is unambiguous given fixed field count — actually re-checking: join uses fixed 5 fields in fixed order, so a space inside name does NOT cause a parse ambiguity (there is no re-parse; the whole string is the key and is only ever compared, never split). The collision risk is therefore weaker than the finder implies — two DISTINCT tuples can only collide if a trailing/leading space in one field equals a different field boundary, which the fixed positional join makes nearly impossible. So the "space could collide" argument is largely overstated; the join is positional, not delimiter-parsed.
- One factual overstatement: the rule is NOT undocumented. register.ts:28-33 carries a clear docstring ("Natural identity of an artifact for idempotent re-registration..."). What's true is that this lives in the handler, not next to ArtifactRequestSchema (schemas.ts:150) or the table (schema.ts:331), so a maintainer reading the schema/table has no signpost. That locality point survives.

Separately noted (NOT this finding): the schema comment at schema.ts:345 claims R2 key convention artifacts/<artifactId>/<safe-filename>, but register.ts:158 builds t/<teamId>/p/<projectId>/runs/... — stale doc drift, out of scope here.

No ADR conflict. A partial unique index would be a fresh numbered migration (consistent with durable decision 8 since nothing has deployed) — does not reverse any settled decision.

Net: real but mislabeled and low-value as a deepening. The genuine improvement is enforcing/declaring the uniqueness invariant, which is robustness + locality, not module depth. Keep only in revised form.

#28 · Artifacts
R2 key construction (register) and its filename-reversal (download) encode the same trailing-segment convention in opposite directions with nothing tying them
low severity effort: small confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:22
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:158
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts:158
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/test-artifact-actions.ts:103
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:271
Problem — the friction

The R2 object key format t/<teamId>/p/<projectId>/runs/<runId>/<testResultId>/<artifactId>/<safeName> is built by string interpolation inline in register.ts:158, and the safeKeySegment sanitizer that shapes its trailing segment lives privately in register.ts:22. The download handler then independently reverses that format with r2Key.split('/').pop() (download.ts:158) to recover a filename for Content-Disposition. The convention — that the last path segment is a sanitized filename, and that team/project/run scope is encoded in the prefix — is known by reference in at least three places and re-derived by hand in the e2e suite. A maintainer who changes the key layout (e.g. to add a date partition for retention sweeps, which is a tracked concern) must edit the interpolation in register, re-audit the .split('/').pop() in download, and update the e2e mirror — with nothing forcing them to find all three. The format is also load-bearing for tenant scope yet is just a template literal.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce src/lib/artifact-key.ts owning the R2 key format as a single seam, with two mutually-inverse functions and safeKeySegment moved in as an implementation detail:
- artifactR2Key(scope, { runId, testResultId, artifactId, name }): string — the sole constructor, replacing register.ts:158.
- filenameFromKey(key): string — the sole reverse, replacing download.ts:158's .split("/").pop().
The pairing is the point: the invariant "the trailing segment is the sanitized download filename" lives in one module, and a colocated unit test (filenameFromKey(artifactR2Key(...)) === safeKeySegment(name)) makes the round-trip a guarded property so a future layout change cannot silently desync construct and reverse. Leave test-artifact-actions.ts untouched (it only passes r2Key through). The e2e regex assertion can optionally import the format but is fine left as a black-box wire check.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get a key from a typed function instead of memorizing a template; the download handler asks for a filename instead of knowing the path shape. Locality: a key-layout change (retention partitioning, sharding) is one edit in one file; the sanitizer and the filename-recovery are guaranteed to move together because they are the same module.

Deletion test

Deleting this module makes the complexity REAPPEAR: the interpolation comes back in register.ts, the .split('/').pop() filename logic comes back in download.ts (and would silently diverge from the format), and the e2e mirror stays hand-rolled. N=3 real callers (register, download, e2e) plus test-artifact-actions which selects r2Key. Earning its keep — a deepening that concentrates a currently-smeared convention.

Testability impact

The key format and filename round-trip (filenameFromKey(artifactR2Key(...)) === sanitized(name)) becomes a pure unit test with no DB or R2. Today the only coverage of the format is the live e2e path; the sanitizer's edge cases (path separators, control chars, length cap) are testable in isolation but the assembled key never is.

Interface sketch
artifactR2Key(scope: TenantScope, parts: { runId; testResultId; artifactId; name }): string filenameFromKey(key: string): string // invariant: trailing segment is the safe download filename
Verifier notes

Read all cited files. The friction is real but the caller count is overstated.

CONFIRMED:
- register.ts:158 builds the key by inline interpolation: t/${scope.teamId}/p/${scope.projectId}/runs/${payload.runId}/${a.testResultId}/${artifactId}/${safeKeySegment(a.name)}. This is the ONLY construction site in the codebase (grep confirms no other t/${...} / runs/${...} interpolation).
- safeKeySegment (register.ts:22) is private to register and shapes the trailing segment.
- download.ts:158 independently reverses the convention: r2Key.split("/").pop() ?? "artifact" to recover the Content-Disposition filename. I verified this reversal is NOT incidental: the artifact token (artifact-tokens.ts:11-16) carries only {r2Key, contentType, exp} — NOT the original name — and the download handler intentionally skips the DB ("skip the DB on the hot path"). So download genuinely has no other source for the filename and MUST rely on the "trailing segment == sanitized filename" invariant. A register-side layout change (e.g. appending a date partition for retention sweeps) would silently corrupt the served filename with no compile error and no test tying the two sites. This is the load-bearing coupling.

OVERSTATED:
- The finder claims "N=3 real callers (register, download, e2e) plus test-artifact-actions." Accurate count: TWO format-coupled sites (register constructs, download reverses) + ONE test mirror (e2e.test.ts:245-249 asserts the format via regex). test-artifact-actions.ts only SELECTs r2Key and passes it into signArtifactToken (lines 111, 157) — it never constructs or parses the key, so it is a pure pass-through, not coupled to the layout. The finder's own deletionTest text actually characterizes it correctly as "selects r2Key," but the headline N inflates it.

DELETION TEST: Passes, modestly. Deleting a hypothetical artifact-key.ts returns the interpolation to register AND the .split().pop() to download, and re-frees them to diverge. This concentrates a genuine cross-file, opposite-direction invariant (construct vs. reverse) — more than a one-adapter hypothetical seam. But the smeared code is small (~3 lines each), so leverage is real but limited.

SECURITY ANGLE: The finding's claim that the format is "load-bearing for tenant scope" is technically true (teamId/projectId are in the prefix), but tenant isolation on download is actually enforced by the HMAC token, not by parsing the key — so consolidating the key builder does not change the security posture. Worth not overselling.

No ADR conflict. The consolidation is orthogonal to all durable decisions.

#29 · Artifacts
Range/206/304/Content-Range math in the artifact download handler is welded to the R2Object shape — extract a pure response builder so the protocol logic is unit-testable
low severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts:42
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts:54
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts:62
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/download.ts:135
Problem — the friction

Both handlers reach straight for storage from void/storage and call .get/.head/.put inline. The non-trivial logic — deriving Content-Range from object.range (download.ts:54-66), the hasBody/304 branch (download.ts:68), the conditional-request passthrough (onlyIf: c.req.raw.headers), and the immutable-cache + Content-Disposition header assembly (buildHeaders, download.ts:135) — is the part most likely to regress, and it is welded to the R2 object shape. There is no adapter, so none of this range/304/header math can be exercised without a real R2 binding (the known-outstanding 'real-DB/R2 test harness not built'). buildHeaders is a free function but takes a raw R2Object, so testing it still requires fabricating a Cloudflare R2Object with writeHttpMetadata/httpEtag.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract the regression-prone HTTP math into a pure, unit-testable function in src/lib and leave the handler as request -> storage -> pure builder. Concretely: define a plain read shape type ArtifactRead = { body: ReadableStream | null; size: number; etag: string; httpMetadata: Headers; range?: { offset: number; length?: number }; notModified: boolean } and a pure buildArtifactResponse(read, { tokenContentType, allowedOrigin, r2Key, method }): Response that owns: writeHttpMetadata-derived headers (passed in pre-written, so the pure fn never touches R2Object), safeContentType override, etag/content-length/immutable-cache/Content-Disposition assembly, Content-Range arithmetic, and the 304/206/200 status selection. Add a tiny adapter readArtifact(key, reqHeaders): Promise<ArtifactRead | null> over storage.get/head that maps the R2Object into ArtifactRead (this thin adapter remains the only part needing a live R2 binding). Co-locate buildArtifactResponse.test.ts in src/__tests__/ following the content-types.test.ts pattern — assert Content-Range strings, 304 on empty body, 206 vs 200, and header sanitisation against plain fixtures (no R2Object fabrication). This is a single-call-site testability extraction, not a multi-caller concentration; justify it on untestability of protocol math, not de-duplication.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the handler becomes request-to-Response plumbing; range/304/header correctness lives behind a stub-able interface. Locality: when Content-Disposition or cache rules change, they change in one pure function with table tests, not inside an R2-coupled handler. Two adapters (real R2 + in-memory fake) make this a real seam, not hypothetical.

Deletion test

Deleting the seam restores direct storage.* calls and inline range math in the handler (today's state). The range/304/header logic does not vanish — it reappears inline and untestable. The pure response builder earns its keep across the GET and HEAD branches (N=2 within the handler) plus any future range-supporting endpoint.

Testability impact

Range responses (206 + Content-Range), 304 from conditional requests, the immutable cache header, and the RFC-5987 Content-Disposition encoding (the header-injection defense at download.ts:159) all become unit-testable against an in-memory ArtifactRead fake. Today every one of these requires a live R2 object.

Interface sketch
getArtifactObject(key, reqHeaders): Promise<ArtifactRead | null> // {body,size,etag,range?,notModified} buildArtifactResponse(read, contentType, filename, corsOrigin): Response // pure: range/304/headers
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. The friction is real but the deletion-test framing is overstated.

CONFIRMED:
- storage from void/storage is called inline in exactly two files: download.ts (head r2Key @34, get with {range, onlyIf} @42) and upload.ts (put @62). grep confirms no storage usage anywhere else and no existing wrapper/seam in src/lib. register.ts does not touch storage.
- The regression-prone logic is welded to the R2 object shape: Content-Range derivation (download.ts:54-66 reads object.range offset/length/size), hasBody/304 branch (68-70), 206/200 status selection (72-75), and buildHeaders (135-172) which calls object.writeHttpMetadata(headers), object.httpEtag, object.size. buildHeaders is already a free function but typed object: R2Object, so unit-testing it today requires fabricating a Cloudflare R2Object with a working writeHttpMetadata — exactly the friction described. No live binding is installed (void package not in node_modules here) so none of this is exercised today.
- The codebase has a strong, demonstrated grain the finder's solution matches: pure logic extracted to src/lib with co-located unit tests (content-types.ts + content-types.test.ts, artifact-tokens, aggregate-delta, merge-run-status, safe-next-path). The download handler's range/header math is the conspicuous exception that escapes this pattern. Proposed buildArtifactResponse(plain shape) -> Response + a thin storage-read adapter fits the grain and is unit-testable.
- No ADR conflict. Does not touch single-D1, logical tenancy, Better Auth ownership, nuqs, ETL, or DO decisions.

OVERSTATED (reason for revise):
- The deletion test does NOT pass as literally defined. The claimed 'N=2 within the handler (GET and HEAD branches)' for the range/304 builder is wrong: the Content-Range/304/206 logic runs in the GET branch ONLY (lines 42-75). The HEAD branch (33-39) shares only buildHeaders, which is ALREADY a free function. So the range/304 complexity is single-call-site, not smeared across N callers — deleting the proposed seam restores inline logic in ONE handler; complexity does not reappear across multiple callers. This is testability extraction of one hot function (moving + exposing complexity for unit tests), not concentration of caller-smeared complexity. Legitimate under category=untestable, but it should be framed honestly as such, not as a multi-caller deepening.
- Severity adjusted medium -> low: single call site, contained logic, and the broader theme is already captured by the known-outstanding 'real-DB/R2 test harness not built'. The marginal win is making one regression-prone HTTP-math function unit-testable in the existing vitest pure-helper style.

Reporter package · 4 findings

#30 · Reporter package
Artifact register->correlate->PUT pipeline lives in private reporter methods with no isolated test surface for the positional-alignment invariant
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable
Files
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:351-391
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:393-422
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:424-471
  • packages/reporter/src/client.ts:172-262
Problem — the friction

The interesting behaviour of the artifact pipeline is not in StreamClient (which only exposes the two leaf primitives registerArtifacts and uploadArtifact) — it is in three private methods on WrightfulReporter: collectArtifacts (walk attachments, path-safety filter, snapshot promotion), fireArtifactUploads (correlate the flushed batch against the server's clientKey->testResultId mapping and build ArtifactRegistration[] + a parallel locals[] array), and uploadArtifactBatch (register, then a bounded-concurrency worker pool that PUTs each upload by positional index i into both uploads[] and locals[]). The load-bearing, easy-to-break invariant is that uploads[i] from the register response lines up positionally with locals[i] (index.ts:446-447); if the dashboard ever returns uploads in a different order or drops one, files silently upload to the wrong R2 key. None of this is reachable by a unit test — grep confirms no test references collectArtifacts/fireArtifactUploads/uploadArtifactBatch. The only way to exercise the positional alignment, the clientKey-miss skip (index.ts:404), or the concurrency worker is to construct a reporter, stub global fetch, and replay onBegin/onTestEnd/onEnd. A maintainer changing the register response shape has to mentally simulate the whole lifecycle to know whether artifacts still land correctly.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract an ArtifactUploader module that owns the batch->register->correlate->PUT pipeline behind a small interface, taking the StreamClient (or just its two primitives) plus a batch of {clientKey, artifacts} as input and returning {ok, failed} counts. The positional-alignment and clientKey-correlation logic moves behind a named function (e.g. correlateUploads(batch, mapping, registerResponse)) that is pure and directly testable. The reporter's fireArtifactUploads becomes a one-line delegate. The bounded-concurrency worker becomes a tested helper.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers (the reporter, and any future CLI re-upload tool) get the entire 'turn a finished batch into uploaded bytes' behaviour behind one call instead of re-implementing correlation and concurrency. Locality: the positional-alignment invariant, the clientKey-miss skip, and the concurrency bound all live in one module a maintainer opens when artifact upload misbehaves, instead of being smeared across three private methods and the batcher flush closure.

Deletion test

Deleting this module makes complexity reappear: the reporter's flush callback would have to re-inline correlation + concurrency, and any second artifact path (e.g. a backfill/retry tool) would duplicate it. It earns its keep across N=2 callers (the live reporter flush; a hypothetical re-upload/backfill utility) and concentrates the alignment invariant that is currently impossible to test in isolation.

Testability impact

Makes the clientKey->testResultId->uploads[i] correlation, the register-failure accounting, the clientKey-miss skip, and the bounded-concurrency fan-out unit-testable with a fake client — none of which is reachable today without stubbing global fetch and replaying the entire Playwright lifecycle. This is the single biggest gap in the package's test coverage.

Interface sketch
class ArtifactUploader { constructor(client: Pick<StreamClient,'registerArtifacts'|'uploadArtifact'>, concurrency=4) async upload(runId, batch: {clientKey,artifacts:PreparedArtifact[]}[], mapping): Promise<{ok:number,failed:number}> } // pure: correlateUploads(batch, mapping): {registrations, locals} — invariant: registrations[i] <-> locals[i]
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited spans. Confirmed:

- StreamClient (client.ts:172-262) exposes only the two leaf primitives registerArtifacts + uploadArtifact, and both ARE independently tested (client.test.ts:309-431). The interesting orchestration is NOT there.
- The orchestration lives in three private WrightfulReporter methods: collectArtifacts (index.ts:351-391, path-safety + snapshot promotion), fireArtifactUploads (393-422, builds registrations[] and locals[] in lockstep — line 417 pushes a for every registrations.push at 407), uploadArtifactBatch (424-471, register then bounded-concurrency worker pool).
- The load-bearing invariant is real and exactly as described: uploadArtifactBatch correlates by positional index i into uploads[i]/locals[i] (446-447). If the dashboard returns uploads reordered or short relative to the submitted registrations order, files PUT to the wrong R2 key with no error. The clientKey-miss skip is at 404-405. The concurrency pool is 441-470.
- grep confirms zero test references to collectArtifacts/fireArtifactUploads/uploadArtifactBatch.
- Critically, the only lifecycle test (reporter.test.ts:78-243) does NOT exercise this path: its fetch handlers never mock /api/artifacts/register (unmatched URLs fall through to a 200 {} → empty uploads[]), and the makeTest/makeResult fixtures default attachments:[] (fixtures.ts:52). So the positional-alignment invariant is genuinely unexercised anywhere in the suite.

Deletion test PASSES on the right basis: the value is not the caller count but concentrating an invariant that currently has NO isolated test surface. Extracting a pure correlateUploads(batch, mapping, registerResponse) pulls the alignment + clientKey-correlation logic out of an untestable private method into a directly-testable function; deleting that module would smear the invariant back into a method only reachable by replaying onBegin/onTestEnd/onEnd against a stubbed global fetch. That is genuine deepening, not a pass-through move.

Two corrections that justify dropping severity high→medium (not dropping the finding):
1. The finder's deletion test cites N=2 callers — but only ONE real caller exists (the batcher flush callback at index.ts:247). The "backfill/retry tool" is admitted-hypothetical, i.e. a one-adapter (hypothetical) seam, not a two-adapter real seam. The finding still stands because the testability argument carries it, but the multi-caller justification is overstated.
2. The title's "untestable" is slightly strong: the behavior IS reachable in principle through the existing lifecycle harness; it's the positional invariant that is awkward-to-impossible to assert through onTestEnd and is currently not asserted at all. "Has no isolated/pure test surface" is the accurate framing.

No ADR conflict — this is reporter-internal structuring and touches none of the durable Void/D1/tenancy decisions.

#31 · Reporter package
Retry/backoff loop is duplicated between fetchWithRetry and uploadArtifact instead of one retry policy
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • packages/reporter/src/client.ts:38-67
  • packages/reporter/src/client.ts:206-262
Problem — the friction

fetchWithRetry (client.ts:38) and uploadArtifact (client.ts:206) each independently implement the same policy: loop to maxRetries, retry on 5xx/429/network-throw but not 4xx, honour Retry-After, otherwise exponential backoff of 2^attempt*500ms. They differ only in incidentals (uploadArtifact re-opens the Blob per attempt because a consumed stream can't replay, uses a longer 120s timeout, and throws terminal HTTP errors outside the try so they can't be caught-and-retried). The shared rule 'what status is retryable and how long to wait' is written twice, so a change to the backoff curve or the retryable-status set must be made in two places and the differences re-justified each time. The two copies have already drifted subtly (uploadArtifact tracks lastError and re-throws it; fetchWithRetry throws a generic 'Retry exhausted').

Solution — the deepened module

Factor the policy into a retry helper that both call sites share: a withRetry(attemptFn, {maxRetries, timeoutMs, isRetryable, retryDelay}) where attemptFn produces a Response (or throws) and the helper owns the loop, the Retry-After parse, and the backoff. uploadArtifact supplies a per-attempt factory (re-open the Blob inside attemptFn) so the stream-replay concern stays local; the shared piece is purely the decide-and-wait logic.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: every call site gets one consistent retry behaviour; tuning the backoff or adding a retryable status is a one-line change. Locality: the 'what is retryable / how long to wait / honour Retry-After' rule lives once, with the two genuine differences (blob re-open, terminal-throw placement) expressed as parameters rather than re-implemented loops.

Deletion test

Deleting the shared helper makes the loop reappear at both call sites (it already does). It earns its keep across N=2 callers (the JSON API methods via fetchWithRetry, and uploadArtifact) and concentrates the retry policy that is presently duplicated and already drifting.

Testability impact

The retryable-status decision and backoff timing become testable once against the helper, rather than re-asserted via separate fake-timer suites for each method (client.test.ts has near-identical retry describes for openRun, completeRun, and uploadArtifact).

Interface sketch
async function withRetry(attempt: () => Promise<Response>, opts: { maxRetries; timeoutMs; isRetryable?(status): boolean }): Promise<Response> // owns: AbortSignal.timeout, Retry-After parse, 2^n*500 backoff, network-throw retry
Verifier notes

Verified against packages/reporter/src/client.ts. The duplication is real and matches the finding precisely.

fetchWithRetry (lines 38-67): loops attempt<=maxRetries; non-retryable predicate is response.ok || (response.status < 500 && response.status !== 429) (returns early); retryable path parses Retry-After header else Math.pow(2, attempt) * 500; catch path retries network throws with Math.pow(2, attempt) * 500; terminal throw is generic new Error("Retry exhausted") (line 66).

uploadArtifact (lines 206-262): identical loop shape and identical retryable rule — non-retryable case response.status < 500 && response.status !== 429 (lines 245-248), same Retry-After-else-2^attempt*500 backoff (lines 255-259), same network-throw catch with 2^attempt*500 (line 241). The differences are exactly the incidentals the finder named: (a) re-opens the Blob inside the loop via openAsBlob (line 228) because a consumed stream can't replay — comment at 199 confirms; (b) longer 120s timeout (ARTIFACT_PUT_TIMEOUT_MS, line 233) vs 30s default; (c) terminal HTTP errors thrown structurally outside the try so they can't be caught-and-retried (comment at 236-238 explicitly explains this); (d) tracks lastError and re-throws it (lines 224, 239-240, 261) where fetchWithRetry throws a generic error. The drift the finder claims (divergent terminal-error messages: "Retry exhausted" vs "artifact PUT: retry exhausted", plus the lastError divergence) is confirmed in the source.

Deletion test PASSES: the proposed withRetry(attemptFn, {maxRetries, timeoutMs, isRetryable, retryDelay}) would concentrate the decide-and-wait policy (retryable-status predicate + Retry-After parse + exponential backoff) that is presently written twice. The per-attempt factory localizes the genuinely-divergent Blob-replay concern. This concentrates rather than moves complexity.

Callers confirmed: fetchWithRetry serves four JSON methods (openRun L96, appendResults L120, completeRun L153, registerArtifacts L176); uploadArtifact is the second copy of the policy, called from src/index.ts:450 via uploadArtifactBatch. So the duplication is between fetchWithRetry (1 copy) and uploadArtifact (1 copy) — N=2 *copies of the policy*. The finder's deletionTest phrasing ("N=2 callers") is slightly loose: fetchWithRetry is already a shared helper for 4 call sites; the duplication is one second hand-rolled copy in uploadArtifact. The architectural insight is unaffected.

I also checked pr-comment.ts:130 (githubFetch) since it uses AbortSignal.timeout — it is NOT a third copy: it is a bare single fetch with a timeout, no retry loop, no Retry-After, no backoff. So the scope is genuinely just the two cited blocks.

No ADR conflict — this is purely internal reporter structure, touches none of the durable decisions. Severity correctly low: ~25 lines each, same file, protocol version stable (only v3 supported), and the observed drift is cosmetic (error message strings) rather than behavioral. Good low-risk consolidation.

#32 · Reporter package
The retries->done buffering Map (onTestEnd accumulation + onEnd fallback drain) is reporter instance state, so the buffer-until-final-retry lifecycle is only testable end-to-end via stubbed fetch
low severity effort: medium confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:325-349
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:143
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:156
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:598-604
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:647-697
Problem — the friction

buildPayload/mapOutcome are pure and tested, but the stateful half of the aggregation — accumulating TestResult[] per test in this.pending (a Map keyed by test.id), deciding when a test is done (isTestDone vs retry budget), deleting the entry on completion, the onEnd fallback flush of still-pending entries (index.ts:479-482), and the running this.counts tally used by the PR comment — is wired directly into onTestEnd/enqueueDone as mutations on the reporter instance. The actual rule 'buffer attempts until the final retry, then emit one row, aggregating retries into flaky' is split between the pure buildPayload and this scattered instance state. To test 'two failing attempts then a pass produces one flaky row and is removed from pending', you must drive onBegin/onTestEnd x3/onEnd against a stubbed fetch (as reporter.test.ts does) rather than asserting the accumulator directly.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract a small TestAccumulator that owns ONLY the buffer-until-final-retry state, reusing the already-pure isTestDone: record(test, result) pushes into a Map keyed by test.id and returns the completed {test, results} entry when isTestDone fires (else undefined); drainPending() yields the leftover entries for the onEnd fallback flush and clears the map. onTestEnd shrinks to const done = acc.record(test, result); if (done) this.artifactTasks.push(this.enqueueDone(done)); and onEnd to for (const e of acc.drainPending()) this.artifactTasks.push(this.enqueueDone(e)). Do NOT move counts() onto the accumulator: counts is derived from buildPayload(...).status and stays in enqueueDone, keeping the accumulator's {test,results} seam clean and upstream of payload building. This makes "two fails then a pass -> one done entry, removed from pending" a direct unit assertion against the accumulator with no stubbed fetch.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the reporter gets the whole 'when is a test done, and what's its aggregate' decision behind one object instead of open-coded Map juggling. Locality: the retries->flaky lifecycle and the pending-fallback rule live in one module a maintainer opens to reason about flaky detection, rather than reading three methods plus two private fields to reconstruct it.

Deletion test

Deleting the accumulator makes complexity reappear inside onTestEnd/onEnd (the Map, the done-check, the fallback drain, the counts). It earns its keep across N=2 call sites in the reporter (onTestEnd accumulation, onEnd fallback flush) and concentrates the buffer-until-final-retry rule that is currently smeared across instance state.

Testability impact

Makes the buffer/done/flaky-aggregation lifecycle and the onEnd fallback-flush unit-testable in isolation (record N attempts, assert done at the right retry, assert leftover drain) instead of only through a fetch-stubbed full-lifecycle test.

Interface sketch
class TestAccumulator { record(test: TestCase, result: TestResult): { done: boolean }; takeDone(): { test: TestCase; results: TestResult[] }[]; // since last call drainPending(): { test: TestCase; results: TestResult[] }[]; counts(): Record<Status, number>; }
Verifier notes

Verified against packages/reporter/src/index.ts and the tests.

CONFIRMED as described:
- this.pending is Map<string,PendingTest> keyed by makeTestKey -> test.id (index.ts:143, 593-596).
- onTestEnd does get-or-create / push / set / isTestDone-gate / delete / enqueue (index.ts:328-336).
- onEnd fallback drain over pending.values() then clear() (index.ts:479-482) — note the problem text cites 479-482 correctly, but the files[] list cited 598-604/647-697, which are isTestDone/buildPayload.
- this.counts[payload.status]++ in enqueueDone (index.ts:341), consumed only by the PR comment (index.ts:535-549).
- The stateful half is indeed tested only end-to-end: aggregation.test.ts unit-tests isTestDone and buildPayload as pure functions, while the accumulation/done/delete/counts loop is exercised only by reporter.test.ts driving onBegin/onTestEnd×N/onEnd against vi.stubGlobal("fetch") (reporter.test.ts:78-243). So the "two fails then a pass -> one flaky row + removed from pending" assertion can only be made via the full fetch-stubbed lifecycle today.

DELETION TEST: passes for the core of the proposal but is narrower than claimed. The genuinely-smeared, untested-in-isolation part is the buffering Map + the two-site drain (onTestEnd at 328-336 and the onEnd fallback at 479-482). Extracting record(test,result)->done? / takeDone / drainPending concentrates that and exposes a {test,results} seam that buildPayload already consumes — that is a real, clean concentration across N=2 sites. No ADR conflict (this is reporter-internal, touches none of the durable D1/tenancy/auth decisions).

WHERE THE FINDING OVERREACHES (why revise, not keep):
1. The deep half is ALREADY extracted. isTestDone (index.ts:598-604) is exported, pure, and directly unit-tested (aggregation.test.ts:5-53); buildPayload/mapOutcome likewise. Citing 598-604 and 647-697 in files[] frames the already-deep, already-tested functions as the friction. The actual friction is only the buffering Map + drain.
2. counts() does NOT belong on the accumulator. this.counts is tallied from buildPayload(...).status (downstream of mapOutcome), not from the accumulator's done-detection. Putting counts() on the accumulator forces it to run buildPayload/mapOutcome internally, coupling the upstream buffer to the downstream status mapping and muddying the very {test,results} seam the proposal is trying to keep clean. counts should stay where the final status is already computed.

Net: real but low-leverage. Medium overstates it — the high-leverage logic (done-detection, outcome mapping, payload construction) is already pure and tested; what's left to extract is a ~10-line buffer with a fallback drain. Worth doing for testability, but it is a small concentration, not a significant locality fix.

#33 · Reporter package
The v3 wire contract is two hand-maintained copies (reporter types.ts + dashboard schemas.ts) with no shared module — only a cross-package relative-import test holds them together
low severity effort: medium confidence: high duplication touches a durable decision
Files
  • packages/reporter/src/types.ts:1-127
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts:1-198
  • packages/reporter/src/__tests__/contract.test.ts:1-16
  • packages/reporter/package.json:30-36
Problem — the friction

TestResultPayload/TestAttemptPayload/OpenRunPayload/ArtifactRegistration/CompleteRunPayload exist as TypeScript interfaces in the reporter (types.ts) and again as Zod schemas in the dashboard (schemas.ts), maintained by hand. The CLAUDE.md prose literally says 'keep them in sync' — the contract is enforced by discipline plus one canary test that imports the dashboard's compiled Zod via a four-level relative path (../../../../apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.js, contract.test.ts:6). The reporter is a standalone publishable npm package with its own zod devDependency and no dependency on the dashboard, so the two definitions can drift in any field the canary happens not to assert (e.g. a new optional field, a widened enum, a nullable change). A maintainer changing the contract must edit two files in two packages and remember the relative-import test exists; an AI making the change has no single source-of-truth module to edit.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a small type-only shared contract package (packages/protocol) that exports ONLY the wire-shape Zod schemas as the single source of truth, with TS types via z.infer, plus the PROTOCOL_VERSION constant and X-Wrightful-Version header name. The reporter imports the inferred types type-only (zod stays dev/peer — no new runtime dep, package stays small for publish). The dashboard imports the same base schemas and LAYERS its server-only validation on top (truncatedText transforms, MAX caps, superRefine, isSafeContentType) — that security logic stays in apps/dashboard and is NOT pushed into the published package. This kills the four-level relative import in contract.test.ts and removes the version-literal duplication. If the cost of a third package outweighs the gain, a cheaper alternative that still closes the drift gap is to make the existing canary assert structural equivalence (e.g. derive an expected key set from the schemas and compare) and dedupe the version constant — but it leaves the two definitions hand-maintained.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: both the reporter and the dashboard consume one definition; adding a field is a one-file edit that propagates types to the reporter and validation to the dashboard automatically. Locality: the wire contract — fields, caps, enums, truncation rules, the visual-artifact superRefine, the version number — lives in one module that anyone touching the protocol opens, instead of being mirrored across a package boundary and reconciled by a fragile relative import.

Deletion test

Deleting the shared module makes the duplication reappear: you are back to two hand-kept copies plus the cross-package canary. It earns its keep across N=2 callers (reporter emit-side types; dashboard ingest-side validation) and concentrates the contract that is currently smeared across two packages.

Testability impact

The contract test becomes a normal in-package import instead of a brittle ../../../../ reach into the dashboard's source tree; drift becomes a compile error (reporter payload typed by z.infer of the same schema) rather than something only a runtime safeParse can catch. New protocol fields get type-checked on the emit side for free.

Interface sketch
// packages/protocol/src/index.ts export const PROTOCOL_VERSION = 3; export const TestResultSchema = z.object({...}); export type TestResultPayload = z.infer<typeof TestResultSchema>; // reporter: import type { TestResultPayload }; dashboard: import { TestResultSchema }
Durable-decision note

Touches durable decision 'Shared schema contract' (the deliberate choice to mirror types in both packages and rely on contract.test.ts). Worth reopening because the reporter is published independently and the relative-import canary is the only thing preventing silent drift — a shared package keeps the contract honest at compile time without coupling the reporter to the dashboard runtime.

Verifier notes

All cited facts verified against the files.

DUPLICATION CONFIRMED: packages/reporter/src/types.ts defines TestAttemptPayload, TestResultPayload, OpenRunPayload, AppendResultsPayload, CompleteRunPayload, ArtifactRegistration as TS interfaces (lines 7-96). apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts defines the same shapes as Zod (TestAttemptSchema, TestResultSchema, OpenRunPayloadSchema, AppendResultsPayloadSchema, CompleteRunPayloadSchema, RegisterArtifactsPayloadSchema). Both files carry explicit "keep in sync" comments (types.ts:1-3, schemas.ts:9-10) — the contract is enforced by discipline.

CANARY CONFIRMED: contract.test.ts:7 imports via ../../../../apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.js (four-level cross-package relative path). The test only asserts positive parse-success on a few reporter-built payloads plus two negatives (empty batch, bad enum). It does NOT assert structural equivalence, so the finder's drift surface is real: a dashboard-side widened enum, a one-sided new optional field, or a nullable flip would pass silently.

STANDALONE PACKAGE CONFIRMED: packages/reporter/package.json has no @wrightful/dashboard dependency. zod is a devDependency only (line 57), so the reporter does NOT ship zod at runtime — its emitted payloads (buildPayload in index.ts) are plain objects typed by the TS interfaces.

THIRD COPY (version): finder's solution correctly notes the protocol version is also duplicated — PROTOCOL_VERSION=3 (reporter client.ts:10) vs SUPPORTED_VERSIONS=new Set(["3"]) (dashboard api-auth.ts:50). Independent literals.

DELETION TEST: passes but narrower than the finder frames it. N=2 callers are real (reporter emit-side types; dashboard ingest-side validation), and deleting a shared module reproduces the two-copy + canary structure. HOWEVER, the bulk of schemas.ts is NOT duplicated logic — it is dashboard-only validation behaviour: truncatedText() transforms, MAX.* security caps, MAX_*-array bounds, superRefine visual-artifact rules, and isSafeContentType refinement. That logic must stay dashboard-side (it's a server trust boundary against a stolen bearer key — see schemas.ts:12-27) and must NOT be pulled into a published npm package. So a shared module concentrates only the wire SHAPE, not the validation. The reporter would consume z.infer types type-only (zod stays a dev/peer concern, not a runtime dep), which is viable, but the leverage is modest: ~6 small interfaces + one version constant.

ADR: honestly flagged. This reopens the deliberate "Shared schema contract" decision. The argument for reopening (published reporter + brittle relative-import canary + no structural-equivalence assertion = silent drift) is sound, so it is legitimate to surface — but the friction is mild, not severe: there is exactly one canary file and the surfaces are small. Severity adjusted medium->low accordingly.

Routes & middleware · 7 findings

#34 · Routes & middleware
Run-detail loader re-inlines loadRunResultsPage's testResults query and skips its status normalization
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-90
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/results.ts:80-157
Problem — the friction

loadRunResultsPage already encapsulates the canonical 'first page of a run's testResults' query: the exact 11-column projection (id/testId/title/file/projectName/status/durationMs/retryCount/errorMessage/errorStack/createdAt), the (createdAt DESC, id DESC) ordering, the projectId+runId scoping, and the row→RunProgressTest mapping including normalizeTestStatus. The run-detail loader re-inlines that identical query and mapping (index.server.ts:67-89 + the map at 120-131) with TESTS_LIMIT=200 — the same default the API uses. The two are seeded into the same useRunProgress accumulator, so they MUST agree on shape and ordering, but nothing enforces that: a column added to one (or a status normalization fix) silently diverges the SSR seed from the paginator's later pages. The loader also re-does the run-ownership probe (index.server.ts:26-32) that loadRunResultsPage already performs internally (results.ts:86-91).

Solution — the deepened module

In the run-detail loader, replace the inlined testResults select (index.server.ts:67-89) and its local map (index.server.ts:120-131) with a call to loadRunResultsPage(scope, runId, { cursor: null, limit: TESTS_LIMIT, status: null }), kept inside the existing Promise.all alongside history + loadProjectBranches to preserve concurrency. Use the returned results array as the tests payload (it is already RunProgressTest[] with normalizeTestStatus applied, fixing the current status-normalization divergence). Keep the loader's existing full-run select() at index.server.ts:26-32 — the page needs the full run row, and the early-return 404 it produces still fires before the Promise.all. (Accept that loadRunResultsPage performs its own {id}-only ownership probe; it is a cheap indexed lookup, and its null return on a foreign/missing run can also feed the 404.) This eliminates the duplicated projection, ordering, and mapping, leaving one canonical definition of 'first page of a run's testResults as RunProgressTest[].'

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the SSR seed and the client paginator are guaranteed identical by construction — one source for projection, ordering, status normalization, and the run-ownership 404. Locality: a change to which test columns the UI needs (or the DESC tuple ordering) is made once in loadRunResultsPage and both the page and the back-paginator follow. Eliminates one redundant per-run-detail-load DB round trip (the duplicate ownership SELECT).

Deletion test

Earns its keep — loadRunResultsPage is already a deep module; the finding is that the run-detail loader (N=1 today, but it is the highest-traffic consumer) fails to depend on it and instead duplicates it. Collapsing the copy concentrates the testResults-page contract behind the one existing seam.

Testability impact

The 'first page seed equals first paginator page' invariant becomes a single unit test on loadRunResultsPage rather than an untested cross-file assumption between a server loader and an API route. The loader's remaining logic (history/branch filtering) is then the only thing that needs its own coverage.

Interface sketch
Reuse existing loadRunResultsPage(scope, runId, { cursor, limit, status }): Promise<RunResultsResponse | null>; loader maps null→404.
Verifier notes

Verified both files line-by-line. The duplication is real: index.server.ts:67-89 inlines the exact same testResults query as loadRunResultsPage (results.ts:117-134) — identical 11-column projection (id/testId/title/file/projectName/status/durationMs/retryCount/errorMessage/errorStack/createdAt), identical orderBy(desc(createdAt), desc(id)), identical projectId+runId scoping — and index.server.ts:120-131 re-does the row->RunProgressTest map that loadRunResultsPage does at results.ts:143-154. TESTS_LIMIT=200 matches the API's DEFAULT_LIMIT=200.

The finder's strongest evidence is actually one it underplayed: the loader's mapping does NOT call normalizeTestStatus, but loadRunResultsPage does (results.ts:149). RunProgressTest.status is typed as plain string (src/live.ts:75), so the type system does NOT catch this — the two RunProgressTest producers already disagree on status normalization today. I confirmed both feed the same accumulator: index.tsx:244 passes initialTests={tests} into RunProgress, which forwards to useRunProgress (run-progress.tsx:67), whose seedById keys by t.id (live-client.ts:48-57). So the SSR seed and any merged rows must agree on shape.

Caveat on the coupling framing: there is currently NO client-side back-paginator wired up. grep found no fetch of /results into the accumulator in run-progress.tsx or index.tsx. The API route's own docstring (results.ts:159-165) claims it's used as 'the client-side back-paginator,' but that consumer doesn't exist yet — so 'the two are seeded into the same accumulator and MUST agree' is latent/aspirational, not active. The duplication and the normalizeTestStatus divergence are real regardless.

Deletion test: loadRunResultsPage is already a deep module (cursor decode/encode, tuple comparison for DESC pagination, status normalization, ownership). The run-detail loader is a real second adapter of that contract that re-inlines instead of depending on the seam. Collapsing concentrates the 'first page of a run's testResults as RunProgressTest[]' contract behind one function — concentrating smeared complexity, not adding a one-adapter seam (the seam exists; the API GET is the other adapter). Passes, but the benefit is bounded (one duplicated SELECT + one map).

Two corrections to the solution:
1. The finder says calling loadRunResultsPage lets the loader 'drop the duplicate ownership probe.' This is INVERTED. The loader's full select() at index.server.ts:26-32 cannot be dropped — index.tsx consumes the full run row heavily (run.ciProvider/repo/prNumber/passed/failed/flaky/totalTests/commitMessage/createdAt, etc., index.tsx:56-157). loadRunResultsPage's internal probe only selects {id} (results.ts:86-91). So routing through it would ADD a second {id}-only probe on runs, not remove a duplicate. Net: the loader keeps its full-run fetch AND gains loadRunResultsPage's ownership check (one extra cheap indexed lookup). Minor, but the framing should not claim a probe is eliminated.
2. The loader currently fetches testRows inside Promise.all alongside history + loadProjectBranches (index.server.ts:51-90). loadRunResultsPage returns a Promise, so it should stay inside that Promise.all to preserve concurrency; don't serialize it.

No ADR conflict.

#35 · Routes & middleware
Tenant read-API handlers re-implement the same auth+param+scope+404 preamble four times
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/summary.ts:31-41
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/test-preview.ts:40-49
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/results.ts:166-185
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/summary.ts:30-41
Problem — the friction

Every GET handler under routes/api/t/... opens with the identical ritual: requireAuth(c), read teamSlug/projectSlug/runId (and sometimes testResultId) via c.req.param, null-check the params into a 404, call tenantScopeForUserBySlugs, null-check the scope into a 404. That is 10-12 lines copied verbatim across four files before any handler does its actual work. The shape of a 'missing param' vs 'no membership' response (both 404 JSON, deliberately to avoid existence-leak) is a security-relevant invariant that lives only as convention — a fifth handler can silently get it wrong (return 403, or skip a param check) with no compile error. A maintainer changing the error contract (e.g. adding a cache header or a structured error code) must edit four files and hope they found them all.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce a helper invoked at the top of each handler body (not a replacement for defineHandler) that performs requireAuth, extracts the route params, resolves via tenantScopeForUserBySlugs, and short-circuits to the canonical leak-safe 404 on any miss — returning a ready { scope, runId } (and testResultId where the route declares it). It is the session-API sibling of requireTenantContext, which can't be reused here because middleware/01.context.ts short-circuits /api/* without populating activeProject. Because results.ts uses defineHandler.withValidator(...), the helper must be a body-level call that composes with both defineHandler and the validator variant — e.g. const ctx = await resolveTenantApiScope(c); if (ctx instanceof Response) return ctx; — rather than wrapping defineHandler itself. The handler body then shrinks to just its query, and the leak-safe-404 contract lives in exactly one place.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: a new tenant read endpoint is one line to get a verified scope instead of a 12-line copy. Locality: the auth contract and the deliberate 404-not-403 existence-hiding rule live in exactly one place; a change to error shape or to adding 'last-used' bumps touches one function, not four. Removes the risk of a future handler diverging from the security convention.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete the wrapper and the preamble reappears in all four current handlers (summary, test-preview, results, tests/.../summary) and every future one. The duplicated code is real complexity smeared across N=4 callers, not a pass-through.

Testability impact

The scope-resolution + 404 contract becomes unit-testable once (does a non-member get 404 not 403? does a missing runId 404?) instead of needing four near-identical handler integration tests. Handlers can then be tested for their query logic alone against a fake scope.

Interface sketch
defineTenantApi(schema?, (c, { scope, runId }) => Response) — resolves TenantScope from route params via tenantScopeForUserBySlugs, 404 (leak-safe) on missing param or no membership; never reaches handler otherwise.
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited files. The preamble is verbatim in each: requireAuth(c) -> c.req.param for teamSlug/projectSlug/runId (+ testResultId in tests/.../summary.ts) -> if(!params) return c.json({error:"Not found"},404) -> tenantScopeForUserBySlugs(user.id, teamSlug, projectSlug) -> if(!scope) return 404. Confirmed at summary.ts:31-41, test-preview.ts:40-49, results.ts:169-178, tests/[testResultId]/summary.ts:30-41. A grep confirms these are the ONLY four files under routes/api/t and all four duplicate it, so N=4 is exact (not inflated).

The page-loader sibling the finder cites is real: requireTenantContext(c) at src/lib/tenant-context.ts:50-53 does exactly this for /t/.../p/... loaders. Crucially, middleware/01.context.ts:96-100 short-circuits with STUB_SHARED on any /api/* path and never sets activeProject, so these API handlers genuinely CANNOT reuse requireTenantContext (requireActiveProject would throw/404) — they are forced onto the manual tenantScopeForUserBySlugs path, which has no wrapper. This asymmetry is the real gap: the session-page side got a helper, the session-API side didn't.

Deletion test PASSES: a wrapper concentrates the auth+param+scope+404 ritual at one seam; deleting it makes the preamble reappear across all four (and every future) handler. Not a pass-through — it absorbs smeared duplication. The leak-safe 404 invariant (missing-param and no-membership both return 404 JSON, deliberately not 403, to avoid existence-leak) currently lives only as convention; a fifth handler can silently diverge with no compile error. That is a genuine locality + security argument.

No ADR conflict: the wrapper still routes through tenantScopeForUserBySlugs -> branded AuthorizedProjectId (scope.ts:13-15,39-53), preserving decision #2 (type-enforced logical tenant isolation). Nothing reversed.

One solution caveat: results.ts uses defineHandler.withValidator({query})(async (c,{query})=>...), NOT bare defineHandler. A wrapper that replaces defineHandler wholesale won't compose with the validator chain. The seam should be a helper invoked INSIDE the handler body that returns the resolved scope/runId (or short-circuits), so it works under both defineHandler and defineHandler.withValidator. This is a sharpening, not a defect in the insight — hence revise.

#36 · Routes & middleware
The 'fetch this run, scoped to project' read probe is hand-rolled in 4 page/API sites — one already drops the branded id
medium severity effort: small confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/summary.ts:42-65
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/results.ts:86-91
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-32
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/runs/[runId]/tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:67-72
Problem — the friction

The pattern select(...).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) then map empty→404 is the load-bearing tenant-isolation check for run-scoped reads, and it is written out by hand at least four times — sometimes as id-only existence probe (results.ts, run-detail loader), sometimes as the full-row fetch (summary.ts, test-detail loader). Because the projectId filter IS the isolation boundary (durable decision #2: logical tenancy), every site that forgets it or transposes the columns is a cross-tenant leak with no type-level guard beyond the branded id being present. The variance (existence-probe vs full-row, throw-Response vs return-c.json) makes it easy for a new run-scoped query to copy the wrong variant.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a scoped run accessor in a shared lib (e.g. src/lib/runs-query.ts) with signature getRunForScope(scope: TenantScope, runId: string): Promise<RunRow | null> and a sibling id-only runBelongsToScope(scope, runId): Promise<boolean>. Both bake the and(eq(runs.projectId, scope.projectId), eq(runs.id, runId)).limit(1) predicate in one place; taking TenantScope (not a raw string) forces AuthorizedProjectId through the type system at every call site — which fixes the current test-detail-loader bypass that passes raw project.id. Route the four read-side sites through these (full-row callers use getRunForScope; loadRunResultsPage's existence probe uses runBelongsToScope). Leave the 404 mapping at each call site (page loaders throw Response, API handlers return c.json/null) since that's genuinely call-site policy, not isolation logic. Do NOT fold the ingest.ts aggregate statement builders or the openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun ownership probes into this accessor — those embed the predicate in batched writes or already sit behind a deep interface; consolidating them is a separate, lower-value change.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get a verified-in-scope run row without re-stating the isolation predicate. Locality: the projectId-scoping rule for runs lives in one function; an audit of 'is run access tenant-safe?' is reading one accessor rather than grepping five WHERE clauses. Reduces the surface where decision #2 can be violated.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete it and the projectId-scoped runs lookup reappears across N=4 known callers (summary, results, run-detail loader, test-detail loader) plus any future run-detail endpoint. The complexity (the isolation predicate) does not vanish — it re-smears.

Testability impact

Tenant isolation for run reads becomes a single focused unit test (a run in project A is invisible to scope B) instead of being implicitly re-tested — or not — per call site.

Interface sketch
getRunInScope(scope: TenantScope, runId: string): Promise<Run | null> — always filters runs.projectId === scope.projectId; null = not in this tenant. Existence callers use Boolean(result).
Verifier notes

Verified all 4 cited read-side sites. The pattern select(...).from(runs).where(and(eq(runs.projectId, <pid>), eq(runs.id, runId))).limit(1) then map-empty-to-404 exists at: summary.ts:42-65 (full-row, scope.projectId, c.json 404); results.ts:86-91 loadRunResultsPage (id-only existence probe, scope.projectId, returns null→404); pages/.../runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:26-32 (full-row, scope.projectId, throw Response 404); pages/.../tests/[testResultId]/index.server.ts:67-71 (full-row, returns not_found tagged union). The cited variance (existence-probe vs full-row; throw-Response vs c.json vs return-null vs tagged-union) is accurate.

STRONGEST EVIDENCE (sharpens the finding): the test-detail loader at line 70 uses eq(runs.projectId, project.id) where project.id is a PLAIN string from ResolvedActiveProject (authz.ts:165-173, id: string) — NOT the branded scope.projectId. So one of the four sites already routes around the AuthorizedProjectId guard the finding leans on. This is a live demonstration that "the brand being present" is not enforced per-call-site, exactly because the WHERE clause is hand-written. An accessor whose signature takes TenantScope would force AuthorizedProjectId back into the path.

UNDERCOUNT CORRECTION: the same runs.projectId AND runs.id predicate also appears in src/lib/ingest.ts: appendRunResults:660-664 and completeRun:770-775 (id-only ownership probes returning {kind:"notFound"}), plus three aggregate statement builders (aggregateDeltaStatement:425, aggregateRecomputeStatement:443, aggregateSummarySelectStatement:460). So N is larger than 4. BUT these should NOT all be folded into one "fetch run row" accessor: the ingest ownership probes already sit behind the deep openRun/appendRunResults/completeRun interface, and the aggregate builders embed the predicate inside batched UPDATE/SELECT statements (not standalone row reads). The accessor should target the read-side probes only.

DELETION TEST: passes. A (scope, runId) → run | null accessor concentrates the isolation predicate; deleting it re-smears the projectId+id WHERE across the read callers. The complexity (the tenant-isolation predicate, durable decision #2) does not vanish — it reappears. Good concentration, not a pass-through.

SEVERITY: finding says high; adjusting to medium. Every cited site currently DOES filter by the correct project id (even the brand-bypass site filters by the right project.id), so there is no active cross-tenant leak today — this is latent-risk + missing-locality, not a present vulnerability. Solid medium. No ADR conflict — this reinforces durable decision #2 (logical tenancy, branded ids) rather than reversing anything.

#37 · Routes & middleware
User-invite-identity lookup is copy-pasted three times beside an existing invite-identity.ts
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/accept.ts:22-42
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/decline.ts:22-41
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:97-118
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/invite-identity.ts:29-52
Problem — the friction

Three call sites independently do the same thing: fetch the signed-in user's recipient identity — email via raw SELECT email FROM "user" plus githubLogin from userGithubAccounts — then build or(eq(teamInvites.email, ...), eq(teamInvites.githubLogin, ...)) match conditions, and treat 'no identity' as 403/empty. accept.ts, decline.ts, and getPendingInvitesForUser each carry their own copy, including the fragile raw-SQL result cast (userRow.results?.[0] as { email?: string }). An invite-identity.ts already exists, but it solves the INVERSE problem (given one invite row + userId, does it match?) for the token-link path — so the query-building direction ('give me this user's identity to filter invites by') has no home and got triplicated. A change to how email is normalized, or capturing a second OAuth provider's login, is a three-file edit with three chances to miss the raw-SQL cast.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a getUserInviteIdentity(userId) -> { email, githubLogin } resolver (the natural complement to invite-identity.ts, ideally living in it) that owns the raw-SQL email read + githubLogin fetch + lowercasing. accept.ts/decline.ts/getPendingInvitesForUser call it and build their OR-conditions from the returned identity (a tiny inviteMatchConditions(identity) helper can fold that too). The 'no identity → 403' rule becomes one branch.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: redemption/decline/list handlers get the caller's invite identity in one call, no raw SQL in handler code. Locality: the void-managed-user email read (raw SQL, decision #3) and the directed-invite matching predicate are defined once; adding a provider or changing matching is a one-file change. Removes three copies of the brittle results-cast.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete the resolver and the user-identity read + OR-condition building reappear across N=3 callers (accept, decline, getPendingInvitesForUser). The raw-SQL/cast complexity is real and currently smeared.

Testability impact

Recipient-matching (does an email-only user match an email-directed invite? a github-only user?) becomes one unit test on the resolver/predicate rather than three integration paths through three handlers, none of which currently isolate it.

Interface sketch
getUserInviteIdentity(userId): Promise<InviteIdentity>; inviteMatchConditions(identity): SQL[] (empty when no identity → caller 403/empties).
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited files. The duplication is real and exactly as described.

Three call sites independently fetch the signed-in user's recipient identity via the same Promise.all([raw-SQL email read, githubLogin select]):
- accept.ts:22-34
- decline.ts:22-34 (byte-for-byte identical to accept.ts's fetch+normalize block)
- authz.ts getPendingInvitesForUser:100-112 (same fetch; lowercases via a slightly different expression but same effect)

All three carry the fragile cast (userRow.results?.[0] as { email?: string } | undefined)?.email. That cast also appears a 4th time inside invite-identity.ts:37. grep confirms the raw SELECT email FROM "user" lives in exactly these four files.

All three also rebuild the OR-match conditions: matchConds.push(eq(teamInvites.email, ...)) + eq(teamInvites.githubLogin, ...) then or(...matchConds), plus the "no identity" branch — accept.ts:40-42 (403), decline.ts:39-41 (403), authz.ts:113 (return []).

The finder's claim about invite-identity.ts is correct: inviteMatchesUser(invite, userId) solves the INVERSE problem (given one invite row, does this user match it?) and is consumed only by the token-link path (pages/invite/[token]/index.server.ts:78,135). The forward direction — "resolve THIS user's identity so I can filter invites by it" — genuinely has no home and got triplicated.

Deletion test passes (concentration, not movement): a getUserInviteIdentity(userId) -> { email, githubLogin } resolver pulls the raw-SQL read + cast + githubLogin fetch + lowercasing out of N=3 callers into one place, sitting beside its natural complement inviteMatchesUser.
