This is a deep helper: small interface (userId in, identity out), real behaviour behind it (cross-table read against the void-owned user table, the documented raw-SQL pattern).

ADR check: no conflict. ADR #3 mandates raw SQL for the void-owned user table; this finding preserves that pattern and in fact centralizes the brittle cast it produces. The resolver complements rather than reverses anything.

One caveat on the solution: the OR-condition shapes differ slightly per caller (accept layers or(...matchConds) inside an and(...) with id+expiry; decline inside and(id, or(...)); getPendingInvitesForUser inside and(or(...), gt(expiresAt))). The core win is the identity resolver; the inviteMatchConditions(identity) fold is optional polish, not load-bearing — worth flagging so the implementer doesn't over-abstract the WHERE assembly.

#38 · Routes & middleware
00.errors.ts is a deep error gate, but its status->outcome policy is duplicated across the catch arm and the post-next() arm (plus a separately-duplicated API logging predicate)
low severity effort: medium confidence: high deep but fragile revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/middleware/00.errors.ts:51-156
Problem — the friction

The error gate is genuinely deep — it hides real Hono unwinding subtleties (thrown Response vs Error-converted-to-c.res, the c.res-setter header-merge bug, the FILE_EXT_RE dev-asset guard, 404-status preservation on rewrite) behind a zero-config middleware, which is exactly the leverage you want. But the same decision table (401→login, 404→not-found rewrite preserving 404, 5xx→oops+log, /api never rewrites) is encoded THREE times: once in the catch block for thrown Responses (54-91), once in the post-next() API branch (94-111), once in the post-next() HTML branch (112-155). Each uses a slightly different mechanism (return c.redirect vs replaceResponse, extractStatus(err) vs c.res?.status), so a change to the policy (e.g. add a 403 case, or change the oops log fields) must be made in two or three spots that look similar but aren't interchangeable. The fragility is that the THREE arms must stay behaviorally identical for two entry conditions (thrown vs swallowed) that the same exception can take depending on whether it was an Error or a Response.

Solution — the deepened module

Keep the middleware shell — the try/catch (thrown Response) + post-next() inspection (Error-swallowed-to-c.res) duality is irreducible. Funnel the HTML arms (catch 74-91, post-next 123-155) into one pure mapStatusToOutcome(status, { isApi, path }) -> { kind: 'pass' | 'redirect-login' | 'rewrite-404' | 'log-and-oops' } plus one applyOutcome(c, outcome) that owns the replaceResponse/c.res-clear trick and the 404-status-preservation. The two HTML entry points then differ only in how they get the status (extractStatus(err) vs c.res?.status). Note this is collapsing TWO duplicated slices, not one triplicated table: (a) the HTML redirect/rewrite decision table, and (b) the API 5xx logging predicate duplicated between the catch arm (60-69) and the post-next API arm (101-109) — fold that into a single shouldLogApiFailure(status)/logApiFailure(c, status) helper. Use the consolidation to also resolve the latent 5xx-status-preservation asymmetry (404 preserves status; /oops currently does not) explicitly in the mapper.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the policy table is one pure function — callers (both arms) get identical behavior for free. Locality: adding a status case or changing the 404-preservation/oops-logging rule is a one-edit change in the mapper instead of reconciling three near-duplicate branches. The irreducible Hono-unwinding knowledge stays in the shell where it belongs.

Deletion test

Earns its keep as a deepening. The pure mapper is not a pass-through: delete it and the decision table re-smears across the catch arm + the two post-next arms (N=3 in-file call sites). It concentrates a policy that is currently triplicated within one file.

Testability impact

mapStatusToOutcome becomes a table-driven unit test (status×isApi → outcome) with zero Hono/Response plumbing. Today the policy can only be exercised through full request integration tests that must trigger each of the thrown-vs-swallowed paths to cover the same logic three ways.

Interface sketch
mapErrorOutcome(status: number|null, ctx: { isApi: boolean; path: string }): Outcome; applyOutcome(c, outcome): Response|void — both catch-arm and post-next() arm derive status then call these.
Verifier notes

Verified against apps/dashboard/middleware/00.errors.ts (167 lines). The module is genuinely deep: the header (lines 6-44) and inline comments document real Hono unwinding subtleties behind a zero-config seam — thrown Response vs Error-converted-to-c.res (the dual entry condition at try/catch + post-next is irreducible, finder correctly says keep the shell), the c.res-setter header-merge bug fixed by replaceResponse() clearing c.res to undefined first (164-167), the FILE_EXT_RE dev-asset guard (37-44, 112), and 404-status preservation on rewrite (75-84, 133-143). This is real leverage.

The duplication is real but the "THREE places" framing is imprecise. The 401/404/5xx HTML redirect/rewrite DECISION TABLE is duplicated TWICE: catch arm (74-91) and post-next HTML arm (123-155). The API branch (94-111) is NOT the same decision table — it never rewrites, it only logs; it's a different shape. What IS triplicated-feeling is the API LOGGING predicate ("log if status===null || >=500"), duplicated between catch (60-69) and post-next (101-109). So there are two distinct duplicated policy slices, not one cleanly triplicated table.

Each arm uses a genuinely different mechanism, confirming the fragility claim: catch 401 = c.redirect("/login"); HTML 401 = manual new Response(null,{status:302,Location}) via replaceResponse. Status obtained via extractStatus(err) (158-162) vs c.res?.status. A policy change (add 403, change log fields) must touch both.

Latent inconsistency the unified mapper would surface: the 5xx arms (91, 152) rewrite to /oops WITHOUT preserving status (renders 200), while the 404 arms deliberately preserve 404 (80-83, 137-143). A mapper makes this asymmetry explicit and drift-resistant.

Deletion test PASSES on the dimension that matters: grep confirms OOPS_PATH/NOT_FOUND_PATH/replaceResponse/extractStatus are referenced ONLY in this file — no external callers, no test file (no error/middleware .test.ts exists). So the proposed mapStatusToOutcome+applyOutcome concentrates policy that is currently duplicated WITHIN one file; it is not a pass-through and not a hypothetical one-adapter seam. It does not relocate complexity elsewhere.

No ADR/durable-decision conflict — pure in-file refactor, touches no tenancy/D1/auth-table/realtime decision. Severity low is right: single ~120-line file, zero external blast radius. Verdict revise only to correct the "encoded THREE times" count in the title/problem.

#39 · Routes & middleware
JSON-or-form body parsing for owner mint endpoints is duplicated inline
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/keys.ts:50-58
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/invites.ts:50-59
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/form.ts:1-5
Problem — the friction

Both mint endpoints (keys, invites) need to accept the same field from either an application/json body or a FormData body (the client posts JSON; the no-JS slow path posts a form). Each handler open-codes the same content-type sniff: if (ctype.includes('application/json')) { body = await c.req.json(); field = typeof body.x==='string' ? body.x.trim() : '' } else { field = readField(form, 'y').trim() }. The form.ts helper only covers the FormData half. The dual-mode read — including the unsafe as { label?: unknown } / as { identifier?: unknown } casts on the JSON branch — is the part that's actually tricky and it's copied per handler, with the JSON key and the form key wired by hand each time.

Solution — the deepened module

Add readBodyField(c, { jsonKey, formKey }): Promise<string> to src/lib/form.ts (next to readField). It sniffs content-type; on application/json it does const body = (await c.req.json()) as Record<string, unknown> and returns typeof body[jsonKey] === "string" ? body[jsonKey].trim() : ""; otherwise readField(await c.req.formData(), formKey).trim(). keys.ts calls readBodyField(c, { jsonKey: "label", formKey: "label" }); invites.ts calls readBodyField(c, { jsonKey: "identifier", formKey: "inviteIdentifier" }). Keep all validation (required, max-length, parseInviteIdentifier) in the handlers. Preserve the existing behavior of letting malformed JSON throw to middleware/00.errors.ts (do not wrap in try/catch unless you intend to change the error contract) — confining the single unsafe cast to this one function is the main locality win.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: a handler that accepts dual-mode input is one call, not a 9-line branch with two unsafe casts. Locality: the JSON-vs-form contract (and the unsafe-cast handling) lives in one helper alongside readField; adding a third dual-mode endpoint is free and can't drift.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. Delete it and the content-type branch + casts reappear across N=2 mint handlers (keys, invites) and any future dual-mode POST. The complexity is real (body parsing + unsafe-cast guarding), not a rename.

Testability impact

Dual-mode body extraction (json path, form path, missing field, non-string field) becomes a small unit test on one helper instead of being implicitly exercised only via the two mint-endpoint integration paths.

Interface sketch
readBodyField(c, { jsonKey, formKey }): Promise<string> — sniffs content-type, reads json[jsonKey] or formData[formKey], guards non-string, trims; '' when absent.
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. The dual-mode (application/json vs FormData) sniff exists verbatim in exactly two route handlers and nowhere else: keys.ts:50-58 reads label (JSON key label / form key label), invites.ts:50-59 reads rawIdentifier (JSON key identifier / form key inviteIdentifier). Both open-code the identical shape: ctype = c.req.header("content-type") ?? ""; if (ctype.includes("application/json")) { body = (await c.req.json()) as { X?: unknown }; field = typeof body.X === "string" ? body.X.trim() : "" } else { form = await c.req.formData(); field = readField(form, "Y").trim() }. The as { label?: unknown } / as { identifier?: unknown } casts are present as claimed and are the genuinely-fiddly part. form.ts (1-5) is exactly the FormData-only half (readField), so the JSON branch is the uncovered duplication.

Grep confirms N: only keys.ts and invites.ts contain the application/json sniff in routes/ (the download.ts:81 hit is an unrelated comment about Accept headers). All other readField/formData callers are form-only no-JS page actions (settings/*.server.ts) and select-workspace.ts — none are dual-mode, so the helper would not over-generalize.

DELETION TEST: passes. A readBodyField(c, { jsonKey, formKey }) concentrates the content-type sniff + json()-with-cast + typeof-string guard + formData()/readField + trim. Deleting it reappears across the 2 mint handlers, plus is the natural seam for any future client-JSON-with-no-JS-form-fallback POST. Not a pass-through rename; it absorbs the unsafe cast in one place (which would also clear 2 of the no-unsafe-type-assertion-style warnings). It is genuine concentration, just small (~7 lines per handler), hence severity stays low.

No ADR conflict — this is a leaf utility in src/lib/form.ts, touches none of the durable decisions (tenancy, D1, auth tables, realtime, nuqs).

One spec sharpening: both handlers currently let c.req.json() throw on malformed JSON, with the throw flowing to middleware/00.errors.ts. The helper must preserve that (don't silently swallow a parse error into ""), or deliberately decide to 400 — the finder's "return '' for missing/non-string" wording doesn't address the throw path. Reflected in revisedSolution.

#40 · Routes & middleware
Owner-gated API handlers bypass requireOwnedProjectScope and hand-roll a divergent 403 gate
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/keys.ts:37-48
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/invites.ts:39-48
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/settings-scope.ts:45-80
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:147-156
Problem — the friction

The settings page loaders/actions already route every owner-only operation through a deep seam — requireOwnedProjectScope / requireOwnerScope (settings-scope.ts) — which does requireAuth, reads slugs, resolves the project/team, enforces role==='owner', and throws a leak-safe 404. But the two API handlers that perform the SAME owner-gated operations for the SAME resources (mint key, mint invite) ignore that seam: keys.ts re-runs resolveProjectBySlugs + project.role !== 'owner' and returns 403; invites.ts calls requireTeamOwner in a try/catch and returns 403. So there are now two contradictory contracts for 'caller isn't an owner' — pages 404 (decision: don't leak existence), API 403 (leaks that the team/project exists). A maintainer reasoning about owner-authz has to know which tier they're in, and the existence-leak hardening applied to pages is silently absent on the API.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract the owner-resolution core shared by requireOwnerScope and requireOwnedProjectScope into a status-agnostic resolver in authz/settings-scope: e.g. resolveOwnedTeam(userId, teamSlug) / resolveOwnedProject(userId, teamSlug, projectSlug) that returns the owned team/project or throws a typed AuthzError (no HTTP Response, no here string). Then: (a) the page wrappers requireOwnerScope/requireOwnedProjectScope call it and map the failure to a 404 Response + build the here redirect URL (preserving the don't-leak-existence rule); (b) keys.ts and invites.ts call the same resolver and map the typed failure to the API's chosen JSON status. This puts the slug-read + membership/owner logic in one place and makes the page-vs-API status difference an explicit, single-line decision at each call site instead of two independently hand-rolled gates. Drop the finder's "even simpler: reuse requireOwnedProjectScope directly" suggestion — those helpers throw redirect-shaped Responses and take a page-only hereFor arg, so they cannot be consumed by JSON API handlers without the extraction.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: minting code in keys.ts/invites.ts drops the auth boilerplate entirely. Locality: owner-authz for projects/teams is defined once; the existence-leak policy (404 vs 403) is decided once instead of diverging by accident between tiers. Closes the current information-leak inconsistency.

Deletion test

Earns its keep. The owner-resolution logic already exists once (settings-scope) and is correctly reused by all settings call sites; the finding is that N=2 API handlers re-implement it divergently. Routing them through the seam concentrates the gate; deleting the seam would re-scatter it across pages AND those handlers.

Testability impact

The owner gate becomes testable as one unit (non-owner → typed failure) shared by both tiers, rather than relying on separate per-handler integration tests that currently don't even agree on the expected status code.

Interface sketch
resolveOwnedProject(c): Promise<OwnedProject> (throws AuthzError) — shared by requireOwnedProjectScope (adds `here`) and the keys/invites API handlers; one place decides 404-vs-403.
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited files. The friction is real and accurately described.

EVIDENCE:
- settings-scope.ts:45-80 — requireOwnerScope (team) and requireOwnedProjectScope (project) are the deep seam: each does requireAuth + reads slugs from route params + resolves (resolveProjectBySlugs / requireTeamOwner) + enforces role==='owner' + throws new Response("Not Found", {status:404}). The docstrings explicitly state "404s instead of 403ing so we don't leak team existence to non-owners."
- These helpers are correctly consumed by 4 page modules: members.server.ts (revokeInvite action via requireOwnerScope), general.server.ts, projects/new.server.ts, keys.server.ts (loader + revokeKey/updateGeneral/deleteProject actions via requireOwnedProjectScope).
- keys.ts:45-48 (API) re-runs resolveProjectBySlugs + if (!project || project.role !== "owner") inline and returns 403 — NOT routed through the seam.
- invites.ts:44-48 (API) wraps requireTeamOwner in try/catch and returns 403 — also not routed through the seam, and uses a *different* shape (try/catch on a throwing helper) than keys.ts (null-check + role compare).

SAME-OPERATION CLAIM CONFIRMED: keys.server.ts docstring — minting "replaces the server-side createKey action"; members.server.ts docstring — invite creation "Replaces the server-side createInvite action." So the two owner-gated mint operations literally moved off the page seam (404-on-failure) onto hand-rolled API handlers (403-on-failure). These are the ONLY two files under routes/api/teams/ — N=2 is exact, not approximate.

DELETION TEST: passes. The owner-resolution logic exists once and is reused by 4 page call sites; the finding is precisely that the 2 API handlers doing the identical owner-gated operations re-implement it divergently (and divergently from EACH OTHER). A shared status-agnostic resolver concentrates the gate; this is concentrating smeared complexity, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam.

ADR: no conflict. This is logical authz consolidation, untouched by the single-D1 / logical-tenancy / void-auth decisions.

CORRECTIONS TO THE FINDING:
1. The finder's "Even simpler" alternative (reuse requireOwnedProjectScope directly / standardize on 404) is misleading: requireOwnerScope/requireOwnedProjectScope throw new Response(...) redirect-shaped responses and take a hereFor redirect-URL builder — that contract is page-specific and wrong for a JSON API handler. So the API handlers cannot just call them as-is; the correct move is the *primary* solution (extract a status-agnostic resolver).
2. Severity downgraded medium->low: blast radius is exactly 2 handlers, no run-scoped/tenant-data path, and the 403-vs-404 "existence leak" is marginal for a session-authed API where the caller is an authenticated user whose membership is already determinable. The defensible core is the inconsistent *contract* (two divergent owner-gate shapes + two different failure statuses for the same operation across tiers), not a serious security hole.

#41 · Analytics & insights
Analytics loaders re-derive branchFilter, window math, and segment defaults inline — with the window math diverged into three forms
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/index.server.ts:13-14,24-34
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:17-23,51-69
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.server.ts:18-31,43-58
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:10-12,71-88
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/flaky.server.ts:14-25,63-72
Problem — the friction

Every loader re-declares the same preamble: a RANGES tuple + parseRange (insights/index, run-duration, suite-size, slowest-tests use makeRangeParser; flaky and tests hand-roll their own parseRange at flaky.server.ts:18-21 and tests.server.ts inline), then re-derives branchParam/branchFilter against ALL_BRANCHES (5 copies of the identical !branchParam || branchParam === ALL_BRANCHES ? null : branchParam), nowSec, rangeSec, and windowStartSec. The windowStart derivation has subtly diverged: insights/index and run-duration compute days = rangeSec/DAY_SEC then nowSec - days*DAY_SEC, while slowest-tests/suite-size/tests compute nowSec - rangeSec directly with a 0 fallback for 'all'. And defaultSegmentForRange exists as two separate near-identical functions (run-duration.server.ts:21-23 vs suite-size.server.ts:26-31). A maintainer touching range/window semantics must reconcile 5 hand-rolled variants.

Solution — the deepened module

Add an analytics request-params resolver to lib/analytics that does NOT assume raw URL access, so it fits both the raw-searchParams loaders and tests.server.ts's withValidator/typed-query path. Two seams:
1. normalizeBranchFilter(branchParam: string | null) → { branchParam, branchFilter, branchAll } — folds the 5x ALL_BRANCHES check (and flaky's branchAll variant) into one tested function.
2. resolveAnalyticsWindow({ range, nowSec?, segmentForRange? }) → { range, segment, window: { nowSec, windowStartSec, days, rangeSec } } — takes an ALREADY-PARSED range (callers keep their own makeRangeParser/z.enum) and applies ONE canonical window formula. Unifying the window math requires a deliberate decision on the "all"/null fallback (currently 30 days vs epoch-0 vs dead code), not a mechanical merge — pick windowStartSec = rangeSec == null ? 0 : nowSec - rangeSec (or an explicit ALL sentinel) and document it. The optional segmentForRange replaces the two divergent defaultSegmentForRange copies; choose the intended mapping deliberately since the two existing versions disagree. Loaders pass window straight to query builders.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: each loader replaces ~15 lines of bespoke parsing with one call and gets a consistent window. Locality: the 'how a range maps to a window' and 'all-branches → null' rules live once; the day-vs-direct windowStart divergence is eliminated and can't re-appear.

Deletion test

Delete the resolver and the preamble reappears in all 5 analytics loaders (N=5) including the divergent windowStart and the two defaultSegmentForRange copies. Earns its keep by collapsing a copy-paste preamble into one parameterized module.

Testability impact

Currently the window math and branch normalization are only exercised by running a loader against a request+DB. As a pure function, parseAnalyticsParams is directly unit-testable (e.g. '90d defaults to week segment', 'all → windowStartSec 0', 'ALL_BRANCHES → null'), which today requires integration setup.

Interface sketch
parseAnalyticsParams<T extends string>(url: URL, cfg: { ranges: readonly T[]; defaultRange: T; segmentForRange?: (r:T)=>Segment }): { range:T; segment:Segment; branchParam:string|null; branchFilter:string|null; window:{ nowSec:number; windowStartSec:number; days:number } }
Verifier notes

Verified against all cited files. The duplication is real and not pre-existing as a resolver (grep for parseAnalyticsParams/AnalyticsParams found nothing).

CONFIRMED:
- RANGES tuple + range parser preamble repeated across 6 loaders: insights/index.server.ts:13-14 and run-duration.server.ts:17-19 and suite-size.server.ts:18-20 and slowest-tests.server.ts:10-12 all do RANGES=[...] + makeRangeParser(RANGES,"30d"); flaky.server.ts:14-25 hand-rolls its own parseRange + rangeToDays; tests.server.ts:14-15 inlines RANGES via z.enum and query.range ?? "14d". (Note: makeRangeParser/rangeToSeconds in lib/analytics/range.ts are already shared & deep — the duplicated part is the per-loader ASSEMBLY, not the primitive parsing.)
- branchFilter normalization !branchParam || branchParam === ALL_BRANCHES ? null : branchParam appears VERBATIM in 5 files: index:28-29, run-duration:58-59, suite-size:50-51, slowest-tests:73-74, tests:79-80. flaky:66-67 is a near-variant (branchAll = ...; branchFilter = branchAll ? null : branchParam). This is the cleanest, most clearly identical duplication. nowSec is also repeated everywhere.
- windowStart math HAS genuinely diverged into 3 forms: (a) index:30-34 and run-duration:60-64 compute days = rangeSec/DAY_SEC (fallback 30) then nowSec - days*DAY_SEC; (b) suite-size:55-57, slowest-tests:80-82, tests:86-87 compute nowSec - rangeSec with a 0 fallback; (c) flaky:69-70 uses rangeToDays(range)*24*60*60. Real divergence and a latent correctness hazard.

CORRECTION to the finding: the two defaultSegmentForRange functions are NOT "near-identical" in behavior. run-duration.server.ts:21-23 is range === "90d" ? "week" : "day"; suite-size.server.ts:26-31 is a 4-branch version (7d/30d→day, 90d→week, else→month). They are similar in SHAPE but produce different results — which is itself a symptom of un-centralized segment-default policy, so centralizing still earns its keep, but a mechanical merge is wrong; the intended behavior must be chosen.

DELETION TEST: deleting a resolver makes the preamble reappear across 5-6 loaders including the divergent window math and the two segment defaulters. It concentrates complexity currently smeared across callers — not a pass-through. N=5-6 real callers. Passes.

FIT PROBLEM (why revise, not keep): the proposed parseAnalyticsParams(url, ...) signature assumes raw URL access, but tests.server.ts uses defineHandler.withValidator({ query: z.object(...) }) and reads query.range from a validated typed query that flows into .void/routes.d.ts. A url-based resolver would force tests.server to either abandon its typed-query contract or re-declare the enum. The resolver should accept already-parsed inputs (or expose a parser both paths can call) rather than assume url.searchParams.

No ADR conflict — this is logical-tenancy-agnostic loader plumbing.

#42 · Analytics & insights
Discrete-percentile picker fragment is re-stated 7× across two analytics loaders
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:88-90
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:110-112
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:182
Problem — the friction

The discrete percentile idiom min(case when rn = max(1, cast(round(cnt * 0.50) as integer)) then duration end) is a subtle, easy-to-get-wrong expression (the max(1,...) clamp keeps a single-row bucket resolvable, and it depends on a row_number() rn + count() over cnt being set up correctly upstream). It appears 6 times in run-duration.server.ts (p50/p90/p95 × perBucket + overall) and once in slowest-tests.server.ts (p95). Each is a separate string literal. A maintainer who wants linear interpolation, a different rounding rule, or to fix an off-by-one must edit all 7 in lockstep, and the invariant ('rn comes from row_number() ordered by the value; cnt from count() over the same partition') is implicit and re-stated each time.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a single helper to src/lib/analytics/bucketing-sql.ts: percentilePick(quantile: number, cols: { rn: string; cnt: string; value: string }): SqlBucketExpr that emits min(case when <rn> = max(1, cast(round(<cnt> * <q>) as integer)) then <value> end), encoding the clamp and rounding rule once and documenting the upstream invariant (rn = row_number() ordered by value, cnt = count() over the same partition) in one JSDoc. Each loader keeps writing its own ranked CTE (they differ in partitioning and pass-through columns) and just calls the helper for each pick. Do NOT add a CTE-skeleton/column-emitter companion — the CTEs are not uniform enough to share, so that part would move complexity rather than concentrate it.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers request p50/p90/p95 by quantile value without re-deriving the CASE/ROUND arithmetic. Locality: the percentile algorithm (clamp, rounding, discrete vs interpolated) is defined once; correctness lives behind the seam where it can be reasoned about.

Deletion test

Delete the helper and the picker idiom reappears across run-duration (6 occurrences) and slowest-tests (1) — N=2 loaders, 7 call sites. Earns its keep by concentrating a fiddly, correctness-sensitive expression.

Testability impact

A pure fragment-emitter is unit-testable: assert the emitted SQL text for a given quantile, and (with a tiny in-memory rank fixture) assert the clamp behaviour for cnt=1, cnt=2, etc. — exactly the edge cases that are currently only exercisable against live D1.

Interface sketch
percentilePick(quantile: number, cols?: { rn?: string; cnt?: string; value?: string }): SqlBucketExpr // emits: min(case when <rn> = max(1, cast(round(<cnt> * q) as integer)) then <value> end)
Verifier notes

Confirmed in the files. A repo-wide grep for round(cnt * 0 returns exactly 7 hits: run-duration.server.ts lines 88-90 (perBucket p50/p90/p95) and 110-112 (overall p50/p90/p95), plus slowest-tests.server.ts line 182 (p95). The two other insights loaders (index.server.ts, suite-size.server.ts) contain no percentile idiom, so the count of N=2 loaders / 7 sites is precise, not undercounted.

The idiom is genuinely subtle and re-stated each time: min(case when <rn> = max(1, cast(round(cnt * <q>) as integer)) then <value> end). The max(1,...) clamp (so a single-row bucket still resolves a rank in [1..cnt]) and the round-based discrete rank are the correctness-sensitive parts, and the doc-comment at run-duration.server.ts:45 even spells the invariant out in prose — evidence it's non-obvious. The invariant "rn comes from row_number() ordered by the value, cnt from count() over the same partition" is implicit and depends on upstream CTE setup the picker can't see.

Crucially, the call sites are NOT character-identical, which validates a parameterized helper rather than a copy: run-duration uses identifiers rn / cnt / duration; slowest-tests uses "rnDur" / cnt / "durationMs" (it has a second rank "rnTime" for the latest-attempt picks). So the picker must take the rn/cnt/value column names as args — exactly the signature the finder proposed.

DELETION TEST: passes. A percentilePick(quantile, {rn, cnt, value}) helper in bucketing-sql.ts concentrates the clamp+rounding expression that is currently smeared across 7 sites in 2 loaders; deleting it makes the fiddly fragment reappear verbatim at each. This concentrates complexity, it does not merely relocate it. Two real callers (run-duration, slowest-tests) = a real seam, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam.

No ADR/durable-decision conflict: this is a read-only analytics SQL helper in an existing lib module (bucketing-sql.ts already exports bucketExpr with the same sql fragment return type, SqlBucketExpr), touches no tenancy/ingest/realtime decision. The picker can return the same ReturnType<typeof sql<...>> fragment type. Severity medium is fair but on the generous side — these are read-path analytics queries, no security/tenant-isolation/ingest-correctness exposure; the risk is a maintainer fixing the rounding/interpolation rule in 6 of 7 places.

One correction to the SOLUTION: the "companion that emits the required ranked-CTE columns" is weaker than the picker and should be dropped from scope. The two ranked CTEs differ materially — run-duration's overall CTE has no partition; its perBucket partitions by bucket; slowest-tests partitions by testId AND carries a second "rnTime" window plus title/file/runId pass-through columns. A one-size CTE-skeleton emitter would be a leaky, low-leverage abstraction. The deep, reusable unit is the percentile-pick fragment alone.

#43 · Analytics & insights
No deep "latest-per-test" analytics query module — three loaders re-inline the same ranked-CTE + status-counter SQL
medium severity effort: large confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:72-114
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:152-194
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/tests.server.ts:216-265
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/flaky.server.ts:204-301
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.server.ts:95-110
Problem — the friction

The analytics lib (bucketing/bucketing-sql/range) captures only trivial fragments — divisors, a range parser, a JS bucket skeleton. Every loader still hand-writes its own multi-CTE raw SQL inside db.run(sql...). The same building blocks recur verbatim: a ranked as (... row_number() over (partition by testId order by createdAt desc) as rnTime ...) CTE to pick latest title/file/status/runId per test (tests.server.ts:223-255, slowest-tests.server.ts:171-189, flaky.server.ts:214-237, 264-288), a discrete-percentile picker, and per-test status counters (sum(case when status = 'flaky' ...)) repeated in flaky.server.ts:84-86, slowest-tests.server.ts:187-188, tests.server.ts:256-259. A maintainer changing how "latest result per test" or "flaky vs failed" is computed must find and edit 4-6 separate SQL string literals and keep them consistent by eye. There is no parameterizable query module the loaders call; the loaders ARE the query layer.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce src/lib/analytics/queries.ts exposing two deep, parameterized builders over a common scope+window+branch(+testIds) input: rankedLatestPerTest(scope, { windowStartSec, branch, testIds }) returning the row_number() over (partition by testId order by createdAt desc) CTE that picks latest title/file/status/runId/testResultId; and perTestStatusCounters() returning the passed/flaky/fail/skipped sums with a SINGLE canonical definition of "fail" (status in 'failed','timedout') and "flaky", so the flaky-vs-failed semantics live in one place. The three callers are tests.server.ts (runAggregateQuery), slowest-tests.server.ts (bottleneck CTE), and flaky.server.ts (loadSparklinesAndMeta / loadRecentFailures) — each becomes orchestration (parse params, call builder, shape props). Do NOT fold in run-duration's bucket-percentile CTE or suite-size's first-seen query; those are different shapes and belong to the separate percentile finding (run-duration + slowest-tests) and to suite-size respectively. The discrete-percentile picker (run-duration ×2, slowest-tests) is a worthwhile but distinct third builder, tracked separately.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: a loader gets correct, scope-filtered, branch-aware ranked/counter SQL from one call instead of re-deriving it. Locality: the definition of "latest result per test" and "flaky count" changes in one function, not 6 string literals; a bug fixed once is fixed everywhere.

Deletion test

Delete the proposed queries.ts and the complexity REAPPEARS as the current state: the same ranked-CTE + counter SQL re-inlined across run-duration, slowest-tests, tests, flaky, suite-size (N=5 loaders). It earns its keep — it concentrates complexity currently smeared across all analytics loaders.

Testability impact

Today the only way to test these queries is to boot a request against a live D1 (the known-missing real-DB harness). Extracted builders return SQL fragments / take a db handle, so the row-shaping and the SQL composition (param binding, branch clause inclusion, having-filters) become unit-testable, and a single integration test per builder covers all callers instead of 6 page-level integration tests.

Interface sketch
rankedLatestPerTest(scope: TenantScope, opts: { window: AnalyticsWindow; branch: string|null; testIds?: string[]; q?: string }): Promise<RankedTestRow[]> perTestCounters(scope, opts): Promise<CounterRow[]> // invariant: every builder injects projectId AND teamId into the WHERE clause

#44 · Analytics & insights
Analytics range/bucketing pure functions are untested — the cheap UTC-month-key vs SQL strftime contract is the real gap (bucketKey is trivial)
low severity effort: small confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/range.ts:15-37
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/bucketing.ts:35-97
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__
Problem — the friction

rangeToSeconds, makeRangeParser, parseSegment, buildEmptyBuckets, and bucketKey are all pure functions with non-trivial branching (regex parse with d/y suffix and an 'all'→null sentinel vs undefined-for-unrecognized; calendar month iteration with UTC alignment; the bucket-key normalization), yet there is no analytics test file (the __tests__ dir has group-tests-by-file and aggregate-delta only). These are the one part of the subsystem that is trivially unit-testable today, and the absence means the date-boundary edge cases (DST-free UTC month rollover, leap handling via the 365-day year approximation, windowStart at month boundaries) are unguarded. This compounds findings above: as logic is extracted out of the loaders into this lib, it inherits the no-test gap.

Solution — the deepened module

Add src/lib/analytics/__tests__/ with two focused files. (1) range.test.ts: rangeToSeconds for "7d"/"90d" (n*DAY_SEC), "2y" (n*365*DAY_SEC), "all" (null), and garbage (undefined); makeRangeParser narrowing to the valid union + null/unknown -> fallback. (2) bucketing.test.ts: parseSegment fallback; and — the highest-value case — buildEmptyBuckets month-segment key format asserting ${year}-${pad2(month)} exactly matches the strftime('%Y-%m') contract in bucketing-sql.ts (a windowStart spanning a year boundary, e.g. Nov->Feb, proving correct count and zero-padded keys), plus day/week integer-division bucket counts. Drop bucketKey as a standalone target — it is String(v); cover it incidentally if at all. This file is the natural home for the bucket-key-reconciliation contract test.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: future extractions (the analytics query builders, parseAnalyticsParams) land into a subsystem with a test harness already established, so they ship tested. Locality: date-boundary correctness is pinned where the logic lives, not discovered via empty charts in production.

Deletion test

N/A as a module extraction — this is a test-coverage gap on existing pure modules. It is the precondition that makes the other findings' testabilityImpact claims real rather than aspirational.

Testability impact

Directly converts the pure lib from untested to unit-tested; establishes the vitest harness the rest of the deepenings will plug into without needing the still-unbuilt real-DB integration harness.

Verifier notes

Code confirms the friction. range.ts:15-21 rangeToSeconds has the exact branching described: "all"->null, regex /^(\d+)([dy])$/ with y=365*DAY_SEC approximation, unrecognized->undefined. makeRangeParser (28-37) and parseSegment (bucketing.ts:35-39) are pure narrowers with fallbacks. buildEmptyBuckets (48-88) is the real substance: integer-division day/week buckets PLUS calendar-month iteration via Date.UTC + setUTCMonth producing ${y}-${pad2(m)} keys. Two corrections to the finding's framing:
1. bucketKey (95-97) is literally return String(v) — a trivial one-liner, NOT "non-trivial branching" or meaningful "normalization." Calling it out as an edge-case-laden function is an overstatement; it is not worth a dedicated test on its own. The finding should drop bucketKey as a primary target.
2. The genuinely load-bearing, currently-unguarded contract is the JS-side month key ${y}-${pad2(m)} (bucketing.ts:84) matching the SQL-side strftime('%Y-%m', ...) in bucketing-sql.ts:20. That cross-implementation agreement is the only place a silent bug could ship, and it is the real reason to test here. The finding gestures at this ("matching strftime here") but buries it.

Callers actually found (real, not hypothetical): insights/index.server.ts, run-duration.server.ts, suite-size.server.ts, slowest-tests.server.ts all use makeRangeParser+rangeToSeconds+parseSegment; tests.server.ts uses rangeToSeconds; insights/index.tsx, suite-size.tsx, run-duration.tsx use buildEmptyBuckets+bucketKey. So coverage genuinely protects 5+ loaders.

DELETION TEST: honestly fails as a deepening. The finder concedes this ("N/A as a module extraction"). A test file does not concentrate complexity smeared across N callers; the modules are ALREADY extracted and deep. This is a test-coverage gap, not a structural deepening — there is no new seam, no adapter, nothing moved. It is real and cheap but it is the weakest category of finding for this exercise: it rides on the other findings rather than standing alone. No ADR conflict — pure additive test work, consistent with the known-outstanding "real-DB test harness not built" gap (these are the pure functions that need NO db harness, which is exactly why they are the cheap win).

#45 · Analytics & insights
bucketExpr hardcodes runs.createdAt, so slowest-tests' day-bucket + the D1 text-affinity caveat are re-implemented inline (one straggler off the seam)
low severity effort: small confidence: high shallow module revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/bucketing-sql.ts:16-21
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:208
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:16
Problem — the friction

bucketExpr hardcodes the table+column runs."createdAt" into the fragment, so it only buckets the runs table. The slowest-tests sparkline needs day-buckets over testResults, and cannot use bucketExpr — it re-writes cast(tr."createdAt" / 86400 as integer) as day inline (line 208) and even redeclares a local DAY_SEC = 86_400 (line 16) despite DAY_SEC already living in bucketing.ts. The divisor 86400 now exists in 3 forms (bucketExpr's literal, slowest-tests' inline literal, and the DAY_SEC constant) and the 'inline numeric literal, never a bound param' invariant documented in bucketing-sql.ts:11-14 is silently re-stated in raw SQL elsewhere where the next maintainer won't see the warning.

Solution — the deepened module

Parameterize bucketExpr by the column it buckets — accept a table-qualified column reference (e.g. a Drizzle column or a sql fragment for tr."createdAt") instead of hardcoding runs."createdAt". Then slowest-tests' sparkline routes its day-bucket through the same seam, so the integer divisor AND the documented D1 text-affinity caveat (currently re-stated only as raw inline SQL at slowest-tests:208) live in exactly one place. While there, delete the shadowing const DAY_SEC = 86_400 at slowest-tests:16 and import DAY_SEC from bucketing.ts like the other three loaders already do. Scope is small: this is consolidating ONE straggler into an existing, already-used seam — not a 4-way smear.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: any analytics query that needs time-bucketing (runs OR testResults) calls one function and inherits the affinity-safe inline-divisor behaviour. Locality: the divisor constants and the D1 text-affinity caveat are defined once; the sparkline stops carrying a stray duplicate.

Deletion test

Delete a column-parameterized bucketExpr and the complexity reappears as today: bucketing inlined separately for runs (3 loaders) and for testResults sparklines (slowest-tests) — N=4 sites — with the affinity caveat re-explained ad hoc. Deepening it concentrates that smear.

Testability impact

bucketExpr emits a Drizzle SQL fragment; a unit test can assert the emitted text per segment for a given column, locking in the affinity-safe literal form that currently can only be verified by reading three different files.

Interface sketch
bucketExpr(segment: Segment, col: SQL | string = sql`runs."createdAt"`): SqlBucketExpr // invariant: divisors stay inline literals (D1 text-affinity), never bound params
Verifier notes

- slowest-tests.server.ts:208 inlines cast(tr."createdAt" / 86400 as integer) as day against testResults tr — it genuinely cannot use bucketExpr because the table/column differ. True.
- slowest-tests.server.ts:16 redeclares const DAY_SEC = 86_400; shadowing the shared DAY_SEC exported from bucketing.ts:5. This is a genuine, avoidable re-declaration — run-duration/index/suite-size all import DAY_SEC from bucketing.ts, so slowest-tests is the lone straggler. True.
- The D1 text-affinity invariant documented at bucketing-sql.ts:11-14 (inline numeric divisor, never a bound param) is silently re-enacted in raw SQL at slowest-tests:208 with no comment, where a maintainer won't see the warning. True and the most load-bearing part of this finding.

They are NOT inlining bucketing. The seam already exists and is already used.

#46 · Analytics & insights
SQL↔JS bucket-key equivalence is an untested cross-file contract with a silent-empty-chart failure mode
low severity effort: medium confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/bucketing.ts:42-97
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/bucketing-sql.ts:16-21
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/index.tsx:40-41
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.tsx:48-49
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.tsx:43-45
Problem — the friction

The client-safe split (bucketing.ts) and SQL split (bucketing-sql.ts) are a principled seam — bucketing.ts must stay importable from .tsx islands without dragging in void/db's server-only client. But the seam leaks a fragile invariant: buildEmptyBuckets must produce keys in EXACTLY the form bucketExpr's SQL produces and bucketKey(String()) normalizes — day/week as String(floor(sec/86400)), month as ${year}-${pad2(month)} matching SQL's strftime('%Y-%m', createdAt, 'unixepoch') (bucketing.ts:46-47,84). This contract is split across two files that share only a Segment type import, has zero tests, and if the divisor or the month format drifts on either side, the .tsx join (byKey.get(s.key)) silently misses and every bucket renders empty — no type error, no exception. The three .tsx consumers each re-do the same shells+byKey+map dance, so the silent-miss failure mode is reproduced 3×.

Solution — the deepened module

Keep the client/SQL file split. The primary deliverable is a CONTRACT TEST that pins the key-format equivalence: for each Segment, assert buildEmptyBuckets produces keys in the exact form bucketKey() expects from bucketExpr's output (e.g. day/week keys are String(floor(sec/DIV)) with DIV matching the SQL literal; month keys match ${year}-${pad2(month)} ⟷ strftime('%Y-%m')). Pull the divisors into shared named constants imported by BOTH files (or assert the SQL literals against DAY_SEC/WEEK_SEC in the test) so they cannot drift independently. Secondarily, add a thin join helper in bucketing.ts — alignBuckets(segment, windowStartSec, nowSec, rows): { key; label; row: Row | undefined }[] — that builds the shells and left-joins on bucketKey(r.bucket), returning shells decorated with the matched row (or undefined). It deliberately does NOT take a projection/keyOf callback: the join key is fixed (the contract), and each caller keeps its own per-row mapping. The three .tsx files then replace their shells+byKey+map preamble with alignBuckets(...).map(({ key, label, row }) => ...). The load-bearing change is the test + shared divisor, not the helper.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: a .tsx page calls alignBuckets(segment, window, perBucket, r=>bucketKey(r.bucket)) and gets a gap-filled series — no hand-rolled Map/shell loop. Locality: the SQL↔JS key-format invariant is asserted in one contract test; drift fails loudly instead of rendering empty charts in three pages.

Deletion test

Delete alignBuckets and the shells+byKey+map join reappears verbatim in index.tsx, run-duration.tsx, suite-size.tsx (N=3 consumers). The key-format contract itself is load-bearing (it's the reason bucketKey exists) — deepening it concentrates a currently-implicit, untested correctness link.

Testability impact

A contract test can assert buildEmptyBuckets keys equal the keys SQL would emit for the same window (especially the month YYYY-MM vs strftime form and the integer-division day/week keys) — a class of silent-empty-chart bugs that is currently undetectable without rendering against live data.

Interface sketch
alignBuckets<R>(segment: Segment, win: { startSec:number; nowSec:number }, rows: R[], keyOf: (r:R)=>string): { key:string; label:string; row: R|undefined }[]
Verifier notes

Verified against all cited files.

SEAM IS REAL AND REQUIRED. bucketing.ts (src/lib/analytics/bucketing.ts) has no void/db import and is imported by the three .tsx islands (index/run-duration/suite-size, line 13/12). bucketing-sql.ts imports sql from void/db (server-only) and is imported only by the three .server.ts loaders. They share solely import type { Segment }. The split is principled — confirmed.

THE CROSS-FILE KEY CONTRACT IS REAL AND DUPLICATED. SQL side (bucketing-sql.ts:17-20): day runs."createdAt" / 86400, week / 604800, month strftime('%Y-%m', runs."createdAt", 'unixepoch'). JS side (bucketing.ts): DAY_SEC=86_400 (line 5), WEEK_SEC=604_800 (line 6), day/week key = String(Math.floor(sec/DIV)) (lines 55-59,66-69), month key = ${y}-${pad2(m)} (line 84). The divisors are duplicated literals, and the month format is a duplicated string pattern. bucketKey() just does String(v) (line 95-96) to coerce the SQL number/string to the JS string form. If either side drifts, byKey.get(s.key) (index.tsx:41,49; run-duration.tsx:48-50; suite-size.tsx:44-51) silently misses — both sides are typed string, so no type error and no exception; every bucket renders empty/null. That silent failure mode is real.

ZERO TESTS — confirmed. No test file references buildEmptyBuckets/bucketKey/bucketExpr (grep found only the source defs + the 6 page usages). Combined with the known-outstanding "real-DB harness not built", the SQL side is currently unverifiable end to end.

DELETION TEST — passes but with a caveat the finder overstated. The genuinely-verbatim duplication across all 3 callers is the JOIN SKELETON only: buildEmptyBuckets(...) -> new Map(rows.map(r => [bucketKey(r.bucket), r])) -> shells.map(s => byKey.get(s.key)). The per-row PROJECTION differs sharply (index = 4 stacked segments + tooltip; run-duration = p50/p90/p95/cnt; suite-size = single peak, and it even stores only r.peak in the map, not the whole row). So a helper must NOT try to absorb the projection — only the shell-build + keyed-left-join. The finder's proposed alignBuckets(...,keyOf) signature is slightly off: rows already carry bucket, so the join key is fixed (bucketKey(r.bucket)); a free keyOf invites the same drift it's meant to kill. The real win is concentrating the currently-implicit key-format equivalence into one tested home, not the 3x DRY (the join is small).

SEVERITY: adjusted to LOW (finder said medium). This is the analytics READ path, not ingest; write rate is single-digit/sec; worst case is a cosmetically-empty chart, not data loss or auth bypass. The zero-tests + silent-miss combination keeps it above trivial, but medium overstates blast radius.

ADR: no conflict. The file split is consistent with isomorphic-pages decision #6 (keep server-only deps out of island-importable modules). The fix lives entirely in the read path and touches none of the durable decisions.

#47 · Frontend components
RunProgress re-implements grouping/severity-ordering inline instead of using the existing pure groupTestsByFile module — duplicated, drifting, untestable
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/run-progress.tsx:60-266
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/live-client.ts
Problem — the friction

RunProgress is the run-detail Tests tab and the most logic-heavy island in this subsystem: it folds live test rows into per-status counts (with timedout->failed collapse), filters by search + status, groups by file/project, sorts groups worst-first by a custom score, sorts rows within a group by STATUS_ORDER, and runs an auto-expand heuristic (worst 6 groups, else first group) with a one-shot useEffect guard. All of this lives inline in the component as useMemo/useEffect bodies, so none of it is testable without rendering the island and feeding it live events. The status-collapse and ordering rules are also re-derivations of the status taxonomy from finding 1. (CLAUDE.md flags run-progress as a 'minimal stub'; the filter/group engine inside it is in fact substantial and worth extracting.)

Solution — the deepened module

Do not create a new groupAndSortTests module from scratch — one already exists and is unused. Instead: (1) extend apps/dashboard/src/lib/group-tests-by-file.ts to cover the two axes the island needs — a groupBy: 'file' | 'project' parameter and a pure filterTests(tests, { search, statusFilter }) predicate (folding the timedout->failed collapse that's currently duplicated at run-progress.tsx:89 and :99 and :295); (2) add a pure selectDefaultExpandedKeys(groups) returning the worst-6-or-first-group key set (the body of the useEffect at 142-160); (3) rewrite RunProgress to call filterTests -> groupTestsByFile(groupBy) -> selectDefaultExpandedKeys, keeping only input state (search/statusFilter/groupBy/expanded) + the toggle handler + presentation. This deletes the inline STATUS_ORDER/reduce-score/count loops in run-progress.tsx and TestGroup, collapses the two parallel severity tables (STATUS_ORDER vs STATUS_SEVERITY) into one, and brings the engine under the existing test suite.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the same grouping/sort/count engine could back any test-list view (e.g. a future static run-detail table) without the live island. Locality: the worst-first sort weights, STATUS_ORDER, and timedout collapse live in one pure function aligned with the status registry, not scattered across three useMemos in JSX.

Deletion test

Delete the extracted module and the grouping/counting/sorting/auto-expand logic reappears inline in RunProgress (where it is today) — and would reappear again in any non-live test table. Earns its keep by concentrating the engine; the React island shrinks to state + presentation.

Testability impact

Turns the currently integration-only behavior (filter by status hides rows, timedout counts as failed, failed groups expand first, groups sort worst-first) into pure unit tests over arrays — directly useful given the known-outstanding lack of a real-DB/island test harness.

Interface sketch
export function groupAndSortTests(tests: RunProgressTest[], opts: { search:string; statusFilter:StatusFilter; groupBy:'file'|'project' }): { groups: [string, RunProgressTest[]][]; statusCounts: Record<string,number>; suggestedExpanded: Set<string> };

Friction is real. run-progress.tsx:81-160 folds tests into per-status counts with timedout->failed collapse (88-91), filters by status+search (95-115), groups by file OR project and sorts groups worst-first by a custom reduce-score (118-138), then runs a one-shot auto-expand useEffect (worst-6-groups else group[0], 142-160). TestGroup (287-345) re-derives per-group counts and sorts rows by STATUS_ORDER. All of it lives in useMemo/useEffect bodies inside a client island — untestable without rendering and feeding live events. So far the finder is correct.

BUT the finder missed a load-bearing fact that both strengthens and reframes the finding: a pure, Node-testable module ALREADY EXISTS at apps/dashboard/src/lib/group-tests-by-file.ts, with a 315-line test suite at src/__tests__/group-tests-by-file.test.ts. #48 · Frontend components
Scalar query-string href builders (hrefWith / pageHref / rangeHref) are copy-pasted across ~7 insights/tests/flaky page modules and have already drifted
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/tests.tsx:51-66
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.tsx:97-111
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/flaky.tsx:46-51
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/index.tsx:56-59
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/index.tsx
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.tsx
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.tsx
Problem — the friction

Almost every list/insights page hand-rolls a closure that rebuilds the URL from the loaded params: const p = new URLSearchParams(); p.set('range', range); if (branchParam) p.set('branch', branchParam); if (q) p.set('q', q); if (currentPage>1) p.set('page', ...); apply overrides; return pathname?qs. The closures differ subtly — tests.tsx and slowest-tests.tsx include q+page, flaky.tsx/insights only carry range+branch, slowest-tests omits the qs ? guard that tests.tsx keeps — so the 'keep all active params, override one, reset page' invariant is reimplemented 7 times with no guarantee they agree. The runs list page builds the same thing on top of toSearchParams (a separate code path). A maintainer adding a new shared filter param (say env on insights) must touch every page and remember each page's idiosyncratic ordering and reset rules.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract one shared scalar-param href builder for the insights/tests/flaky family (the ~6-8 sites that hand-roll new URLSearchParams from current params): e.g. buildHref(pathname, current: Record<string,string|null>, overrides: Record<string,string|null>) that encodes "omit empty values", "drop key on null override", and the conditional ? guard once; plus thin pageHref/rangeHref derived from it where "page resets to 1 unless overridden" lives in one place. Leave the runs-list path on its existing toSearchParams(RunsFilters) in src/lib/runs-filters.ts — it is already a single centralized builder for a richer typed filter model and should NOT be folded into the scalar seam. This concentrates the param-preservation + page-reset + conditional-? rules that currently drift across the page modules without coupling the two genuinely-different param shapes.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: pages get correct, consistent filter-preserving navigation (including the page-reset-on-filter-change invariant) from one call. Locality: a new carried param or a change to reset semantics is one edit, not seven; the qs-empty guard inconsistency between tests.tsx and slowest-tests.tsx can't recur.

Deletion test

Delete the builder and the closure reappears verbatim in 7 page modules (it currently does). Earns its keep — it concentrates the param-preservation + page-reset logic that is presently smeared.

Testability impact

URL composition is currently only exercisable by rendering a page and inspecting hrefs. A pure builder makes 'override range resets page', 'empty q is omitted', 'page=1 drops the param' directly unit-testable, matching how runs-filters.ts (toSearchParams/parseRunsFilters) is already tested.

Interface sketch
// lib/page-links.ts export function makeHrefBuilder(pathname: string, base: Record<string,string|null>) { const withParams = (o: Record<string,string|null>) => /* merge, drop nulls/empties, build qs */; return { with: withParams, pageHref:(p:number)=>withParams({page:p===1?null:String(p)}) }; }
Verifier notes

Verified all cited files plus the runs-filters helper. The duplication is real and the specific divergence the finder called out is exactly right.

Confirmed sites:
- tests.tsx:51-66 — hrefWith(range+branch+q+page>1, null-delete override loop) WITH the qs ? ... : pathname guard; + pageHref.
- slowest-tests.tsx:97-111 — byte-identical hrefWith seed, but OMITS the qs ? guard (returns ${pathname}?${p.toString()} unconditionally). Confirms "slowest-tests omits the qs guard tests.tsx keeps."
- flaky.tsx:46-51 — rangeHref only, carries range+branch, no override loop, no guard.
- index.tsx:56-59 (runs list) — pageHref built on toSearchParams({...filters, page}) from src/lib/runs-filters.ts — a genuinely separate, already-centralized code path.
- insights/index.tsx:118-125, run-duration.tsx:107-114, suite-size.tsx:89-96 — three byte-identical hrefWith closures carrying range+segment+branch, set-only override loop (no null/delete), no guard.
- UNCITED 8th site: runs/[runId]/index.tsx:110-116 — tabHref carries branch+tab with the guard. Same param-preservation idiom, different params.

So ~7-8 hand-rolled closures across three idiom variants. Deletion test passes: removing a shared builder makes the closure reappear verbatim, and the existing guard-present-vs-absent and null-delete-vs-set-only drift is concrete evidence the smearing has already caused silent divergence (the invariant is genuinely reimplemented, not shared).

Two corrections to the finding:
1. The problem statement says "flaky.tsx/insights only carry range+branch" — understated: the three insights pages also carry segment. Minor; doesn't weaken the core claim.
2. ADR conflict: none. Pure frontend href construction, unrelated to the durable-decision list.

Revise (not keep) because the solution over-reaches: routing RunsFilters/toSearchParams through the same with()/pageHref() seam is wrong. RunsFilters is a richer typed list model (status[]/actor[]/env[]/date-range/comma-joining) and is already centralized in runs-filters.ts; forcing it through a with(overrides: Record<string,string|null>) scalar seam would either bloat the interface or lose its typed structure. The finding itself concedes the runs list "keeps toSearchParams" — so the seam should cover the scalar range/branch/segment/page/tab family (tests, slowest-tests, flaky, the 3 insights pages, optionally run-detail tabHref) and leave toSearchParams as the runs-list's own builder.

(1) FIX FIRST (decoupled from refactor): the flaky-tests filter is dead. Either wire flaky.tsx's input into a GET <form method="get"> with name="q" + hidden range/branch inputs (mirroring tests.tsx) AND teach flaky.server.ts to read+apply the q searchParam, or remove the input entirely if filtering flaky tests isn't a supported feature. This is the high-value part and needs no component extraction.

Do NOT attempt a single submit/debounce contract — the sites have three distinct behaviors. Benefits — leverage & locality

Deletion test

Testability impact

A SearchFilterInput with an explicit onSubmit/onDebouncedChange contract is testable in isolation (does it emit on debounce? does Enter submit?), surfacing the flaky.tsx dead-input regression that is currently invisible because it is inert inline JSX.

Interface sketch
export function SearchFilterInput({ defaultValue, placeholder, onSubmit }: { defaultValue?: string; placeholder: string; onSubmit:(q:string)=>void }): React.ReactElement; // catalog page: <FilterToolbar left={<SearchFilterInput.../>} right={<><RunHistoryBranchFilter/><AnalyticsButtonGroup/></>}/>

#50 · Frontend components
Status taxonomy (color token / label / badge variant / severity / collapse rule) is smeared across ~10 frontend components in four conflicting encodings, with lib/status.ts hex silently drifting from the styles.css oklch tokens
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/status.ts:16-25
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/outcome-bar.tsx:31-36
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/run-progress.tsx:33-40
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/runs-filter-bar.tsx:41-57
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/run-tests-popover.tsx:23-35
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/status-glyph.tsx:18-26
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/status-badge.tsx:7-16
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/analytics/kpi-card.tsx:51-58
Problem — the friction

The same status domain (passed/failed/flaky/timedout/interrupted/skipped) is encoded independently in at least three incompatible forms with no single seam. lib/status.ts STATUS_COLORS uses raw hex (#16a34a, #dc2626, #ea580c) while outcome-bar, run-progress, runs-filter-bar, run-tests-popover, status-glyph and kpi-card all use CSS custom properties (var(--pass)/var(--fail)/var(--flaky)/var(--skipped)). status-badge.tsx maps to Badge variants (success/error/warning/secondary). Several files re-declare their own status->label map (runs-filter-bar STATUS_LABEL, run-tests-popover VARIANT_LABEL) and their own collapse rules (timedout->failed appears in run-progress STATUS_ORDER and statusCounts, again in TestGroup counts). A maintainer adding a new Playwright status, or renaming a color token, must hunt down and edit ~10 files, and the hex-vs-CSS-var split means lib/status.ts and the components can drift out of visual agreement silently (they already encode the same colors twice).

Solution — the deepened module

Make lib/status.ts the single status registry: one keyed record per status carrying { cssVar, label, badgeVariant, severity/order, collapsesTo }, plus accessors statusToken(status) (returns the CSS var name like "var(--pass)", NOT a raw color — styles.css remains the sole owner of the actual oklch values so theming/dark-mode keep working), statusLabel(status), statusBadgeVariant(status), statusSeverity(status), and statusGroupKey(status) for the timedout->failed / interrupted->flaky collapse. Delete STATUS_COLORS hex entirely; rewrite sparkline.tsx and run-history-chart.tsx to consume statusToken() so charts theme and match the rest of the UI. Migrate outcome-bar, run-progress (both count maps + STATUS_ORDER), runs-filter-bar (STATUS_LABEL + STATUS_DOT_CLASS), run-tests-popover (TRIGGER_COLOR + VARIANT_LABEL), status-glyph, status-badge, segmented-control, and group-tests-by-file (STATUS_SEVERITY) to the accessors. Do NOT touch kpi-card — its var(--pass)/var(--fail) encodes delta sign, not status.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: every status-aware component (bar, glyph, badge, filter, popover, chart, KPI) gets correct color/label/order/collapse from one import. Locality: adding or recoloring a status, or fixing the hex/CSS-var disagreement, is a one-file edit instead of a 10-file sweep; the canary that lib/status and components agree disappears because they are the same source.

Deletion test

Delete the registry and complexity reappears across at least 8 callers (outcome-bar, run-progress x2 count maps, runs-filter-bar, run-tests-popover, status-glyph, status-badge, kpi-card, sparkline/run-history-chart via statusColor) each re-deriving its own color/label/order map. Earns its keep.

Testability impact

Currently the only testable piece is statusColor(); label/variant/order/collapse logic is buried in JSX and untestable without rendering. A registry exposes statusLabel/statusBadgeVariant/statusSortKey/statusGroupKey as pure functions with trivial unit tests, including the timedout/interrupted aliasing that today is silently re-implemented in two RunProgress reducers.

Interface sketch
// lib/status.ts export const STATUS = { passed: { cssVar:'--pass', label:'Passed', badge:'success', order:5, groupKey:'passed' }, failed:{...}, timedout:{ ...groupKey:'failed' }, ... } as const; export function statusLabel(s:string): string; export function statusToken(s:string): string; // CSS var export function statusSortKey(s:string): number; export function statusGroupKey(s:string): 'passed'|'failed'|'flaky'|'skipped';
Verifier notes

Friction is real and, if anything, understated. Three genuinely incompatible encodings of the same status domain (passed/failed/flaky/timedout/interrupted/skipped) confirmed in the cited files:
- lib/status.ts:16-23 STATUS_COLORS uses raw hex (#16a34a, #dc2626, #ea580c, #9ca3af, #9333ea).
- CSS-var components use var(--pass)/var(--fail)/var(--flaky)/var(--skipped): outcome-bar.tsx:32-35, run-progress.tsx:328-336 + TestRow:399, run-tests-popover.tsx:23-28, status-glyph.tsx:17-25, and (not cited by finder) segmented-control.tsx:40-49.

- runs-filter-bar.tsx:41-57 has its own STATUS_LABEL + STATUS_DOT_CLASS (bg-pass/bg-fail/...) — a fourth encoding (Tailwind classes), not just the three the finder named.

REAL color drift, stronger than claimed: the hex in lib/status.ts is wholly independent of the oklch tokens in styles.css:291-300 (--pass: oklch(0.55 0.16 152), --fail: oklch(0.55 0.22 24), etc.). They are not the same color space, so sparkline.tsx and run-history-chart.tsx (the only two consumers of statusColor, confirmed via grep) render visually different greens/reds than the rest of the dashboard, and lib/status.ts colors do not theme with light/dark. Concretely: interrupted is purple (#9333ea) in lib/status.ts but collapses to flaky/orange (var(--flaky), Badge "warning") everywhere else — an observable inconsistency, not hypothetical.

Duplicated collapse/order rules confirmed and broader than cited: timedout->failed appears in run-progress.tsx:89,295, status-glyph.tsx:96, status-badge.tsx:9. Worst-status order/severity maps are duplicated across run-progress.tsx:33-40 (STATUS_ORDER), lib/group-tests-by-file.ts:23-30 (STATUS_SEVERITY) — finder MISSED this file — and ingest.ts:721. CORRECTION — one citation is wrong: kpi-card.tsx:51-58 is NOT a status taxonomy map. Drop kpi-card from the file list. DELETION TEST: deleting a unified registry forces each of those ~10 callers back to its own per-encoding map — which is precisely the current smeared state — so a registry CONCENTRATES complexity rather than moving it. Passes.

ADR check: no conflict. These are presentation tokens; nothing touches single-D1, logical tenancy, Better Auth ownership, void/live, or nuqs. One important constraint the solution must honor: colors must remain CSS vars (styles.css owns light/dark theming via the oklch blocks at :291 and the dark block at :396), so the registry must carry a token NAME (cssVar) rather than own raw color literals. The finder's solution already says exactly this ("drop hex entirely and reference the token"), so framing is sound. Severity medium is fair: visual-only drift, not a correctness/security bug, but it touches ~10 files and silently desyncs charts from the rest of the UI today.

#51 · Frontend components
Branch-param decode (`__all__`/empty -> null) is duplicated in 6 loaders instead of living with ALL_BRANCHES
low severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/index.server.ts:27-29
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/run-duration.server.ts:57-59
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:72-74
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/suite-size.server.ts:49-51
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/tests.server.ts:80
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/flaky.server.ts:65-66
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/run-history-branch-filter.shared.ts
Problem — the friction

The ALL_BRANCHES sentinel (__all__) leaks its decode rule into every loader: each one re-writes const branchAll = !branchParam || branchParam === ALL_BRANCHES; const branchFilter = branchAll ? null : branchParam. The sentinel and its meaning are defined in run-history-branch-filter.shared.ts (a UI component file), but the canonical 'sentinel-or-empty means no filter' decode is the consumers' responsibility, repeated 6-7 times. The seam is leaky because the component owns the sentinel value but not the parse, so the two can drift (e.g. if the sentinel changes, every loader must be updated).

Solution — the deepened module

Export parseBranchParam(raw: string | null): string | null from run-history-branch-filter.shared.ts (it already owns ALL_BRANCHES), returning null for empty/missing or ALL_BRANCHES and the branch otherwise. Replace the 2-line decode in all 6 analytics loaders (insights/index, run-duration, slowest-tests, suite-size, tests, flaky). Do NOT touch runs/[runId]/index.server.ts — it intentionally decodes differently (missing param falls back to the run's own branch, not no-filter), so the sentinel string staying visible there is correct.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: loaders get the resolved branch filter with one call and never reference the sentinel string. Locality: the sentinel value and its meaning live together; changing the encoding is one edit.

Deletion test

Delete parseBranchParam and the 2-line normalization reappears in 6 loaders (it currently does). Earns its keep.

Testability impact

Today the normalization is inline in loaders that require a request + DB to exercise. A pure parseBranchParam is a trivial unit test (null, '', '__all__', 'main' -> null/null/null/'main').

Interface sketch
export function parseBranchParam(raw: string | null): string | null { return (!raw || raw === ALL_BRANCHES) ? null : raw; }
Verifier notes

Verified all cited files. The decode !branchParam || branchParam === ALL_BRANCHES ? null : branchParam is duplicated verbatim in 6 server loaders: insights/index.server.ts:28-29, insights/run-duration.server.ts:58-59, insights/slowest-tests.server.ts:73-74, insights/suite-size.server.ts:50-51, tests.server.ts:79-80, and flaky.server.ts:66-67 (the last spelled branchAll = ...; branchFilter = branchAll ? null : branchParam). Each imports ALL_BRANCHES from run-history-branch-filter.shared.ts, which (per its own doc comment, lines 1-8) defines only the string "__all__" and exists as a plain non-"use client" module precisely so server loaders can import the literal. So the sentinel VALUE has a single owner but its DECODE rule does not — exactly the leaky seam described.

Deletion test holds: a parseBranchParam(raw): string | null would concentrate the "sentinel-or-empty means no filter" rule (currently smeared across 6 call sites) into one place co-located with the sentinel. Delete it and the 2-line normalization reappears 6 times. This is concentration of smeared complexity, not relocation of a single use — a real (if small) seam, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam.

Count correction: the title says "7 loaders" but the body hedges "6-7 times". It is 6 loaders. The shared module (the 7th cited file) is the sentinel DEFINITION site, not a consumer of the decode — so it should be the HOME of the new helper, not counted as a duplicate. Recommend retitling to 6.

Scoping caveat (does not invalidate the finding): runs/[runId]/index.server.ts:36-48 also consumes ALL_BRANCHES but with DIFFERENT semantics — effectiveBranch = branchParam ?? (run.branch ?? ALL_BRANCHES) then if (effectiveBranch !== ALL_BRANCHES). Here a missing param falls back to the current run's branch, not to null/no-filter. A parseBranchParam returning null for empty would be WRONG for this loader, so it must (correctly) be excluded. The finding already excludes it. The proposed helper should be documented as "decode for the analytics loaders where empty == all", and the run-detail divergence is a separate, legitimately different decode that should stay as-is.

No ADR conflict. This is a pure frontend/loader DX cleanup; touches none of the durable decisions (tenant scoping, D1/Drizzle, void/live, etc.).
