#53 · Frontend components
Two numeric-line sparklines (MetricSparkline + page-private DurationSparkline) duplicate the same job with incompatible x-spacing
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/sparkline.tsx:33-79
  • apps/dashboard/src/components/analytics/metric-sparkline.tsx:18-58
  • apps/dashboard/pages/t/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/insights/slowest-tests.tsx:392-435
Problem — the friction

There are three distinct sparkline components: Sparkline (categorical status-history bars, lib/status colored), MetricSparkline (numeric line+area, in analytics/), and a page-private DurationSparkline (numeric line over {day,avg} points, hand-rolled in slowest-tests.tsx). The first two even carry overlapping names and the source files contain comments apologizing for the collision ('still named Sparkline for historical reasons', 'different visualization despite the shared name'). DurationSparkline is a third numeric line sparkline that duplicates MetricSparkline's job with a different point shape, so a maintainer wanting 'a numeric trend sparkline' finds two answers and may pick or rebuild the wrong one.

Solution — the deepened module

Two independent moves, do not bundle: (1) Consolidate the two numeric-line sparklines: extend MetricSparkline to accept an optional explicit x-coordinate per point (e.g. points: {x: number; y: number}[] adapter alongside the existing values: number[] fast path) plus an area?: boolean toggle, and port DurationSparkline's degenerate-count handling (empty 0-point SVG, single-point dot). Critically, slowest-tests must pass real day values as x so sparse days keep rendering as gaps — index-spacing would be a silent regression. Then delete DurationSparkline and call MetricSparkline from slowest-tests.tsx:323. Also collapse the two clashing SparklinePoint types. (2) Separately and lower priority: rename the categorical Sparkline -> StatusHistoryBar (its design-bundle name) to kill the name collision; pure clarity, no behavior. Only (1) carries deepening value; (2) is optional polish.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers wanting a numeric trend have exactly one component (MetricSparkline); the categorical bar has an unambiguous name. Locality: numeric-sparkline rendering math lives once, not in MetricSparkline plus a page-private clone.

Deletion test

Delete DurationSparkline: complexity reappears only in slowest-tests (1 caller) but is identical to MetricSparkline's job, so it collapses cleanly into the existing module rather than earning independent existence. The rename of Sparkline is pure clarity (no behavior), lower priority.

Testability impact

Consolidating numeric sparklines lets the min/max/scale path be unit-tested once (degenerate cases: 0, 1, equal values) instead of being duplicated in an un-exported page function.

Interface sketch
export function MetricSparkline({ values }: { values:number[] }) // DurationSparkline callers map points->avg[] then reuse; rename component Sparkline -> StatusHistoryBar
Verifier notes

Friction is real and accurately cited. Confirmed three distinct sparkline visualizations:

1. Sparkline (apps/dashboard/src/components/sparkline.tsx:33-79) — categorical status bars, points: SparklinePoint[] where SparklinePoint = {status, label?}, colored via statusColor. The apologetic comment is verbatim at lines 28-31 ("still named Sparkline for historical reasons... separate DurationSparkline"). One render caller: flaky-test-row.tsx:127.

2. MetricSparkline (analytics/metric-sparkline.tsx:18-58) — numeric line + area fill, values: number[]. Apologetic comment verbatim at 13-16 ("different visualization despite the shared name"). It assumes EVENLY-SPACED x: stepX derived from array index i (line 32-37). One direct caller: kpi-card.tsx:83 (AnalyticsKpiCard, itself used by 4 insights pages, but always via values).

3. DurationSparkline (slowest-tests.tsx:392-453) — numeric line, no area fill, points: SparklinePoint[] where that SparklinePoint is a DIFFERENT type imported from slowest-tests.server.ts (line 35: {day, avg}, schema confirmed at server line 37-39). One caller: slowest-tests.tsx:323.

So the collision is worse than the finder stated: there are TWO unrelated types both named SparklinePoint (one in sparkline.tsx, one in slowest-tests.server.ts) in addition to two components effectively named "Sparkline".

DELETION TEST: I confirmed exactly one render call site per component (3 total). DurationSparkline's logic is genuinely duplicate-numeric-line work currently smeared across two files, so folding it into MetricSparkline concentrates real duplicated implementation rather than minting a one-adapter seam — deletionTestPasses=true. HOWEVER the leverage is modest (two call sites for the numeric primitives), and the fold is NOT free: DurationSparkline differs from MetricSparkline in three behaviors MetricSparkline lacks — (a) it positions x by the real day value ((p.day-minX)/rangeX, line 436) so sparse/missing days render as gaps, whereas MetricSparkline index-spaces; (b) degenerate-count special cases (empty SVG for 0 points, single <circle> dot for 1 point, lines 401-423) — MetricSparkline just returns null on empty and has no 1-point handling; (c) no area fill. The finder's solution honestly acknowledges (a) ("accept either values:number[] or a points adapter"), but understates (b)/(c). A correct fold must absorb all three or it changes behavior (sparse days would silently become evenly-spaced — a real regression for the duration trend).

No ADR conflict — these are leaf presentational islands, untouched by durable decisions. severity correctly low.

Verdict revise (not keep): the headline frames the rename as the lead, but the rename is pure cosmetics with zero behavioral leverage, while the only deepening with real (if small) payoff is the numeric-sparkline consolidation — and that consolidation must be stated with its behavioral caveats so it isn't mis-executed as a lossy merge.

Dashboard auth · 5 findings

#54 · Dashboard auth
Caller's directed-invite identity (raw-SQL user.email + githubLogin) is re-resolved in four redemption paths; the matchConds predicate in three
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:100-118
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/invite-identity.ts:29-52
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/accept.ts:22-42
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/decline.ts:22-41
Problem — the friction

Four call sites independently resolve the caller's invite-addressing identity: fetch user.email via raw SQL, lowercase it, fetch userGithubAccounts.githubLogin via Drizzle, then build matchConds = [eq(teamInvites.email, email), eq(teamInvites.githubLogin, githubLogin)]. accept.ts and decline.ts are near-identical for lines 22-42. inviteMatchesUser does the same comparison imperatively; getPendingInvitesForUser does it as a query. This is a security-sensitive invariant (a leaked token must only redeem for the addressed identity) replicated four ways — if the matching rule changes (e.g. case-insensitive github logins, or a new identity channel like SSO), four sites drift independently and one missed site is an authz hole. The decline route's comment even explains why the binding matters, underlining that this is load-bearing logic that should not be hand-copied.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce one identity module that both halves consume:
1. getInviteIdentity(userId): Promise<InviteIdentity> — the 4-way-shared piece: the raw-SQL user.email fetch (lowercased) + userGithubAccounts.githubLogin select, returning { email: string|null; githubLogin: string|null }. This is the strongest seam — it sits on top of the auth-users raw-SQL read mandated by the Better-Auth-tables-not-in-Drizzle decision and concentrates that touchpoint.
2. inviteMatchConds(identity): SQL | null — the 3-way-shared piece: returns the Drizzle OR-conditions over teamInvites (and the "no addressable identity" null case that accept/decline currently turn into a 403, and authz turns into an early []). getPendingInvitesForUser, accept, and decline consume this.
3. Re-express inviteMatchesUser(invite, userId) on top of getInviteIdentity(userId) rather than re-fetching: compare the resolved identity against invite.email/invite.githubLogin (its check is the inverse of building matchConds, so it consumes the identity object, not the matchConds). This keeps invite-identity.ts the single home for both directed-invite operations.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: redemption routes shrink to const id = await getInviteIdentity(user.id); const conds = inviteMatchConds(id); if (!conds) return 403; — the matching rule is stated once. LOCALITY: the directed-invite security invariant lives in one tested function; adding an identity channel (SSO email alias, multiple github logins) is a one-place change that every redemption path inherits.

Deletion test

Deleting it makes the identity-fetch + matchConds construction reappear in all four redemption paths. Complexity reappears across 4 callers — earns its keep as a deepening.

Testability impact

The matching rule (the actual authz decision) becomes a pure, unit-testable function over an identity object — today it is only exercisable end-to-end through a live invite + live user table. A leaked-token-can't-redeem regression test stops requiring a full DB round-trip.

Interface sketch
getInviteIdentity(userId): Promise<{email:string|null; githubLogin:string|null}> inviteMatchConds(id): SQL[] | null // null => no addressable identity, caller 403s // invariant: a token only redeems for an identity the caller actually holds
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited sites. The duplication is real.

IDENTITY-FETCH (raw SQL select email from "user" where id = ... + .toLowerCase() + Drizzle userGithubAccounts.githubLogin fetch) is replicated at all 4 sites:
- authz.ts:100-112 (getPendingInvitesForUser) — Promise.all of raw-SQL email + githubLogin select, lowercases email.
- invite-identity.ts:33-49 (inviteMatchesUser) — same raw-SQL email fetch (lowercased) + githubLogin select, but used INVERSELY: it takes invite.email/invite.githubLogin and checks the caller against them, rather than building OR-conds over teamInvites.
- accept.ts:22-34 and decline.ts:22-34 — byte-for-byte identical identity-fetch blocks (confirmed via diff: the ONLY difference between accept.ts:22-42 and decline.ts:22-41 is the now line accept needs for its expiry filter).

MATCHCONDS construction ([eq(teamInvites.email, email), eq(teamInvites.githubLogin, githubLogin)] OR-conditions) is replicated at 3 of the 4: authz.ts:116-118 (as conds), accept.ts:37-42, decline.ts:36-41 (latter two include the identical matchConds.length===0 -> 403 guard). invite-identity.ts does the equivalent comparison imperatively (the inverse), so it does NOT literally build matchConds.

So the finder's title slightly overstates: matchConds-proper is 3-way; the identity FETCH is the 4-way shared piece. Both halves reappear on deletion across the cited callers — DELETION TEST PASSES (complexity is smeared across callers, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam).

Security-sensitivity confirmed: decline.ts:9-13 comment ("Without this binding any signed-in user could enumerate invite ids and burn other users' invites") and decline.ts:46-52 (0-changes -> 404 so callers can't distinguish "exists but not yours") show this matching is load-bearing authz. A missed site on a rule change (e.g. case-insensitive github logins, or a new SSO identity channel) is a genuine authz-drift risk.

NO ADR CONFLICT. The raw-SQL user.email read exists precisely because of Decision 3 (Better Auth user table owned by void/auth, not in db/schema.ts, joined via raw SQL). Consolidating it into one helper concentrates that migration-mandated raw-SQL touchpoint rather than reversing any decision — it complements the auth-users module the finding references.

Correctly EXCLUDED: pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/members.server.ts touches teamInvites.email/githubLogin but it is the invite LISTING/CREATION path (admin enters the addressee), not caller-self-identity resolution — so it's rightly outside this finding.

Severity adjusted high->medium: real and security-relevant, but the surface is small/contained (4 sites, all in the invite subsystem) and the system is pre-launch with no live data (Decision 9). Worth doing; not urgent.

#55 · Dashboard auth
GitHub-login mirror hook is best-effort glue welded into config, with no test seam and a silently-swallowed failure
medium severity effort: small confidence: high untestable
Files
  • apps/dashboard/auth.ts:37-66
  • apps/dashboard/auth.ts:114-152
Problem — the friction

captureGithubLogin (the GitHub /user fetch + upsert into userGithubAccounts) is a private function inside auth.ts, called only from inline databaseHooks.account.create/update.after closures. It cannot be imported or unit-tested — it lives in a config module that uses dynamic import("void/db")/import("@schema") specifically so void prepare can load the file at config time. The create and update hooks are byte-identical (chain default → if providerId !== "github" return → try/captureGithubLogin/catch{}), so the dedup logic is itself duplicated. Failures are swallowed entirely (catch {} / if (!res.ok) return), so a user whose github login silently failed to mirror gets directed invites that never resolve, with zero signal in logs (CLAUDE.md explicitly wants such errors routed through logger.*). This is the thing the assignment flags: fragile glue, not a deep isolated module.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract captureGithubLogin(userId, accessToken) (plus a shared mirrorGithubAccount(account, context) that does the providerId guard + default-chain + log-on-failure) into a small importable module (e.g. src/lib/github-account-mirror.ts). auth.ts's two hooks become one-line delegations to the shared function. Replace the empty catch with logger.warn. The dynamic-import-at-runtime trick stays inside the extracted module so auth.ts's config-time loadability is preserved.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: the create and update hooks share one tested function instead of two hand-kept-in-sync copies. LOCALITY: the GitHub-login mirroring invariant (only github accounts, best-effort, observable on failure) lives in one place; auth.ts shrinks to pure provider/signup configuration. Failures become visible in void project logs.

Deletion test

Partial pass-through risk: if the two hooks were trivial this would be a style nit. But they are not — they carry the default-chain-then-mirror ordering invariant and the providerId guard, duplicated. Deleting the extraction reinstates that logic in both hooks (2 call sites) and re-buries it untestably in config. Earns its keep as a small deepening + testability win.

Testability impact

captureGithubLogin and the providerId-guard become unit-testable (mock fetch + a stub db) — currently the only way to exercise GitHub-login capture is a full OAuth round-trip against real GitHub and a real D1, so it is effectively untested (no test references it).

Interface sketch
mirrorGithubAccount(account, context, chainDefault): Promise<void> // guards providerId==="github"; awaits chainDefault first; logger.warn on failure; never throws into the hook
Verifier notes

Every claim verified against apps/dashboard/auth.ts. captureGithubLogin (lines 37-66) is module-private — the only export is export default defineAuth(...) (line 84). Its only two call sites are the inline databaseHooks.account.create.after (line 129) and update.after (line 144) closures, which are byte-identical apart from create->update in the default-chain call: both do chain-to-default .after, then if (account.providerId !== "github") return, then try { captureGithubLogin } catch {} (lines 118-149). Dynamic import("void/db")/import("@schema") for config-time loadability confirmed (lines 55-58), and documented in the header comment (lines 34-35). Failure is doubly swallowed: if (!res.ok) return (line 50) and empty catch {} (lines 130-132, 145-147), with NO log signal — grep shows only one file in the entire dashboard (src/lib/action-errors.ts) imports void/log, so this hook is invisible to Cloudflare Tail, contradicting CLAUDE.md's explicit guidance to route caught errors through logger.*. The downstream-impact claim is real and material: the mirrored userGithubAccounts.githubLogin is the resolution key for github-directed invites in src/lib/invite-identity.ts, src/lib/authz.ts (findDirectedInvitesForUser), and routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/{accept,decline}.ts — so a silent mirror failure means a github-directed invite never resolves with zero diagnostic trail. No test references the function; the schemas.test.ts grep hit was a false positive on the CI-provider string "github-actions" (line 83), so coverage is genuinely zero. DELETION TEST (my own): the extraction concentrates ~12 lines of duplicated guard+default-chain+upsert logic currently smeared across the two identical hook closures into one importable module + makes the network/DB upsert unit-testable; deleting it re-duplicates and re-buries that logic. It concentrates rather than moves complexity, so it passes — but it is a modest deepening (2 call sites), consistent with the finder's own "small deepening + testability win" framing. ADR check: no durable decision is reversed. Decision 4 (github login mirrored into sibling userGithubAccounts table) is preserved by the extraction, and the config-time dynamic-import trick stays inside the extracted module, so auth.ts remains void-prepare-loadable. No adrConflict. The observability fix (logger.warn over empty catch) is the higher-value half; the extraction is the enabling seam. Severity medium is fair — not a correctness bug today (best-effort by design; accept/decline re-derive identity at redemption), but untestable network+DB glue plus a silent failure gating invite resolution clears the bar over low.

#56 · Dashboard auth
No owner module for void-managed auth tables — raw SQL + result-envelope casts against "user"/"account" are duplicated across 6 invite/profile/members callers
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/authz.ts:100-112
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/invite-identity.ts:33-41
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/accept.ts:22-34
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/decline.ts:22-34
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/profile.server.ts:19-33
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/members.server.ts:36-78
Problem — the friction

Decision #3 says the Better Auth user/session/account tables are not in the Drizzle schema and cross-table reads use raw SQL. That decision is fine, but there is no module that owns it — the raw SQL leaks everywhere. Six sites independently hand-write sql\select email from "user" where id = ${id}\` (varying in case: select/SELECT, limit 1/LIMIT 1), each re-derives the userRow.results?.[0] as { email?: string } cast shape, and the members loader hand-writes a memberships INNER JOIN "user" raw join with its own column-aliasing and a second as Array<{...}> cast. A maintainer changing how the user table is read (e.g. the table name, the D1 result envelope shape, adding email normalization) must find and edit all of them, and each cast is an untyped trust boundary against the void-owned schema. The knowledge that "user"` is the magic table name and how to safely shape its rows is smeared, not concentrated.

Solution — the deepened module

Introduce a deep src/lib/auth-users.ts as the ONLY place raw SQL touches the void-owned user/account tables. Surface three typed reads behind the seam — raw SQL, the .results?.[0]/.results ?? [] envelope handling, the casts, and email lowercasing all live inside:

- getUserIdentity(userId): Promise<{ email: string | null; githubLogin: string | null }> — used by all four invite-redemption callers (authz.getPendingInvitesForUser, invite-identity.inviteMatchesUser, invites/accept, invites/decline). This owns BOTH the lowercased email read AND the parallel userGithubAccounts lookup that every one of these sites currently re-writes, so the whole identity-resolution pattern (not just half) is concentrated. (If a caller ever needs only the email, a thin getUserEmail can delegate, but the four real callers all need the pair.)
- getUsersByIds(ids): Promise<Map<string, { email: string; name: string; image: string | null }>> — for the members loader; absorbs the raw memberships INNER JOIN "user" join and its as Array<{...}> cast.
- getUserAccounts(userId): Promise<{ providerId: string; createdAt: number | string | null }[]> — for settings/profile; absorbs the raw account read and its cast.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: callers get typed, normalized user/account data from one import and never touch raw SQL or D1 result envelopes again — the members loader collapses to a single getUsersByIds call. LOCALITY: the one fact that bridges our schema to void's (table names, result shape, normalization) lives in one file; a void upgrade that changes the user-table column casing is a one-file edit, not a six-site grep.

Deletion test

Deleting this module makes the raw SQL + casts reappear verbatim at all six callers (authz.getPendingInvitesForUser, invite-identity.inviteMatchesUser, invites/accept, invites/decline, settings/profile, settings/members). Complexity reappears across 6 callers — it earns its keep; this is a deepening that concentrates currently-smeared complexity.

Testability impact

Today every consumer must integrate against a live D1 with a real void-owned user table to be tested at all. With the seam, callers can be unit-tested with a stubbed getUserEmail/getUsersByIds, and the single raw-SQL adapter is the only thing needing the real-DB harness (which is a known-outstanding gap) — shrinking the integration-test surface from 6 sites to 1.

Interface sketch
getUserEmail(userId): Promise<string|null> // lowercased getUsersByIds(ids: string[]): Promise<Map<string,{email;name;image:string|null}>> getUserAccounts(userId): Promise<{providerId:string; createdAt:number|string|null}[]> // invariant: only file in the app that issues raw SQL against "user"/account
Verifier notes

All six cited sites verified against the files. (1) Four sites read user.email via raw SQL with a VERBATIM-duplicated cast userRow.results?.[0] as { email?: string } | undefined: authz.ts:101/109, invite-identity.ts:35/37, accept.ts:23/32, decline.ts:23/32. (2) Case variation is real — authz.ts + invite-identity.ts use lowercase select ... from "user" ... limit 1; accept.ts + decline.ts use uppercase SELECT ... FROM "user" ... LIMIT 1. (3) .toLowerCase() re-derived at each. (4) members.server.ts:37-42 hand-writes a raw memberships INNER JOIN "user" u join with its own column aliasing + a separate as Array<{userId,role,email,name,image}> cast (62-69). (5) profile.server.ts:20-38 reads the void-owned account table via raw SQL with its own as Array<{providerId,createdAt}> cast. (6) src/lib/ has no owner module (only api-auth, auth-client, authz, invite-identity) — confirmed no existing seam.

DELETION TEST PASSES: 6 real callers today (authz.getPendingInvitesForUser, invite-identity.inviteMatchesUser, invites/accept, invites/decline, settings/profile, settings/members). Deleting an auth-users.ts module makes the raw SQL + .results?.[0] envelope handling + the untyped as casts reappear verbatim at all six. This concentrates currently-smeared complexity — not a hypothetical one-adapter seam.

NO ADR CONFLICT: Decision #3 keeps Better Auth tables out of Drizzle and mandates raw SQL for cross-table reads. This finding does NOT reverse that — it routes that same raw SQL through ONE owner module. It actually fulfills the spirit of #3 by giving the "this is the magic table name + how to safely shape its rows" knowledge a single home. Good to flag adrConflict=none.

SEVERITY: down to medium. It's auth/identity-adjacent (each as cast is an untyped trust boundary against the void-owned schema; a single site forgetting .toLowerCase() is an invite-hijack vector — that's why concentration matters), but it's 6 small, currently-correct sites with low churn. "high" overstates it.

SOLUTION NEEDS SHARPENING (why revise, not keep): the proposed getUserEmail(userId) is necessary but INSUFFICIENT for the four invite sites. Each of those does the email read in a Promise.all ALONGSIDE a userGithubAccounts Drizzle query, then merges into an {email, githubLogin} identity (and three then build identical matchConds). A bare getUserEmail concentrates only the raw-SQL/cast half and leaves the parallel-query + merge pattern smeared across all four. The honest seam for the invite callers is a getUserIdentity that returns the full lowercased {email, githubLogin} pair. getUsersByIds (members) and getUserAccounts (profile) are correct as proposed.

#57 · Dashboard auth
Member-gated settings loaders open-code requireAuth->resolve->404 instead of a sibling member seam (owner seam already exists in settings-scope.ts)
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/settings-scope.ts:45-80
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/members.server.ts:29-34
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/projects.server.ts:15
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/general.server.ts:28
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/teams/[teamSlug]/projects/new.server.ts:46-65
Problem — the friction

settings-scope.ts already deepened the owner-gated path (requireOwnerScope / requireOwnedProjectScope concentrate requireAuth + param extraction + resolve + 404-not-403). But the *member-gated* read path is not covered: the members loader open-codes requireAuth(c) → c.req.param("teamSlug") → null-check → resolveTeamBySlug → 404, and the same skeleton recurs in the other team-settings loaders. So there are two parallel conventions — the deep owner seam and the open-coded member seam — and a maintainer must know which loaders went through settings-scope and which didn't. The dashboard-auth knowledge (requireAuth throws vs returns, the deliberate 404-not-403 leak-avoidance rule) is partly behind a seam and partly inline.

Solution — the deepened module

Add requireMemberScope(c, hereFor?) to settings-scope.ts mirroring requireOwnerScope but calling resolveTeamBySlug (any membership role) and 404-ing on null; make hereFor optional and return { team, here? } so loaders (which discard here) and actions (which need it) share one seam — exactly as keys.server.ts already does with requireOwnedProjectScope. Migrate the three member-gated LOADERS (members.server.ts:30-34, projects.server.ts:15-19, general.server.ts:28-32) onto it. Separately (and not part of this finding's deletion test), migrate the already-owner-gated projects/new.server.ts loader+action onto the EXISTING requireOwnerScope rather than its open-coded requireTeamOwner+try/catch. Optionally also fold a member project variant later if a member-gated project loader appears.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: member-gated loaders drop to one call and inherit the 404-not-403 rule for free. LOCALITY: the 'how a settings loader authenticates + resolves + handles missing/forbidden' policy lives entirely in settings-scope.ts; the leak-avoidance invariant is enforced in one place instead of trusted to each loader to re-implement.

Deletion test

Deleting requireMemberScope makes the requireAuth+param+resolve+404 skeleton reappear across the ~3-4 member-gated team-settings loaders (members, projects, general, plus any future ones). Complexity reappears across N≈4 callers — earns its keep. (This extends an existing deep module rather than creating a pass-through.)

Testability impact

The auth-and-resolve policy becomes testable once via the helper (correct 404 vs forbidden behavior) rather than re-verified per loader; loaders can be tested against a stubbed scope helper instead of needing a real membership row.

Interface sketch
requireMemberScope(c, hereFor?): Promise<{team; here}> // any role; 404 (not 403) on non-member or missing requireMemberProjectScope(c, hereFor?): Promise<{project; here}>
Verifier notes

Verified all cited files plus authz.ts and the keys.server.ts precedent.

REAL: settings-scope.ts:45-80 deepens the OWNER path (requireOwnerScope/requireOwnedProjectScope concentrate requireAuth + param + resolve + the deliberate 404-not-403 rule). Three member-gated settings LOADERS open-code the identical skeleton requireAuth(c) -> c.req.param("teamSlug") -> if(!teamSlug) throw 404 -> resolveTeamBySlug(user.id, teamSlug) -> if(!team) throw 404:
- members.server.ts:30-34
- projects.server.ts:15-19
- general.server.ts:28-32 (loader only; its actions DO use requireOwnerScope)
This is genuine triple duplication and a real inconsistency. The seam pattern is proven to work for loaders: keys.server.ts:27 already calls requireOwnedProjectScope(c, hereFor) from a loader and discards here. So a member-role sibling is a faithful extension, not a speculative seam.

DELETION TEST PASSES: delete a hypothetical requireMemberScope and the requireAuth+param+resolve+404 stanza reappears across members/projects/general (N=3) plus any future team-settings loaders. Concentrates complexity smeared across callers; extends an already-deep module (settings-scope.ts). Not a pass-through.

CORRECTIONS to the finding (why revise, not keep):
1. projects/new.server.ts:46-65 is MIS-CITED. It is OWNER-gated (uses requireTeamOwner with try/catch->404), NOT member-gated (resolveTeamBySlug). It does not belong in the member-skeleton tally. It is a separate, smaller miss: an owner loader+action that open-codes instead of reusing the EXISTING requireOwnerScope. So the real member-seam caller count is N=3, not "~3-4". Drop projects/new from the member-scope migration list; optionally note it as a one-line "migrate projects/new onto existing requireOwnerScope" cleanup.
2. The "two parallel conventions; must know which loaders went through settings-scope" framing slightly overstates. Within general/members the split is by handler ROLE (actions use the seam, loaders don't), not by file. The inconsistency is real but it's loader-vs-action, not whole-file.
3. t/[teamSlug]/index.server.ts:14-20 ALSO open-codes the same member skeleton (with getSession instead of requireAuth) but lives outside the settings tree — out of scope for a settings-scope helper unless the seam is promoted to a general authz helper.

ADR conflict: none. Consistent with logical tenant isolation / type-enforced scope (decision 2). The 404-not-403 leak-avoidance invariant is the single non-obvious bit of knowledge worth concentrating behind the seam.

Severity low is correct: 3 short read-path stanzas, no correctness risk (each copy 404s correctly today).

#58 · Dashboard auth
profile loader embeds void account-table storage knowledge (createdAt number/string coercion + credential/github providerId semantics) — fold into finding #1's getUserAccounts adapter rather than extract standalone
low severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/profile.server.ts:35-59
Problem — the friction

The profile loader doesn't just read the void-owned account table via raw SQL — it also embeds knowledge of that table's storage quirk: createdAt may come back as a number OR an ISO string, so it branches (typeof ts === "number" vs Date.parse(ts) → floor/1000) and reasons about providerId === "credential" (= has-password) and providerId === "github" inline. This is dashboard-auth/Better-Auth internal storage knowledge (how void persists account timestamps and what the credential provider id means) leaking into a page loader. If void changes its account-row encoding, this page breaks with no other site to consult, and the hasPassword/githubAccount derivation can't be reused by any future 'connected accounts' UI.

Solution — the deepened module

Do NOT extract a standalone adapter for this alone. Fold the number/string createdAt coercion and the credential/github providerId interpretation INTO finding #1's getUserAccounts adapter so it returns normalized rows ({ providerId, connectedAt: number | null }) with the timestamp coercion done once behind the seam. This finding should be tracked as a sub-item of finding #1: it has independent value only insofar as #1 is adopted. If #1 is dropped, drop this too rather than create a one-caller seam. (Optional, still only if #1 lands: a composing getUserAuthProfile(userId): { hasPassword; github: {login; connectedAt} | null } that joins userGithubAccounts, leaving the loader a pure projection.)

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: the loader receives ready-to-render fields; any future account-management surface reuses getUserAuthProfile. LOCALITY: the 'void stores account.createdAt as number-or-ISO-string' fact and the 'credential providerId means has-password' fact live behind the auth-user seam, not in a page.

Deletion test

Borderline today (one caller), but it is the same adapter as finding #1 — folding the timestamp coercion in is concentrating a void-storage detail, not adding a pass-through. As a standalone extraction it would be weak; bundled into getUserAccounts it earns its place and removes Better-Auth knowledge from the page tier.

Testability impact

The number-vs-ISO-string coercion and hasPassword/github derivation become unit-testable pure logic; today they're only reachable by rendering the profile loader against a real account table with real Better-Auth timestamp encoding.

Interface sketch
getUserAuthProfile(userId): Promise<{hasPassword:boolean; github:{login:string; connectedAt:number|null}|null}> // invariant: hides void account-row storage shape (number|ISO createdAt, credential/github providerIds)
Verifier notes

Friction is real and quoted accurately. apps/dashboard/pages/settings/profile.server.ts:35-59 casts the raw account SQL results and embeds void/Better-Auth storage knowledge in page-tier code: the number-OR-string createdAt coercion (typeof ts === "number" else Date.parse(ts) → Math.floor(parsed/1000) at lines 48-52), plus providerId === "credential" (= has-password, line 40) and providerId === "github" (line 41) semantics. This is exactly the "how void persists account rows" detail that should not live in a page loader.

DELETION TEST — fails as a standalone. I grepped the whole dashboard: the raw account-table read (FROM account) exists ONLY in profile.server.ts. The Date.parse / Math.floor(parsed/1000) timestamp coercion exists ONLY here (grep returned just lines 50-51). getUserAccounts does NOT exist yet. The other providerId references are unrelated: auth.ts:127/142 are Better Auth's own githubProfile callback hooks, and profile.tsx:142 is the client-side authClient.unlinkAccount call — neither is a duplicate raw-SQL read. Consumer profile.tsx reads only hasPassword / githubAccount.login / githubAccount.connectedAt (formatted via formatRelativeTime); it never touches the raw row. So N=1: deleting a hypothetical getUserAuthProfile/getUserAccounts adapter re-concentrates complexity in one loader, not across N callers. It would be a one-adapter hypothetical seam justified only by a speculative future "connected accounts UI."

The finder concedes this ("As a standalone extraction it would be weak") and the finding is explicitly parasitic on finding #1 — it only earns its place when the timestamp coercion is folded INTO finding #1's getUserAccounts adapter so the void-storage detail is concentrated there rather than created anew. That is a fair concentration argument, but it is entirely conditional on finding #1 standing; on its own merits this finding's deletion test does not pass.

No ADR conflict: reading void-owned Better Auth tables via raw SQL is the sanctioned pattern (durable decision #3), and the proposed adapter preserves that — it does not propose declaring account in db/schema.ts. Severity low is correct.

Disposition: keep the insight but reframe it as a rider on finding #1, not a standalone seam, and stop implying it independently concentrates smeared complexity (it does not — N=1).

Scripts, tooling & config · 6 findings

#59 · Scripts, tooling & config
Demo bootstrap screen-scrapes form-action 302s for team/project creation; seed-demo.mjs still parses a key-reveal cookie that the app already removed
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high deep but fragile revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/seed-demo.mjs:163-297
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/seed-demo.mjs:252-297
Problem — the friction

seed-demo.mjs creates the team, project, and API key by POSTing to the human-facing form-action routes (/settings/teams/new, /settings/teams/:slug/projects/new, /settings/teams/:slug/p/:proj/keys?createKey) with redirect:'manual', then inferring success/failure by regex-matching the 302 Location header (team slug at line 181, project success path at line 229) and recovering the plaintext API key by parsing the Set-Cookie list for wrightful_reveal_key and URL-decoding it (lines 252-297). This couples the bootstrap deeply to UI route shapes and a UI-only one-time-reveal cookie mechanism: a refactor that changes the keys route's actionName, the redirect target, the reveal-cookie name, or that route's success/error 302 convention silently breaks pnpm setup:local with errors like 'reveal cookie was missing'. The script even documents that team creation is INSERT-ALWAYS so a re-run makes a duplicate team (lines 190-199) — fragility it can only detect, not avoid. None of this scope/provisioning logic is shared with the app; the app already has authz + scope helpers (authz.ts resolveTeamBySlug/resolveProjectBySlugs, api-key.ts minting) that encode the canonical create-team/create-project/mint-key operations.

Solution — the deepened module

Two parts. (1) Immediate bug fix: seed-demo.mjs:252-297 targets a route/action and cookie that no longer exist (POST /settings/teams/.../keys?createKey + wrightful_reveal_key). Repoint it at the existing JSON minting seam POST /api/teams/:teamSlug/p/:projectSlug/keys and read body.token — exactly what dashboard-fixture.ts:337-354 already does. (2) Close the remaining gap by extending the same JSON-route pattern to team + project creation: add owner-auth'd JSON routes (e.g. POST /api/teams returning { teamSlug }, POST /api/teams/:teamSlug/projects returning { projectSlug }) that run the canonical slug-pick + insert path currently inlined in pages/settings/teams/new.server.ts and projects/new.server.ts. Extract that create logic into a small src/lib helper the form action AND the new route share, so the screen-scraping callers (seed-demo.mjs and dashboard-fixture.ts) consume a stable typed JSON contract instead of parsing 302 Location headers — and the two bootstrap copies stop drifting. Prefer this over the finder's proposed net-new POST /api/dev/bootstrap-demo endpoint: a single bespoke bootstrap endpoint is shallower (one caller shape) than reusing the per-resource JSON-route pattern the key route already established.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: bootstrap becomes one call returning the three values the seeder needs, instead of three brittle HTTP-redirect dances. Locality: team/project/key provisioning is defined once in src/lib (where authz + api-key already live); UI route refactors (actionName, redirect targets, the reveal-cookie name) no longer break local setup. Idempotency can be solved properly behind the seam (upsert team) instead of the seeder bailing on a 'demo-2' slug.

Deletion test

Deleting the HTTP-scraping bootstrap does NOT remove the need to create team+project+key — that complexity reappears wherever a demo environment is stood up (setup:local AND the e2e dashboard-fixture, which boots its own ephemeral dashboard + API key per the upload-fixtures comment at lines 22-26). A shared provisioning seam earns its keep across 2 callers (local seeder, e2e fixture). The redirect/cookie scraping is fragile incidental complexity that vanishes once a real seam exists.

Testability impact

Provisioning is currently only validated by running the whole live flow and observing it didn't abort. A lib-level bootstrap function (or dev endpoint) can be unit/integration tested against the real-DB harness once it exists, and the e2e fixture's parallel bootstrap can share the same code path instead of maintaining its own.

Interface sketch
// dev-only, guarded by ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP && !prod bootstrapDemo(opts: { email; password; teamName; projectName; keyLabel }): Promise<{ teamSlug; projectSlug; apiKey }> // idempotent: upsert team/project, mint fresh key
Verifier notes

Friction is real but the finding is partly stale and must be revised.

CONFIRMED:
- Two real callers screen-scrape the human form-action routes to bootstrap a demo account: apps/dashboard/scripts/seed-demo.mjs and packages/e2e/src/dashboard-fixture.ts. Both POST /settings/teams/new and regex-match the 302 Location for the team slug (seed-demo.mjs:181; dashboard-fixture.ts:302), and POST /settings/teams/:slug/projects/new then compare the 302 Location path to infer success vs validation error (seed-demo.mjs:229-237; dashboard-fixture.ts:320-332). This is genuine fragile coupling to UI route shapes.
- The create-team operation (slug-pick + db.batch insert team + owner membership) lives INLINE in pages/settings/teams/new.server.ts:58-119 with no shared lib helper and no JSON route; project-new is the same shape. So a Node script genuinely cannot reach the canonical create path except by scraping the form action. routes/api/teams/ contains only invites.ts and keys.ts — no team/project create route.
- INSERT-ALWAYS duplicate-team fragility at seed-demo.mjs:189-199 is real.
- Deletion test holds and is STRONGER than the finder argued: the bootstrap complexity demonstrably reappears across both callers, and the copy-paste has already drifted into a latent bug.

FINDER GOT WRONG (the reason for revise, not keep):
- The reveal-cookie half is STALE. There is NO createKey server action and NO wrightful_reveal_key cookie anywhere in the dashboard (grep across apps/dashboard returned zero hits). Commit 1d854e3 already replaced server-side key minting with POST /api/teams/:teamSlug/p/:projectSlug/keys returning { token } as JSON (routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/p/[projectSlug]/keys.ts:26-93; keys.server.ts:18-25 doc explicitly says "no flash cookie, no full reload" and "This replaces the server-side createKey action"). dashboard-fixture.ts:334-354 already mints via that JSON route and its comment notes "there's no pre-Void server-action reveal cookie." BUT seed-demo.mjs:252-297 was never migrated — it still POSTs to the dead /keys?createKey route and parses the dead wrightful_reveal_key cookie. So seed-demo.mjs is already broken on key minting; this is a live bug, not a hypothetical future refactor risk.
- Finder cites "api-key.ts minting" as an existing canonical helper; api-key.ts only exports validateApiKey (minting is inlined in the route). authz.ts exports only resolve/read helpers, not create helpers. So the canonical create helpers the finding leans on do not exist for team/project — that is the actual gap.

ADR CONFLICT: none. The fix stays within existing patterns (extend the existing JSON-route convention; no DO/auth/nuqs/ETL reversal).

#60 · Scripts, tooling & config
Base-URL env var is named two different ways across the script pipeline
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/seed-demo.mjs:43
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/setup-local.mjs:147
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/setup-local.mjs:192
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/upload-fixtures.mjs:27
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:164
Problem — the friction

The same concept — 'the dashboard origin to talk to' — is plumbed under two different env-var names. seed-demo.mjs requires WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL (line 43); upload-fixtures.mjs, the reporter, and the entire e2e suite use WRIGHTFUL_URL. As a result setup-local.mjs has to set BOTH depending on which child it spawns: WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL when invoking seed-demo (line 147) and WRIGHTFUL_URL when invoking upload-fixtures (line 192). This is a leaky seam: the orchestrator must memorise that two of its children disagree on the variable name. Anyone wiring a new script against the demo flow has a coin-flip chance of picking the wrong name and getting a silent 'requires WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL' abort.

Solution — the deepened module

Standardise on WRIGHTFUL_URL — the name the reporter, e2e, upload-fixtures, and all public docs already share. In seed-demo.mjs read process.env.WRIGHTFUL_URL (update the line 17 doc comment and the line 45 abort message to match), and in setup-local.mjs delete the WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL line (:147) so the seed child gets WRIGHTFUL_URL: baseUrl like the fixtures child (:192). Because nothing has deployed and seed-demo is an internal/dev-only script (its only non-orchestrator caller is the manual pnpm db:seed-demo), skip the deprecated WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL fallback the finder proposed — it adds branch logic for a back-compat obligation that doesn't exist. A straight rename is the cleaner collapse: one name, no alias to maintain.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: every script + the reporter accept the same variable, so any of them can be pointed at any dashboard with one consistent flag. Locality: the orchestrator stops carrying per-child env-name knowledge; the credential-injection comment in upload-fixtures (the e2e suite passes WRIGHTFUL_URL) and seed-demo finally agree.

Deletion test

This is a collapse, not an extraction: removing the WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL alias and using one name removes the orchestrator's special-casing (setup-local sets one var, not two). The 'inconsistency' complexity vanishes entirely — confirming it was incidental, not load-bearing.

Testability impact

Minor: a single, documented env contract makes the scripts easier to drive from a test harness (the e2e global-setup already passes WRIGHTFUL_URL; seed-demo currently can't be driven the same way). Reduces the surface where a wrong-name typo produces an opaque failure.

Interface sketch
const baseUrl = process.env.WRIGHTFUL_URL ?? process.env.WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL; // BASE_URL deprecated
Verifier notes

Verified every cited line. seed-demo.mjs:43 reads process.env.WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL and aborts at :45 with "requires WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL" (also documented at :17). setup-local.mjs sets WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL: baseUrl for the seed-demo child (:147) and WRIGHTFUL_URL: baseUrl for the upload-fixtures child (:192) — same baseUrl value from startDevServerForSeed, two different names. A repo-wide grep confirms WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL exists in exactly 4 places, ALL inside the seed pipeline (seed-demo read + its doc comment + setup-local set). Every other consumer uses WRIGHTFUL_URL: the reporter (packages/reporter/src/index.ts:164), the entire e2e suite (packages/e2e/vitest.globalSetup.ts:48, tests-dashboard/global-setup.ts:70, playwright.config.ts), upload-fixtures.mjs:27, and all public docs (README.md:38, SELF-HOSTING.md:111, reporter README). So WRIGHTFUL_URL is unambiguously the de-facto contract and WRIGHTFUL_BASE_URL is the lone dissenter — the finding's factual claims are exact.

Deletion test PASSES as a collapse, not a move. The "two names" complexity exists solely because seed-demo disagrees with the canonical name. Renaming seed-demo to read WRIGHTFUL_URL makes setup-local.mjs:147 and :192 set the same single var, and the inconsistency disappears with nothing reappearing elsewhere — no new seam, no adapter, no relocated logic. Callers/consumers of the shared name confirmed: reporter, e2e (3 files), upload-fixtures, public docs — the inconsistency is smeared across the orchestrator's two spawn sites and the standalone path.

Strengthening evidence the finder missed: seed-demo.mjs is ALSO a user-facing entry point via pnpm db:seed-demo (apps/dashboard/package.json:23), referenced as such in worklogs. Run standalone it passes no env, so a developer must hand-set the base URL — under the one name that contradicts every doc and sibling script. That is precisely the "coin-flip / silent abort" path the finding describes.

ADR conflict: none. This is a script-tooling rename, untouched by any durable decision. No env key is declared in apps/dashboard/env.ts for either name (these are process env for Node scripts, not Void-declared keys), so no env.ts schema change is needed.

Severity correctly low: dev-only seeding scripts, no production/wire impact; mild DX papercut on the standalone db:seed-demo path.

#61 · Scripts, tooling & config
History-seeding loop hand-rolls an untested, no-retry copy of the reporter's StreamClient ingest path
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/setup-local.mjs:234-273
  • packages/reporter/src/client.ts:38-170
  • packages/reporter/src/index.ts:21
Problem — the friction

setup-local.mjs's --history path opens runs, batches results, and completes them by inlining its own HTTP client (lines 240-249: a bare postJson that JSON-stringifies, sets the Bearer + Content-Type + X-Wrightful-Version:3 headers, and throws on !res.ok). This is a strictly weaker re-implementation of StreamClient.openRun/appendResults/completeRun in packages/reporter/src/client.ts, which already encodes the hard-won ingest behaviour: retry on 5xx/429, per-attempt AbortSignal timeouts, Retry-After honoring, AuthError hinting, and aggressive retry on completeRun (maxRetries 5) precisely because a dropped complete leaves a run stuck at status='running'. The script's loop has none of this: a single 429 from the API_RATE_LIMITER (120/min, declared in wrangler.jsonc) during a multi-hundred-run seed just increments failedCount and moves on, and a transient 5xx aborts a whole run. A maintainer touching ingest semantics now has two clients to keep honest, only one of which is tested. The reporter already ships X-Wrightful-Version + headers logic centrally; the script re-types the magic '3' string by hand.

Solution — the deepened module

Re-export StreamClient (and AuthError) from packages/reporter/src/index.ts so it's available via the package's public . export, then have the history seeder in setup-local.mjs construct new StreamClient(baseUrl, seedConfig.apiKey) and call openRun → chunked appendResults → completeRun. This single-sources the protocol version, header assembly, and retry/timeout/Retry-After/idempotency behind one tested interface, eliminating the hand-retyped "X-Wrightful-Version": "3" and the second untested client. Frame the benefit primarily as duplication/single-sourcing and DX correctness (one client to keep honest, the magic version string stops being duplicated), NOT as fixing a production 429/availability risk — the script runs against local miniflare where rate limiting fails open. Caveat: setup-local.mjs is .mjs importing local .mjs siblings; it would now need to import the built reporter (dist) or its TS source via the workspace package, so confirm the import resolves in the script's runtime before adopting.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the seeder gets production-grade ingest reliability (429 backoff, 5xx retry, complete-run durability) with zero added code — exactly what callers want from a deep client. Locality: ingest HTTP semantics live in one tested module; a change to the wire headers or retry policy no longer needs a mirror edit in a .mjs script. Removes the second hand-typed 'X-Wrightful-Version: 3'.

Deletion test

Deleting the inline postJson loop does NOT vanish complexity — the same open/append/complete + retry behaviour reappears, and StreamClient already provides it for the reporter caller and the (hypothetical) seeder caller. So a shared StreamClient earns its keep across 2 callers (reporter onEnd flush, history seeder). The inline postJson, by contrast, is a shallow re-derivation that should be collapsed into the existing deep module.

Testability impact

Today the seeder's ingest behaviour is only exercised end-to-end against a live dev server inside setup:local — there is no unit test and the known-outstanding real-DB harness gap means it is effectively untested. Routing it through StreamClient means its reliability is covered by the reporter's existing client tests; the seeder's only remaining responsibility (payload generation, already pure in generator.mjs) stays unit-testable.

Interface sketch
// re-export from packages/reporter/src/index.ts export { StreamClient } from "./client.js"; // seeder: const client = new StreamClient(baseUrl, apiKey); // const { runId } = await client.openRun(run.openPayload); ... await client.completeRun(runId, status, durationMs)
Verifier notes

Factual claims verified against the cited code:

- setup-local.mjs:234-273 inlines exactly what's described: a headers object with hand-written "X-Wrightful-Version": "3" + Bearer + Content-Type (lines 234-238), a bare postJson (240-249) that JSON-stringifies, throws on !res.ok, no retry; the loop (255-273) does open → chunked append (BATCH_SIZE 50) → complete and on any throw just failedCount++.
- client.ts:79-263: StreamClient genuinely encodes the hard-won behaviour — fetchWithRetry retries 5xx/429 (line 52), per-attempt AbortSignal.timeout (50), Retry-After honoring (56-59), AuthError hinting (69-77/107-108), and completeRun uses { maxRetries: 5 } (160) with the documented "leaves the run stuck at status='running'" rationale (142-146). headers getter (85-91) single-sources PROTOCOL_VERSION=3.
- StreamClient is NOT re-exported: index.ts:21 imports it internally only; index.ts exports just the WrightfulReporter default (137) + helpers (79/598/613/647). package.json exports map exposes only "." → dist/index.js. So the solution's premise (add the export) is correct.
- Two real callers confirmed: WrightfulReporter (index.ts:183 new StreamClient) and the hypothetical seeder. Deletion test passes — removing the inline loop, the open/append/complete+retry behaviour reappears and is already provided by the deep StreamClient.
- Seeder needs no artifacts (seed/generator.mjs builds openPayload/resultsPayload/completePayload only; clientKey is just r.testId echoed at line 265). So it uses a clean subset of StreamClient — good fit, no artifact-path complications.

Correction that lowers severity (the finder oversells the runtime risk): the headline "a single 429 during a multi-hundred-run seed" scenario is essentially inert here. setup-local.mjs seeds against a LOCAL vp dev/miniflare server, and middleware/03.rate-limit.ts:20-21 explicitly documents that checkRateLimit FAILS OPEN when the API_RATE_LIMITER binding is missing (local dev) — the binding lives only in wrangler.jsonc and is merged at deploy time. So 429s won't occur during the local seed. The transient-5xx and lost-complete risks are real in principle but the script targets localhost and already exits non-zero on any failure (lines 284-287). This is a local-dev convenience script, not the production ingest path — hence low, not medium.

No ADR conflict: the finding consolidates an HTTP client, touches none of the durable decisions (single D1, logical tenancy, void/auth ownership, void/live, etc.).

#62 · Scripts, tooling & config
sha40 helper duplicated across upload-fixtures and the seed generator with two divergent algorithms (minor duplication, not a depth win)
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/upload-fixtures.mjs:209-219
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/seed/generator.mjs:42-46
Problem — the friction

Both fixture generators need a deterministic 40-char hex commit SHA, and each rolls its own sha40. upload-fixtures.mjs:209 uses a self-seeded LCG keyed by an integer n; generator.mjs:42 uses 20 random bytes drawn from the shared PRNG. They produce different distributions and neither is shared, so the 'fake but stable commit SHA' concept lives in two places with two implementations. Minor on its own, but it is a symptom of the larger pattern: the synthetic-data primitives (PRNG, sha40, pick, randInt) exist only in generator.mjs (where they're clean and pure) yet upload-fixtures re-invents the ones it needs rather than importing the catalog/generator helpers.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract a single deterministic sha40 into scripts/seed/lib (or export from generator.mjs) and have both call sites use it. Pick one contract — the cleanest is sha40(rand) taking a PRNG, with upload-fixtures deriving a per-index PRNG via makePrng(String(n)) so its volume SHAs stay stable. Note generator.mjs's helpers (sha40/randInt/pick/makePrng) are currently UNTESTED, so if this is consolidated it would be worth adding a small unit test for the shared helper at the same time (do not describe the existing code as already tested). This is a minor duplication cleanup on shallow leaf utilities, not a depth/leverage win.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: any script needing fake-but-deterministic test metadata pulls from one helper set. Locality: the synthetic-data vocabulary (SHA, branch picker, PRNG) is single-sourced in scripts/seed, matching where the catalog already lives.

Deletion test

Deleting upload-fixtures' inline sha40 does NOT remove the need for a deterministic SHA — it reappears (generator.mjs needs it too). A shared helper earns its keep across 2 callers (upload-fixtures volume scenarios, generator buildRun). The duplicate LCG is a shallow re-derivation.

Testability impact

Low — both are pure already. Consolidating gives one place to unit-test 'sha40 is stable + 40 hex chars' rather than two divergent versions, one of which (the LCG) is otherwise untested.

Interface sketch
// scripts/seed/catalog.mjs or a new lib: export function sha40(rand): string // 40 lowercase hex, deterministic given rand
Verifier notes

Duplication is real and the technical description is accurate. upload-fixtures.mjs:209-219 defines sha40(n): a self-seeded LCG keyed by integer index n ((n+1)*0x9e3779b1, no PRNG dep), used at line 229 for volume-scenario SHAs. generator.mjs:42-46 defines sha40(rand): draws 20 bytes from the shared xorshift32 PRNG, used at line 248 for commitSha. Different signatures, algorithms, and distributions. Confirmed neither is shared: generator.mjs exports only makePrng and generateHistory (sha40/randInt/pick are module-private, lines 34/38/42), and upload-fixtures imports only node:child_process, node:fs, node:url, picocolors, and ./lib/spinner.mjs — nothing from seed/. The two scripts are independent entrypoints (upload-fixtures spawns playwright; setup-local.mjs dynamically imports generateHistory at line 223).

TWO CORRECTIONS to the finding:
(1) The solution's claim that generator.mjs "already defines tested versions" is FALSE. grep across all .test.*/.spec.* files found zero unit tests for sha40, makePrng, or generateHistory. The only seed/playwright/*.spec.ts files are synthetic fixtures the generator PRODUCES, not tests OF it. This matches the KNOWN-OUTSTANDING note that lib/integration tests are unported. The revised solution must not lean on a non-existent tested helper.
(2) Deletion test fails under the DEPTH lens. sha40 is a ~10-line pure leaf utility — a shallow module whose interface (deterministic 40-hex string) is nearly as complex as its implementation. The finder's deletion-test argument ("need reappears in generator") is the DRY/duplication argument, not a leverage/depth argument. Consolidating concentrates ~10 lines across exactly 2 call sites; it centralizes no behaviour, invariant, ordering, or error mode. Locality improves marginally; leverage does not. Also the two functions have incompatible signatures (n:int vs rand:fn), so a shared helper can't be a drop-in for both without choosing one contract — slightly more work than "import rather than re-derive."

No ADR conflict. Severity low is correct (dev-only seed tooling, off all runtime/tenant/ingest paths). Keep as a duplication cleanup, not a deepening opportunity.

#63 · Scripts, tooling & config
Synthetic-run seeder hand-builds the v3 wire payload as an untested third copy of the reporter contract, and has already drifted (omits projectName/workerIndex)
low severity effort: medium confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/seed/generator.mjs:135-281
  • packages/reporter/src/types.ts:7-69
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts:64-148
Problem — the friction

generator.mjs assembles openPayload (run meta + plannedTests), resultsPayload (per-test results + attempts), and completePayload literally by hand (lines 240-272), duplicating the structure that already exists in two synced places: the reporter's TS interfaces (OpenRunPayload/TestResultPayload/TestAttemptPayload in types.ts) and the dashboard's Zod schemas (OpenRunPayloadSchema etc. in schemas.ts). CLAUDE.md explicitly calls this a 'shared schema contract' kept in sync via a canary contract test — but the seed generator is a THIRD, untested hand-maintained copy of the same wire shape, with no canary. It has already drifted: the generator's plannedTests omit projectName (types.ts PlannedTestDescriptor requires it), and its result objects omit projectName and workerIndex (TestResultPayload requires them). It survives only because schemas.ts marks those fields .optional(). The generator also encodes createdAt/completedAt backdating that depends on the dev-only BackdateSeconds escape hatch in schemas.ts:129 — a coupling no type checks. A maintainer adding a required wire field updates types.ts + schemas.ts + the contract test, and silently leaves the seeder producing invalid payloads that only fail at runtime against a live server.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract a tiny plain-data payload builder that both the reporter and the seeder feed (the reporter would call it after deriving fields from Playwright via buildTestDescriptor; the seeder calls it with synthetic fields). Functions like buildOpenRunPayload(meta, plannedTests), buildResultPayload(testFields, attempts) returning objects typed against the same interfaces the Zod schemas mirror, and validating required fields (projectName, workerIndex) at runtime so the .mjs seeder fails loudly rather than at the server. Do NOT use the finder's path (a): buildPayload/buildTestDescriptor consume Playwright TestCase/PendingTest objects the seeder does not have. The generator keeps its PRNG/incident/lifecycle/backdating logic and just feeds the builder. As a cheaper alternative if a new module is unwanted: add the seeder's payloads to contract.test.ts as fixtures so the existing canary catches drift.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the seeder gets a guaranteed-valid v3 payload for free and inherits any new required field automatically. Locality: the wire shape is defined once (or twice with a contract test), not three times; drift like the current missing projectName/workerIndex becomes a type error at the seeder's call site instead of a latent runtime failure.

Deletion test

Deleting the hand-built object literals does NOT remove complexity — the v3 payload shape must still be produced. It reappears identically across 3 callers (reporter onEnd, generator.mjs history seeder, and the contract test's fixtures). A shared builder concentrates that shape; the literals are a shallow re-derivation that should collapse into it.

Testability impact

generator.mjs is already pure and unit-testable, but nothing asserts its output conforms to the contract. Routing through a shared builder (or importing schemas.ts to parse generator output in a test, as the reporter's contract.test.ts already does for reporter payloads) makes 'seeder emits valid v3' a fast unit assertion instead of a live-server discovery.

Interface sketch
// shared (reporter + scripts): buildOpenRunPayload(meta: RunMeta, planned: PlannedTestDescriptor[]): OpenRunPayload buildResult(t: { testId; title; file; projectName }, attempts: TestAttemptPayload[]): TestResultPayload // invariant: output parses through schemas.ts OpenRunPayloadSchema/TestResultSchema
Verifier notes

Verified against all cited files plus the seed driver.

DUPLICATION IS REAL. generator.mjs:240-272 hand-builds openPayload/resultsPayload/completePayload as object literals; buildTestResult (135-198) hand-builds the per-test result + attempts. This is a third encoding of the v3 wire shape alongside the reporter's TS interfaces (types.ts) and the dashboard's Zod schemas (schemas.ts). The seeder is a .mjs script that posts raw JSON via fetch (setup-local.mjs:240-265, X-Wrightful-Version: 3 at :237) — it imports neither the TS interfaces nor the Zod schemas, so there is no compile-time check and the contract.test.ts canary does not cover it. Confirmed it is untested against the contract.

DRIFT IS REAL AND CORRECTLY DIAGNOSED. plannedTests (generator.mjs:256-260) omits projectName; the buildTestResult return (183-197) omits both projectName and workerIndex. types.ts requires projectName (lines 22, 40) and workerIndex (line 29). It only validates because schemas.ts marks projectName .nullable().optional() (79, 105) and workerIndex .optional() (85). The BackdateSeconds coupling is also real: createdAt (generator.mjs:242 via openPayload) and completedAt (:271) ride the dev-only BackdateSeconds escape hatch (schemas.ts:129/134/146), type-unchecked.

DELETION TEST PASSES. Three live sites encode the shape: reporter buildPayload/buildTestDescriptor (index.ts:613,647), seeder buildRun/buildTestResult, and contract.test.ts fixtures. Deleting the seeder literals does not remove the need to produce a valid v3 payload — it reappears. A shared plain-data builder concentrates it. The seeder retains genuinely unique logic (PRNG, incidents, lifecycle, backdating), which is correct — that is not the duplicated part.

CORRECTIONS TO THE FINDING:
1. Solution path (a) is NOT viable. buildPayload/buildTestDescriptor take Playwright TestCase/PendingTest objects (index.ts:613-650, reads test.parent.project(), test.titlePath(), test.location); the seeder has only synthetic plain data and no Playwright runtime. Only path (b) — a shared plain-data builder — applies. The finder's "where shapes overlap" hedge papers over this.
2. Cross-language caveat: the seeder is untyped .mjs. A shared TS builder gives runtime structural correctness but still no compile-time check inside the .mjs seeder unless the builder validates required fields at runtime (or the seeder is converted to .ts/checked). The "silently invalid until runtime" failure mode is only fully closed if the builder requires the fields at runtime.

SEVERITY: lowered to low. This is a dev-only seed/setup tool, not production ingest. Blast radius is "seeded local data is slightly unrealistic" and "a future required wire field silently produces bad seed payloads." Real maintenance trap, but confined to the dev loop — medium overstates it.

No ADR conflict. Reusing the reporter's exports or extracting a shared @wrightful/protocol builder touches none of the durable decisions.

upload-fixtures.mjs re-derives dev-server.mjs's dashboard-readiness probe instead of importing it
low severity effort: small confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/lib/dev-server.mjs:71-111
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/upload-fixtures.mjs:53-71
  • apps/dashboard/scripts/setup-local.mjs:240-249
Problem — the friction

There are three near-identical 'is the dashboard up?' probes. dev-server.mjs exports two (probeDashboard: POST /api/runs with Bearer, treats 400=up/401=auth-rejected; probeDashboardUnauthed: GET /api/auth/get-session, any response=up). upload-fixtures.mjs:53-71 inlines a FOURTH copy of the authed probe verbatim (same POST /api/runs, same body '{}', same 400/401 status comment) instead of importing the one in dev-server.mjs — even though both live in scripts/. The 'X-Wrightful-Version: 3' header and the 400-means-ready convention are copy-pasted into each. A maintainer who changes the readiness contract (e.g. adds a /health route, or the empty-body POST stops returning 400) must find and fix every copy; missing one leaves a script hanging for its full 90s/180s deadline before a confusing timeout.

Solution — the deepened module

Two-step, in order of value:

(1) upload-fixtures.mjs should import { probeDashboard } from "./lib/dev-server.mjs" and delete its verbatim local probe() (lines 53-71), so the authed-probe convention (POST /api/runs, empty body, 400=ready, X-Wrightful-Version:3) lives behind ONE function with ONE comment block. This is the safe, behaviour-preserving step.

(2) To also collapse upload-fixtures' bespoke ensureDashboardRunning (line 90) into lib/dev-server.mjs:ensureDashboardRunning, first generalize the lib helper to accept an injected auth-rejected callback/message (today it hardcodes the ".env.seed.json" remediation at line 142). upload-fixtures needs the env-mode variant of that message (lines 73-86) for its e2e-suite caller. Once the message is a parameter, upload-fixtures calls the shared helper and its duplicate poll/spawn/signal-handler block disappears.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers say 'ensure it's up, give me the baseUrl' and get spawn + poll + auth-rejection handling for free. Locality: the 400-means-ready convention and the X-Wrightful-Version constant exist once; changing the health-probe endpoint is a one-line edit.

Deletion test

Deleting the inlined probe in upload-fixtures.mjs does NOT vanish complexity — probing reappears (it's the same logic dev-server.mjs already has). The dev-server.mjs ensureDashboardRunning earns its keep across 2 real callers (setup-local via startDevServerForSeed, upload-fixtures via its own duplicate). The duplicate is pure pass-through re-derivation that should collapse.

Testability impact

Probe semantics are currently only validated by running the full setup flow. A single exported probe/ensure function can be unit-tested against a stub fetch (200/400/401/network-error → up/up/auth-rejected/down), which is impossible when the logic is smeared across three inline copies.

Interface sketch
// already exists at dev-server.mjs:127 — just consume it everywhere: ensureDashboardRunning(seed: { url; apiKey }, opts?): Promise<{ baseUrl; spawned }>
Verifier notes

Core duplication is real but the "three times" count is wrong. Verified all three cited locations:

1. dev-server.mjs:71-111 — CONFIRMED. probeDashboard (authed POST /api/runs, body "{}", X-Wrightful-Version:3, 400=up/401=auth-rejected) + probeDashboardUnauthed (GET /api/auth/get-session, any response=up). These two are intentionally DISTINCT (one needs an API key, one doesn't for pre-seed), not duplicates of each other. Both feed ensureDashboardRunning (line 127) and startDevServerForSeed (line 232).

2. upload-fixtures.mjs:53-71 — CONFIRMED as a genuine verbatim duplicate of probeDashboard: same POST /api/runs, same body:"{}", same "X-Wrightful-Version":"3", same 400/401 comment block. No import from lib/dev-server.mjs despite both living in scripts/. Additionally its ensureDashboardRunning (line 90) re-implements the full probe+90s-poll+spawn+SIGINT/SIGTERM-handler orchestration that lib/dev-server.mjs:ensureDashboardRunning already provides.

3. setup-local.mjs:240-249 — MISCITED. These lines are the headers object + postJson helper for the --history ingest loop (postJson posts /api/runs, /results, /complete), NOT a readiness probe. setup-local does ZERO inline probing — it imports startDevServerForSeed (line 7) and delegates at line 137. It is the CLEAN caller / counterexample, the opposite of a duplicate.

So the real picture: ONE verbatim probe duplicate (upload-fixtures) against the canonical pair in dev-server.mjs — not "three near-identical probes." Title should drop the "three times" claim.

Deletion test PASSES: removing upload-fixtures' inline probe()+ensureDashboardRunning does not vanish complexity — the readiness convention (POST /api/runs empty body => 400=ready) plus spawn/poll/signal-handler orchestration must still exist and already does in lib/dev-server.mjs. Real callers of the lib helper: setup-local (via startDevServerForSeed) is the first; upload-fixtures should be the second. Pure re-derivation collapsing into an existing deep module.

Solution caveat the finder glossed: upload-fixtures cannot drop-in call lib's ensureDashboardRunning unchanged, because upload-fixtures supports env-mode callers (the e2e suite, lines 21-30) whose authRejected() remediation message differs (lines 73-86) from lib's hardcoded ".env.seed.json" message (line 142). The minimal honest fix is importing probeDashboard to kill the verbatim duplicate; the fuller collapse requires lib's ensureDashboardRunning to accept an injected auth-rejected handler/message.

No ADR conflict — this is dev-tooling under scripts/, untouched by the durable decisions. Severity low confirmed: not request-path; worst case is a confusing 90s timeout exactly as described.
