#65 · Tests & testability
Tenant-isolation scope predicates are emitted in 18 inline query sites but asserted only by one 5-case live browser spec covering 2 endpoints
high severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable revised by verifier touches a durable decision
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/scope.ts:61
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:66
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/branches-query.ts:13
  • packages/e2e/tests-dashboard/cross-tenant.spec.ts:100
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:660
Problem — the friction

Logical tenant isolation is THE durable security invariant (every run-scoped query must filter by projectId, and teamId where present). Yet the only test that proves a foreign caller can't read/write another tenant's data is cross-tenant.spec.ts — which seeds a second user via HTTP, opens a real run, and asserts 404s through a live Playwright browser + booted dashboard. There is no unit-level assertion that, e.g., appendRunResults' ownership SELECT (ingest.ts:660-665) actually filters by projectId, or that scopedRunsWhere (runs-filters-where.ts:66-75) always AND-s both eq predicates. The bug surface (a dropped eq(runs.projectId, …) anywhere) is enormous and the test surface for it is a single heavyweight integration spec. A regression in a non-runs table (testResults, artifacts) wouldn't even be caught by cross-tenant.spec.ts since it only probes /results and /register.

Solution — the deepened module

Two-tier, ordered by cost. (1) Cheap, no-DB, do now: unit-test the predicate emission. scopedRunsWhere, the appendRunResults ownership predicate, loadProjectBranches' where, and register.ts's three predicates all build Drizzle SQL fragments — call them with two distinct project ids and assert via toSQL()/serialization that BOTH eq(projectId) and eq(teamId) (where applicable) are present, so a dropped predicate fails compilation-time. This needs no database and closes the "is the scoped predicate actually emitted" runtime gap the brand can't cover. (2) Behavioral, contingent: once the real-DB Drizzle test harness (KNOWN-OUTSTANDING — not yet built; void-db-stub.ts is a throwing placeholder, not an in-memory adapter) lands, seed two projects and assert each scoped op returns/writes nothing across the tenant line, including the non-runs tables (testResults, artifacts) that cross-tenant.spec.ts never probes. Keep cross-tenant.spec.ts as the final integration gate. Do NOT frame tier (2) as if the adapter already exists.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get a regression net on the system's core security property without booting a browser. Locality: 'is this query tenant-scoped' becomes answerable in one fast test per operation instead of inferring it from one broad e2e that only covers two endpoints.

Deletion test

cross-tenant.spec.ts is earning its keep as a final integration gate, but its scope-coverage responsibility is smeared too thin (2 endpoints). The proposed unit-level scope tests concentrate the invariant per-operation; deleting them would re-expose every scoped query (N = every DB-touching lib) to silent isolation regressions.

Testability impact

Per-table, per-operation isolation becomes a fast unit assertion. Today only /results and /register cross-tenant denials are tested, and only via live browser; testResults/artifacts/summary scope leaks are entirely uncovered.

Interface sketch
test: seed projA, projB runs; expect appendRunResults(scopeA, runOwnedByB) === {kind:'notFound'}; expect scopedRunsWhere(teamA,projA,f) compiles with both eq predicates present
Durable-decision note

Touches durable decision #2 (logical tenant isolation, type-enforced). Not reopening it — reinforcing it: the type brand prevents passing a raw id, but nothing currently asserts at runtime that the scoped predicate is actually emitted.

Verifier notes

All cited code verified and accurately described. scope.ts:61 tenantScopeForApiKey returns the branded scope; the brand is compile-time only — nothing asserts the predicate is actually emitted at runtime. runs-filters-where.ts:66-75 scopedRunsWhere AND-s eq(runs.teamId) + eq(runs.projectId) inline in both branches; a dropped predicate leaks silently. branches-query.ts:13 loadProjectBranches filters teamId+projectId+isNotNull inline. ingest.ts:660-665 appendRunResults ownership SELECT filters by (projectId, id) and returns notFound — verified. cross-tenant.spec.ts confirmed: a single heavyweight spec that seeds User B over HTTP, boots a real dashboard, and probes exactly two ingest endpoints (/results, /register) plus three UI routes through a live Playwright browser. It does NOT assert isolation on testResults reads, branches, insights, run-detail loaders, or the artifact testResultId/artifacts ownership predicates.

No unit-level scope test exists: all 10 dashboard test files are pure-function (aggregate-delta, schemas, rate-limit, etc.); the only references to scopedRunsWhere/loadProjectBranches/tenantScopeForApiKey are their own definition files. The scope predicate is genuinely smeared across 18 distinct query call sites (8 page .server.ts loaders + several routes/api/* + lib). DELETION TEST PASSES: per-operation unit tests concentrate the projectId-emission invariant; deleting them re-exposes every one of those 18 sites to silent regression. register.ts (the third "non-runs table" surface the finding names) independently scopes runs(:71), testResults(:88), and artifacts(:125) by projectId — three separate predicates, none covered by any unit test, and a regression in the testResults/artifacts predicate would NOT be caught by cross-tenant.spec.ts (which only asserts a 404 on a fake testResultId, not cross-tenant projectId scoping).

CORRECTION TO SOLUTION (reason for revise, not keep): the solution opens with "With the in-memory db adapter in place, add focused scope tests..." — but that adapter does NOT exist. The only db test helper is src/__tests__/helpers/void-db-stub.ts, whose db export is a Proxy that THROWS on any property access; its own docstring says DB-touching tests must use vi.mock('void/db', ...) "with a real Drizzle binding" — which is the unbuilt real-DB harness from KNOWN-OUTSTANDING. So the finding's solution is contingent on infrastructure that isn't committed. The honest, immediately-actionable half of the solution is the WHERE-fragment snapshot: compile scopedRunsWhere / the ownership predicate to a Drizzle SQL fragment and assert both eq(projectId) and eq(teamId) appear — this needs NO database and catches a dropped predicate directly.

No ADR conflict: reinforces durable decision #2 (logical, type-enforced tenant isolation) rather than reopening it; adrConflict honestly flagged by finder.

#66 · Tests & testability
API-key resolution (hash lookup + revocation + timing-safe compare) has no unit coverage despite being pure-enough to extract
medium severity effort: small confidence: high untestable
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/api-key.ts:31
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/api-key.ts:13
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/api-auth.ts:23
Problem — the friction

validateApiKey (api-key.ts:31) is the entire ingest auth gate: prefix slice, SHA-256 hash, candidate fetch, timing-safe compare across same-prefix keys, revoked check, and a waitUntil lastUsedAt bump. Only the live e2e proves 'bad key -> 401' (e2e.test.ts) — the branch logic (multiple same-prefix candidates, revokedAt set, malformed header) is untested because the function takes a Hono Context and queries db inline. The genuinely tricky parts (timingSafeEqualHex, the find-among-candidates loop, the revoked gate) are buried behind a Context + db dependency that no unit test can satisfy.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract a pure, IO-free selector: selectMatchingKey(candidates: ApiKey[], rawKey: string): Promise<ApiKey | null> (async only because hashKey uses crypto.subtle) that hashes rawKey, runs timingSafeEqualHex across candidates, and applies the revokedAt filter. validateApiKey stays the thin IO wrapper: parse the Bearer header, fetch candidates by prefix, delegate to selectMatchingKey, then fire the waitUntil lastUsedAt bump. Unit-test selectMatchingKey with hand-built candidate rows covering: single match, two same-prefix rows where only one hash matches, a matched-but-revoked row (-> null), and no-match. Mirror the existing apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/artifact-tokens.test.ts pattern (which already mocks void/env and tests the sibling timingSafeEqual). Frame the payoff as a unit-test seam for the security decision, not as cross-caller consolidation — there is only one caller.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the auth decision is exercisable with fixtures (matching key, revoked key, prefix collision, wrong hash) in milliseconds. Locality: the security-sensitive compare/revoke logic concentrates in one pure function with one test file, instead of being provable only by spinning a Worker.

Deletion test

Extracting the selector then deleting it would push hash/compare/revoke logic back inline into a Context-bound function — complexity reappears at the one caller (api-auth.ts -> middleware/02) and stays integration-only. The extraction earns its keep by giving the decision a unit-test seam.

Testability impact

Prefix-collision correctness, revoked-key rejection, and constant-time-compare behavior become unit-testable. Currently only the happy/401 paths are covered, and only via the booted dashboard.

Interface sketch
selectMatchingKey(candidates: ApiKey[], rawKey: string): ApiKey | null // hash + timing-safe compare + drop revoked validateApiKey = thin IO wrapper that fetches candidates and delegates
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. validateApiKey (api-key.ts:31) does exactly what the finder claims, inline in one function: Bearer parse (line 36-37), 8-char prefix slice (line 40), SHA-256 hashKey (line 41), candidate fetch by prefix from db (line 43-46), timing-safe compare across same-prefix candidates via candidates.find(...timingSafeEqualHex) (line 48), revokedAt gate (line 50), and an executionCtx.waitUntil lastUsedAt bump (line 52-58). timingSafeEqualHex (line 13) is pure.

Coverage claim confirmed: zero unit tests reference validateApiKey or timingSafeEqualHex (grep across apps/dashboard/src/__tests__ and whole tree). The only coverage is live e2e — packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:85 ("rejects requests without an auth token (401)") and :94 ("rejects requests with a bad API key (401)"). Those exercise only the no-header and single-bad-key paths over HTTP; the genuinely tricky branches (two rows sharing a prefix, revokedAt set on the matched row, malformed-but-present header) are never reached.

The friction (pure decision buried behind Context + inline db) is exactly as described — no unit test can satisfy a Hono Context + live D1.

Strong in-repo precedent for the proposed extraction: artifact-tokens.ts already factors a security-critical pure crypto decision (HMAC sign/verify, with its own timingSafeEqual at line 60) and artifact-tokens.test.ts unit-tests it with forged/tampered/expired inputs (no Context/db). selectMatchingKey(candidates, rawKey) is directly analogous and unit-testable with hand-built rows. There's even a near-duplicate: two separate timing-safe comparators exist (api-key.ts hex string vs artifact-tokens.ts Uint8Array), and only the latter is tested.

No ADR conflict. The extraction does not touch logical-tenancy, branded ids, or single-D1 decisions; it's a same-file refactor.

Deletion-test caveat: validateApiKey has exactly ONE caller (api-auth.ts:27 -> middleware/02.api-auth.ts). So the finder's framing — "complexity reappears across N callers" — is slightly off; the complexity is not smeared across N call sites. The real payoff is concentrating the pure security decision (hash + timing-safe match + revoked filter) into a named, IO-free seam that is currently unreachable by any unit test. deletionTestPasses=true on the corrected basis: deleting selectMatchingKey forces hash/compare/revoke back into a Context+db-bound function, re-burying the security decision behind IO and re-collapsing the test surface. The value is locality + a real unit-test seam, not cross-caller leverage. Severity medium is fair: it is the ingest auth gate, but it's one small function and the happy/sad extremes do have superficial e2e coverage.

#67 · Tests & testability
Ingest orchestrators' composition is untestable through their interface — and the one "merge" unit test exercises a JS reference completeRun never calls
medium severity effort: medium confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:547
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:654
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:764
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:683
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/aggregate-delta.test.ts
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/merge-run-status.test.ts
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/helpers/void-db-stub.ts:55
Problem — the friction

ingest.ts cleanly extracts the tricky algorithms (computeAggregateDelta, mergeRunStatus, statusBucket, buildChangedTests) and unit-tests them thoroughly. But the actual bug surface is the composition in appendRunResults/completeRun: the ordering invariant that the LAST batch statement must be the summary .returning() (ingest.ts:683-696 reads batchResults[batchResults.length - 1]), the delta-vs-recompute selection, the verify-ownership→batch→bump→broadcast sequencing, and the heterogeneous as never batch casts. None of that is reachable in a unit test because the orchestrators import db from void/db, which the stub Proxy throws on (void-db-stub.ts:55-66). A maintainer changing the batch shape (e.g. inserting a statement after the summary SELECT, or reordering tag-delete vs insert) gets a green unit suite and only learns of the break from the full booted-dashboard e2e — if at all, since the dogfood path only asserts on rendered HTML.

Solution — the deepened module

Two viable surfaces; lead with the lighter one. (a) Minimum: in ingest.ts replace the direct db import with an injectable parameter (or a module-scoped dbFor() indirection) defaulting to the void/db db, so tests can pass a fake exposing select/batch that records the statement array and returns canned summary rows. Assert the invariants that have no other guardrail: the last batch statement is the summary (returning/select), ownership-check precedes any write, bumpTeamActivity and broadcastRunUpdate fire only after a successful batch, and the duplicate/notFound short-circuits skip writes. (b) Critically, add at least one test that drives the REAL SQL merge in completeRun (currentStatusSeveritySql/statusExpr), not just the mergeRunStatus JS reference — today a green merge-run-status suite tests a function completeRun never calls. Either approach is acceptable; prefer reusing the planned real-Drizzle harness (per the void-db-stub docstring) if it lands first, so this doesn't add a parallel abstraction the harness would obviate.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers (the 3 route handlers) keep the same one-call interface but the composition becomes assertable. Locality: the batch-ordering invariant and the 'last statement is the summary' coupling — currently smeared as an implicit contract between buildResultInsertStatements, aggregateDeltaStatement, and the array-index read — concentrate into one seam a maintainer can pin with a recorded-statement test.

Deletion test

Deleting the proposed executor seam makes complexity REAPPEAR: the ordering/ownership/broadcast logic is real and currently has N=3 callers (routes/api/runs/index.ts, [id]/results.ts, [id]/complete.ts) plus crons/finalizeStaleRun, all of which can only be exercised end-to-end today. Earning its keep.

Testability impact

appendRunResults can be tested for: notFound when ownership SELECT is empty; the no-delta path appending aggregateSummarySelectStatement as the last statement; mapping returned only for results with a clientKey; broadcast called with the summary from the last batch row. completeRun can assert the SQL status-merge expression position and that broadcast fires only when a summary row exists. All currently integration-only.

Interface sketch
interface RunWriter { select(q): Promise<Row[]>; batch(stmts): Promise<unknown[]>; } appendRunResults(scope, runId, payload, now, w: RunWriter = db): Promise<Outcome> // invariant: last stmt in batch yields the broadcastable summary row
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited code; the friction is real on every material point.

INTERFACE / SEAM: openRun (ingest.ts:547), appendRunResults (:654), completeRun (:764), and finalizeStaleRun (:824) all reference the module-level db imported from void/db. The test stub db (void-db-stub.ts:55-66) is a Proxy that throws on ANY property access. I grepped the whole suite: there is exactly ONE reference to vi.mock("void/db") and it's only inside the stub's own docstring — no test actually mocks it with a real binding. So none of the four orchestrators are reachable through their interface in a unit test. Confirmed.

COVERAGE IS PURE-LEAVES-ONLY: test inventory is aggregate-delta.test.ts (computeAggregateDelta), merge-run-status.test.ts (mergeRunStatus), build-changed-tests.test.ts, schemas.test.ts, plus unrelated (rate-limit, artifact-tokens, safe-next-path, active-project, content-types, group-tests-by-file). All pure functions. Confirmed.

ORDERING INVARIANT IS REAL: all three batch sites read batchResults[batchResults.length - 1] (:692, :799, :842) and rely on the summary statement being pushed last — appendRunResults does statements.push(summaryStmt as never) (:685), completeRun puts aggregateRecomputeStatement last (:795), finalizeStaleRun likewise (:839). Inserting any statement after the summary, or reordering, silently corrupts the broadcast with no unit-test failure. The heterogeneous as never casts (:243,:253,:263,:294,:579,:623,:685,:688,:796,:840) also defeat the compiler as a backstop, so ordering is enforced by nothing.

CALLERS (deletion test): routes/api/runs/index.ts (openRun), routes/api/runs/[id]/results.ts (appendRunResults — I read it; it is pure auth+translation), routes/api/runs/[id]/complete.ts (completeRun), crons/sweep-stuck-runs.ts (finalizeStaleRun). N=4. None can exercise the composition except end-to-end. A BatchExecutor seam concentrates the smeared composition invariants into one surface; deleting it scatters them back to e2e-only. Concentration, not movement — deletionTestPasses=true.

STRENGTHENING CORRECTION the finder missed: completeRun does NOT call mergeRunStatus. It uses a parallel SQL construction — currentStatusSeveritySql() (:745) feeding statusExpr (:783). So merge-run-status.test.ts greens a function the shipping orchestrator never invokes; the actual atomic-merge SQL that runs in production is untested. This is a textbook case of "pure leaf tested, real composition untested" and reinforces the finding.

NO ADR CONFLICT: the proposed executor wraps the same single-D1 Drizzle db; it introduces no per-team DO, no Better-Auth table declaration, no nuqs, no ETL. Decision 1/2/10 untouched.

WHY MEDIUM not HIGH: known-outstanding already tracks "real-DB test harness not built (most lib/integration tests unported)", and the stub's own docstring (lines 8-9) prescribes the conventional fix — vi.mock("void/db") with a real Drizzle binding — which would also cover these orchestrators end-to-end without adding a production abstraction. The executor seam is a sharper, faster surface for the composition invariants specifically, but it overlaps the already-tracked harness work and is one of several routes to coverage, so it is not independently high-severity.

#68 · Tests & testability
Artifact-register handler skips the ingest.ts planning/IO split, leaving safeKeySegment + artifactIdentity (idempotency key + key-sanitizer) with no unit seam
low severity effort: medium confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:51
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:108
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:142
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:158

Problem — the friction

Unlike the runs handlers (which delegate to ingest.ts), register.ts inlines ~140 lines of real logic in the route: size-limit check, ownership SELECT, per-testResultId validation chunked under D1's param cap, idempotent re-registration keyed by artifactIdentity (register.ts:34-42), R2 key construction with safeKeySegment, and presign URL emission. The only test is the e2e 'registers, uploads, downloads end-to-end' (e2e.test.ts:206) which needs a booted dashboard, a streamed run, and a scraped (runId,testResultId). The two purest, most bug-prone bits — artifactIdentity (tuple join, role-null normalization) and safeKeySegment (path-strip, charset, length bound, traversal defense) — are private functions with zero direct coverage, even though safeKeySegment is a security control against header/key injection.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract the pure planning step from register.ts into ingest.ts (the file that already owns this pattern) as planArtifactRegistration({ requestedArtifacts, existingRows, scope, runId, now }) returning { rowsToInsert, uploads }, and export safeKeySegment + artifactIdentity for direct unit testing. The handler keeps exactly the IO it must own: the size-limit guard, the two SELECTs (ownership + existing-by-testResultId), and the conditional chunked batch insert (181-190). Everything between the fetched rows and the response becomes a pure function over already-fetched data. Add a vitest (alongside aggregate-delta.test.ts) covering: safeKeySegment path-strip/control-char/leading-dot/length-bound/empty-fallback cases; artifactIdentity role-null normalization and within-request duplicate collapsing; and the reuse-vs-insert branch of the planner. Frame this as a testability + consistency fix (aligning register.ts with the appendRunResults/computeAggregateDelta convention), not as a depth gain — there is one caller, so the value is the test seam and uniformity, not concentrating smeared complexity.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the route shrinks to auth + IO + translation, consistent with the runs handlers. Locality: idempotent-reuse and key-sanitization rules live in one tested place instead of being provable only by the heaviest e2e in the suite.

Deletion test

Inlining is the anti-pattern here — the logic is real and currently has 1 caller, but it duplicates the 'planning vs IO' split ingest.ts already established for runs. Extracting concentrates it; deleting the extraction returns to an untestable 140-line handler. Net deepening.

Testability impact

safeKeySegment (traversal/charset/length), artifactIdentity collisions, and the within-request duplicate-dedup (register.ts:178) become unit-testable. Idempotent reuse of an existing r2Key is currently only exercisable end-to-end.

Interface sketch
planArtifactRegistration(args): { rowsToInsert: ArtifactInsert[]; uploads: Upload[] } export function safeKeySegment(name): string; export function artifactIdentity(a): string
Verifier notes

Code claims all verified against the files.

register.ts (read in full, 193 lines): the handler genuinely inlines all the logic the finding lists — size-limit check (54-64), ownership SELECT (68-73), per-testResultId validation chunked at MAX_IN_ARRAY_IDS=99 (77-104), idempotent re-registration keyed by artifactIdentity (109-132, 142-156), R2 key construction with safeKeySegment (158), and presign URL emission (150-178). safeKeySegment (22-26) and artifactIdentity (34-42) are module-private with no exports.

Contrast with runs handlers is real and stark: routes/api/runs/[id]/results.ts is 26 lines and is pure auth+translation, delegating to appendRunResults in src/lib/ingest.ts (header comment literally says "the handler is auth + translation only"). complete.ts is 33 lines, index.ts 40. register.ts is the outlier ingest-adjacent route that never adopted the pattern.

No vitest in apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/ references register. The only coverage is packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:206, which needs inject("dashboardUrl") (a booted dashboard), a seeded run, and a scraped (runId, testResultId) pair via beforeAll — confirmed at e2e.test.ts:182-301. It exercises one happy path (trace.zip) + one not-found case; it cannot enumerate the safeKeySegment edge cases (path-strip, control-char→underscore, leading-dot strip, 200-char bound, empty→"artifact" fallback) or artifactIdentity role-null normalization.

The pattern the finding wants ALREADY EXISTS as precedent: computeAggregateDelta is exported from ingest.ts and unit-tested directly in aggregate-delta.test.ts:2 with no DB. So "pull pure planning logic out of the ingest path, export it, unit-test it" is an established, blessed pattern here — the solution is idiomatic, not speculative.

WHY REVISE NOT KEEP: the finder's own deletionTest text is honest — "the logic is real and currently has 1 caller." That means the CLASSIC deletion test (complexity smeared across N callers reappearing on deletion) does NOT pass: N=1, so deleting the extraction does not make complexity reappear across multiple call sites. This is not a depth/leverage win and shouldn't be framed as "net deepening." It is a localize-for-testability + consistency move: it concentrates two bug-prone, security-sensitive pure functions behind a testable seam and aligns register.ts with the ingest.ts convention. That is a legitimate missing-locality finding, but the framing should drop the "net deepening" language. Severity adjusted high→… the finder said medium; I lower to LOW because: (a) it's a single-caller refactor, no correctness bug, no duplication being removed; (b) safeKeySegment's security value is modest — R2 keyspace is flat (the doc comment at 14-20 explicitly says "no real path traversal"); the function defends against malformed keys, not a live exploit; (c) it's pure DX/test-seam improvement on ~140 lines that currently work. Worth doing, low urgency.

No ADR conflict — mirrors decision 10 (db.batch chunking) and the existing ingest split; reverses nothing.

#69 · Tests & testability
E2E dogfood harness scrapes runIds from runs-list HTML and hand-copies the artifact-token HMAC (hardcoding only BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, drifting from the ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET fallback) — test-fragility, not a deepening
low severity effort: small confidence: high coupling revised by verifier
Files
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:315
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:34
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:148
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/artifact-tokens.ts:67
Problem — the friction

readSeededTestResult (e2e.test.ts:315-352) recovers a runId by regex-matching the runs-list HTML, then hits an internal preview API. The artifact tests re-implement signArtifactToken in the test (e2e.test.ts:34-47), duplicating the HMAC scheme from artifact-tokens.ts:67 and re-injecting BETTER_AUTH_SECRET. This couples the e2e's ability to find data to the exact HTML the runs-list renders (a render-only refactor — e.g. the regex-targeted href format — silently breaks data discovery, not a UI assertion), and couples token-forging correctness to a hand-copied crypto routine that can drift from the source. The 'renders ... test result data' assertions (e2e.test.ts:159-176) also OR over loose substrings ('demo'||'spec'||'Test Results'), so they pass on almost any non-empty page.

Solution — the deepened module

Two independent test-fragility cleanups (not a deepening):
1) Data discovery: stop scraping runId from runs-list HTML. Have globalSetup learn the seeded runId/testResultId once (capture them from the reporter run, or make one query to the stable internal test-preview/summary API) and expose them via project.provide() alongside the other injected fixture values, so the artifact tests consume given ids instead of regexing render output. Keep the HTML-substring checks only as explicit UI-render assertions, and tighten them to a stable data-testid rather than the 'demo'||'spec'||'Test Results' OR.
2) Token signing: eliminate the hand-copied HMAC. Extract the dashboard's token crypto into a void/env-free helper that takes the secret as an argument (signArtifactToken delegates to it, reading env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET), then import that helper from the e2e and pass the injected secret. This removes the silent drift on ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET. A direct import of the current signArtifactToken is not viable due to its void/env coupling and divergent signature.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: the data-driven artifact/round-trip tests stop being hostage to render markup and to a duplicated crypto copy. Locality: the token scheme has one definition; a change to it breaks compilation in the test rather than silently passing a stale forgery.

Deletion test

The HTML-scrape and the duplicated signer are pass-throughs that ADD fragility without hiding complexity — deleting them in favor of provided ids + the real signer removes coupling and loses nothing. This is a collapse, not a deepening, but it directly shrinks the bug surface the e2e introduces.

Testability impact

Artifact register/upload/download e2e becomes deterministic (no HTML-shape dependency) and the token path tests the real signer, so a token-format change can't pass against a stale copy.

Interface sketch
globalSetup: project.provide('seededRunId', …); project.provide('seededTestResultId', …) import { signArtifactToken } from '@wrightful/dashboard/src/lib/artifact-tokens'
Verifier notes

All cited code verified.

HTML-scrape (e2e.test.ts:315-352 readSeededTestResult): confirmed. It fetches PROJECT_URL HTML, regex-matches /t/${TEAM_SLUG}/p/${PROJECT_SLUG}/runs/([\w]+) to recover a runId (also done inline at lines 161-166), then calls the internal route GET /api/t/.../runs/:runId/test-preview (verified to exist at apps/dashboard/routes/api/.../test-preview.ts) and takes the first id across failed/flaky/passed/skipped buckets. So data discovery for the artifact tests is genuinely coupled to the exact runs-list href format — a render-only href refactor breaks data discovery, not a UI assertion. Real friction.

Duplicated signer (e2e.test.ts:34-47): confirmed. The e2e reimplements the token scheme with node:crypto createHmac, while the source (artifact-tokens.ts:67-86) uses Web Crypto crypto.subtle. Real latent-drift bug the finder under-stated: artifact-tokens.ts:50 keys on env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, and ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is a declared (optional) env var (env.ts:25). The e2e copy hardcodes BETTER_AUTH_SECRET only. If ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is ever set in the e2e fixture env the download test silently mis-signs. Today the fixture never sets it, so the bug is dormant — hence low, not medium.

Loose render assertions (e2e.test.ts:171-176 OR over 'demo'||'spec'||'Test Results'): confirmed, they pass on nearly any non-empty page.

DELETION TEST FAILS as a deepening. readSeededTestResult has exactly ONE caller (the Artifacts beforeAll at e2e.test.ts:184-191); signArtifactToken-copy has one caller (line 271). The finder concedes "this is a collapse, not a deepening." Nothing is smeared across N callers to concentrate; this is test-fragility cleanup, not interface leverage. No deep module is created or strengthened.

SOLUTION IS PARTLY WRONG. (1) "globalSetup already runs the reporter and knows the run" overstates it: globalSetup (vitest.globalSetup.ts:40-54) runs execSync('npx playwright test', { stdio:'pipe' }) and DISCARDS stdout; the runId lives only in the reporter process / dashboard DB. To provide it via project.provide() the fixture must additionally learn it (parse reporter output, or query a stable internal API once). (2) "Import the dashboard's signArtifactToken — it's a plain async function" is not clean: packages/e2e has NO dependency on @wrightful/dashboard (package.json), artifact-tokens.ts imports void/env (line 2) which is a Void-runtime binding not resolvable in a plain Node vitest process, the function reads its secret from env not from a param, and its signature is (payload: {r2Key,contentType}, ttl) vs the e2e copy's (r2Key, contentType, ttl). Importing it would require first extracting a void-free, secret-injectable crypto helper.

No ADR conflict.

#70 · Tests & testability
finalizeStaleRun and completeRun share a batch-recompute-broadcast tail by copy, not by construction (no enforcing seam)
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:824
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:786
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:799
Problem — the friction

finalizeStaleRun (ingest.ts:824-849) is the cron watchdog's terminal path. It re-implements completeRun's tail: db.batch([statusUpdate, aggregateRecomputeStatement]), read the last row as the summary, broadcast if present (compare ingest.ts:786-805). The two share the 'recompute is the last statement, its returning() row is the broadcast summary' invariant by copy, not by construction. Neither path has a unit test (both need the real-DB harness), and the cron caller is even further from any test than the route handlers. If completeRun's batch tail changes (e.g. summary moves position), finalizeStaleRun won't follow and stale runs will broadcast a wrong/absent summary — caught by nothing.

Solution — the deepened module

Factor the shared tail into reconcileAndBroadcast(runId, statusUpdateStmt, scopeForRecompute, { changedTests = [] }) that: appends aggregateRecomputeStatement, runs db.batch, extracts the last-row summary, and broadcasts when present. completeRun and finalizeStaleRun pass their own status-update statement (the one part that genuinely differs). Do NOT make this depend on the separately-proposed RunWriter seam — the consolidation stands on its own as a plain function and is worthwhile regardless. Note the consolidated helper becomes unit-testable only once the real-DB harness (known-outstanding) lands; until then the win is locality — the last-statement/returning-summary invariant lives in one place instead of being mirrored by convention across two functions (and the cron docstring). Optionally extend it to also cover appendRunResults's tail (passing changedTests + the trailing delta/select stmt) for a 3rd caller.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: both terminal paths share one verified implementation of the 'recompute + broadcast final summary' behavior. Locality: the last-statement-is-summary invariant lives in one function rather than being duplicated across the normal-complete and watchdog paths.

Deletion test

Deleting the shared tail makes the duplication reappear in its current 2 callers (completeRun, finalizeStaleRun). Concentrating it is a deepening; the invariant currently smeared across both is exactly what the deletion test rewards consolidating.

Testability impact

The terminal recompute+broadcast (currently only reachable by waiting out the stale window in a booted dashboard, or by /complete e2e) becomes a unit test over a recorded batch and a captured broadcast.

Interface sketch
reconcileAndBroadcast(w: RunWriter, runId, statusUpdate): Promise<RunAggregateSummary | undefined> // completeRun and finalizeStaleRun both delegate the recompute+broadcast tail here
Verifier notes

Verified against ingest.ts. The duplication is real and matches the description. completeRun's tail (786-805) and finalizeStaleRun (824-849) are structurally identical: db.batch([<statusUpdate>, aggregateRecomputeStatement(...)]) with the recompute LAST, then summaryRows = batchResults[batchResults.length-1] as readonly RunAggregateSummary[] | undefined, summary = summaryRows?.[0], and if (summary) broadcastRunUpdate(runId, [], summary). The "recompute is last statement → its .returning() row is the broadcast summary" invariant is shared by copy, exactly as claimed. aggregateRecomputeStatement (429-444) ends in .returning(AGGREGATE_SUMMARY_COLUMNS), confirming the contract.

DELETION TEST: shared tail across 2 real callers (completeRun, finalizeStaleRun). Cron caller crons/sweep-stuck-runs.ts:35 invokes finalizeStaleRun in a loop — even its docstring (lines 13-18) asserts it is "the same reconcile-and-broadcast path completeRun uses", so the duplication is acknowledged in-tree as an intended mirror, which is precisely the kind of by-convention invariant a seam should enforce by construction. Concentrating it concentrates currently-smeared complexity. Passes.

Two corrections to the finding's framing (don't change the verdict):
1. appendRunResults (687-699) follows the SAME structural pattern (push summary stmt last → batch → read last row → broadcast) but is NOT identical: it pushes deltaStmt ?? aggregateSummarySelectStatement, broadcasts WITH changedTests, and returns notFound when summary absent. So the truly-identical tail is exactly the 2 callers the finder named — the count is correct. A well-designed reconcileAndBroadcast could optionally absorb appendRunResults too (3rd caller) if it takes changedTests + the trailing stmt, strengthening the case.
2. The status-UPDATE statements differ materially (completeRun: monotonic SQL case status merge + max() on duration/completedAt; finalizeStaleRun: flat status:"interrupted" guarded by status="running"). The finder's proposed signature already passes the whole status-update stmt as a param, so this is handled — but it confirms the shared part is only the tail MECHANICS (append recompute, batch, extract last row, broadcast), not status logic.

No ADR conflict — pure intra-ingest.ts refactor; touches no durable decision.

Severity low is honest: both duplicated tails are realtime-only broadcast (the durable recompute is already shared via aggregateRecomputeStatement). Drift would corrupt a live event, not stored data; cron-driven and low-frequency. Test claim verified: grep of apps/dashboard/src/__tests__ shows no behavioral test of completeRun/finalizeStaleRun/appendRunResults — merge-run-status.test.ts only mentions completeRun in a comment. Both paths need the unbuilt real-DB harness (a known-outstanding item), so the testability upside is real but contingent on that harness.

#71 · Tests & testability
SQL-semantics builders (LIKE-escape, bucket divisor, status→bucket recompute) lack parity/escaping unit tests
low severity effort: small confidence: high untestable revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:8
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/runs-filters-where.ts:47
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/analytics/bucketing-sql.ts:16
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:429
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/ingest.ts:745
Problem — the friction

Several builders hand-write SQL semantics that the type system can't check: escapeLike (runs-filters-where.ts:8) escapes \ % _ before a LIKE; bucketExpr (bucketing-sql.ts:16) inlines divisors as literals specifically because D1 applies text affinity to numeric params (a subtle correctness landmine called out in the comment but unverified); aggregateRecomputeStatement (ingest.ts:429-445) hardcodes the status->bucket mapping in five raw subqueries that must stay in sync with statusBucket; currentStatusSeveritySql (ingest.ts:745) builds a CASE from RUN_STATUS_SEVERITY. These import void/db's sql/operators, which the stub DOES provide as placeholders — but no test renders the fragment to a SQL string to assert escaping, literal-inlining, or bucket-mapping parity. A LIKE-escape regression or a recompute that drifts from statusBucket is invisible until production data is wrong.

Solution — the deepened module

Treat this as a test-surface gap, not a deepening — and target the parts the current pure-function harness can actually reach (the void/db stub is identity placeholders; db is a throwing Proxy, so aggregateRecomputeStatement cannot be invoked under it). Concretely: (1) Highest value, zero infra: add a pure-JS parity test asserting the status→bucket mapping in statusBucket equals the mapping encoded in the recompute subqueries — ideally by extracting that mapping into one shared constant both sides consume (a small genuine deepening: one source of truth instead of two hand-kept-in-sync encodings), then the test is trivial and drift is structurally prevented. (2) Export escapeLike (or assert via buildRunsWhere's recorded like() arg under the stub) and test that \, %, _ are each doubled and ordinary chars pass through. (3) For bucketExpr, assert under the stub that the divisor is in the template strings with no bound args (literal inlining); do NOT claim to verify D1's text-affinity behavior — that is a runtime property unit tests can't reach. (4) currentStatusSeveritySql's SQL CASE rendering only becomes testable once the real-DB / real-Drizzle harness (KNOWN-OUTSTANDING) lands; until then its JS sibling mergeRunStatus is already covered, which is the behavior that matters.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers get confidence the WHERE/aggregate SQL is what they think without a DB round-trip. Locality: the 'these two representations of the status->bucket mapping must agree' invariant gets a single failing test instead of relying on a comment ('so it can't drift', ingest.ts:741) that nothing enforces.

Deletion test

These builders earn their keep (escaping/affinity/atomic-merge logic is real, with N callers across runs-list, analytics, ingest). The gap is purely test-surface. A parity test between aggregateRecomputeStatement and statusBucket prevents the exact drift the code comments fear.

Testability impact

LIKE-injection escaping, D1 numeric-affinity literal inlining, and recompute<->statusBucket parity become unit-assertable. Today they're only implicitly exercised by aggregate counts in the e2e dogfood run, which can't distinguish a bucket-mapping bug from a count that happens to match.

Interface sketch
expect(compile(buildRunsWhere({q:'50%_x'})).sql).toContain('like'); params escape \\%_ // parity: statuses in aggregateRecomputeStatement === statuses statusBucket maps to each column
Verifier notes

The cited code exists as described and the friction (untested SQL semantics) is real, but the finding is a testability gap, NOT a deepening, and its solution rests on a false premise about the stub.

VERIFIED CODE:
- escapeLike (runs-filters-where.ts:8) = value.replace(/[\\%_]/g, (c) => \\\${c}\). Pure 1-line function, NOT exported. Used only inside buildRunsWhere when filters.q is set.
- bucketExpr (bucketing-sql.ts:16) inlines 86400/604800 as SQL literals; comment explicitly cites D1 text-affinity on numeric bound params. Confirmed.
- aggregateRecomputeStatement (ingest.ts:429-445): five raw subqueries — total=COUNT(*), passed='passed', failed IN ('failed','timedout'), flaky='flaky', skipped='skipped'.
- statusBucket (ingest.ts:354-368): passed→passed, failed/timedout→failed, flaky→flaky, skipped→skipped, default→null. The mappings DO correspond, so the drift risk the finder names is genuine.
- currentStatusSeveritySql (ingest.ts:745) builds a CASE from RUN_STATUS_SEVERITY (ingest.ts:716); the JS sibling mergeRunStatus IS already covered by merge-run-status.test.ts, but the SQL CASE rendering is not.

CALLERS (deletion test): scopedRunsWhere → 1 page, 2 call sites (index.server.ts:35,94). bucketExpr → 3 insights pages (index/run-duration/suite-size .server.ts). aggregateRecomputeStatement → 2 internal ingest call sites (completeRun :795, plus :839). currentStatusSeveritySql → 1 (completeRun :783). The builders already concentrate their SQL semantics in one place each — they are already as-deep-as-they-get. The finding proposes ADDING TESTS, which neither concentrates smeared complexity nor introduces a seam, so the deletion test does not apply and deletionTestPasses=false. The finder even concedes "the gap is purely test-surface."

FALSE PREMISE IN SOLUTION: the stub (src/__tests__/helpers/void-db-stub.ts) is identity placeholders — sql returns {__op:"sql", strings, args} and operators return {__op, args}; it does NOT compile to SQL, escape LIKE, or distinguish bound params from inlined literals. So "render each fragment and assert on the emitted SQL/params" via the stub is only partially feasible: you can inspect the recorded pattern arg for escapeLike (via like()'s recorded args) and the template strings/empty-args for bucketExpr, but aggregateRecomputeStatement calls db.update(...) and db is a THROWING Proxy under the stub — that function is literally unrunnable in unit tests today. A real SQL-string assertion needs vi.mock("void/db") with a real Drizzle binding, i.e. the real-DB test harness that is already a KNOWN-OUTSTANDING item.

VALUE THAT SURVIVES: the highest-value, cheapest, infrastructure-free win is a pure-JS parity guard between statusBucket and the recompute mapping (and they genuinely must not drift). escapeLike deserves a 3-line pure-string test (export it or test through buildRunsWhere's recorded LIKE arg). bucketExpr's D1-affinity concern is a runtime property no unit test can prove — a test can only assert the divisor is inlined (args empty), not that D1 would mis-bind a param. No ADR conflict.

Cross-cutting concerns · 8 findings

#72 · Cross-cutting concerns
Identity resolution against the void-owned user/account tables (raw SQL + cast + email/githubLogin matchConds) is copy-pasted across four invite/email call sites with a fifth account-table variant
medium severity effort: small confidence: high duplication revised by verifier
Files
  • src/lib/authz.ts:100-111
  • src/lib/invite-identity.ts:33-41
  • routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/accept.ts:22-33
  • routes/api/invites/[inviteId]/decline.ts:30-33
  • pages/settings/profile.server.ts:19-41
Problem — the friction

Better Auth's user/account tables are intentionally NOT in db/schema.ts (durable decision 3), so every read goes through db.run(sql\select email from \"user\" ...\) followed by (row.results?.[0] as { email?: string } | undefined)?.email. That exact untyped shape appears verbatim in authz.ts, invite-identity.ts, accept.ts, decline.ts, and a select providerId, createdAt from account variant in profile.server.ts. There is no single place that knows the column names, the .results?.[0] D1 envelope, the cast shape, or the .toLowerCase() normalization. A maintainer adding a column, or an AI trying to learn 'how do I get the signed-in user's email', has to discover and replicate the raw-SQL idiom and re-author the cast each time; a typo in the table/column name fails silently at runtime because the cast suppresses all type checking.

Solution — the deepened module

Add a small auth-tables accessor module (e.g. src/lib/auth-tables.ts) that owns every raw-SQL read of the void-owned user/account tables. The load-bearing export is a combined identity accessor — getInviteIdentity(userId): Promise<{ email: string | null; githubLogin: string | null }> — that runs the parallel user-email read + userGithubAccounts join, unwraps the D1 .results?.[0] envelope, applies the cast once, and lower-cases the email. Pair it with a directedInviteMatchConds(identity) helper (or have accept/decline call getInviteIdentity then reuse inviteMatchesUser's matching) so the [eq(teamInvites.email,...), eq(teamInvites.githubLogin,...)] block stops being copy-pasted across authz/accept/decline. Add getUserAccounts(userId): Promise<{ providerId: string; createdAt: number | string | null }[]> for profile.server.ts so the account-table cast lives in one place too. The raw SQL, table/column names, envelope unwrap, casts, and email normalization then exist exactly once; callers get typed returns and never author the cast. Keep it strictly read-only over the void-managed tables — do NOT declare them in db/schema.ts (decision 3).

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers ask for email/accounts/inviteIdentity and get typed values — the invite-accept/decline/picker paths collapse to one line each. Locality: the cross-schema raw-SQL coupling to Better Auth's column names is concentrated in one file, so a Better Auth upgrade or a column rename is a one-file change instead of a five-site grep, and the type-unsafe as casts shrink from five to zero.

Deletion test

Deleting the accessor makes the complexity REAPPEAR at all five call sites (authz.getPendingInvitesForUser, invite-identity.inviteMatchesUser, invites/accept, invites/decline, settings/profile loader) — each would re-grow its own raw SQL + cast. Earns its keep.

Testability impact

The auth-table read becomes mockable through one interface, so getPendingInvitesForUser / inviteMatchesUser / the invite routes can be unit-tested by stubbing authTables.getUserEmail instead of needing a real D1 with a Better-Auth-seeded user table — directly relevant to the known-outstanding 'real-DB test harness not built' item.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/auth-tables.ts export function getUserEmail(userId: string): Promise<string | null>; export function getUserAccounts(userId): Promise<{providerId: string; createdAt: number|string|null}[]>; export function getInviteIdentity(userId): Promise<{email: string|null; githubLogin: string|null}>; // invariant: emails returned already lower-cased; no caller writes raw SQL against user/account
Verifier notes

Verified all five cited files. The friction exists verbatim. Four sites repeat the identical idiom: db.run(sqlselect email from "user" where id = ${id} limit 1) then (userRow.results?.[0] as { email?: string } | undefined)?.email + .toLowerCase() — authz.ts:100-111, invite-identity.ts:33-41, accept.ts:22-33, decline.ts:22-33. profile.server.ts:19-41 is a related-but-distinct variant reading the account table (SELECT providerId, createdAt) with its own results ?? [] as Array<{providerId, createdAt}> cast — same untyped-D1-envelope pattern, different shape and no email lower-casing. grep confirms NO existing accessor (authTables/getUserEmail/getInviteIdentity absent).

Three of the four email sites (authz.getPendingInvitesForUser, accept, decline) actually duplicate a larger composite, not just the bare SQL: Promise.all([raw user-email read, userGithubAccounts.githubLogin select]) followed by building matchConds = [eq(teamInvites.email, email), eq(teamInvites.githubLogin, githubLogin)]. That whole identity-resolution block is copy-pasted, which strengthens the case beyond what the finder framed.

The broader results?.[0] as ... envelope idiom also appears in insights/*.server.ts (slowest-tests, suite-size, run-duration), but those read tenant tables (runs/testResults/testTags) for aggregates via raw SQL — a separate concern from the void-owned auth tables (decision 3). Correctly excluded from this finding's scope.

Deletion test passes: removing the accessor regrows raw SQL + cast + envelope-unwrap + lower-casing + matchConds assembly at the four invite/email sites. Complexity concentrates, not just moves. Two+ real callers = real seam, not hypothetical.

No ADR conflict: the accessor sits ON TOP of the raw-SQL escape hatch that decision 3 requires; it does not propose declaring user/account in db/schema.ts. Finder correctly flagged no adrConflict.

Severity lowered high->medium: this is a narrow (5-site) duplication/silent-typo risk in an auth-adjacent corner, not a hot path; the security-critical matching is already centralized in inviteMatchesUser. Real, worth doing, but not high.

#73 · Cross-cutting concerns
requireTeamOwner signals not-owner via a bare Error, forcing callers into untyped catches that swallow D1 failures as 404 (invisible to Tail)
medium severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • src/lib/settings-scope.ts:52-57
  • src/lib/authz.ts:147-156
Problem — the friction

requireOwnerScope wraps requireTeamOwner in try { … } catch { throw new Response('Not Found', {status:404}) }. But requireTeamOwner throws a bare new Error('forbidden') for the legitimately-not-an-owner case AND would throw for any D1/transport failure — both land in the same catch and become a 404. A real database outage on a settings page is silently presented as 'not found' and never reaches logger.error / Cloudflare Tail (CLAUDE.md is explicit that swallowed errors are invisible to Tail). The catch can't tell intentional control-flow from infrastructure failure because the seam communicates not-owner via a generic Error rather than a typed result.

Solution — the deepened module

Change requireTeamOwner (authz.ts:147) to return {id,slug,name} | null instead of throwing new Error("forbidden") — mirroring resolveTeamBySlug, which already returns null on not-member. Then the three call patterns map only the null case to 404/403 and let any thrown Error (D1/transport failure) propagate uncaught, where 00.errors.ts logs it to Tail and rewrites to /oops: (1) requireOwnerScope (settings-scope.ts:53-57) drops its try/catch and does const team = await requireTeamOwner(...); if (!team) throw new Response("Not Found",{status:404});; (2) projects/new.server.ts (both sites, lines 50-54 / 69-73) does the same; (3) routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/invites.ts (lines 44-48) does if (!team) return c.json({error:"Forbidden"},403);. Do NOT touch requireOwnedProjectScope / keys.server.ts — that path already uses the null pattern via resolveProjectBySlugs and is correct (use it as the reference shape).

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers of requireOwnerScope keep their one-line 'give me the owned team or 404' contract, but a real failure now surfaces. Locality: the not-owner-vs-broken distinction is decided once at the authz seam instead of being lost in a blanket catch at every owner-gated settings action.

Deletion test

This is a leaky-seam fix, not a new module: tightening the contract concentrates the authz-vs-error decision in requireTeamOwner. The N affected callers are every settings owner-gated action that goes through requireOwnerScope/requireOwnedProjectScope (team general, project keys, projects/new).

Testability impact

Lets a test assert that a DB-layer throw produces a 500/logged error rather than a 404 — currently indistinguishable without inspecting Tail, so the misclassification is untestable through the HTTP surface.

Interface sketch
function requireTeamOwner(userId, teamSlug): Promise<OwnedTeam | null>; // null = not owner / not member; throws only on infra failure
Verifier notes

Code claims verified. settings-scope.ts:53-57 wraps requireTeamOwner in an UNTYPED catch that converts everything to throw new Response("Not Found",{status:404}). authz.ts:151-153: requireTeamOwner calls resolveTeamBySlug (which does db.select — a D1/transport failure throws a real Error) and ALSO throws new Error("forbidden") for the not-owner case. Both land in the same catch → both become 404. Confirmed.

The Tail-invisibility claim is strongly corroborated by middleware/00.errors.ts, which is deliberately architected around the convention "404 = intentional control-flow, stay quiet; raw throw / 5xx = logger.error to Tail." For HTML requests it rewrites 404→/not-found with NO logger.error (lines 75-84 and 133-145); only status===null/>=500 is logged (lines 86-90, 146-155). So a D1 outage repackaged as a 404 by requireOwnerScope is genuinely swallowed before it can reach Tail. The middleware's own comment (lines 56-59) states this contract explicitly. The finding's leaky-seam diagnosis is accurate: communicating not-owner via a generic Error prevents the catch from distinguishing authz control-flow from infrastructure failure.

CALLER-SET CORRECTIONS (the finding is imprecise here):
- The leaky catch is ONLY in requireOwnerScope (wrapping requireTeamOwner). Affected page actions: general.server.ts (2 call sites: loader/updateGeneral region + line 103), members.server.ts (1, line 90).
- requireOwnedProjectScope is NOT affected — it uses resolveProjectBySlugs which RETURNS null (the exact typed-result pattern the finding recommends), maps null→404 (lines 76-78), and lets any DB Error propagate uncaught → logged to Tail. So the finding's inclusion of "project keys" (keys.server.ts) is wrong; that path is already correct.
- TWO MORE sites replicate the same untyped-catch-around-requireTeamOwner anti-pattern INLINE, broadening the smear beyond requireOwnerScope: projects/new.server.ts (lines 50-54 and 69-73, both catch→404) and routes/api/teams/[teamSlug]/invites.ts (lines 44-48, catch→403). The invites route at least 403s rather than 404s, but still swallows DB failures.

DELETION TEST: passes. resolveTeamBySlug already returns null on not-member (authz.ts:55) — the project has the null-returning pattern. Making requireTeamOwner return null on not-owner (or a typed NotAuthorized result) concentrates the authz-vs-infra decision in one function and lets all 5 call sites across 3 files map null→404/403 while real Errors propagate to Tail. That removes complexity currently smeared across callers rather than moving it. No ADR conflict.

#74 · Cross-cutting concerns
`rateLimit()` per-route middleware factory is exported but has zero callers
low severity effort: small confidence: high dead / vestigial
Files
  • src/lib/rate-limit.ts:50-61
  • middleware/03.rate-limit.ts:45-83
Problem — the friction

rate-limit.ts exports two surfaces: checkRateLimit (the deep primitive, used by the global gate) and rateLimit(bindingName, keyFn), a per-route Hono-middleware factory. Grepping src/routes/middleware/pages shows rateLimit( has no callers — all throttling is done by the global path-matched gate in 03.rate-limit.ts, which calls checkRateLimit directly and builds its own 429 with a retry-after header. The factory builds a *different* 429 (c.json(..., 429) with no retry-after), so it isn't even a consistent alternative. It reads as a leftover from an abandoned per-route design and invites a future maintainer to wire throttling two incompatible ways.

Solution — the deepened module

Delete the rateLimit() factory (rate-limit.ts:50-61) and trim the now-stale doc-comment on rate-limit.ts:34-36 (drop the "Shared by the rateLimit() per-route factory and..." sentence, leaving just the global-gate reference). Keep checkRateLimit + clientIp as the primitives the single global gate composes. If per-route limiting is ever wanted, reuse the gate's tooManyRequests(retryAfterSeconds) helper so the 429 shape (with retry-after) stays uniform.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: one documented way to throttle (the global gate), so contributors don't author a second, header-incompatible path. Locality: the 429 response shape lives in exactly one place (03.rate-limit.ts#tooManyRequests) instead of two divergent ones.

Deletion test

Deleting rateLimit() makes NO complexity reappear — it has zero callers and the global gate already covers every throttled surface. Pure dead-code removal (the collapse-a-pass-through case).

Testability impact

Removes a public export that currently looks testable but is untested and unused; narrows the module's tested surface to checkRateLimit, which the regression test in rate-limit.test.ts already exercises.

Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. rate-limit.ts:50-61 defines rateLimit(bindingName, keyFn) as a Hono middleware factory; rate-limit.ts:38-48 defines checkRateLimit (the deep primitive) and rate-limit.ts:70-76 defines clientIp. Repo-wide grep for rateLimit( returns only the definition (line 50) and a doc-comment self-reference (line 34) — ZERO callers in routes/middleware/pages/tests. The sole composer of throttling is middleware/03.rate-limit.ts, which imports and calls checkRateLimit + clientIp directly (lines 49, 61, 76, 52, 75) across three path-matched surfaces (AUTH/ARTIFACT_DOWNLOAD/API ingest). The finder's "inconsistent 429" claim is correct: the factory returns c.json({error:"Too many requests"}, 429) (line 57, no retry-after), whereas the gate's tooManyRequests(retryAfterSeconds) (03.rate-limit.ts:35-43) always sets a retry-after header. The regression test (src/__tests__/rate-limit.test.ts) exercises checkRateLimit and the 03.rate-limit default-export middleware, never the rateLimit factory — so deleting the factory breaks no test.

Deletion test: deleting rateLimit() makes no complexity reappear — zero callers, and the global gate independently covers every throttled path. This is the collapse-a-pass-through case (dead/vestigial removal), correctly categorized. Not a deepening that concentrates smeared complexity; the value is locality/clarity (removing a second, incompatible way to wire throttling) rather than leverage. No durable-decision conflict — rate-limiting provisioning is already a known-outstanding item, and removing an unused per-route factory doesn't touch the single-D1/logical-tenancy/void-live decisions.

Minor correction to the solution: deleting the factory should ALSO trim the stale doc-comment on rate-limit.ts:34-36, which currently claims checkRateLimit is "Shared by the rateLimit() per-route factory and the global ... gate" — that shared-by relationship is one-sided/aspirational and would dangle after removal.

#75 · Cross-cutting concerns
app-layout and workspace-switcher hand-roll local Team/Project/SelectedTeam types, widening the branded TeamRole to a loose string at the owner gate
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • middleware/01.context.ts:34-56
  • src/components/app-layout.tsx:24-36
  • src/lib/authz.ts:158-180
Problem — the friction

The SharedBundle context (the project's one shared per-request grab-bag, read via useShared) is actually fairly disciplined — it carries auth + the four tenant lists and nothing else. But its element types are spelled three times: authz.ts defines ResolvedActiveTeam/ResolvedActiveProject (with a precise role: TeamRole), 01.context.ts inlines { slug; name }[] and references the Resolved* types, and app-layout.tsx re-declares its OWN local Team/Project/SelectedTeam interfaces with role?: string — widening the branded TeamRole union back to a loose optional string right where it's compared (selectedTeam.role === 'owner'). The consumer's hand-rolled mirror types can silently drift from the producer's, and the role-based owner gate loses its type safety at the exact comparison that authorizes UI.

Solution — the deepened module

Export the SharedBundle element shapes from one place and import them at the consumers. Concretely: lift SharedBundle (and a small WorkspaceListItem = { slug; name } for the userTeams/teamProjects lists) out of the declare module "void" block — either into authz.ts next to the Resolved* types, or a dedicated src/lib/shared-bundle.ts — so 01.context.ts imports it instead of inlining the list shapes. Then app-layout.tsx and workspace-switcher.tsx delete their local Team/Project/SelectedTeam and import ResolvedActiveTeam/ResolvedActiveProject/WorkspaceListItem, keeping role: TeamRole end-to-end so the === "owner" gate is union-checked. Note this is a localized type-DRY fix, not a behavioral deepening — frame it as such; it removes ~5 redundant local declarations and keeps the branded role precise at the authorization comparison.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: any consumer of useShared imports the same typed shape the middleware produces; adding a field to the bundle is one edit the consumers pick up. Locality: the producer (middleware) and consumers (app-layout, workspace-switcher) share one definition, so the shape can't drift and role keeps its narrow union.

Deletion test

Deleting app-layout's local interfaces makes the shapes reappear only if no shared export exists — providing the shared export removes 3 redundant declarations of the same data. The N consumers are app-layout, workspace-switcher, and the index/layout loaders that read c.get('shared').

Testability impact

Minor but real: a typed SharedBundle export can be constructed directly in component tests instead of mocking useShared with a loosely-typed literal; catches role-string typos at compile time.

Interface sketch
// one module owns: export interface SharedBundle { auth: AuthUser|null; userTeams: TeamRef[]; selectedTeam: ResolvedActiveTeam|null; teamProjects: TeamRef[]; selectedProject: ResolvedActiveProject|null } // app-layout imports SharedBundle/ResolvedActiveTeam; role stays TeamRole, no local re-decl
Verifier notes

The friction is real and cited accurately. Verified: authz.ts:158-173 defines ResolvedActiveTeam/ResolvedActiveProject both with role: TeamRole, where TeamRole = MembershipRole = "owner" | "member" (db/schema.ts:3). 01.context.ts:34-47 SharedBundle references those Resolved* types for selectedTeam/selectedProject and inlines { slug: string; name: string }[] for userTeams/teamProjects — and note those inlined list shapes ALSO already exist in authz.ts as TenantBundle.userTeams/teamProjects (lines 176,178), so the inlining is itself a third spelling. app-layout.tsx:24-36 re-declares local Team/Project/SelectedTeam extends Team { role?: string }, widening the branded TeamRole union to optional loose string. The owner gate at app-layout.tsx:169 (isOwner={selectedTeam.role === "owner"}) does compare against role?: string, so the comparison loses union narrowing.

Two corrections to the finder's framing: (1) The runtime data is NOT actually wrong — useShared() returns the real ResolvedActiveTeam with a true TeamRole; only app-layout's LOCAL prop type loosens it. So the gate works at runtime; the loss is compile-time precision (a typo like === "ownerr" wouldn't be caught). (2) The consumer count is slightly off. workspace-switcher.tsx:9-25 re-declares its own Team/Project but takes isOwner: boolean (line 24), NOT role — so it never touches the role-widening issue and is only a fourth {slug;name} spelling. index.server.ts:31-39 reads c.get("shared") with the correct middleware-declared type and does NOT redeclare anything; the layout loaders likewise pass through. So the redundant local re-declarations are: app-layout (Team, Project, SelectedTeam) + workspace-switcher (Team, Project) = 5 declarations of shapes that authz.ts/01.context.ts already own.

This is genuine type-hygiene friction but it is shallow: it's a UI-layer DRY/precision cleanup, not a deepening that concentrates behavior behind an interface. No ADR conflict. Severity low is correct.

#76 · Cross-cutting concerns
contract.test.ts guards wire-payload shapes but not the X-Wrightful-Version literal, which drifts independently across reporter and dashboard
low severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • src/lib/api-auth.ts:50-70
  • packages/reporter/src/client.ts:10
Problem — the friction

X-Wrightful-Version is the project's versioning seam, and negotiateVersionOrResponse is a genuinely deep little module (it hides the missing-vs-unsupported distinction, the upgrade-hint copy, and the 409 shape behind a one-call interface). The weakness is that the *value* lives in two unconnected places: the dashboard's SUPPORTED_VERSIONS = new Set(["3"]) and the reporter's PROTOCOL_VERSION = 3. The shared-contract files that exist precisely to keep wire types in sync (packages/reporter/src/types.ts <-> apps/dashboard/src/lib/schemas.ts, with contract.test.ts as the canary) do NOT carry the version number. When v4 ships, a maintainer must remember to bump two literals in two packages with no test asserting they relate — the same class of drift the contract test was built to catch for payload shapes.

Solution — the deepened module

Close the drift gap with the lowest-friction form first: extend packages/reporter/src/__tests__/contract.test.ts (the existing canary that already imports the dashboard's modules cross-package) with an assertion that the reporter's emitted X-Wrightful-Version is a member of the dashboard's accepted set. This requires exporting the accepted set (e.g. SUPPORTED_VERSIONS from api-auth.ts, or a small protocol.ts) and the reporter's PROTOCOL_VERSION (currently module-private in client.ts) so the test can compare them. negotiateVersionOrResponse stays unchanged as the deep negotiation seam — it just reads from the now-exported constant. Do NOT introduce a runtime module shared between the two packages; they have no shared runtime and the coupling only needs to hold at contract-test time, mirroring how schemas.ts is already imported relatively by the reporter's tests.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers/maintainers bump one constant; the negotiation behaviour is unchanged. Locality: the version number joins the existing reporter<->dashboard contract canary, so a forgotten bump fails a test instead of shipping a 409-everything or accept-everything mismatch.

Deletion test

This deepens the existing seam rather than adding a module: it concentrates the version literal that is currently smeared across 2 packages into the one contract surface. The N coordinated sites are reporter/client.ts and dashboard/api-auth.ts.

Testability impact

contract.test.ts already imports the dashboard schemas and parses reporter payloads; extending it to the version constant makes version-skew a unit-test failure instead of an integration-time 409 that only the not-yet-built E2E harness would surface.

Interface sketch
// shared wire contract export const PROTOCOL_VERSION = 3; export const SUPPORTED_PROTOCOL_VERSIONS = new Set([3]); // contract.test.ts: expect(SUPPORTED_PROTOCOL_VERSIONS.has(PROTOCOL_VERSION)).toBe(true)
Verifier notes

Verified against the cited files. The friction is real and exactly as described.

- packages/reporter/src/client.ts:10 declares const PROTOCOL_VERSION = 3; and sends "X-Wrightful-Version": String(PROTOCOL_VERSION) at lines 89 and 216.
- apps/dashboard/src/lib/api-auth.ts:50 declares const SUPPORTED_VERSIONS = new Set(["3"]); consumed only by negotiateVersionOrResponse (api-auth.ts:52-70), which is genuinely a deep little module — it hides the missing-vs-unsupported distinction, the upgrade-hint copy, and the 409 shape behind a one-call interface (the finder's characterization is accurate). Only caller is middleware/02.api-auth.ts:40.
- The two literals are unconnected. types.ts (header comment "keep in sync") and schemas.ts (header comment "Keep this file in sync") coordinate wire SHAPES but carry no version number. contract.test.ts is the canary for shapes (imports dashboard schemas at line 7, parses reporter payloads) but never references PROTOCOL_VERSION / SUPPORTED_VERSIONS / X-Wrightful-Version. So the finder's core claim — the version literal is the one wire-contract element the existing sync mechanism does NOT cover — is confirmed.

DELETION TEST: passes. The literal is smeared across exactly 2 source sites (reporter/client.ts, dashboard/api-auth.ts). The proposed canary assertion concentrates the coupling into the one place that already exists to catch contract drift, rather than moving it or inventing a one-adapter seam.

Two corrections that lower severity from medium to low:
1. The "promote to a shared module both packages import" half of the solution is overspecified and partly infeasible. The reporter is a published npm package (bundled via vp pack) and the dashboard is a Cloudflare worker; they share NO runtime module today. The only existing cross-package coupling is test-time: schemas.ts uses a deliberately relative import (schemas.ts:2-4 comment) precisely so contract.test.ts can reach it. A literal exported "from the place types.ts/schemas.ts coordinate" would still be a test-only import for the reporter, not a runtime share. The valuable, low-risk piece is the canary assertion, not a new shared export.
2. Partial coverage already exists. packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts already exercises server-side negotiation: line 127 sends "2", line 140 sends "99" (rejection cases), line 112 sends "3" (accept). What is genuinely missing is a single assertion tying the reporter's EMITTED version to the dashboard's accepted set — exactly the drift the finder names. Several test files hard-code "3" independently (client.test.ts:111,350; e2e specs), which is itself the smear in miniature.

No ADR conflict — versioning seam is orthogonal to the durable decisions. Severity is low because the blast radius is a single one-line bump that ships in one repo (monorepo, both packages versioned together) and a v4 bump is a deliberate, reviewed event, not an everyday edit — the drift window is narrow.

Several files exist only to preserve the shape of the abandoned rwsdk API across the Void migration. live-client.ts exports useRunProgress as useSyncedState 'until they're rewritten one by one' — but grep shows zero remaining useSyncedState consumers, so the alias is pure dead weight. links.ts is a runtime string-substitution link() shim explicitly described as a placeholder 'until we migrate the call sites to <Link href> literals', yet it's still imported by workspace-switcher.tsx and command-menu.tsx, sitting alongside the project rule (and Void's typed <Link>) it was meant to be replaced by — so two route-building idioms coexist. auth-client.ts and navigate.ts re-export Void primitives under their old rwsdk names. Benefits — leverage & locality

Deleting links.ts makes complexity reappear at 2 callers, so it must be migrated to <Link> rather than dropped. navigate.ts would make real complexity reappear at 5+ callers (it encodes the rwsdk->Void option remap) — it earns its keep and should NOT be deleted.

Testability impact

Minor: removes untested aliasing indirection so test imports point at the canonical hook; not a primary testability lever.

Verifier notes

All four cited files verified, and all caller counts are exactly as the finder claims. They were all introduced together in the single Void-migration commit faff356, matching the "migration-era shim" framing.

- live-client.ts:19 export { useRunProgress as useSyncedState }: grep across apps/packages for useSyncedState returns ZERO live .ts/.tsx consumers — only the comment at line 15 and historical worklogs. - links.ts: imported only by workspace-switcher.tsx:7 and command-menu.tsx:26 (5 link(...) invocations total). The impl is a real runtime :param substitution with encodeURIComponent + a missing-param throw — thin but not zero-logic. Deleting it makes that substitution reappear at the call sites, so the finder's "migrate to <Link>, don't drop" is right. Note void/routes only exposes typed route *types* in .void/routes.d.ts, not a typed-builder API — so migration target is <Link href> literals, not a drop-in builder.

deletionTestPasses=false: this is a dead-or-vestigial CLEANUP finding, not a deepening that concentrates complexity smeared across N callers behind a deeper interface. The finder's own analysis correctly classifies two of the four files (navigate, partly links) as NOT problems — so the item is a grab-bag, and the deepening/deletion-test framework doesn't really apply to it. No ADR conflict (it endorses the durable rwsdk->Void decisions; the shims are the migration residue, not a proposal to reverse anything).

#78 · Cross-cutting concerns
The github-enabled predicate is re-derived in four loaders and open-signup is decoded by two incompatible rules — no shared flag helper
low severity effort: small confidence: high inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files

Problem — the friction

CLAUDE.md mandates import { env } from "void/env", and env.ts is the declared source of truth — but the same values are read three different ways. ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP is read as typed env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP (signup.server.ts, login.server.ts) AND as process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP parsed by a hand-rolled /^(true|1)$/i regex (auth.ts:80) — two different boolean-coercion rules for one flag. githubEnabled/githubProviderEnabled is computed from process.env.AUTH_GITHUB_* in BOTH auth.ts:73-75 (decides whether to register the provider) and profile.server.ts:61-63 (decides whether to show the connect button), as independent Boolean(id && secret) expressions that can silently diverge. ingest.ts reaches past env entirely to import.meta.env.VITE_IS_DEV_SERVER. A maintainer can't answer 'is GitHub login on?' or 'how is backdating gated?' from one place.

Solution — the deepened module

Add one tiny helper, src/lib/feature-flags.ts, that owns the two DERIVED flags only: githubEnabled (the Boolean(id && secret) predicate) and openSignupAllowed. For auth.ts's config-time constraint, the helper can still read process.env (it doesn't need the typed proxy to AND two strings), so all four github sites collapse to one definition and the regex-vs-boolean open-signup decode collapses to one coercion rule. Do NOT touch backdatingAllowed() — it is already a single deep reader; including it would just relocate code. Drop artifact-tokens.ts from the finding entirely (different value, clean read).

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers import appConfig.githubEnabled instead of re-deriving from raw env; the provider-registration and the connect-button can never disagree. Locality: the one legitimate process.env-at-config-time exception (documented in auth.ts) is isolated, and the coercion rule for each flag lives once, so 'turn on open signup' or 'change the GitHub gate' is a single-line edit.

Deleting the module makes the github-enabled derivation REAPPEAR in 2 sites (auth.ts, profile.server.ts) and the open-signup coercion REAPPEAR in 2 sites (auth.ts vs signup/login loaders) with two different rules — the exact divergence risk it would remove. Earns its keep as a deepening of scattered flag logic.

Testability impact

Derived flags become pure functions of an injected env object, unit-testable without booting the worker; today verifying 'github button hidden iff provider not registered' requires running both auth.ts config evaluation and the profile loader against matching process.env.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/app-config.ts export const appConfig = { githubEnabled: boolean, // single source for provider-registration + connect-button openSignupAllowed: boolean, // single coercion rule backdatingAllowed(): boolean, // wraps import.meta.env.VITE_IS_DEV_SERVER };

Read all cited files. The core duplication is real and the finder actually UNDERCOUNTED it.

GITHUB-ENABLED DERIVATION — Boolean(id && secret) is independently re-derived in 4 sites, not 2:

- pages/login.server.ts:17-19 via typed env (gates the GitHub button)

OPEN-SIGNUP DUAL-DECODE — real. auth.ts:80 hand-rolls /^(true|1)$/i.test(process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP ??
