Leave ansi.ts and safe-next-path.ts out — they defend different threats (rendered-error-text XSS; open-redirect) and already have their own tests (safe-next-path.test.ts); folding them in over-couples three unrelated concerns.

Benefits — leverage & locality

LEVERAGE: a maintainer or AI touching any one leg (CSP, allowlist, redirect guard, ansi sink) has one place to read the whole threat model and one test that fails if the legs drift apart. LOCALITY: the 'what may render on our origin' decision stops being smeared across five files with four hand-copied threat sentences; widening the allowlist or relaxing Content-Disposition now visibly touches the policy module and trips a cross-check.

Deletion test

This is a consolidation, not a new abstraction over runtime behaviour — deleting the proposed locality just returns to the status quo where the policy is rediscovered file-by-file. It earns its keep as the place N=4 currently-disconnected defenses (CSP, content-type allowlist, ansi sink, redirect guard) are kept consistent; the friction it removes is the silent-drift class of bug, not duplicated runtime code.

Testability impact

Cross-leg consistency (allowlist excludes exactly the renderable types CSP can't block, download always forces attachment) becomes a single assertion suite. Today each leg is tested in isolation (or not at all, for ansi) and their mutual consistency is untested — a widened allowlist passes all existing tests.

Interface sketch
// content-types.ts becomes the canonical render policy: SAFE_CONTENT_TYPES: ReadonlySet<string> // single source for register-refine + download/upload normalize // + policy.test.ts: asserts no SAFE type is executable, download forces attachment, CSP comment references this module
Verifier notes

Cited code verified. The four mechanisms exist exactly as cited: CSP in void.json:19 (img-src 'self' data: blob:, object-src 'none', frame-ancestors 'none'); SAFE_CONTENT_TYPES allowlist with deliberate SVG/text-html exclusion in content-types.ts:11-38; ansiToHtml escaping in ansi.ts:9-11 (consumed via dangerouslySetInnerHTML in test-error-alert.tsx + flaky-test-row.tsx); redirect/header-injection guard in safe-next-path.ts. download.ts:147 forces safeContentType() and :159-162 forces Content-Disposition: attachment. The "three copies of one sentence" claim is partly true: rg confirms the "dashboard origin" threat sentence appears in schemas.ts (x2), content-types.ts (x3), download.ts (x2) — but the ansi and redirect legs do NOT share that phrasing and defend genuinely distinct threats (stored-XSS-via-rendered-error-text, open-redirect/header-injection), not "attacker artifact bytes served from origin".

The finding's central premise (N=4 disconnected defenses for ONE invariant) is overstated and fails the deletion test. The content-type allowlist is ALREADY a single deep module: content-types.ts is the sole home of SAFE_CONTENT_TYPES, with all three real callers (schemas.ts:160 isSafeContentType in the Zod refine, upload.ts:63 safeContentType, download.ts:147 safeContentType) routing through it. There is no smear to concentrate — the allowlist locality the finding asks for already exists, and schemas.ts:158-159 even cross-references it ("see src/lib/content-types.ts"). A proposed "origin-safety module owning all four" cannot host runtime behaviour for three of the legs: CSP is static Cloudflare config in void.json (can't move into TS), and ansi/redirect have zero shared implementation with the allowlist. Grouping them concentrates a slogan, not complexity. So deletionTestPasses=false: the deepening would mostly MOVE/relabel, not concentrate smeared logic.

The genuine residual friction is narrow and real: (1) no test ties the allowlist to the download handler's attachment-forcing + safeContentType override (content-types.test.ts only tests the pure allowlist functions; grep found no test asserting Content-Disposition: attachment or download-handler behaviour); (2) the CSP string has no comment pointing back at the allowlist as the companion defense. That is a doc-comment + one integration-style test, not a module. Severity adjusted down to low — it's a missing regression test + a back-reference comment, not missing locality. No ADR conflict.

Gap · Config & secrets fallback · 4 findings

#91 · Gap · Config & secrets fallback
E2e artifact-token forger silently diverges from the dashboard the moment a dedicated ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is set — the fixture injects BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, not the resolved signing secret
medium severity effort: small confidence: high missing locality revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/src/lib/artifact-tokens.ts:46-58
  • apps/dashboard/env.ts:18-25
  • packages/e2e/src/e2e.test.ts:34-46
  • packages/e2e/src/dashboard-fixture.ts:34-40
  • apps/dashboard/src/__tests__/artifact-tokens.test.ts:4-9
Problem — the friction

The rule 'sign artifact tokens with ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET, else fall back to BETTER_AUTH_SECRET' lives in three places that must agree but have no enforced link. It is documented in env.ts:23, implemented in getKey() at artifact-tokens.ts:50 (env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET), and re-assumed by the e2e HMAC forger at e2e.test.ts:44 (createHmac('sha256', BETTER_AUTH_SECRET)), which only ever knows BETTER_AUTH_SECRET because dashboard-fixture.ts writes only that into .env.local (line 206) and never sets ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET. Today the fallback masks the divergence: with ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET unset, both sides resolve to BETTER_AUTH_SECRET and tokens verify. The instant prod (or any future fixture) sets ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET, the dashboard signs with the dedicated secret while the e2e clone still signs with BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, so every forged download token 401s — and because the selection logic is duplicated by hand rather than imported, nothing fails at compile time; it surfaces only at deploy/e2e run. A maintainer rotating to a dedicated secret has to know to also touch a test fixture in a different package.

Solution — the deepened module

Don't lead with an in-worker resolveArtifactTokenSecret(env) extraction — inside the dashboard that is a one-caller helper (getKey() is the sole consumer of the ??) and a shallow move. The earning-its-keep seam is the cross-package one: guarantee the secret the e2e forger signs with is provably the same value the dashboard's getKey() resolves under. Concretely: (1) in dashboard-fixture.ts, decide the artifact-signing secret the boot uses — if a dedicated ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is set, write it into .env.local AND inject it (rename the injected channel to e.g. artifactTokenSecret); otherwise inject the BETTER_AUTH_SECRET fallback. The forger then reads the resolved secret instead of re-deriving the precedence by hand. (2) Optionally factor the ?? precedence into one tiny pure function so the fixture and getKey() express it identically, but treat that as a readability nicety, not the load-bearing fix. The seam should answer exactly one question for any token-minting party — "what secret signs artifact tokens under this boot" — so the e2e forger can never silently diverge from the producer.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: callers (the download handler, the e2e forger, any future CLI that needs a download link) get the correct key from one call instead of re-deriving the precedence rule. Locality: the fallback precedence, and the eventual removal of the fallback, change in exactly one function; a secret rotation can't silently desync the test harness because the harness resolves through the same interface.

Deletion test

Earning its keep. Delete the resolver and the precedence rule reappears in at least 3 callers that must stay byte-identical: getKey() in artifact-tokens.ts, the e2e HMAC clone in e2e.test.ts, and the env.ts documentation comment (a fourth latent caller is any future presigned-link minting outside the dashboard worker). It is not a pass-through — it concentrates a correctness invariant currently smeared across two packages.

Testability impact

Today the e2e suite tests artifact download against a hand-cloned signer that is only accidentally correct; there is no test that the fallback precedence itself holds (the unit test at artifact-tokens.test.ts mocks ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET: undefined, so the 'dedicated secret wins' branch is never exercised). A resolver makes the precedence directly unit-testable (set both, assert ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET wins; unset the dedicated, assert fallback) and lets the e2e forger import the real signer, eliminating the clone entirely.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/config.ts (or artifact-tokens.ts) export function artifactTokenSecret(): string // env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET; the ONLY place this precedence exists // e2e imports the real signArtifactToken, or the fixture returns the resolved secret it booted under
Verifier notes

All five cited locations verified exactly as described. artifact-tokens.ts:50 — getKey() resolves env.ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET ?? env.BETTER_AUTH_SECRET. env.ts:18-25 — ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET is .optional() and its comment (line 23) documents the same fallback in prose. e2e.test.ts:34-47 — a hand-written forger calls createHmac("sha256", BETTER_AUTH_SECRET), where BETTER_AUTH_SECRET comes from inject("betterAuthSecret") (line 19). dashboard-fixture.ts:204-218 — the fixture writes ONLY BETTER_AUTH_SECRET into .env.local (line 206) and never sets ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET; it injects fixture.betterAuthSecret (project.provide("betterAuthSecret", ...) in vitest.globalSetup.ts confirmed). So the forger always signs with BETTER_AUTH_SECRET and only verifies today because getKey()'s ?? falls back to the same value. The silent-divergence trap is real: the instant any deployment/fixture sets ARTIFACT_TOKEN_SECRET, the dashboard signs with the dedicated secret while the e2e forger keeps using BETTER_AUTH_SECRET, every forged download token 401s, and nothing fails at compile time because the rule is copied by hand across a package + runtime boundary.

Where the finding over-claims: the deletion test. I traced every caller. Inside the dashboard worker, getKey() is the SOLE consumer of the ?? precedence — signArtifactToken/verifyArtifactToken both call getKey(), and the only external signing caller, test-artifact-actions.ts:156, calls signArtifactToken (the public interface), NOT a secret resolver. So a resolveArtifactTokenSecret(env) extracted purely inside the dashboard is a one-caller, shallow helper — it does not concentrate complexity smeared across N in-worker callers. The finder's "at least 3 callers that must stay byte-identical" is inflated: env.ts:23 is a documentation comment (not an executing caller), and the e2e forger lives in a different package/runtime (node:crypto, vitest Node globalSetup; packages/e2e has no dependency on @wrightful/dashboard) that physically cannot import the WebCrypto + void/env-bound getKey(). The genuine concentration is the cross-package seam, not an in-worker extraction.

ADR check: no conflict with any durable decision. Severity reduced high->medium: it is latent (bites only when a dedicated secret is introduced — which nothing currently does), it is a test-fidelity gap rather than a production-correctness bug, and it sits adjacent to the already-tracked known-outstanding item "build/deploy/E2E against the Void dashboard not yet exercised."

#92 · Gap · Config & secrets fallback
"Is GitHub OAuth enabled" is inlined in four loaders, splitting an unavoidable config-time/request-time env-source choice across copies
low severity effort: small confidence: high duplication
Files
  • apps/dashboard/auth.ts:73-75
  • apps/dashboard/pages/login.server.ts:17-19
  • apps/dashboard/pages/signup.server.ts:22-24
  • apps/dashboard/pages/settings/profile.server.ts:61-62
Problem — the friction

The predicate 'both AUTH_GITHUB_CLIENT_ID and AUTH_GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET are set' is hand-written in four places, and split across two sources: auth.ts:73-75 and profile.server.ts:61-62 read raw process.env, while login.server.ts:17 and signup.server.ts:22 read the typed env. Booleanness is by truthiness of (possibly empty) strings vs typed-optional values — so an empty-string secret (allowed by an .optional() string) is falsy here but the same raw '' could behave differently across the two sources, and the auth provider actually registered (auth.ts:75 githubProviderEnabled) can drift from the 'Continue with GitHub' button the loaders render. A maintainer changing the rule (e.g. to also require a configured callback URL) must find and edit four copies in two pack)-of-the-app and keep the process.env/env split straight.

Solution — the deepened module

Add one resolver, githubOAuthEnabled(source: "config" | "request"): boolean, in a small auth-config module (co-located with an openSignupAllowed() resolver for the parallel ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP flag). The resolver OWNS the dual-reader: at config time it reads process.env (auth.ts at void prepare), at request time it reads the typed env (loaders). auth.ts decides provider registration through it; login/signup/profile loaders call the request-time variant and pass the result to their pages. Frame this as concentrating the config-time-vs-request-time reader choice in one place (not as eliminating it — that constraint is real per auth.ts:68-72), which removes the 4-way duplication and makes a future rule change a single edit.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: provider registration and every UI that conditionally renders the GitHub button derive from one source, so the button can never appear when the provider isn't actually wired. Locality: the cred-presence rule and the source split change once; the four current copies collapse to four call sites of one function.

Deletion test

Earning its keep. Delete it and the same Boolean(id && secret) predicate reappears in 4 callers (auth.ts, login.server.ts, signup.server.ts, profile.server.ts) — already duplicated today, with two of them on a different env source, which is exactly the drift risk a resolver removes.

Testability impact

Currently the only way to verify the button matches the registered provider is to boot the app and inspect rendered HTML. A resolver makes the predicate unit-testable and lets auth-config tests assert provider registration without a live Better Auth instance.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/config.ts export function githubOAuthEnabled(): boolean // both AUTH_GITHUB_CLIENT_ID & _SECRET present; one source-of-truth for provider + UI
Verifier notes

All four sites verified exactly as cited. auth.ts:73-75 reads process.env.AUTH_GITHUB_CLIENT_ID/SECRET into githubProviderEnabled (gates provider registration at lines 98-112); profile.server.ts:61-63 reads process.env; login.server.ts:17-19 and signup.server.ts:22-24 read the typed env from void/env. So the predicate Boolean(id && secret) is inlined in 4 places, split 2/2 across two env sources — confirmed by grep, no shared resolver exists anywhere in src/. env.ts:33-34 declares both creds as .optional() strings, so the empty-string-is-falsy concern is real (an "" secret passes the optional schema but is falsy here).

Two corrections to the finder's framing: (1) The two-source split is NOT a free design choice — auth.ts:68-72 documents that it must use process.env because it is evaluated at void prepare/config-evaluation time, before void's typed env proxy is bound; the loaders run at request time where typed env is available. The proposed resolver therefore cannot eliminate the dual-reader — it concentrates it. The finder's solution already acknowledges this ("config-time-vs-request-time source choice"), so the solution is honest, but the title/problem oversell it as gratuitous duplication. (2) The "registered provider can drift from the button" risk is overstated: all four predicates apply the identical Boolean(id && secret) rule against the same underlying Cloudflare env (process.env and the typed proxy resolve from the same source at runtime), so practical drift today is near-zero. The genuine value is locality + capturing the non-obvious dual-reader rationale in one named place, so a future rule change (e.g. also require a callback URL) edits one site instead of four.

Deletion test: delete the resolver and Boolean(id && secret) reappears verbatim across auth.ts, login.server.ts, signup.server.ts, profile.server.ts — 2 of them on a different env source. That is smeared complexity being concentrated, not a hypothetical one-adapter seam. Passes. Severity low is correct: the rule is trivial and currently consistent; this is drift-prevention/locality, not a latent bug. No ADR conflict — this is fully compatible with the durable decisions (it touches only env-flag derivation, not tenancy/D1/auth-table ownership).

#93 · Gap · Config & secrets fallback
env.ts comment overstates artifact byte-cap enforcement: upload only matches the registered size, it does not re-check the cap
low severity effort: small confidence: high leaky seam revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/env.ts:36-40
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/register.ts:54-64
  • apps/dashboard/routes/api/artifacts/[id]/upload.ts:40-54
Problem — the friction

env.ts:37-38 documents WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES as 'Enforced in /api/artifacts/register and again as Content-Length in /api/artifacts/:id/upload'. Only register.ts:54 actually reads the cap (rejects sizeBytes > maxBytes with 413). upload.ts never reads env.WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES at all — its line 45 check is contentLength !== row.sizeBytes, i.e. it enforces that the body matches the REGISTERED size, not that it's under the cap. The cap is only transitively enforced at upload because an oversized artifact never gets a row at register. The doc comment overstates the invariant: a maintainer who lowers the cap will reasonably assume in-flight/already-registered uploads are also bounded, but they aren't re-checked. The 'what is the byte cap and where does it bind' decision is split between a route that knows the cap and a route that only knows the per-row size, with the contract narrated (inaccurately) in a third place.

Solution — the deepened module

Drop the accessor framing — the cap has a single reader (register.ts:54), so there is no smeared complexity to concentrate and a maxArtifactBytes() wrapper would be a pass-through. The real defect is the inaccurate interface narration. Correct env.ts:37-38 to state that the cap binds only at /api/artifacts/register (413 on oversized), and that /api/artifacts/:id/upload does not re-check the cap — it only asserts Content-Length equals the already-registered sizeBytes (which is transitively cap-bound because an oversized artifact never gets a row). Optionally, if a maintainer genuinely wants the cap re-asserted at the streaming boundary (e.g. to defend against the cap being lowered between register and an in-flight upload), add an explicit row.sizeBytes <= env.WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES guard in upload.ts AND keep the comment accurate — but treat that as an optional behavioral hardening, not a refactor.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: register, upload, and tests read the cap from one place instead of one route hardcoding the env read and the other implicitly trusting it. Locality: lowering the cap, or moving to per-project caps later, changes one accessor; the documented contract and the code agree because there's one place to keep honest.

Deletion test

Mostly earning its keep as documentation-of-an-invariant rather than code volume — the accessor concentrates the limit definition that register.ts currently owns alone and upload.ts implicitly depends on. Deleting it re-smears the cap read into register and forces the contract to stay narrated correctly by hand across two routes plus env.ts.

Testability impact

Today the cap is only tested via an integration call to register (and the brief notes that real-DB harness isn't built). An accessor + an explicit upload-side guard make the cap boundary unit-testable: assert register 413s over-cap, and assert upload also refuses an over-cap registered row, without R2 or D1.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/config.ts export function maxArtifactBytes(): number // env.WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES; single definition // upload.ts: if (row.sizeBytes > maxArtifactBytes()) -> 413 (make the doc's 'again' true, or fix the doc)
Verifier notes

Factual claims verified against all three cited files. env.ts:37-38 does narrate dual enforcement ("Enforced in /api/artifacts/register and again as Content-Length in /api/artifacts/:id/upload"). register.ts:54-64 is the sole reader of WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES — it finds any artifact with sizeBytes > maxBytes and returns 413. upload.ts has NO env import at all; line 44-45 checks contentLength !== row.sizeBytes, i.e. body-matches-REGISTERED-size, not under-the-cap. So the comment is genuinely misleading: it conflates "Content-Length equals registered size" with "Content-Length under the cap." The cap is only transitively enforced at upload (an oversized artifact never gets a row at register, so its size can never be matched). The interface-narration defect is REAL.

However the proposed deepening fails the deletion test. I grepped the whole repo: WRIGHTFUL_MAX_ARTIFACT_BYTES is read in EXACTLY ONE place (register.ts:54). schemas.ts references an unrelated MAX_ARTIFACTS_PER_REQUEST (a count cap). The reporter (client.ts:217) only sends Content-Length: String(sizeBytes) — it has no awareness of the cap. download.ts reads no env. So the cap has a single caller, not N. The finder's deletion-test rationale ("re-smears the cap read into register and forces the contract to stay narrated correctly across two routes") is FALSE — upload.ts does not read the cap, and there is nothing smeared to concentrate. A maxArtifactBytes() accessor wrapping a one-line single-site env read is a textbook one-adapter pass-through (deletionTestPasses=false). Option (a), adding row.sizeBytes <= maxArtifactBytes() in upload.ts, would CREATE a second reader for a defensively-redundant re-check (the row already passed the cap at register and contentLength must already equal row.sizeBytes); it guards only the narrow lower-the-cap-mid-flight window — a behavioral hardening, not a deepening.

The only sound action is option (b): correct the env.ts comment so it stops overstating the invariant. That is a trivial doc fix, not a structural deepening. No ADR conflict (cap lives in env.ts per decision-set; nothing reversed).

#94 · Gap · Config & secrets fallback
ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP truthiness is decoded by two unrelated rules (regex vs void boolean coercion) that can drift
low severity effort: small confidence: medium inconsistent interface revised by verifier
Files
  • apps/dashboard/auth.ts:77-82
  • apps/dashboard/pages/signup.server.ts:14-25
  • apps/dashboard/pages/login.server.ts:12-24
  • apps/dashboard/env.ts:49-54
Problem — the friction

ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP is declared once as boolean().default(false) in env.ts but consumed through two different access paths with two different coercion rules. auth.ts:80-82 reads the RAW string process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP and runs it through /^(true|1)$/i to decide disableSignUp (it has to use process.env because Better Auth config evaluates before void's typed env proxy is bound). The page loaders read the already-coerced typed env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP boolean (signup.server.ts:19 gates the UI redirect; login.server.ts:22 passes signupAllowed to the page). These can disagree: a value the void env layer coerces to true but that the regex rejects (e.g. 'TRUE\n', 'yes', '1 ') would show the signup UI while Better Auth's API still rejects sign-up — or vice versa. The decode rule and the source-of-truth ('which env reader, and does it run before or after coercion') are re-decided at every consumer, so a maintainer can't reason about the flag without reading all three call sites.

Solution — the deepened module

Extract one shared truthiness predicate, e.g. isEnvTruthy(raw: string | undefined): boolean (the canonical /^(true|1)$/i rule), in a small env-utils module. Have auth.ts call isEnvTruthy(process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP) at config time (it must stay on process.env because Better Auth config evaluates before the typed env proxy is bound) and keep the loaders reading the typed env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP at request time. The seam concentrates the one decision — how a string becomes a feature gate — and removes the second, divergent decode rule, while preserving the correct per-context source. Document the config-time-vs-request-time split in one place so a maintainer reasons about it once rather than at three call sites. Do NOT route the request-time loaders through process.env.

Benefits — leverage & locality

Leverage: auth config and every page loader get the same boolean from one call instead of re-implementing parsing. Locality: the 'how do we read a flag that must work at config-eval time AND request time' subtlety lives in one place; adding email-verification gating later changes one function, not three.

Deletion test

Earning its keep. Delete it and the dual-source + dual-decode logic reappears across 3 callers (auth.ts, signup.server.ts, login.server.ts) that currently already disagree — proof the smear is a live hazard, not hypothetical.

Testability impact

The flag's behavior is currently only observable through booting the full app (auth.ts can't even import the typed env at config time, so it's untestable in isolation). A resolver makes 'these string inputs map to these booleans' a table-driven unit test, and lets the auth-config branch be asserted without standing up Better Auth.

Interface sketch
// src/lib/config.ts export function openSignupAllowed(): boolean // canonical decode of process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP; usable at config-eval AND request time
Verifier notes

Verified all four cited sites. env.ts:54 declares ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP: boolean().default(false) — single declaration. auth.ts:80-82 reads the RAW string process.env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP ?? "" through /^(true|1)$/i; the comment at auth.ts:77-79 explicitly confirms the finder's reasoning ("Read via process.env for the same config-time-evaluation reason as the GitHub creds above" — Better Auth config evaluates at prepare/config time before void's typed env proxy is bound). signup.server.ts:19 reads the coerced typed env.ALLOW_OPEN_SIGNUP boolean to gate the redirect; login.server.ts:22 reads the same typed boolean and passes signupAllowed to login.tsx:107 which conditionally renders the signup link. So two access paths (process.env+regex vs typed env proxy) and three consumers are real, exactly as cited. The inconsistent-interface friction is genuine: there is no shared decode definition, so the truthiness rule and the source-selection are re-decided at each site.

Two corrections to the finder's framing. (1) The deletion-test claim that callers "currently already disagree" is overstated — for the documented/normal inputs (true/1/false/unset) the void boolean() coercion and the regex agree, so there is no live divergence today; the disagreement is LATENT, only on edge inputs (e.g. yes, TRUE\n, 1 ). I could not read void's exact boolean() coercion source (the void package is not present in node_modules at this checkout, so the precise coercion rule is unconfirmed), which is why confidence is medium and severity adjusted to low. The structural deletion test still passes: a shared seam concentrates the truthiness rule plus the genuinely tricky config-time-vs-request-time knowledge that is currently smeared across 3 sites.

(2) The proposed solution is subtly wrong: "internally reading process.env once" cannot serve the request-time loaders correctly on Cloudflare Workers — the whole reason void exposes a typed env proxy is that it is the correct request-time source for secrets/bindings, which process.env may not carry at request time. Forcing both contexts through process.env risks regressing the loaders. The seam should concentrate the DECODE RULE (one truthiness predicate) and accept each context's correct source, not collapse both to process.env. No ADR conflict.
